Direct links to specific content often require purchasing access). Although the website doesn't directly offer
the answer, it provides the detailed information on the ITIL framework and its core concepts.
ITIL Foundation Handbook: Search for 'ITIL Foundation Handbook' (various publishers). These handbooks
describe the Continual Improvement Model in detail.
Question: 93 CertyIQ
What MAIN factors are considered to assess the priority of an incident?
A.The urgency and impact
B.The impact and complexity
C.The cost and urgency
D.The complexity and cost
Answer: A
Explanation:
The correct answer is A: The urgency and impact. Incident priority is a critical aspect of ITIL 4 incident
management, as it dictates the speed and resources allocated to resolving the incident. It's determined by
assessing two key factors: urgency and impact.
Impact refers to the extent to which an incident affects the business. A high-impact incident significantly
disrupts operations, affects a large number of users, or causes financial loss. For example, a complete outage
of a critical cloud service like a company's CRM has a high impact.
Urgency, on the other hand, represents the time sensitivity of the incident. An incident with high urgency
requires immediate attention because further delay will cause significant harm. Imagine a situation where a
financial institution experiences a security breach that could expose customer data; this has high urgency.
By considering both impact and urgency, organizations can prioritize incidents effectively. For example, a
high-impact, high-urgency incident (like the security breach) would be given the highest priority, ensuring
immediate action. A low-impact, low-urgency incident (like a minor software glitch affecting a single user)
would receive a lower priority.
Complexity and cost (options B, C, and D) might be considered during incident resolution and resource
allocation, but they are not primary factors in initially determining the priority. Complexity influences the
effort required for resolution, and cost comes into play when considering different resolution options, but
neither directly informs the immediate need for intervention like impact and urgency do. A simple incident can
still have a high impact (e.g., a single typo in a database leading to a widespread application failure), and a
complex incident might have a low impact (e.g., a difficult-to-diagnose network issue affecting a non-critical
system). Therefore, prioritising using only cost and/or complexity would not be optimal.
Therefore, the interplay of impact and urgency is crucial in prioritizing incidents and directing the appropriate
level of attention to restore services quickly and efficiently. This aligns directly with ITIL 4 best practices for
incident management.
Authoritative Links:

AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Guidance: https://www.axelos.com/ (While a direct link to the specific guidance
requires a paid subscription, the AXELOS website provides general information on ITIL 4.)
ITIL Foundation Handbook: Several publishers offer ITIL 4 Foundation handbooks that detail incident
management and prioritization based on impact and urgency. These are widely available for purchase.
Question: 94 CertyIQ
Which term is used to describe the prediction and control of income and expenditure within an organization?
A.Charging
B.Governance
C.Budgeting
D.Accounting
Answer: C
Explanation:
The correct answer is C. Budgeting. Here's why:
Budgeting is the process of creating a financial plan, typically on an annual basis, which outlines projected
income and expenditure for an organization. It involves forecasting revenues, allocating funds to various
departments and projects, and monitoring actual performance against the budget. This planning process
allows organizations to predict financial needs, control spending, and ensure financial stability. Budgeting is a
proactive measure, aimed at guiding financial decisions and resource allocation.
Charging (A) relates to billing customers for services used. Governance (B) focuses on the framework for
making decisions and providing direction. Accounting (D) involves recording, classifying, and summarizing
financial transactions to create financial statements. While accounting is essential for tracking actual income
and expenditure, it's a retrospective activity. Accounting provides the data used in the budgeting process, but
it is not the prediction and control process itself. While charging can influence income, it's not the
comprehensive process of predicting and controlling both income and expenditure. Governance creates the
framework within which budgeting operates, but it doesn't define the budgeting process itself.
Therefore, budgeting is the only option that accurately describes the prediction (forecasting income) and
control (managing expenditure) of financial resources within an organization.
For further information on budgeting, consider these resources:
Investopedia: https://www.investopedia.com/terms/b/budgeting.asp
Corporate Finance Institute (CFI):
https://corporatefinanceinstitute.com/resources/knowledge/accounting/budgeting-process/
Question: 95 CertyIQ
Where should all master copies of controlled software and documentation be stored?
A.In the definitive capacity library
B.In the definitive media library
C.In the definitive security library
D.In the definitive production library

Answer: B
Explanation:
The correct answer is B. In ITIL 4, the Definitive Media Library (DML) is the secure location where the definitive
or master copies of all software, documentation, and related components are stored. It acts as a single,
secure repository for controlled versions of these assets.
Here's why the other options are incorrect:
Definitive Capacity Library: Deals with information relating to resource capacity and performance
management, not software storage.
Definitive Security Library: This isn't a standard ITIL term. Security considerations are addressed across all
ITIL practices.
Definitive Production Library: This also isn't a standard ITIL term and the production environment generally
contains running instances, not master copies, of software.
The DML is a crucial component for change management, release management, and configuration
management. By storing the master copies in a controlled environment, organizations ensure that only
authorized and tested software is deployed. This minimizes risks associated with unauthorized or untested
code. All software deployments must trace back to the DML. Consistent backups are performed on the DML
to protect the master copies of the software. Access to the DML is strictly controlled to prevent unauthorized
modifications.
Think of the DML as a highly secured vault where the blueprint and original materials for every software
application within an organization reside.
Further Information can be found here:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation: ITIL 4 Edition (Official Source - requires purchase of materials for detailed
content)
SearchITOperations - Definitive Media Library (DML)
Question: 96 CertyIQ
Which stage of the service lifecycle has the purpose of looking for ways to improve process efficiency and cost
effectiveness?
A.Service operation
B.Service transition
C.Continual service improvement
D.Service strategy
Answer: C
Explanation:
The correct answer is C, Continual Service Improvement (CSI). CSI is specifically designed to identify and
implement improvements across all aspects of the IT service lifecycle. Its core purpose is to continuously
align IT services with evolving business needs, focusing on enhancing efficiency, effectiveness, and cost-
effectiveness. It achieves this by regularly evaluating services, processes, and practices to identify
opportunities for optimization.
Service operation (A) focuses primarily on day-to-day activities, such as resolving incidents and fulfilling
service requests. It is more concerned with maintaining service stability rather than proactively seeking

improvements, though operational experiences might highlight areas needing improvement for CSI. Service
transition (B) concentrates on the planning and implementation of new or changed services, ensuring they
meet requirements and are successfully deployed. While it considers efficiency during the transition phase,
its main goal isn't continuous improvement across the whole lifecycle. Service strategy (D) defines the overall
approach to managing IT services and their alignment with business goals. It sets the direction, but it doesn't
directly handle the day-to-day improvement activities that are the core function of CSI. CSI uses
methodologies such as Deming Cycle (Plan-Do-Check-Act) to drive improvements systematically. CSI's
activities involve analyzing data, identifying trends, and making recommendations for enhancing the value and
performance of services. The 'Seven-Step Improvement Process' is a key framework within CSI, guiding
organizations through structured improvement initiatives.
Therefore, CSI is uniquely positioned as the lifecycle stage with the specific objective of continually looking
for ways to improve process efficiency and cost-effectiveness, making it the only correct answer.Reference:
AXELOS. ITIL Foundation: ITIL 4 Edition. TSO, 2019.
Official ITIL Website: https://www.axelos.com/
Question: 97 CertyIQ
Which of the following should IT service continuity strategy be based on?
1. Design of the service metrics
2. Business continuity strategy
3. Business impact analysis (BIA)
4. Risk assessment
A.1, 2 and 4 only
B.1, 2 and 3 only
C.2, 3 and 4 only
D.1, 3 and 4 only
Answer: C
Explanation:
The correct answer is C (2, 3, and 4 only) because an IT service continuity strategy is fundamentally about
ensuring business operations can continue, even in the face of disruptions. A Business Continuity Strategy (2)
forms the overarching framework that IT service continuity supports. The Business Impact Analysis (BIA) (3)
identifies critical business functions and their dependencies on IT services, determining the acceptable
downtime and data loss (Recovery Time Objective - RTO and Recovery Point Objective - RPO). A Risk
Assessment (4) identifies potential threats and vulnerabilities that could disrupt IT services and evaluates the
likelihood and impact of those disruptions. These three elements together provide the information needed to
develop a robust and realistic IT service continuity plan.
Service metrics (1) are important for monitoring service performance and effectiveness, but they don't directly
inform the strategy for ensuring continuity. While metrics can help trigger continuity plans when thresholds
are breached, the strategy itself is driven by the business's needs in a disruptive scenario. Therefore, design
of service metrics plays a secondary role to BIA, Risk Assessment, and Business Continuity Strategy. The
strategy relies upon understanding critical business operations and the risks that may threaten them.
Therefore option C, encompassing Business Continuity Strategy, Business Impact Analysis, and Risk
Assessment, aligns perfectly with the objective of IT service continuity in supporting the overall business
resilience.
For further research, consult these resources:
ITIL 4 Foundation Handbook: Provides comprehensive coverage of ITIL 4 principles and practices, including IT

service continuity.
AXELOS Official Website: https://www.axelos.com/ (AXELOS is the owner of ITIL)
NIST Special Publication 800-34: Contingency Planning Guide for Federal Information Systems:
https://csrc.nist.gov/publications/detail/sp/800-34/rev-1/final (While focused on US Federal Systems, it
provides a good overview of IT contingency planning relevant to IT Service Continuity).
Question: 98 CertyIQ
Which practice recommends using tools for collaboration and the automated matching of symptoms?
A.Problem management
B.Service level management
C.Incident management
D.Service request management
Answer: C
Explanation:
The correct answer is Incident Management because it directly addresses the need for rapid resolution of
service disruptions. Incident Management's goal is to restore normal service operation as quickly as possible,
minimizing business impact.
Here's the justification:
Incident Management prioritizes swift resolution and leverages tools to achieve this. Collaboration tools allow
incident responders to communicate effectively, share information, and coordinate efforts in real-time, crucial
for complex incidents. Automated symptom matching uses knowledge bases and AI to quickly identify
potential causes and solutions based on reported symptoms, streamlining the diagnostic process.
Problem Management, while related, focuses on preventing incidents from recurring. Service Level
Management concentrates on defining and managing service performance against agreed-upon targets.
Service Request Management deals with fulfilling routine requests. While collaboration and automation can
be utilized in these practices, they are not as centrally important as they are to Incident Management's
objective of rapid service restoration.
The emphasis on tools for collaboration and automated symptom matching clearly points to Incident
Management as the practice where these capabilities provide the greatest value in reducing downtime and
business impact.Therefore Incident Management practice recommends using tools for collaboration and the
automated matching of symptoms.

ITIL 4 Foundation: ITIL 4 Edition

Question: 99 CertyIQ
What three elements make up the Service Portfolio?
A.Customer portfolio, service catalogue and retired services
B.Customer portfolio, configuration management system and service catalogue

C.Service pipeline, service catalogue and retired services
D.Service pipeline, configuration management system and service catalogue
Answer: C
Explanation:
The correct answer is C: Service pipeline, service catalogue, and retired services. The Service Portfolio is a
complete set of services that are managed by a service provider. It represents the provider's commitments
and investments across all customers and market spaces.
The Service Pipeline contains services that are under development or being considered for future delivery.
These are ideas and proposals not yet offered to customers.
The Service Catalogue contains details of all services currently available to customers. It's the only part of the
Service Portfolio visible to customers and provides information about service offerings, pricing, service level
agreements (SLAs), and how to request the service.
The Retired Services section contains services that are no longer offered to customers. Keeping track of
retired services is essential for managing the service lifecycle and understanding past service offerings.
Options A, B, and D are incorrect because the Customer Portfolio and Configuration Management System are
not directly part of the Service Portfolio. The Customer Portfolio is a different entity representing
relationships with customers, and the Configuration Management System (CMS) supports service
management processes but is not a component of the Service Portfolio. It contains data about configuration
items, but is not the service catalogue. The Service Portfolio manages the entire lifecycle of services, from
idea to retirement.
Further reading on this topic can be found here:
AXELOS official ITIL documentation.
https://www.bmc.com/blogs/itil-service-portfolio-management/ (This is a third party source and should be
used with caution)
Question: 100 CertyIQ
What is used to link activities within the service value chain?
A.Service level agreements
B.Inputs, outputs and triggers
C.Opportunity, demand and value
D.Service desk
Answer: B
Explanation:
The correct answer is B: Inputs, outputs, and triggers. The service value chain in ITIL 4 describes a set of
interconnected activities an organization performs to deliver value. These activities aren't isolated; they're
linked in a chain. Inputs represent resources, information, or other items required by an activity. Outputs are
the results or deliverables produced by an activity. Triggers are events or conditions that initiate an activity.
Without these connections, activities would operate in isolation, hindering value creation.
Service level agreements (SLAs) (Option A) are agreements defining the level of service expected from a
provider, but they don't directly link activities within the chain. Opportunity, demand, and value (Option C)

relate to identifying needs and realizing benefits, not the operational connection between chain activities. The
service desk (Option D) is a function for user support, not a mechanism for linking value chain activities.
The inputs, outputs, and triggers ensure that activities follow a defined flow. For instance, the "Design and
Transition" activity might require inputs from "Plan" (e.g., architectural guidelines) and its output (e.g., a
documented design) might trigger the "Obtain/Build" activity. This flow ensures a coordinated approach. The
whole value chain is designed with the guiding principles in mind. The guiding principles, when applied, allow
for maximum value for all stakeholders. The framework of the service value system supports consistent
governance.
Authoritative links:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Handbook: This provides a detailed explanation of the service value chain and its
components.
Official ITIL 4 documentation: This source offers the definitive description of ITIL 4 concepts.
Question: 101 CertyIQ
Which is a supplier category?
A.Technical
B.Commodity
C.Customer
D.Resource
Answer: B
Explanation:
The correct answer is B. Commodity because in the context of ITIL 4 and service management, suppliers are
often categorized based on the nature and strategic importance of the goods or services they provide. A
'Commodity' supplier falls under this categorization. Let's explore why the other options are incorrect, and
why 'Commodity' is the best fit.
A. Technical is not a recognized supplier category within ITIL. While suppliers may offer technical services or
products, 'Technical' itself isn't a defined category. Technical aspects would influence the classification, but
not be the category itself.
C. Customer refers to the recipient of services, not a supplier. A customer consumes services, whereas a
supplier provides them. This is a fundamental difference in roles.
D. Resource is too broad. While suppliers provide resources, 'Resource' is not a specific supplier category
defined in ITIL. Resources could be hardware, software, personnel, etc., but a supplier category aims for a
more focused classification.
'Commodity' as a supplier category signifies suppliers providing standardized, readily available goods or
services. These items are typically not highly differentiated, and the primary selection factor often revolves
around price and availability. Think of things like generic office supplies, standard cloud storage, or widely
available network bandwidth. The emphasis is less on unique expertise and more on cost-effectiveness and
ease of procurement.
In ITIL 4, managing supplier relationships strategically is crucial for ensuring value co-creation and service
quality. Categorizing suppliers helps organizations tailor their management approach based on the
importance and characteristics of each supplier relationship. Commodity suppliers, for example, might be
managed using standard contracts and automated procurement processes, while strategic suppliers might

require closer collaboration and ongoing performance monitoring.
Therefore, 'Commodity' aligns most closely with the recognized categories for suppliers in ITIL 4, focusing on
the nature of the goods or services provided.https://www.axelos.com/ - Official ITIL
websitehttps://www.bmc.com/blogs/itil-supplier-management/ - Blog article on ITIL and supplier
management.
Question: 102 CertyIQ
Which process is used to compare the value that new services offer with the value of the services they have
replaced?
A.Availability management
B.Capacity management
C.Service portfolio management
D.Service catalogue management
Answer: C
Explanation:
The correct answer is C, Service Portfolio Management. Here's why:
Service Portfolio Management (SPM) is concerned with holistically managing all services across their
lifecycle, including planning, defining, analyzing, and charting the course for future service offerings. A core
function of SPM is strategically evaluating and justifying investments in new or changed services. When a new
service replaces an existing one, SPM actively compares the expected or realized value of the new service
against the value previously provided by the replaced service. This comparison helps organizations determine
if the investment in the new service was beneficial and aligned with strategic goals.
Availability Management focuses on ensuring services meet agreed availability targets. Capacity
Management centers on ensuring sufficient capacity to meet demand. Service Catalogue Management
focuses on providing a single source of information about services offered. While these practices contribute
to overall service value, they don't directly address the comparative analysis of value between replaced and
new services in the same strategic manner as SPM. SPM's key activities include defining, analyzing,
approving, and chartering services, constantly evaluating their contribution to the business. It maintains a
record of investments and justifications. Consequently, only Service Portfolio Management offers the
necessary framework and activities to explicitly compare the value of a new service against the value of its
predecessor.
https://www.axelos.com/ (Official ITIL website)https://www.bmc.com/blogs/itil-service-portfolio-
management/
Question: 103 CertyIQ
Which is an important principle of communication in service operation?
A.Information should always be communicated
B.It has an intended purpose or a resultant action
C.Meetings are always the best method of communication
D.It is stored in the configuration management system

Answer: B
Explanation:
The correct answer is B: It has an intended purpose or a resultant action. Communication in ITIL 4 Service
Operation is not simply about disseminating information (as suggested by option A). Effective communication
must have a clear objective. It should aim to achieve a specific outcome or trigger a particular action from the
recipient. This aligns with the ITIL 4 guiding principle of "Focus on Value." Each communication should
contribute to delivering value, whether it's resolving an incident, informing users about an upcoming change,
or requesting feedback.
Option C is incorrect because meetings aren't always the optimal method. Selecting the appropriate
communication channel is crucial (email, instant messaging, knowledge base articles, etc.), depending on the
urgency, audience, and complexity of the information. Option D is also incorrect; while the Configuration
Management System (CMS) is vital for storing information about IT assets, it's not directly related to the
principle of communication itself. The focus of ITIL 4's communication principle is on why and how we
communicate, not where we store data.
In the context of cloud computing, this principle remains highly relevant. For example, communicating a
service outage to users must have an intended purpose (informing them of the issue and expected resolution
time) and a resultant action (users may adjust their workflows or report further issues). Similarly, informing
development teams about performance bottlenecks detected by cloud monitoring tools should prompt
investigation and remediation actions. The communication must drive action to improve cloud service
reliability and user experience.
Focusing on purpose and resultant action ensures communications are targeted, efficient, and contribute to
the overall value stream within IT service management.
For further reading:
Axelos ITIL 4 Foundation guidance.
https://www.axelos.com/ (Official Axelos website)
Question: 104 CertyIQ
What do customer perceptions and business outcomes help to define?
A.The value of a service
B.Service metrics
C.The total cost of a service
D.Key performance indicators (KPIs)
Answer: A
Explanation:
The correct answer is A: The value of a service. Customer perceptions and business outcomes are the
cornerstones in determining the perceived and actual value derived from a service.
Here's why:
Value in ITIL 4: ITIL 4 places a strong emphasis on value co-creation. Value isn't just about the service itself,
but about the benefits the customer realizes.
Customer Perceptions: These encompass the customer's experience, satisfaction, and perceived usefulness

of the service. A positive perception directly contributes to a higher perceived value. If customers find the
service easy to use, reliable, and helpful in achieving their goals, they will perceive it as valuable.
Business Outcomes: These are the tangible results that the service helps the customer achieve. Did the
service increase revenue, reduce costs, improve efficiency, or mitigate risks? Positive business outcomes are
direct indicators of the service's value to the customer's organization.
Relationship: Customer perception and business outcomes are related. A service delivering positive business
outcomes typically leads to favorable customer perceptions. Conversely, a service with poor customer
perceptions is less likely to contribute to desired business outcomes.
Other Options:
Service metrics: While important, service metrics (like uptime and response time) are indicators of how well
the service is performing, but they don't directly define the value itself.
Total cost of a service: Cost is a factor in value, but value is about the benefit relative to the cost. A high-cost
service can still be valuable if the benefits outweigh the expense.
Key performance indicators (KPIs): KPIs measure progress toward goals, but the goals themselves, and
whether they align with business outcomes and customer perceptions, define value. KPIs often support the
assessment of outcomes but aren't the primary definers of value.
In summary, the value of a service is intrinsically linked to how customers perceive it and the business results
it enables. By considering both, service providers can better understand and enhance the value they deliver.

specific page requires registration)
ITIL Foundation Handbook: (Consult the official handbook for detailed explanations of ITIL 4 concepts. This is
usually acquired through training providers.)
Question: 105 CertyIQ
What is defined as a change of state that has significance for the management of an IT service?
A.Event
B.Incident
C.Problem
D.Known error
Answer: A
Explanation:
The correct answer, an Event, is defined as a change of state that holds significance for IT service
management. This significance arises from the need to monitor, manage, and potentially react to the event to
maintain service health and performance.
Events in ITIL 4 encompass a wide spectrum, from simple informational messages to warnings and
exceptions. Informational events might track successful log-ins or routine backups, while warnings could flag
potential resource bottlenecks in a cloud environment, such as nearing storage capacity limits or exceeding
CPU utilization thresholds. Exceptions represent abnormal states, like application errors or server crashes.
The importance of defining an event lies in its role as a trigger for action. For example, a warning event
indicating high CPU usage on a virtual machine might prompt automated scaling measures in a cloud

environment, adding more compute resources to handle the load. Similarly, an exception event signaling a
database error could initiate an automated failover to a standby database server.
Events are the building blocks of proactive monitoring and management. Through effective event
management, organizations can detect and address potential issues before they impact users, leading to
increased service availability and reliability, particularly crucial in cloud-based service delivery.
Incidents, problems, and known errors are related but distinct concepts. An Incident is an unplanned
interruption to or reduction in the quality of an IT service. A Problem is the cause of one or more incidents. A
Known Error is a problem that has been analyzed but not yet resolved. While these are crucial for service
management, they stem from or contribute to events.
The ITIL 4 framework emphasizes the value of proactive service management. This requires establishing
robust event management capabilities to identify, analyze, and respond to changes in state before they
escalate into major incidents. Event management enables teams to react swiftly and effectively to changes in
the IT environment, ensuring service stability and user satisfaction. Consequently, the ITIL 4 Foundation
definition specifically points to an "Event" as the fundamental element representing a significant state
change in IT service management.
Authoritative links for further research:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Official Website: https://www.axelos.com/ (You'll need to navigate to the ITIL 4 section)
ITIL Foundation Handbook: (Available for purchase, provides detailed explanations of ITIL 4 concepts)
Question: 106 CertyIQ
What takes place in the `Did we get there?` step of the continual service improvement (CSI) approach?
A.An initial baseline assessment
B.The production of a detailed CSI plan
C.Verifying that improvement targets have been achieved
D.Understanding priorities for improvement
Answer: C
Explanation:
The "Did we get there?" step in the ITIL 4 Continual Service Improvement (CSI) approach focuses on
evaluating the success of implemented improvement initiatives against predefined targets and metrics. This
stage involves verifying whether the intended outcomes have been achieved and quantifying the actual
impact of the changes. Essentially, it's about confirming whether the "current state" after the improvement
matches the desired "future state" established during the earlier stages of the CSI model.
Option A, an initial baseline assessment, occurs much earlier, typically during the "What is the vision?" or
"Where are we now?" steps, to establish a starting point for measuring improvement. Option B, producing a
detailed CSI plan, happens in the "How do we get there?" step, outlining the roadmap for achieving the
desired state. Option D, understanding priorities for improvement, is addressed in the "What is the vision?" and
"Where do we want to be?" stages, where goals are defined and gaps identified. Therefore, only option C
directly reflects the purpose of the "Did we get there?" stage, which is the final verification of achieved
targets. This verification allows organizations to demonstrate the value of CSI efforts, identify any remaining
gaps, and inform future improvement initiatives, thereby completing the feedback
loop.https://www.axelos.com/https://www.bmc.com/blogs/itil-4-continuous-improvement/

Question: 107 CertyIQ
What is the PRIMARY use of a change schedule?
A.To support the 'incident management' practice and improvement planning
B.To manage emergency changes
C.To plan changes and help avoid conflicts
D.To manage standard changes
Answer: C
Explanation:
The correct answer is C, "To plan changes and help avoid conflicts." Here's a detailed justification:
The primary purpose of a change schedule within the ITIL 4 framework is to provide a holistic view of planned
changes, including their timelines and dependencies. This visibility is crucial for proactive planning and
minimizing disruptions. By centralizing information about upcoming changes, the change schedule allows
stakeholders to identify potential conflicts and overlaps early in the process. For example, if two teams are
planning changes that affect the same critical service, the change schedule highlights this conflict, allowing
for adjustments to be made to avoid outages or performance degradation.
Option A, "To support the 'incident management' practice and improvement planning," is related but not the
primary use. While the change schedule can inform incident management by providing context on recent
changes that might have triggered incidents, its main focus is not incident support. Improvement planning
could utilize data from the change schedule (e.g., change success rates, conflict frequency) but the schedule
itself does not directly drive the improvement planning.
Option B, "To manage emergency changes," is incorrect. Emergency changes, by their nature, require
immediate action and often bypass the standard change schedule process due to the urgency of the situation.
While emergency changes are documented, the schedule is not designed for managing them; it is used for
planned changes. Emergency changes will eventually be recorded, but they are not managed via the normal
scheduling process.
Option D, "To manage standard changes," is also incorrect. Standard changes are pre-approved, low-risk, and
well-understood changes with established procedures. While standard changes are recorded in the schedule,
the schedule isn't for managing them; the process for executing standard changes is established elsewhere
(e.g., in a playbook). The schedule provides visibility but does not actively manage the standard changes that
are pre-approved.
In summary, the change schedule facilitates proactive planning, conflict avoidance, and improved
communication around planned changes, making it a central tool for effective change management. It offers a
consolidated view of planned changes, their timing, and dependencies, thereby enabling better coordination
and reducing the risk of disruptions.
Authoritative Links:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Handbook: This is the official source for ITIL 4 guidance.
ITIL 4 Change Enablement Practice Guide: While not freely available without a subscription, this guide
provides detailed information on change management practices, including the role of the change schedule.
You may be able to find summaries of the change enablement practice from reputable sources, like:
https://www.bmc.com/blogs/itil-change-management/
https://www.atlassian.com/itsm/change-management

Question: 108 CertyIQ
What is the CORRECT definition of service management?
A.A set of specialized assets for transitioning services into the live operational environment
B.A set of specialized organizational capabilities for delivering value to customers in the form of services
C.The capability of supplier to deliver services to providers in exchange for money
D.The capability of service providers to minimize their costs without reducing the value of the services
Answer: B
Explanation:
The correct definition of service management is B. A set of specialized organizational capabilities for
delivering value to customers in the form of services.
Here's why: Service management, within the ITIL 4 framework, emphasizes creating value. It's not simply
about technology; it's about how an organization utilizes its skills, processes, and resources (capabilities) to
provide services that meet customer needs and deliver tangible benefits. Option A describes something
related to transitioning or deployment, not the overall management of services. Option C describes a supplier-
provider relationship, a facet of service management, but not its core definition. Option D focuses on cost
reduction, which is a consideration within service management, but not the defining principle. ITIL 4 focuses
on value co-creation, meaning service providers and consumers collaborate to define and achieve value.
In essence, service management is the application of these organizational capabilities to plan, deliver, and
improve services. It includes understanding customer needs, designing appropriate services, and effectively
managing resources to ensure services meet defined quality standards. This leads to enhanced customer
satisfaction, improved business outcomes, and a stronger competitive advantage. The value delivered is the
driving force and the ultimate measure of success.

provides a good overview)
Question: 109 CertyIQ
Which is the correct combination of items that makes up an IT service?
A.Customers, providers and documents
B.Information technology, people and processes
C.Information technology, networks and people
D.People, processes and customers
Answer: B
Explanation:
The correct answer is B: Information technology, people, and processes. An IT service is not simply
technology, but a combination of components working together to deliver value.
Information Technology (IT) forms the technical backbone. This includes the hardware, software,
infrastructure, and network components used to deliver the service. Without the underlying technology, there
would be no service to offer. Think of servers, applications, databases, and network devices – all working

together to provide a functioning service.
People are crucial because they design, build, run, and maintain the IT service. This includes IT staff, support
personnel, service desk agents, and even end-users who interact with the service. The human element
ensures the service is correctly managed, operated, and improved over time.
Processes define how the IT service is delivered and managed. This includes documented procedures,
workflows, and activities that ensure the service is consistent, repeatable, and reliable. Processes can cover
incident management, change management, problem management, and service request fulfillment.
Customers are not a part of the service itself, but the beneficiaries of the service. Documents, while important,
are supporting materials and not the primary components. Networks are part of the technology infrastructure.
Therefore, the synergistic combination of IT infrastructure, skilled people managing the service, and well-
defined processes working in harmony are essential to create a successful IT service, providing value and
outcomes desired by the customer.

Official ITIL 4 Foundation publications.
Question: 110 CertyIQ
Which problem management activity ensures that a problem can be easily tracked and management information
can be obtained?
A.Categorization
B.Detection
C.Prioritization
D.Escalation
Answer: A
Explanation:
The correct answer is A. Categorization. Here's why:
Categorization in problem management involves assigning specific labels or classifications to problems. This
process is crucial for several reasons that directly support tracking and information retrieval. A well-defined
categorization schema allows for consistent reporting and analysis of problems. For example, problems
related to a specific application, server, or type of failure can be easily grouped together. This aggregation
facilitates trend analysis, identifying recurring issues, and enabling proactive problem resolution.
Without proper categorization, problem records become difficult to search, filter, and analyze effectively. You
would struggle to determine the root cause of common issues or identify areas where preventative measures
are needed. Standardized categories facilitate the creation of reports and dashboards that provide valuable
management information about problem trends, impact, and resolution effectiveness. The chosen categories
act as metadata, enhancing the discoverability of problem records within the problem management system.
Detection (B) focuses on identifying that a problem exists. Prioritization (C) determines the order in which
problems are addressed based on their impact and urgency. Escalation (D) is the process of transferring a
problem to a higher level of support or management. While these activities are important in problem
management, none of them directly ensure easy tracking and retrieval of management information like
categorization does. Categorization provides the framework for organizing and analyzing problem data.

In essence, effective categorization transforms raw problem data into actionable insights, directly supporting
informed decision-making and continuous service improvement within an IT environment. The systematic
classification made possible by categorization is what allows for tracking, trending, and extracting valuable
management data.
Question: 111 CertyIQ
What can be used to help determine the impact level of a problem?
A.Definitive media library (DML)
B.Configuration management system (CMS)
C.Statement of requirements (SOR)
D.Standard operating procedures (SOP)
Answer: B
Explanation:
The correct answer is B, Configuration Management System (CMS). Here's why:
A Configuration Management System (CMS) holds vital information about the components of an IT
environment, called configuration items (CIs), and their relationships. When assessing the impact of a
problem, understanding which CIs are affected and how they interconnect is crucial.
A problem affecting a critical server, for example, has a high impact. The CMS reveals this criticality by
showing the server's role in delivering essential services and its dependencies on other CIs. A problem
affecting a less critical workstation might have a lower impact. The CMS allows the service desk to quickly
identify the users impacted.
Using the CMS, incident and problem management teams can understand the scope of the disruption. Is it a
widespread issue affecting many users and services, or is it isolated? This information allows for appropriate
prioritization and resource allocation.
A definitive media library (DML) stores the master copies of software, and while important for recovery,
doesn't directly help assess impact. A statement of requirements (SOR) outlines project needs, and standard
operating procedures (SOPs) document routine tasks; neither provides the real-time relationship and
dependency information held within a CMS. Therefore, only the CMS provides the context needed to
accurately determine a problem's impact level.
The CMS provides the holistic view necessary for understanding cascading failures or identifying single points
of failure exposed by the problem. By mapping relationships between services, applications, and
infrastructure, the CMS helps categorize the severity based on service level agreements (SLAs) and business
priorities. This enables the service desk to prioritize incidents and problems effectively, minimizing downtime
and business disruption. It further helps in identifying the upstream and downstream impacts of the problem.
For further research, consult the official ITIL 4 Foundation publications and online resources:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Handbook
https://www.axelos.com/
Question: 112 CertyIQ
Which are phases of the release and deployment process?

1. Release build and test
2. Review and close
3. Categorize and record
4. Change authorization and schedule
A.1 and 2
B.1 and 3
C.2 and 4
D.3 and 4
Answer: A
Explanation:
The correct answer is A (1 and 2: Release build and test, Review and close).
Here's why: The release and deployment process in ITIL 4 focuses on moving new or changed services,
components, or applications into the live environment. Key activities directly related to this process include
building and testing the release to ensure it meets requirements and doesn't negatively impact the production
environment. After deployment, a review and close process is essential to evaluate the success of the
deployment, identify any lessons learned, and formally close out the release. This involves assessing whether
the release achieved its objectives and documenting any issues encountered.
Categorizing and recording (3) is typically part of incident, problem, or change management, not directly
related to release and deployment steps. Change authorization and schedule (4) is part of change
management, which provides the overall framework and governance for changes, including releases, but isn't
a phase within the release and deployment process itself. While change management approves and schedules
releases, the release and deployment process executes the actual steps to move the release into production.
Therefore, only release build and test, and review and close, accurately reflect phases within the release and
deployment process.
For further research on ITIL 4 release management, refer to the official AXELOS ITIL 4 publications and
related training materials. While no single URL provides a complete breakdown due to the proprietary nature
of the content, searching "ITIL 4 release management" on reputable IT service management websites will
yield valuable insights.
Question: 113 CertyIQ
Which function is responsible for the management of a data centre?
A.Technical management
B.Service desk
C.Application management
D.Facilities management
Answer: D
Explanation:
Facilities management is the correct function responsible for the management of a data centre. Data centres
are physical locations requiring specific infrastructure and environmental controls to operate effectively and
reliably.
Technical management focuses on managing and maintaining the IT infrastructure components (servers,

networks, storage) within the data centre, but doesn't handle the physical environment. Application
management concentrates on the lifecycle of applications running on the infrastructure. The service desk is a
function to support users and resolving incidents, and while a service desk may handle issues related to the
data centre, it is not responsible for the physical infrastructure and its management.
Facilities management, however, is specifically concerned with the physical aspects of a data centre,
including the building, power, cooling, security, and other environmental controls. This encompasses tasks
such as:
Ensuring reliable power supply (generators, UPS systems).
Maintaining optimal temperature and humidity levels (HVAC systems).
Managing physical security (access control, surveillance).
Handling fire suppression and prevention systems.
Overseeing the physical layout and organization of the data centre.
Waste management and disposal
Data centre management is inherently multi-faceted, so facilities management collaborates with technical
management to ensure the physical environment supports the IT equipment's operational needs. A failure in
facilities management, such as a power outage or overheating, can lead to significant IT disruptions and
service unavailability. Therefore, a well-defined facilities management function is crucial for data centre
availability and resilience. Its primary goal is to maintain an environment conducive to reliable and efficient IT
operations.Therefore, the correct answer is D.
Further Reading:
Data Center Infrastructure Management (DCIM): https://www.gartner.com/en/information-
technology/glossary/data-center-infrastructure-management-dcim
Uptime Institute Tier Standard: Topology: https://uptimeinstitute.com/solutions/tier-standard
Question: 114 CertyIQ
Which helps to manage an incident when it is unclear which support team should be working on the incident?
A.Disaster recovery plans
B.Swarming
C.Target resolution times
D.Self-help
Answer: B
Explanation:
The correct answer is B, Swarming. Here's why:
When an incident arises and it's uncertain which support team possesses the specific expertise needed for
resolution, traditional hierarchical escalation methods can be slow and inefficient. Swarming offers a dynamic
and collaborative alternative. It involves bringing together individuals from different teams who collectively
possess the required knowledge to address the incident.
Instead of sequentially escalating the incident through various levels of support, potentially delaying
resolution, swarming promotes simultaneous involvement. Experts from various domains (e.g., networking,
database, application) collaborate directly to diagnose the root cause and implement a solution. This
coordinated effort helps avoid delays caused by misrouting the incident to the wrong team initially.
Disaster recovery plans (A) focus on restoring services after a major disruption, not on routing individual

incidents. Target resolution times (C) set expectations for incident resolution speed but don't help in
determining which team should handle an incident initially. Self-help (D) empowers users to resolve common
issues independently but doesn't address situations requiring specialized support from various teams.
Swarming leverages the collective intelligence of the organization, improving incident resolution efficiency
and reducing downtime. Its agile approach is particularly effective in complex environments where incidents
often span multiple domains or technologies.
In essence, swarming is a collaborative approach specifically designed to handle incidents where initial team
assignment is unclear, providing a faster and more effective resolution compared to other options. It fosters
teamwork and ensures the appropriate expertise is applied promptly.
For further research:
Axelos ITIL 4 Foundation Syllabus: (https://www.axelos.com/) - Look for information on incident management
and collaborative practices. (Note: This is a general link to the Axelos website. You might need to search
within the site for the specific syllabus.)
ITIL 4 Foundation Handbook: Many publications cover the ITIL 4 Foundation material and explain swarming in
the context of incident management. Search for "ITIL 4 Foundation Handbook Swarming" on your preferred
search engine.
Question: 115 CertyIQ
Which processes are responsible for the regular review of underpinning contracts?
A.Supplier management and service level management
B.Supplier management and change management
C.Availability management and service level management
D.Supplier management and availability management
Answer: A
Explanation:
The correct answer is A: Supplier management and service level management. Here's why:
Supplier Management: This practice is specifically responsible for managing relationships with suppliers who
provide goods and services necessary for delivering IT services. A key aspect of this management involves the
regular review of underpinning contracts (UCs). These contracts define the terms and conditions under which
suppliers provide their services. Supplier management ensures that these contracts are still relevant, cost-
effective, and meet the organization's evolving needs. This includes reviewing performance, compliance, and
potential improvements.
Service Level Management (SLM): SLM ensures that IT services are delivered according to agreed-upon
service levels. These service levels are often documented in Service Level Agreements (SLAs). SLM is
intricately linked to supplier management because the ability of IT to meet its SLAs often depends on the
performance of its suppliers as defined within the UCs. Therefore, SLM has a vested interest in the regular
review of UCs to ensure that suppliers can continue to support the agreed service levels. SLM needs to be
involved to align the needs of the customers of IT services with the services IT procures from its suppliers.
Change management, availability management, while relevant to the overall quality of service, do not have the
specific remit for the contractual obligations and performance metrics within the underpinning contracts.
Why not other options?

Change Management focuses on controlling changes to the IT environment. While changes might impact
supplier performance, it isn't directly responsible for reviewing supplier contracts.
Availability Management focuses on ensuring that IT services are available as agreed. While supplier
performance affects availability, availability management doesn't directly manage or review the contracts
themselves.
In summary: Supplier management owns the supplier relationship and associated contracts (UCs). Service
level management relies on supplier performance to meet agreed service levels (SLAs) and therefore, is
critically interested in UC reviews. Both practices collaborating ensures that supplier services support
business needs and are delivered according to agreed terms.
Authoritative Links for Further Research:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Syllabus: The official ITIL 4 Foundation syllabus provides detailed information on
all ITIL practices, including supplier management and service level management. Look for these specific
practice descriptions.
ITIL 4 Practice Guides: AXELOS also publishes more detailed practice guides for each ITIL 4 practice. These
guides provide in-depth information on the activities, roles, and responsibilities within each practice.
Question: 116 CertyIQ
Which statement BEST describes the value of service strategy to the business?
A.It allows higher volumes of successful change
B.It reduces unplanned costs through optimized handling of service outages
C.It reduces the duration and frequency of service outages
D.It enables the service provider to understand what levels of service will make their customers successful
Answer: D
Explanation:
The best answer is D: "It enables the service provider to understand what levels of service will make their
customers successful." Here's why:
Service strategy, within the ITIL 4 framework, is about defining the perspective, position, plans, and patterns
that a service provider needs to execute its business strategy and meet customer outcomes. It's the
foundation upon which all other service management activities are built. It focuses on understanding
customer needs and translating those needs into service offerings that deliver value. This understanding is
key to ensuring customer success because a successful service strategy ensures that the service provider
aligns its resources and capabilities to provide services that directly contribute to the customer's desired
business outcomes.
Option A, focusing on higher volumes of successful change, is more closely related to service design and
transition, not the overarching strategic view. While important, it doesn't represent the fundamental value of
service strategy.
Option B, reducing unplanned costs through optimized handling of service outages, pertains more to service
operation. Service strategy can inform efficient incident management, but its primary goal isn't direct cost
reduction through outage handling.
Option C, reducing the duration and frequency of service outages, is also related to service operation and
continual service improvement. Again, strategy provides the context, but it's not the direct driver of outage

reduction.
Service strategy is about market analysis, understanding the customer's business goals, identifying
competitive advantages, and defining a service portfolio that aligns with those objectives. It is a customer-
centric view of service delivery and includes the overall strategic approach to service management. By
focusing on the factors which lead to customer success, other factors such as outages and change success
are inherently improved as a result of a well-defined strategy.
In essence, a strong service strategy enables the provider to answer fundamental questions like: "What
services should we offer?", "Who are our customers?", "What is our value proposition?", and "How can we
differentiate ourselves?". Answering these questions correctly leads to the service provider understanding
what outcomes customers want to achieve and what levels of service are required for customer success.
For further information, refer to the official ITIL 4 Foundation syllabus and publications. Also, explore
resources like:
AXELOS: https://www.axelos.com/ (the official ITIL governing body)
Official ITIL 4 Foundation publications.
Question: 117 CertyIQ
What is a definition of a service improvement plan (SIP)?
A.A formal plan to implement improvements to a customer's business processes
B.An input from availability management to service level management, detailing the service design plan
C.A formal plan to implement improvements to a service or process
D.An input from financial management for IT services to service level management, detailing the budget plan
Answer: C
Explanation:
The correct answer is C. A formal plan to implement improvements to a service or process.
A Service Improvement Plan (SIP), within the ITIL 4 framework, is a structured and documented approach to
enhancing services, processes, or any element contributing to service value. Its core purpose is to identify
areas of weakness or opportunity and create a roadmap for achieving tangible and measurable improvements.
SIPs are proactive, aiming to prevent issues and continuously optimize service delivery.
Options A, B, and D are incorrect because they either narrowly focus on customer business processes (A), are
linked to specific management disciplines and their interactions (B & D), or financial considerations which
while impacting SIP implementation, do not define what a SIP fundamentally is. A SIP can target any aspect of
service management including processes, skills, tools and technologies.
A good SIP will define the current state, the desired future state, the steps required to get there, the
resources needed, the timelines, and the metrics for success. These elements are crucial for tracking
progress and ensuring that the improvement efforts are aligned with the overall organizational goals.
Further Reading:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Book: This provides a comprehensive overview of ITIL 4 concepts, including
Service Improvement.
https://www.axelos.com/ (AXELOS, the official ITIL body) provides resources and information on best
practices. While specific SIP examples might vary, understanding that ITIL promotes continuous improvement
allows for a broad application of the concept within your organization.

Question: 118 CertyIQ
Which statement about the known error database (KEDB) is CORRECT?
A.It is maintained by the service desk and updated with the details of each new incident
B.It is a part of the configuration management database (CMDB) and contains workarounds
C.It is maintained by problem management and is used by the service desk to help resolve incidents
D.It is maintained by incident management and contains solutions to be implemented by problem management
Answer: C
Explanation:
The correct answer is C because the Known Error Database (KEDB) is primarily maintained by the problem
management practice. Problem management is responsible for identifying the root causes of incidents and
developing workarounds or permanent solutions. These workarounds and solutions, along with the associated
known errors (problems that have a documented root cause and a workaround), are documented in the KEDB.
The service desk uses the KEDB as a valuable resource to quickly resolve incidents by applying the known
workarounds. This reduces resolution times and improves user satisfaction. By having access to the KEDB, the
service desk can bypass lengthy troubleshooting processes for recurring issues.
Option A is incorrect because while the service desk uses the KEDB, they do not maintain it. The service desk
documents incidents, but the information that populates the KEDB comes from problem management's
investigation of the root cause.
Option B is incorrect because the KEDB is related to the CMDB but isn't a direct part of it. The CMDB stores
configuration items (CIs) and their relationships, while the KEDB stores information about known errors and
their associated workarounds. While a known error might relate to a CI in the CMDB, the KEDB itself is a
distinct database.
Option D is incorrect because incident management focuses on restoring service quickly. While incident
management might identify the need for a problem investigation that ultimately populates the KEDB, they
don't maintain the KEDB itself, nor do they provide solutions for problem management to implement. Problem
Management provides the Solutions.
In summary, the KEDB is a critical tool for efficient incident resolution, and its upkeep is primarily the
responsibility of the problem management practice.
Reference link for further reading on ITIL 4:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation guidance (official source, behind paywall): https://www.axelos.com/
General information on ITIL 4: https://www.bmc.com/blogs/itil-4-overview/
Question: 119 CertyIQ
What is a service?
A.A possible event that could cause harm or loss, or make it more difficult to achieve objectives
B.A means of enabling value co-creation by facilitating outcomes that customers want to achieve, without the
customer having to manage specific costs and risks
C.A tangible or intangible deliverable of an activity
D.Joint activities performed by a service provider and a service consumer to ensure continual value co-creation

based on agreed and available service offerings
Answer: B
Explanation:
The correct answer is B. The ITIL 4 definition of a service centers on value co-creation. It emphasizes that
services exist to help customers achieve desired outcomes without the burden of managing the underlying
complexities, costs, and risks. This aligns with the core principle of ITIL 4, which focuses on delivering value
through service management practices.
Option A describes a risk, a common term in IT service management but not the definition of a service. Risks
are factors that can hinder value creation or service delivery.
Option C, describing "a tangible or intangible deliverable of an activity," better aligns with the definition of an
output. While services generate outputs, the service itself is more than just a deliverable; it's the mechanism
for facilitating outcomes.
Option D describes service relationships, which are the cooperative interactions between service providers
and consumers. While important for value co-creation, it's not the definition of the service itself. The service is
the means through which that relationship delivers value by enabling desired outcomes.
The value co-creation aspect of the ITIL 4 definition highlights the importance of collaboration and mutual
understanding between the provider and the consumer. The customer benefits because they achieve their
desired outcomes without being overly concerned with the underlying infrastructure, processes, or personnel.
The provider benefits through establishing a solid relationship, continual service improvement, and enabling a
better-fulfilled customer. ITIL 4 emphasizes a holistic approach to service management, recognizing that
value is created through the interplay of various components, including service offerings, resources, and
capabilities.
For more information, consult the official ITIL 4 Foundation guidance and the AXELOS website:
AXELOS Official Website: https://www.axelos.com/ (search for ITIL 4 Foundation guidance)
Question: 120 CertyIQ
What should a release policy include?
A.The process owner and process manager for each type of release
B.The roles and responsibilities for incident and problem resolution
C.The naming convention and expected frequency of each type of release
D.The naming convention for all configuration items (CI) recorded in the configuration management system
(CMS)
Answer: C
Explanation:
The correct answer is C. The naming convention and expected frequency of each type of release.
A release policy should primarily define the practical aspects of how releases are handled within an
organization. Naming conventions ensure consistency and ease of identification for different releases.
Knowing the expected frequency of each release type (e.g., major, minor, emergency) allows teams to plan
resources, manage expectations, and align with business needs.
Option A is incorrect because process owners and managers are more closely associated with process

documentation rather than the specifics of release handling. Incident and problem resolution (Option B) is
related to service management more broadly but not exclusively about releases; they are parts of the broader
service restoration process following a potentially problematic release. Option D is related to configuration
management, not release management. While a release policy might reference the CMS, it does not primarily
focus on the naming conventions for all CIs. The core purpose of a release policy is to govern the planned
introduction of changes into live environments.
In the context of ITIL 4, the focus is on value co-creation and adaptability. Consistent naming conventions and
understanding release frequencies directly enable efficient delivery and minimize disruption, contributing to
value for the customer.Authoritative links:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation guidance (official ITIL documentation - paywalled)
Although a direct, free URL is not available to a detailed ITIL 4 Foundation text, searching for "ITIL 4 Release
Management" online will provide numerous secondary sources reinforcing this explanation.
Question: 121 CertyIQ
Which guiding principle is PRIMARILY concerned with end-to-end service delivery?
A.Focus on value
B.Think and work holistically
C.Optimize and automate
D.Collaborate and promote
Answer: B
Explanation:
The correct answer is B. Think and work holistically. This principle emphasizes understanding how all parts of
an organization work together in an integrated way, including IT and business processes.
Here's the detailed justification:
Holistic Thinking and Service Delivery: Thinking and working holistically involves understanding how the
different elements of an organization, its processes, and its partners interact to deliver value. This is crucial
for end-to-end service delivery because it ensures that all aspects, from initial customer request to final
delivery and support, are considered.
End-to-End Perspective: This principle necessitates a complete view of the service value stream, including
how different teams, departments, and even external providers contribute to the delivery of a service. It goes
beyond individual tasks and considers the entire process.
Identifying Interdependencies: By thinking holistically, organizations can identify interdependencies between
different processes and systems. This awareness helps in managing potential bottlenecks and ensuring
smooth service delivery.
Focus on Value (A): While focusing on value is essential, it does not directly ensure comprehensive end-to-
end integration. Focusing on value primarily ensures that every action contributes to customer and business
value.
Optimize and Automate (C): Optimization and automation are important for efficiency, but they don't
inherently guarantee a holistic view of service delivery. They improve specific processes within the service
value stream but don't necessarily ensure all parts work together seamlessly.
Collaborate and Promote (D): Collaboration is important for service management, it is mainly used in breaking

down silos between departments and teams.
The Big Picture: In essence, "Think and work holistically" ensures that the big picture is always in view. It
fosters a shared understanding of how everything fits together and contributes to the delivery of valuable
services. This is particularly important in cloud environments where services often rely on a complex mix of
internal and external components.
ITIL 4 Guidance: ITIL 4 emphasizes that a service is not just a collection of components, but an integrated
system that delivers value. Holistic thinking is essential for designing and managing such systems effectively.
Preventing Silos: This principle helps to prevent the formation of silos within an organization, ensuring that
teams work together towards common goals. This is especially important in cloud environments where
different teams may be responsible for different aspects of the infrastructure.
Understanding Dependencies: It promotes a deep understanding of the dependencies between different
services and systems, allowing organizations to proactively address potential issues and ensure service
availability.
Authoritative Links for Further Research:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Syllabus: https://www.axelos.com/ (Refer to the section on Guiding Principles)
Official ITIL 4 Publications: Available through various sources, these provide detailed explanations of each
principle.
Therefore, "Think and work holistically" is the guiding principle that is PRIMARILY concerned with end-to-end
service delivery because it ensures a comprehensive and integrated approach to delivering value.
Question: 122 CertyIQ
Which practice establishes a channel between the service provider and its users?
A.Relationship management
B.Change enablement
C.Supplier management
D.Service desk
Answer: D
Explanation:
The correct answer is D: Service desk. Here's why:
The service desk practice is specifically designed to be the single point of contact between the service
provider and its users. It acts as a central communication hub, handling incidents, service requests, and
providing information. A key function is incident management, helping restore normal service operation as
quickly as possible after a disruption. They log all issues and requests into the IT service management (ITSM)
system.
Relationship management, while important for maintaining positive long-term connections with stakeholders,
doesn't primarily function as the immediate channel for daily interactions and issue resolution. Change
enablement focuses on managing changes in a controlled manner to minimize disruptions, but it's not the
primary channel for user communication. Supplier management deals with external vendors and suppliers, not
direct user interaction. The service desk is often the first point of contact for users experiencing issues,
requesting services, or seeking information. This allows for quick resolution and an improved user experience.
The efficient handling of communications strengthens the confidence users have in the service provider.

Therefore, the service desk directly establishes and manages the communication channel required.
https://www.axelos.com/ (Official ITIL source)
https://www.bmc.com/blogs/itil-service-desk/
Question: 123 CertyIQ
Which practice includes the use of approaches such as Lean, Agile and DevOps with the aim of facilitating a
greater amount of change at a quicker rate?
A.Service desk
B.Monitoring and event management
C.Service level management
D.Continual improvement
Answer: D
Explanation:
The correct answer is D, Continual Improvement. Here's a detailed justification:
Continual improvement focuses on the ongoing enhancement of products, services, and practices. The explicit
aim is to increase efficiency, effectiveness, and overall value. Crucially, it's directly linked to adopting
methodologies like Lean, Agile, and DevOps.
Lean principles prioritize eliminating waste and streamlining processes, accelerating change implementation.
Agile emphasizes iterative development, rapid feedback loops, and collaboration, fostering a quicker pace of
change. DevOps bridges the gap between development and operations, enabling faster and more reliable
deployments, thus greatly enhancing the rate of change.
Service Desk (A) provides a single point of contact for users, focusing on incident and service request
management. While important, it doesn't directly facilitate large-scale, rapid change initiatives like Continual
Improvement.
Monitoring and Event Management (B) focuses on observing systems and identifying anomalies. It provides
data that can inform improvement efforts, but it isn't inherently geared towards actively implementing
changes.
Service Level Management (C) focuses on defining and maintaining agreed-upon service levels. It sets the
standards that improvement efforts strive to meet, but does not drive the actual implementation of change at
an accelerated rate.
Continual Improvement provides the framework and mindset for incorporating Lean, Agile, and DevOps
practices to accelerate the pace of change across the IT environment. Its core purpose is to identify and
implement improvements, leveraging these methodologies for faster and more effective outcomes. The other
options are supportive practices but don't inherently drive the overall rate of change.
Supporting Links:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation: (Check the official AXELOS website for the latest ITIL 4 Foundation materials.)
Atlassian - DevOps Tutorial: https://www.atlassian.com/devops
Lean Enterprise Institute: https://www.lean.org/

Question: 124 CertyIQ
Which practice has a purpose that includes maximizing success by ensuring that risks have been properly
assessed?
A.Relationship management
B.Change enablement
C.Release management
D.Monitoring and event management
Answer: B
Explanation:
The correct answer is B, Change Enablement. Change Enablement's core purpose is to maximize the number
of successful IT changes by ensuring that risks have been properly assessed and managed. This practice
focuses on managing changes effectively to support the rapid delivery of services while minimizing negative
impacts. A critical aspect of Change Enablement is risk assessment, which involves identifying, analyzing, and
evaluating potential risks associated with each change. This proactive approach helps to avoid incidents,
minimize disruptions, and ensure the stability and reliability of services. Change enablement involves a
process of evaluating, prioritizing, and scheduling changes. A thorough review of each change proposal
includes assessing the potential impact, the likelihood of success, and identifying any rollback plans. This
enables informed decision-making about whether to proceed with a change and how to mitigate any risks that
may arise.
Relationship Management focuses on maintaining positive relationships with stakeholders, but its primary
goal isn't specifically risk assessment within the context of changes. Release Management is concerned with
the planning, scheduling, and controlling of the build, test, and deployment of releases, but it doesn't have the
risk assessment focus of Change Enablement at the individual change level. Monitoring and Event
Management focuses on observing services and components and reacting to events. While it can help detect
issues arising from a change, it does not proactively assess risks before the change is implemented. Change
Enablement directly addresses the assessment of risks associated with changes to IT services, making it the
best answer.
For further research:
ITIL 4 Foundation: Change Enablement: Explore the official ITIL 4 framework documents or training
materials.
AXELOS Official Website: https://www.axelos.com/ Look for resources on Change Enablement within the ITIL
4 framework. While specific pages may change, the general website provides resources.
Question: 125 CertyIQ
Which practice provides users with a way to get various requests arranged, explained and coordinated?
A.Service level management
B.Relationship management
C.Continual improvement
D.Service desk
Answer: D
Explanation:

The correct answer is D, Service Desk. The Service Desk practice is designed to be the single point of contact
between the service provider and all users. Its core function is to handle incidents, service requests, and
provide information to users. Specifically relating to the question, the Service Desk handles requests, ensures
they are properly arranged (prioritized), explained to the user (regarding status or further needed
information), and coordinated between different teams if needed for fulfillment.
The Service Desk acts as a communication hub, facilitating efficient and effective interaction between users
and the IT organization. This practice focuses on understanding user needs and ensuring that these needs are
met through appropriate service delivery. It ensures users are informed about their requests from start to
finish.
Service Level Management (SLM) focuses on defining, agreeing upon, and monitoring service levels, not on
handling individual user requests in the way the question describes. Relationship Management focuses on
building and maintaining relationships with stakeholders, not on the day-to-day handling of user requests.
Continual Improvement is a guiding principle and practice aimed at improving processes and services over
time, but not on handling specific user requests, arrangement, explanation and coordination, and related
communication with the end user as the service desk does.
Therefore, the Service Desk is the only practice from the options presented that directly provides a way for
users to have requests arranged, explained, and coordinated from initial submission to resolution.
Relevant links for more research:

guidance from AXELOS for the most authoritative information).
