professionals; provides resources and best practices).
Atlassian - What is a Service Desk?: https://www.atlassian.com/itsm/service-desk (A vendor perspective on
service desks).
Question: 126 CertyIQ
Which helps to streamline the fulfilment of service requests?
A.Understanding which service requests can be accomplished with limited approvals
B.Creating new workflows for every service request
C.Separating requests relating to service failures from the degradation of services
D.Eliminating service requests which have complex workflows
Answer: A
Explanation:
The correct answer is A. Understanding which service requests can be accomplished with limited approvals.
This is because streamlining service request fulfillment centers around efficiency and speed. Identifying
service requests that require minimal approvals allows for faster processing and delivery.
Creating new workflows for every service request (option B) would be incredibly inefficient and lead to
bottlenecks. It defeats the purpose of streamlining by introducing unnecessary complexity.
Separating requests related to service failures from degradation of services (option C), while important for
incident management, doesn't directly contribute to streamlining service request fulfillment. These are
distinct processes.
Eliminating service requests with complex workflows (option D) might seem appealing for simplicity, but it

could mean denying legitimate user needs and negatively impacting service quality. It's better to streamline
these complex requests rather than eliminate them entirely.
By understanding which requests can proceed quickly with limited approvals, organizations can create
standardized procedures and automation rules. This reduces manual intervention, shortens turnaround times,
and improves user satisfaction. The focus is on identifying opportunities for acceleration without sacrificing
necessary checks and balances. This approach aligns with the ITIL 4 guiding principle of "focus on value" by
delivering services quickly and efficiently.
An example would be automating password resets. If a user has verified their identity, a password reset
request could be automatically approved and fulfilled without human intervention. Another example is
standard software installations for new employees. If the software is pre-approved, the request can be
automatically provisioned. This automation reduces wait times and increases efficiency.
Therefore, concentrating on simplified approval paths for suitable service requests is the most direct method
to streamline their fulfillment process according to ITIL 4 principles.
Authoritative Links:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Study Guide: This is the primary resource for understanding ITIL 4 concepts.
While a direct link to the free study guide is unavailable, authorized training providers often offer excerpts
and summaries online. Search for "ITIL 4 Foundation study guide free" for available resources.
ITIL 4 Practices Guide: Although access usually requires a subscription, descriptions of the various ITIL 4
practices (including service request management) provide deeper insight into how to implement these
concepts. Search "ITIL 4 Practices" for more information and summaries.
Question: 127 CertyIQ
Which statement about outcomes is CORRECT?
A.They are deliverables provided to service consumers
B.They allow service consumers to achieve a desired result
C.They provide products to service providers based on outputs
D.They co-create value for service providers by reducing costs and risks
Answer: B
Explanation:
The correct answer is B: They allow service consumers to achieve a desired result.
Here's why:
ITIL 4 defines an outcome as a result for a stakeholder enabled by one or more outputs. Outcomes are what
the service consumer ultimately wants to achieve by using the service. They focus on the value derived by the
consumer, not just the deliverables or products (outputs) provided by the service provider.
A is incorrect because deliverables are outputs, not outcomes. Outputs are the tangible (or intangible) things
delivered to the service consumer.
C is incorrect because it reverses the roles. Service providers provide products (outputs) based on inputs,
processes, and resources.
D is incorrect because while co-creation of value can reduce costs and risks, the primary focus of an outcome
is on the benefits and results for the service consumer, not the service provider. Outcomes are about the
stakeholder's (typically the service consumer) perspective of value. The service provider benefits indirectly by

enabling positive outcomes and thereby ensuring continued use of the service.
In essence, outcomes are tied to the service consumer's goals and objectives. They're the reason the
consumer is using the service in the first place. They represent the realized value and benefits after the
service has been consumed. Outcomes represent the "what" and "why" from the consumer's perspective.
For further research and authoritative definitions, refer to the official ITIL 4 publications and the AXELOS
website.
AXELOS: https://www.axelos.com/ (Official ITIL body)
Question: 128 CertyIQ
Which guiding principle says that services and processes should NOT provide a solution for every exception?
A.Keep it simple and practical
B.Collaborate and promote visibility
C.Think and work holistically
D.Optimize and automate
Answer: A
Explanation:
The guiding principle "Keep it simple and practical" directly addresses the need to avoid over-engineering
solutions and focusing on essential value. This principle advocates for using the minimum number of steps to
achieve an objective. Attempting to create solutions for every exception, particularly edge cases, often leads
to increased complexity, higher costs, and reduced usability. It's about pragmatism and recognizing that
sometimes workarounds or manual interventions are more efficient than building elaborate systems to handle
infrequent occurrences.
The other principles are less directly related to this concept. "Collaborate and promote visibility" focuses on
communication and transparency. "Think and work holistically" encourages a broader system-wide
perspective. "Optimize and automate" advocates for efficiency improvements. While these principles are all
important, they don't specifically address the idea of avoiding solutions for every exception like "Keep it
simple and practical" does. Over-automation or complex solutions that cater to every exception can
contradict the goals of simplification and practicality. Such solutions frequently become unwieldy,
challenging to maintain, and potentially detrimental to the overall service value. Finding a balance between
handling common scenarios efficiently and dealing with exceptions appropriately is key, often favoring
simpler processes for less frequent needs.
For further research, refer to official ITIL 4 documentation, Axelos resources, and reputable IT service
management blogs and articles. While specific links addressing this exact phrasing might be rare, content on
ITIL 4 guiding principles in general will provide further context. Focus specifically on sections detailing the
interpretation and practical application of "Keep it simple and practical." While not a direct link, exploring
resources on "minimal viable product (MVP)" development in software engineering provides analogous
insights into the principle of focusing on core functionality and avoiding feature creep. This links to related
concept. The goal is to build a robust, maintainable system that effectively delivers value while avoiding
unnecessary complication.
Question: 129 CertyIQ

Identify the missing word in the following sentence.
The purpose of the 'supplier management' practice is to ensure that the organization's suppliers and their
performances are [?] appropriately to support the seamless provision of quality products and services.
A.measured
B.rewarded
C.managed
D.defined
Answer: C
Explanation:
The correct answer is C, "managed". The ITIL 4 Foundation guidance defines the purpose of supplier
management as ensuring suppliers and their performance are actively and systematically managed to
support the delivery of seamless, high-quality products and services. This holistic approach encompasses
more than just measuring performance (A), which is a component of management, but doesn't capture the
entirety of the practice. Rewarding suppliers (B) might be part of a supplier management strategy, but it's not
the primary purpose. Defining suppliers (D) is an initial step, but again, it falls short of the ongoing oversight
and control implied by "managed."
Supplier management involves activities like supplier selection, contract negotiation, performance
monitoring, relationship management, and dispute resolution. Effective supplier management ensures
alignment between supplier capabilities and the organization's needs, mitigating risks associated with
dependencies on external providers. It's a continuous cycle of planning, doing, checking, and acting to
optimize value from suppliers. Without proper management, organizations risk supply chain disruptions, poor
service quality, increased costs, and reputational damage. The 'managed' approach provides a framework for
maintaining healthy supplier relationships and ensuring they contribute positively to the overall service value
stream.
Consider a cloud service provider as a supplier. Supplier management ensures their service level agreements
(SLAs) are met, potential security vulnerabilities are addressed, and costs are optimized. Organizations need
to actively manage these cloud providers, not just measure their performance metrics, to ensure business
continuity and prevent outages or security breaches. This involves regular reviews, capacity planning, and
collaboration to align the supplier's roadmap with the organization's evolving needs. A comprehensive
supplier management practice ensures this proactive and holistic oversight.
For further research on ITIL 4 and Supplier Management:
AXELOS Official Website: https://www.axelos.com/ (Provides access to ITIL 4 publications and resources)
ITIL Foundation Handbook: (A core text for understanding ITIL 4 principles and practices)
Question: 130 CertyIQ
Identify the missing words in the following sentence.
The purpose of the service configuration management practice is to ensure that accurate and reliable information
about the [?], and the CIs that support them, is available when and where it is needed.
A.relationships with suppliers
B.configuration of services
C.skills of people
D.authorization of changes
Answer: B

Explanation:
The purpose of Service Configuration Management is fundamentally about understanding and managing the
components that make up a service. The practice focuses on maintaining information about the IT
infrastructure, applications, data, and other resources required to deliver a service. These individual
components and their interdependencies are known as Configuration Items (CIs). Accurate and reliable
information about the configuration of services and the CIs that support them is crucial for a number of ITIL 4
practices.
Change Enablement, for instance, needs configuration data to assess the impact of proposed changes.
Incident Management relies on it to quickly diagnose and resolve issues. Problem Management uses
configuration data to identify the root causes of problems and prevent recurrence. Release Management
requires accurate configuration baselines to ensure successful deployments. Without accurate configuration
information, these practices become significantly less effective.
Option A, "relationships with suppliers," is related to Supplier Management, not Service Configuration
Management. Option C, "skills of people," pertains to Workforce and Talent Management. Option D,
"authorization of changes," is directly related to Change Enablement, but it is not the primary focus of service
configuration management.
The key to understanding the role of Service Configuration Management lies in its focus on what constitutes a
service – the underlying configuration of hardware, software, networks, and data that allows it to function.
The practice ensures that this information is accurately documented and readily available. Therefore,
"configuration of services" accurately reflects the missing element in the given ITIL 4 definition.
For further reading, refer to the official ITIL 4 Foundation publications by Axelos:
Axelos, ITIL Foundation: ITIL 4 Edition (TSO, 2019). This is the core text for the ITIL 4 Foundation certification
and details all the practices, including Service Configuration Management. While not freely available, it is the
definitive resource.
While a freely available specific page that exactly defines and relates Configuration Management to other
practices within ITIL 4 practices isn't available through a specific URL, searching for "ITIL 4 Service
Configuration Management" on reputable IT service management websites will provide further supporting
information and definitions aligned with the answer.
Question: 131 CertyIQ
Which practice requires skills and competencies related to business analysis, supplier management and
relationship management?
A.Incident management
B.Monitoring and event management
C.Service level management
D.IT asset management
Answer: C
Explanation:
The correct answer is indeed C, Service Level Management. Service Level Management (SLM) is the practice
responsible for setting clear targets for service performance, and then measuring and monitoring whether the
organization is achieving them.

SLM necessitates a deep understanding of business needs (business analysis) to define service levels that are
relevant and valuable to the organization. This involves understanding the business processes that rely on IT
services and the impact of service performance on business outcomes.
Supplier management is crucial because many organizations rely on external vendors for providing parts of
their IT services. SLM needs to ensure that vendor agreements (Underpinning Contracts or OAs) align with the
overall service levels promised to the business. If a key supplier fails to meet its commitments, it will directly
impact the organization's ability to meet its own service level agreements (SLAs).
Relationship management is paramount because SLM acts as the primary interface between the service
provider and the customer/business. This involves managing customer expectations, communicating service
performance, and addressing any concerns or issues related to service delivery. Building and maintaining
strong relationships is essential for ensuring customer satisfaction and achieving a mutual understanding of
service requirements. Incidents, events, and asset management, while important IT practices, do not
inherently necessitate the same breadth of skills in business analysis, supplier management, and relationship
management. They are often components or inputs to Service Level Management. For example, incident
management performance might be tracked as part of a service level agreement. Event data might be used to
identify areas where service levels are being threatened.
Relevant links for further study:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Handbook: This is the official guide for the ITIL 4 Foundation certification.
ITIL 4 Service Value System: Explains the importance of Service Level Agreements to ensure customer
satisfaction.
Question: 132 CertyIQ
When should a workaround be created?
A.As soon as possible, once the incident is logged
B.After the resolution of a problem
C.When a problem cannot be resolved quickly
D.When a potential permanent solution has been identified
Answer: C
Explanation:
A workaround should be created when a problem cannot be resolved quickly. Here's why:
Focus on Service Continuity: The primary goal of incident management and problem management is to
restore service as quickly as possible and prevent recurrence. When a permanent solution isn't immediately
available, a workaround provides a temporary fix to mitigate the impact.
Problem vs. Incident: Incidents are disruptions to service, while problems are the underlying causes of those
incidents. A workaround addresses the incident, allowing users to continue working while the root cause (the
problem) is investigated and a permanent solution is developed.
Immediate Relief: Creating a workaround as soon as possible after logging an incident (Option A) might be
premature. Investigation is needed to understand the problem. Resolving a problem before a workaround
(Option B) defeats the purpose of a temporary fix. Waiting for a potential permanent solution (Option D) could
leave users without service for an extended period.
Practical Example: Imagine a cloud service outage due to a faulty load balancer. A workaround might involve
temporarily routing traffic to a different server or using a different region until the load balancer is fixed.

ITIL Guidance: ITIL emphasizes the importance of rapid incident resolution and service continuity.
Workarounds are a key tool in achieving this.
In essence, workarounds bridge the gap between service disruption and a permanent solution, minimizing the
impact on users and the business.
For further research, consider these authoritative links:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Book: This is the primary source for ITIL 4 guidance.
Official ITIL Website: https://www.axelos.com/
Question: 133 CertyIQ
What is a configuration item?
A.Any financially valuable component that can contribute to the delivery of an IT product or service
B.Any change of state that has significance for the management of a service
C.Any component that needs to be managed in order to deliver an IT service
D.A problem that has been analyzed but has not been resolved
Answer: C
Explanation:
The correct answer is C: "Any component that needs to be managed in order to deliver an IT service." This
definition aligns directly with the ITIL 4 Foundation principles concerning configuration management and
service delivery. Configuration items (CIs) are the fundamental building blocks of an IT service and can include
hardware, software, networks, documentation, and even people.
The core of ITIL's configuration management is to identify, control, record, and verify CIs. Effectively
managing CIs ensures that services are delivered reliably and consistently. Choice A is incorrect because
while financial value might be relevant, the manageability of the component is the defining characteristic.
Choice B refers more closely to the definition of an event or change, not a CI itself. Choice D defines a known
error, a distinct concept from a CI.
Consider a cloud-based web application. CIs would include the virtual machines hosting the application, the
database server, the load balancer, the application code, and any supporting middleware. Proper
configuration management would track versions, configurations, and dependencies among these CIs. Without
proper management of these components, service outages, performance degradation, and security
vulnerabilities can occur. Understanding and managing these CIs is fundamental for delivering and
maintaining a stable and effective IT service.
In summary, CIs are the constituent parts of an IT service that must be controlled and tracked to ensure
reliable service delivery. Their management is crucial for effective service management practices.

framework.

Question: 134 CertyIQ
Identify the missing words in the following sentence.
When an organization has decided to improve a service, it should start by considering [?].
A.existing information
B.new methods
C.additional measurements
D.revised processes
Answer: A
Explanation:
The correct answer is A (existing information) because ITIL 4 emphasizes a practical and value-driven
approach to service improvement. When embarking on service improvement, an organization should first
leverage the knowledge and data it already possesses.
Here's a breakdown of why the other options are less suitable:
B. new methods: Introducing new methods without understanding the current situation is akin to shooting in
the dark. It's essential to assess what's working and what isn't before adopting new approaches. New
methods might be considered later, informed by the initial analysis of existing information.
C. additional measurements: While measurements are crucial for improvement, they are most effective when
targeted. Before collecting new data, it's important to understand what existing data reveals about the
service's performance and areas for improvement. Additional measurements might be needed, but only after
analyzing existing information to pinpoint the gaps.
D. revised processes: Revising processes without a solid understanding of the current state can lead to
ineffective or even detrimental changes. Processes should be revised based on evidence gathered from
existing data and insights.
ITIL 4 advocates for a cyclical approach to service management, encompassing planning, doing, checking, and
acting (PDCA). Analyzing existing information aligns with the "check" phase, where performance data, user
feedback, incident reports, and other relevant sources are scrutinized to identify areas needing improvement.
Only after a thorough understanding of the current state can informed decisions be made about new methods,
additional measurements, or revised processes. By leveraging existing information, organizations can ensure
that improvement efforts are targeted, efficient, and aligned with business objectives. This minimizes the risk
of wasted resources and ineffective changes. Analyzing existing information is part of establishing a baseline
against which improvements can be measured. This baseline will also inform the new methods and processes
to be adopted.
Authoritative Links:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Guidance: You can purchase official ITIL 4 guides from AXELOS, the organization
behind ITIL, for comprehensive information.
PeopleCert Website: PeopleCert is an examination institute. Its website offers resources and guides on the
ITIL 4 framework.
Question: 135 CertyIQ
Which is a use of the change schedule?
A.Assigning resources to changes

B.Deciding the approval authority for changes
C.Automating the change process
D.Creating change models
Answer: A
Explanation:
The correct answer is A, assigning resources to changes, because the change schedule's primary purpose is
to provide a view of planned changes. This visibility enables organizations to effectively manage and
coordinate resources, ensuring that the right people and tools are available at the right time for each change.
The change schedule acts as a planning tool, facilitating the allocation of resources by showing when
different changes are scheduled to occur. This prevents resource contention and ensures smooth change
implementation.
While the change schedule indirectly informs other aspects of change management, its core function revolves
around scheduling and resource allocation. Options B, C, and D relate to other aspects of change
management but aren't directly facilitated by the change schedule itself. Deciding the approval authority for
changes is a function of the change authority, not the schedule. Automating the change process involves
workflows and orchestration, not scheduling. Creating change models is a design activity that precedes
scheduling. The change schedule leverages the other processes, but does not do the tasks itself.
In essence, the change schedule is a calendar of planned changes with visibility and resource management
being the two important elements. It's a critical tool for communication, coordination, and resource
optimization within the change management process. Organizations leverage the change schedule to improve
change success rates by improving resource availability and mitigating conflicts.

Question: 136 CertyIQ
Which dimension of service management considers the workflows and controls needed to deliver services?
A.Organizations and people
B.Information and technology
C.Partners and suppliers
D.Value streams and processes
Answer: D
Explanation:
The correct answer is D, Value streams and processes, because this dimension directly addresses how an
organization structures its activities to create value. This encompasses defining the steps, workflows,
controls, and procedures necessary to deliver services effectively.
Let's break it down:
Value Streams: A value stream is a series of steps an organization undertakes to create and deliver products

and services to a consumer. They outline the specific activities and resources needed to transform a demand
into value.
Processes: Processes are a structured set of activities designed to accomplish a specific objective. They
define how things are done and ensure consistency and repeatability in service delivery.
The ITIL 4 framework emphasizes designing efficient and effective value streams to optimize service creation,
delivery, and support. This includes carefully mapping processes, identifying potential bottlenecks, and
implementing controls to ensure quality and compliance. By focusing on value streams and processes,
organizations can streamline their operations, reduce costs, and improve customer satisfaction. The other
dimensions are important, but they are not focused on the workflows and controls as described. Organizations
and People deals with roles, responsibilities, and organizational culture. Information and Technology focuses
on the tools and data used. Partners and Suppliers involves the external relationships required.
For further research, you can consult the official ITIL 4 Foundation guide from AXELOS:
https://www.axelos.com/ and explore resources that define the 4 Dimensions of Service Management:
https://www.bmc.com/blogs/itil-4-four-dimensions/
Question: 137 CertyIQ
Which guiding principle considers how the steps of a process can be performed as efficiently as possible?
A.Focus on value
B.Start where you are
C.Think and work holistically
D.Optimize and automate
Answer: D
Explanation:
The question focuses on identifying the ITIL 4 guiding principle that emphasizes efficiency in process
execution. The correct answer is Optimize and Automate (D). This principle directly advocates for streamlining
processes and minimizing manual effort wherever possible. It encourages organizations to look for
opportunities to enhance efficiency by identifying and eliminating bottlenecks, reducing waste, and
automating repetitive tasks. Options A, B, and C, while important, do not directly address the core concept of
optimizing process efficiency. Focus on value emphasizes delivering value to the customer, Start where you
are emphasizes leveraging existing resources and knowledge, and Think and work holistically emphasizes
understanding the interconnectedness of systems and processes. While these principles indirectly contribute
to efficiency, Optimize and Automate is the most direct and relevant answer. By automating tasks and
optimizing processes, organizations can reduce errors, improve speed, and free up resources for more
strategic initiatives. This principle can be effectively applied to cloud environments by leveraging automation
tools for infrastructure provisioning, deployment, and management, as well as automating incident response
processes. It also supports continuous improvement by analyzing process performance and identifying areas
for optimization.
Supporting resources:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Guidance: https://www.axelos.com/ (Official source for ITIL 4 information)

service management websites and forums.

Question: 138 CertyIQ
Which statement about the 'incident management' practice is CORRECT?
A.It identifies the cause of major incidents
B.It authorizes changes to resolve incidents
C.It maintains detailed procedures for diagnosing incidents
D.It resolves the highest impact incidents first
Answer: D
Explanation:
Here's a detailed justification for why the correct answer is D:
The ITIL 4 Foundation guidance defines Incident Management as the practice focused on restoring normal
service operation as quickly as possible to minimize the impact on business operations, ensuring that the best
possible levels of service quality and availability are maintained. This aligns directly with prioritizing incidents
based on their impact. Options A, B, and C, while related to IT service management, are not the primary focus
of incident management.
Option A is incorrect because identifying the root cause of major incidents falls under Problem Management.
While incident management might uncover clues, the formal root cause analysis is handled elsewhere.
Option B is incorrect because authorizing changes, even those aimed at resolving incidents, is the
responsibility of Change Management. Incident Management focuses on rapid restoration; changes,
especially significant ones, need proper authorization.
Option C is related but incomplete. While documented procedures can aid in incident diagnosis, the practice
itself is not defined by maintaining those procedures. Moreover, effective incident management also relies on
the skills of the incident resolvers and the available knowledge base.
Therefore, option D is the most accurate. Prioritizing the highest-impact incidents is the core principle. This
ensures that the most critical business functions are recovered first, minimizing overall disruption and loss.
High-impact incidents are those that affect a large number of users or essential services, so resolving them
quickly is crucial.
In cloud environments, this prioritization becomes even more critical. Cloud services often underpin numerous
dependent systems. An incident affecting a core cloud service could have widespread repercussions. Incident
management practices must be tailored to these complexities, with clear escalation paths and robust
communication plans.
Further reading:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation: ITIL 4 Edition: Provides the foundational knowledge and concepts of ITIL 4.
ITIL 4 Practice Guides: Provides detailed guidance on each ITIL 4 practice, including Incident Management.
Available via subscription to the My ITIL platform. You may find relevant excerpts publicly.
Question: 139 CertyIQ
How should an organization prioritize incidents?
A.Ask the user for their preferred resolution timeframe
B.Assess the availability of the appropriate support team
C.Use an agreed classification which is based on the business impact of the incident
D.Create an order of incidents based on the dates and times when they were logged

Answer: C
Explanation:
Here's a detailed justification for why option C is the correct answer and why the other options are incorrect,
in the context of ITIL 4 Foundation principles:
Option C, "Use an agreed classification which is based on the business impact of the incident," is the correct
approach for prioritizing incidents according to ITIL 4 best practices. Incident prioritization aims to restore
normal service operation as quickly as possible while minimizing business disruption. The impact an incident
has on business operations, processes, and critical services should be the primary driver of its priority. An
"agreed classification" implies a documented and understood scheme, ideally part of a service level
agreement (SLA) or operating level agreement (OLA), that considers the business impact, urgency (time
sensitivity), and potentially the number of users affected. Using such a scheme ensures consistency and
alignment with business needs. High-impact incidents, like those causing significant financial loss,
reputational damage, or legal non-compliance, must be addressed with the highest priority.
Option A, "Ask the user for their preferred resolution timeframe," is incorrect because relying solely on the
user's desired timeframe isn't an objective or business-aligned approach. Users might not be fully aware of
the broader business implications of the incident or the relative importance of other incidents. While user
input is valuable in understanding the incident's urgency, it shouldn't be the sole determinant of priority.
Option B, "Assess the availability of the appropriate support team," is incorrect as the availability of a support
team should not dictate the prioritization of an incident. The incident's impact on the business should
determine its priority. If a high-impact incident occurs, resources must be found or shifted to address it, even
if the initially assigned team is occupied. Resource allocation should follow from priority, not the other way
around.
Option D, "Create an order of incidents based on the dates and times when they were logged," is incorrect
because first-come, first-served (FCFS) is not an effective method for prioritizing incidents. This approach
doesn't account for the relative business impact. An incident logged earlier might have a minimal impact,
while a more recently logged incident might be causing a critical business outage. Business impact is far more
important than chronological order.
In summary, effective incident prioritization requires a structured approach based on the agreed upon
business impact and urgency. The impact and urgency should be defined in service agreements and incident
management policies.
Further Reading:
Axelos ITIL 4 Foundation Publications: (Official ITIL guidance, available through Axelos or accredited training
organizations). While specific URLs aren't available for sections of the book, searching for "ITIL 4 incident
prioritization" will provide relevant excerpts and discussions in forums.
ITIL Foundation Handbook: Offers a comprehensive guide to the ITIL 4 framework, including incident
management and prioritization.
Question: 140 CertyIQ
Which is a purpose of the 'relationship management' practice?
A.To systematically observe services and service components
B.To protect the information needed by the organization to conduct its business
C.To be the entry point and single point of contact for the service provider with all of its users
D.To identify, analyze, monitor, and continually improve links with stakeholders

Answer: D
Explanation:
The correct answer is D. To identify, analyze, monitor, and continually improve links with stakeholders is a core
purpose of the 'relationship management' practice in ITIL 4. This practice focuses on fostering positive
relationships with all stakeholders, including customers, users, suppliers, and partners. This involves
understanding their needs, managing expectations, and ensuring satisfaction through effective
communication and collaboration. By actively managing these relationships, organizations can gain valuable
insights into customer needs, improve service quality, enhance customer loyalty, and ultimately drive
business value. Options A, B, and C relate to different ITIL 4 practices, such as 'monitoring and event
management' for A, 'information security management' for B, and 'service desk' for C. Relationship
management specifically is about the two-way communication and partnership aspects. It moves beyond
simply reacting to incidents (service desk) or protecting information (security management) to proactively
shaping and nurturing stakeholder engagements to maximize mutual benefit.Here are authoritative links for
further research on ITIL 4 Relationship Management:
