Question: 141 CertyIQ
Which statement about problems is CORRECT?
A.Problems are not related to incidents
B.Problems must be resolved quickly in order to restore normal business activity
C.Problem analysis should focus on one of the four dimensions to achieve a fast diagnosis
D.Problem prioritization involves risk assessment
Answer: D
Explanation:
The correct answer, "Problem prioritization involves risk assessment," accurately reflects ITIL 4's guidance on
problem management. Problems, unlike incidents, are about identifying the underlying cause of one or more
incidents. While incident management prioritizes quick restoration of service, problem management focuses
on long-term solutions and prevention of recurrence.
Option D is correct because prioritization is a crucial step in problem management. Not every problem can or
should be addressed immediately due to resource constraints. Risk assessment becomes the determining
factor, considering the likelihood and impact of the problem recurring and potentially causing more incidents
or impacting services. High-risk problems, such as those frequently causing critical service outages, rightfully
take precedence. This assessment isn't merely about the immediate incident; it's about potential future harm
to the business.
Option A is incorrect because problems are directly related to incidents. Problem management aims to
prevent incidents. Option B is also incorrect; fast resolution is the goal of incident management, not problem
management. Problem resolution is a longer-term process. Option C is incorrect as problem analysis requires
a holistic view, considering all four dimensions of service management: organizations and people, information
and technology, partners and suppliers, and value streams and processes. Focusing solely on one dimension
would lead to incomplete and potentially ineffective analysis.

In essence, prioritizing problems based on risk ensures that resources are allocated to the most impactful
issues first, preventing future disruptions and aligning with business needs. Risk assessment helps determine
which problems warrant immediate attention and deeper investigation, thus streamlining the problem
management process and maximizing its effectiveness.Authoritative Links for Further Research:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Guidance: (Unfortunately, I cannot provide a direct link to the AXELOS official
documentation as it often requires a subscription or purchase. However, searching for "ITIL 4 Foundation" will
lead you to official or accredited training materials that cover this topic in detail.)
ITIL Foundation Handbook: Again, specific links to purchasable books are not possible, but searching for "ITIL
Foundation Handbook" will yield relevant resources.
Question: 142 CertyIQ
Which is a risk that might be removed from a service consumer by an IT service?
A.Service provider ceasing to trade
B.Security breach
C.Failure of server hardware
D.Cost of purchasing servers
Answer: C
Explanation:
The correct answer is C: Failure of server hardware. Here's why:
ITIL 4 emphasizes how IT services create value by facilitating outcomes for service consumers. One crucial
aspect of this value is risk mitigation. A key benefit of IT services is absorbing risks that would otherwise
burden the service consumer.
Let's analyze each option:
A. Service provider ceasing to trade: While service continuity is important, the risk of a provider going out of
business isn't removed by the core service itself. Contingency planning addresses this, but the inherent
business risk remains.
B. Security breach: While IT services can implement security measures, they cannot completely eliminate the
risk of a security breach. Security is a shared responsibility, and some residual risk always exists.
C. Failure of server hardware: This is the most direct example of risk removal. When a service consumer
utilizes an IT service (e.g., cloud computing, SaaS), the service provider assumes responsibility for the
underlying infrastructure, including servers. The consumer doesn't need to worry about purchasing,
maintaining, or replacing servers. The risk associated with server failures (downtime, data loss) is mitigated by
the service provider's infrastructure management and redundancy measures.
D. Cost of purchasing servers: While the cost is reduced or shifted to a subscription model, it is not a risk
removal. Cost management still exists for the consumer.
Therefore, the failure of server hardware is a risk directly addressed and minimized by the service provider,
effectively removing it as a concern for the service consumer. The service consumer is insulated from the
technical complexities and potential failures of the underlying hardware. Cloud computing platforms are built
with redundancy and fault tolerance to minimize the risks of server failures.
Supporting Concepts:

Cloud Computing: Cloud services abstract the underlying infrastructure, shielding users from hardware
concerns.
Infrastructure as a Service (IaaS): Example of shifting server hardware responsibility to the provider.
ITIL 4 Value Co-creation: The service provider assumes responsibilities (like hardware maintenance) to
facilitate better outcomes for the service consumer.
Authoritative Links:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Guidance
NIST Definition of Cloud Computing
Question: 143 CertyIQ
In which step of the "˜continual improvement model' is an improvement plan implemented?
A.What is the vision?
B.How do we get there?
C.Take action
D.Did we get there?
Answer: C
Explanation:
The correct answer is C. Take action because the "continual improvement model" is a structured approach to
implementing improvements based on a cyclical process. Let's break down why the other options are
incorrect and then solidify why "Take action" is the right choice.
Option A, "What is the vision?" falls into the initial stage of the model, primarily focusing on understanding the
overall goals and direction of the improvement initiative. This step identifies the desired future state, like
migrating a specific workload to a more cost-effective cloud instance or automating a process.
Option B, "How do we get there?" refers to planning and strategizing. Here, the specific steps needed to
achieve the vision are defined. For example, this could involve selecting the right cloud services, designing a
migration strategy, or creating a detailed automation workflow.
Option D, "Did we get there?" is the assessment and evaluation phase, where the results of the implemented
improvements are measured and compared against the initial goals. This step determines if the implemented
actions were successful and if further adjustments are needed.
The "Take action" step, on the other hand, is the point where the improvement plan, formulated in previous
steps, is actually executed. This involves actively making the changes, implementing the solutions, and
performing the tasks identified in the plan. For instance, this could be deploying the new cloud infrastructure,
executing the data migration, or enabling the automated processes. This is where the planning becomes a
tangible change. It is the culmination of the earlier phases, where the strategies and plans are put into motion
to drive actual improvements within the organization.
In cloud computing environments, the "Take action" phase could involve deploying new virtual machines,
configuring security settings in the cloud console, or integrating different cloud services using APIs.
Successfully executing this phase relies on the correct implementation of cloud best practices and adherence
to security and compliance policies.
For further reading on the continual improvement model:
AXELOS Official ITIL 4 Website: https://www.axelos.com/ (Search for "continual improvement model")

ITIL 4 Foundation Handbook
Therefore, "Take action" is the definitive step where improvement plans are implemented.
Question: 144 CertyIQ
Which is a purpose of the 'service level management' practice?
A.To establish and nurture the links between the organization and its stakeholders
B.To ensure that the organization's suppliers and their performance are managed appropriately
C.To set clear business-based targets for service levels
D.To support the agreed quality of a service handling all agreed, user-initiated service requests
Answer: C
Explanation:
The correct answer is C: To set clear business-based targets for service levels.
Service Level Management (SLM) is fundamentally about defining, agreeing upon, and managing service
levels that meet the needs of the business. The core purpose is to ensure that IT services are delivered at the
agreed-upon levels, supporting business outcomes. This involves establishing Service Level Agreements
(SLAs) that outline specific, measurable, achievable, relevant, and time-bound (SMART) targets. These targets
are directly linked to business objectives and are not arbitrary technical metrics.
Option A is more closely related to Relationship Management. This practice focuses on building and
maintaining strong relationships with stakeholders.
Option B aligns with Supplier Management, which is concerned with ensuring that suppliers deliver services
and products in accordance with agreed terms.
Option D is more connected to Service Desk Management, which handles user requests and aims to restore
service as quickly as possible. While the service desk interacts with users regarding service quality, it is not
responsible for setting the targets for those service levels.
Therefore, setting clear business-based targets for service levels is the central objective of the Service Level
Management practice within the ITIL 4 framework, ensuring IT aligns with and supports business
requirements.
Further reading can be found at:
Axelos ITIL 4 Foundation Study Guide
Official ITIL 4 Publications
Question: 145 CertyIQ
What can be described as an operating model for the creation and management of products and services?
A.Governance
B.Service value chain
C.Guiding principles
D.Practices

Answer: B
Explanation:
The correct answer is B, the Service Value Chain. Let's examine why this is the best choice and why the others
are not.
The Service Value Chain in ITIL 4 describes a series of interconnected activities an organization undertakes to
deliver value to stakeholders. It's the core of the Service Value System (SVS). These activities are: Plan,
Improve, Engage, Design and Transition, Obtain/Build, and Deliver and Support. They're not performed in a
linear fashion but are combined in multiple ways to form value streams. Each value stream is a specific
combination of activities designed to create a particular product or service.
This makes the Service Value Chain an operating model because it defines how resources are utilized,
activities are orchestrated, and value is ultimately created. It’s the engine room for managing products and
services. Each of the six activities contributes to the creation, delivery, and improvement of services. They
illustrate how different parts of the organization interact and collaborate to achieve desired outcomes. The
value chain provides a structured approach to understanding and managing service delivery.
Now, let's consider why the other options are incorrect:
A. Governance: While important, governance provides direction and oversight. It's not the operational
mechanism by which services are created and managed. Governance sets the policies and guidelines; the
value chain executes those policies.
C. Guiding Principles: ITIL 4 Guiding Principles (Focus on Value, Start Where You Are, Progress Iteratively
with Feedback, Collaborate and Promote Visibility, Think and Work Holistically, Keep It Simple and Practical,
Optimize and Automate) provide guidance and recommendations on how to approach service management.
They inform decisions within the Service Value Chain but are not the operating model itself. They are how to
use the operating model effectively.
D. Practices: ITIL 4 practices are sets of organizational resources designed for performing work or
accomplishing an objective. While practices are employed within the Service Value Chain, they aren't the
operating model itself. They are tools and resources used by the chain. Practices, such as Incident
Management or Change Enablement, are applied to one or more of the value chain activities.
Therefore, the Service Value Chain is most accurately described as an operating model for the creation and
management of products and services within the ITIL 4 framework.
Authoritative Links:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Publication: (Available for purchase) - The official source of information on ITIL 4
concepts.
AXELOS Website: https://www.axelos.com/ - Offers resources and information about ITIL.
Official ITIL 4 Foundation Study Guides: Various publishers offer study guides that provide detailed
explanations of the Service Value Chain.
Question: 146 CertyIQ
Which action is performed by a service provider?
A.Requesting required service actions
B.Authorizing budget for service consumption
C.Ensuring access to agreed resources
D.Receiving of the agreed goods

Answer: C
Explanation:
The correct answer is C, ensuring access to agreed resources. Here's a detailed justification:
A service provider is an organization that provides services to consumers. A core responsibility of a service
provider, as defined by ITIL, is to manage resources effectively to deliver services according to agreed-upon
service levels. This inherently includes ensuring that service consumers have the access they require to those
resources in order to benefit from the service. The resources could be IT infrastructure (servers, network,
storage), software, personnel expertise, or other assets necessary for the service to function.
Option A, requesting required service actions, is more aligned with the role of a service consumer, who would
request services from the provider. Option B, authorizing budget for service consumption, pertains to the
financial aspects of the service relationship, a responsibility typically held by the service consumer or a
budget holder within their organization. Option D, receiving of the agreed goods, sounds more like the process
of receiving deliverables or tangible items, which is a component of procurement but doesn’t encapsulate the
broader responsibility of a service provider.
In the context of IT service management, particularly ITIL 4, the focus is on value co-creation. This means the
service provider must actively manage resources and ensure consumers can utilize them effectively to
achieve their desired outcomes. Access management, a critical process within service management, directly
supports this by granting users the rights to use specific services and resources. Without adequate access,
the service can't be consumed, and value cannot be realized.
Therefore, ensuring access to agreed resources is a fundamental action performed by a service provider to
enable service consumption and value creation.
Relevant link for further research:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation guidance: While not a direct URL to a definition, searching for "ITIL 4 service
provider responsibilities" on AXELOS will provide valuable insights into the roles and responsibilities of
service providers.
Question: 147 CertyIQ
Which step of the continual improvement model includes baseline assessments?
A.Did we get there?
B.Where are we now?
C.What is the vision?
D.Where do we want to be?
Answer: B
Explanation:
The correct answer is B. Where are we now? because baseline assessments are fundamental to
understanding the current state before embarking on any improvement initiative.
The ITIL 4 continual improvement model emphasizes a structured approach to ongoing service improvement.
The "Where are we now?" step focuses specifically on assessing the current performance and maturity of the
service or process being examined. This involves gathering data, performing analysis, and creating a baseline
measurement. The baseline acts as a point of reference against which future improvements can be measured.
Without understanding the current state through a baseline, it's impossible to accurately determine the scope

of improvement needed or to effectively track progress later.
This step often entails conducting audits, surveys, performance monitoring, and analyzing existing data. The
baseline assessment highlights strengths and weaknesses, identifies areas for improvement, and provides a
realistic view of the current situation. For example, a baseline might involve assessing the current mean time
to resolve (MTTR) for incidents, customer satisfaction scores related to a particular service, or the utilization
of a specific cloud resource. Only with this information can organizations set realistic and measurable
improvement targets. The baseline also informs the later steps of the model, such as defining the desired
future state ("Where do we want to be?") and measuring the success of implemented changes ("Did we get
there?"). In essence, knowing "Where are we now?" provides the foundation for informed decision-making
throughout the continual improvement process. Choices A, C, and D involve subsequent steps building upon
this initial assessment phase.
Refer to these resources for further information:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Handbook: This provides a comprehensive overview of the ITIL 4 framework,
including the continual improvement model. (Purchase required, but often available through training courses).
Official ITIL Website (AXELOS): https://www.axelos.com/ (Explore the ITIL 4 section for more details on the
guiding principles and practices).
"The ITIL Foundation Handbook: Based on ITIL 4" by AXELOS: (A detailed guide for understanding ITIL 4
foundation concepts).
Question: 148 CertyIQ
Which describes a 'change authority'?
A.A model used to determine who will assess a change
B.A person who approves a change
C.A tool used to help plan changes
D.A way to manage the people aspects of change
Answer: B
Explanation:
The correct answer is B. A 'change authority' is a person (or group) who is authorized to approve changes. This
role is critical in ITIL 4's change management (now called change enablement) practice because it provides
the necessary governance and oversight to ensure changes are properly assessed, authorized, and
implemented, minimizing disruption and risk to IT services. Change authorities are delegated the power to
decide whether a change should proceed based on its potential impact, value, and alignment with
organizational goals.
Option A is incorrect because while models are used to assess changes, they don't define who will assess
them. Option C describes a tool used for planning, not the authority to approve. Option D refers to change
management as a broader concept including people and culture, but the 'change authority' is specifically
about approval, not the entirety of managing the people aspects of change.
The change authority's responsibilities extend to evaluating the risk and reward associated with a proposed
change. They might delegate specific change approvals to others based on the type of change, its urgency,
and the risk involved. The importance lies in having designated individuals accountable for the authorization
process. In the cloud computing context, where changes can have rapid and far-reaching effects, a properly
defined change authority is crucial for preventing outages, security breaches, and compliance violations. They
might approve changes such as updating firewall rules, scaling cloud resources, or deploying new application
versions.https://www.axelos.com/https://www.bmc.com/blogs/itil-change-management/

Question: 149 CertyIQ
Which is NOT a component of the service value system?
A.The service value chain
B.Opportunity and demand
C.Continual improvement
D.Governance
Answer: B
Explanation:
The correct answer, "Opportunity and Demand," is not a component of the ITIL 4 Service Value System (SVS).
The Service Value System, a core concept in ITIL 4, describes how all the components and activities of an
organization work together as a system to enable value creation.
The SVS is comprised of five key components:
1. Guiding Principles: These are recommendations that can guide an organization in all circumstances,
regardless of changes in its goals, strategies, type of work, or management structure.
2. Governance: Governance directs and controls an organization. It is the means by which an
organization is directed and controlled.
3. Service Value Chain: This is a set of interconnected activities that an organization performs to deliver
a valuable product or service to its consumers and to facilitate value creation.
4. Practices: These are sets of organizational resources designed for performing work or accomplishing
an objective. They provide a structured way of managing activities.
5. Continual Improvement: This encompasses a recurring organizational activity performed at all levels
to ensure that the organization's performance continually meets stakeholders' expectations.
While "Opportunity and Demand" are critical inputs that trigger activities within the SVS, they aren't
components of the SVS itself. Opportunity represents the options or possibilities to add value for
stakeholders, and demand represents the need or desire for products and services among internal and
external customers. The SVS then uses these inputs to plan and execute services through its components.
The service value chain utilizes opportunity and demand to engage, plan, design, transition, obtain/build,
deliver, and improve. Continual improvement focuses on improving the service value chain and practices.
Governance sets the direction for the SVS to effectively address opportunity and demand. Therefore,
opportunity and demand are drivers acted upon by the SVS, rather than being integral parts of it.
For further reading on the ITIL 4 Service Value System, refer to the official AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation
publication.https://www.axelos.com/(While the provided link leads to the overall AXELOS website, you can
find more detailed information about ITIL 4 Foundation there, or through searching for "ITIL 4 Foundation" on
trusted sources like ServiceNow's documentation or other IT service management blogs).
Question: 150 CertyIQ
What is a change schedule PRIMARILY used for?
A.To help plan, authorize and schedule emergency changes
B.To publish a list of service requests that users can select

C.To ensure that a single change authority reviews every change
D.To help plan changes, assist in communication and avoid conflicts
Answer: D
Explanation:
The correct answer is D: To help plan changes, assist in communication, and avoid conflicts.
A change schedule is a crucial tool in IT service management, particularly within the ITIL 4 framework. Its
primary purpose is to provide a comprehensive overview of planned changes, offering transparency and
coordination across the IT organization.
Option A is incorrect because while a change schedule might include emergency changes, it isn't primarily for
planning them. Emergency changes have their own expedited process. Option B is incorrect because a list of
service requests typically resides in a service catalog, not a change schedule. Option C is incorrect because
the change authority's role is broader than just reviewing every change; they also consider impact, risk, and
resources.
The change schedule facilitates effective planning by allowing teams to visualize dependencies and potential
conflicts between proposed changes. This proactive approach enables informed decision-making and
resource allocation. Moreover, the change schedule serves as a central communication hub, keeping all
stakeholders informed about upcoming changes and their potential impact on services. This heightened
awareness reduces the likelihood of unexpected disruptions and ensures a smoother change implementation
process. Finally, by visualizing changes in a timeline, potential conflicts (e.g., two changes affecting the same
system simultaneously) become readily apparent, allowing for proactive resolution and preventing service
outages. The schedule typically includes details such as change description, affected services,
implementation dates/times, and responsible parties. It aligns with ITIL's guiding principles, particularly
"focus on value," "collaborate and promote visibility," and "optimize and automate," by streamlining change
management processes and minimizing negative impacts on service delivery. Properly maintained change
schedules are fundamental for effective service management and underpin the success of change
enablement practices.
Refer to these resources for further information:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Handbook: (The official ITIL 4 Foundation publication)
ITIL 4 Change Enablement Practice Guide: Provides detailed guidance on change enablement practices,
including the use of change schedules. (Available through AXELOS)
Question: 151 CertyIQ
What is the MOST important reason for prioritizing incidents?
A.To ensure that user expectations are realistic
B.To ensure that incidents with highest impact are resolved first
C.To help information-sharing and learning
D.To provide links to related changes and known errors
Answer: B
Explanation:
The correct answer is B: To ensure that incidents with the highest impact are resolved first. Prioritization in
incident management, particularly within the ITIL 4 framework, focuses on efficiently addressing service

disruptions and minimizing business impact. While all options contribute to good incident management,
prioritizing based on impact is paramount. Addressing high-impact incidents first minimizes the overall
disruption to the organization's operations, revenue, and customer satisfaction.
Impact refers to the severity of the incident's effect on the business, typically considering factors like the
number of affected users, the criticality of the affected service, and the potential financial losses.
Prioritization, therefore, ensures that resources are allocated to resolving the most critical issues first,
preventing further escalation and minimizing downtime. Options A, C, and D are valuable aspects of incident
management, but they are secondary to the primary goal of restoring service quickly and efficiently when
there's a significant impact. For example, while sharing information and linking to changes is helpful, it's less
critical than immediately restoring a critical service outage that is impacting a large user base. Realistic
expectations (A) and links to changes (D) contribute to better incident resolution in the long term, and
information sharing (C) improves learning and prevention. However, focusing on high-impact incidents directly
minimizes damage and ensures business continuity, which is the immediate and most crucial goal.
Further reading:
Axelos. ITIL Foundation: ITIL 4 Edition. TSO, 2019.
"ITIL 4 Incident Management: A Comprehensive Guide". BMC. https://www.bmc.com/blogs/itil-incident-
management/
Question: 152 CertyIQ
Which 'service level management' activity helps staff to deliver a more business-focused service?
A.Creating targets based on the percentage of uptime of a service
B.Understanding the ongoing requirements of customers
C.Using complex technical terminology in service level agreements (SLAs)
D.Measuring low-level operational activities
Answer: B
Explanation:
The correct answer is B, understanding the ongoing requirements of customers. Service Level Management
(SLM) in ITIL 4 aims to align IT services with business needs and priorities. Creating targets solely based on
uptime percentage (A) focuses on a technical metric rather than the actual business impact of the service.
While uptime is important, it doesn't necessarily translate to customer satisfaction or meeting their evolving
needs.
Using complex technical jargon in SLAs (C) hinders understanding and collaboration between IT and the
business, making it difficult to ensure the service meets business requirements. Technical language may
alienate the client, while using business-oriented metrics helps align IT services with business expectations.
Measuring low-level operational activities (D) might provide insights for internal improvements, but it doesn't
directly address the crucial aspect of understanding and meeting customer needs.
Understanding the ongoing requirements of customers (B), on the other hand, directly contributes to
delivering a more business-focused service. By actively engaging with customers, SLM can identify their
priorities, pain points, and evolving expectations. This allows IT to tailor services, SLAs, and delivery
approaches to directly address the business's needs. This alignment ensures that IT services are not just
technically sound but also contribute to business outcomes and customer satisfaction. This is key to effective
service management. This proactive approach enables IT to be a strategic partner to the business, instead of
just a support function.

Relevant Links for Further Research:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Guidance: (Refer to official ITIL 4 documentation as this is proprietary) Search for
ITIL 4 Foundation study guides online.
Service Level Management Best Practices: https://www.bmc.com/blogs/service-level-management-best-
practices/
Question: 153 CertyIQ
Which practice has a purpose that includes the handling of pre-defined, user-initiated demands for service?
A.Service request management
B.Service configuration management
C.Deployment management
D.Change enablement
Answer: A
Explanation:
The correct answer is A, Service Request Management. The purpose of Service Request Management is
specifically focused on handling pre-defined, user-initiated demands for service. These requests are typically
standard, low-risk, and frequent in nature. Examples include password resets, software installations, or
requests for information. Service Request Management aims to fulfill these requests efficiently and
effectively, minimizing disruption to the user and the IT environment.
Let's examine why the other options are incorrect. Service Configuration Management (SCM) deals with
identifying, controlling, and tracking IT assets and their configurations. It doesn't directly handle user
requests but focuses on maintaining accurate information about IT infrastructure. Deployment Management is
concerned with moving new or changed hardware, software, documentation, processes, or any other
component to a live environment. While it might be triggered by a service request in some cases, it's not the
primary practice for handling them. Change Enablement (formerly Change Management) focuses on
controlling changes in the IT environment to minimize risk and disruption. While a service request might
require a change, Change Enablement is the process for managing that broader change, not the service
request itself.
Service request management provides a streamlined and standardized approach to fulfilling common user
needs. This enhances user satisfaction, improves IT efficiency, and frees up IT staff to focus on more complex
and strategic initiatives. The other practices play different but equally important roles in ensuring smooth IT
operations, but they are not primarily designed to handle user-initiated demands for pre-defined services.
Service Request Management ensures that these demands are met in a timely and efficient manner.
Here are some authoritative links for further research:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Guidance: https://www.axelos.com/ (While specific pages may change, this is the
official source for ITIL information.)
BMC - ITIL Service Request Management: https://www.bmc.com/blogs/itil-service-request-management/
Atlassian - Service Request Management: https://www.atlassian.com/itsm/service-request-management
Question: 154 CertyIQ
Which guiding principle considers which parts of an existing process should be kept by identifying how they
contribute to value creation?

A.Progress iteratively with feedback
B.Collaborate and promote visibility
C.Think and work holistically
D.Keep it simple and practical
Answer: D
Explanation:
The answer is D. Keep it simple and practical.
Here's why: The "Keep it simple and practical" guiding principle emphasizes streamlining processes and
eliminating unnecessary complexity. When evaluating an existing process, this principle focuses on
identifying elements that directly contribute to value and removing those that don't. The aim is to keep the
process efficient and focused on delivering the desired outcome.
Options A, B, and C, while valuable ITIL 4 guiding principles, do not directly address identifying which parts of
an existing process to keep based on their contribution to value creation. "Progress iteratively with feedback"
focuses on incremental improvements, "Collaborate and promote visibility" emphasizes communication and
transparency, and "Think and work holistically" promotes understanding the big picture, but none specifically
pinpoint the selection of process components based on value delivery. Option D is the only option that
addresses simplification, practicality, and value, making it most appropriate.
Consider this example: A complex incident management process includes 10 steps. Applying "Keep it simple
and practical" might reveal that only 5 of these steps directly lead to faster incident resolution (value). The
other 5 steps, while seemingly useful, are redundant or create bottlenecks. This principle would advocate
keeping the 5 value-adding steps and eliminating or streamlining the other 5.
ITIL 4 Foundation guidance discusses the keep it simple and practical guiding principle. This information can
be found in the official ITIL 4 Foundation publications and training materials. While direct links to online books
are paywalled, you can find general information on the ITIL 4 guiding principles at sources such as:
AXELOS Website (ITIL Owners): This is where you can find official information on ITIL 4 and related topics.
(https://www.axelos.com/)
Various IT Service Management (ITSM) blogs and articles: Search for "ITIL 4 guiding principles explained" to
find various reputable sources.
Question: 155 CertyIQ
Which is included in the purpose of the "˜deliver and support' value chain activity?
A.Meeting stakeholder expectations for time to market
B.Understanding the organization's service vision
C.Understanding stakeholder needs
D.Providing services to agreed specifications
Answer: D
Explanation:
Here's a detailed justification for why option D, "Providing services to agreed specifications," is the correct
answer for the purpose of the 'Deliver and Support' value chain activity in ITIL 4 Foundation:

The "Deliver and Support" value chain activity in ITIL 4 focuses on ensuring services are provided to end-users
and customers in accordance with agreed-upon terms. This directly translates to meeting established
specifications.
Focus on Operational Delivery: This activity is heavily geared towards the operational aspects of service
management, encompassing the actual execution of services.
Service Level Agreements (SLAs): The services delivered must adhere to the Service Level Agreements
(SLAs), ensuring agreed-upon quality, availability, and performance. Specifications are critical elements
defining what is expected in SLAs.
Meeting Requirements: The service delivery and support must meet the previously established requirements
of the stakeholders.
Customer Satisfaction: Delivering services to agreed-upon specifications contributes directly to customer
satisfaction and business outcomes.
Now let's look at why the other options are not the best fit:
A. Meeting stakeholder expectations for time to market: While time-to-market is important, it's more closely
associated with the "Plan" and "Improve" value chain activities that focus on strategy and continuous
improvement to quickly deliver needed services.
B. Understanding the organization's service vision: This is mainly a part of the "Plan" value chain activity
where strategic direction is defined.
C. Understanding stakeholder needs: This is primarily covered in "Engage" value chain activity, before
"Deliver and Support". This activity is where the customer communicates their requirements and feedback is
gathered.
In conclusion, 'Deliver and Support' is all about the effective and efficient delivery of services that meet
predefined quality, availability, and performance standards. The option "Providing services to agreed
specifications" perfectly aligns with this core objective.
Authoritative Links for further research:
Axelos ITIL 4 Foundation Guide: (Requires purchase). This is the official source for ITIL 4 knowledge. Look for
sections detailing the Service Value System (SVS) and the Service Value Chain.
Official ITIL Website: https://www.axelos.com/ (provides general information and training resources).
Question: 156 CertyIQ
Which statement about outcomes is CORRECT?
A.Outcomes rely on outputs to deliver results for a stakeholder
B.Outcomes use activities to produce tangible or intangible deliverables
C.Outcomes give service consumers assurance of products or services
D.Outcomes help a service consumer to assess the cost of a specific activity
Answer: A
Explanation:
The correct answer is A: Outcomes rely on outputs to deliver results for a stakeholder. This choice directly
reflects the core concept of outcomes within the ITIL 4 framework. ITIL 4 emphasizes value co-creation,
where the service provider and consumer collaborate to achieve desired outcomes.
Let's break down why the other options are incorrect:
B. Outcomes use activities to produce tangible or intangible deliverables: This statement describes the

relationship between activities and outputs, not outcomes. Activities lead to outputs.
C. Outcomes give service consumers assurance of products or services: While assurance is important, it's
not the primary definition of an outcome. Assurance contributes to achieving the outcome, but it isn't the
outcome itself.
D. Outcomes help a service consumer to assess the cost of a specific activity: Cost assessment is related to
value, but it's not the definition of an outcome. Outcomes are about the results achieved, while cost is a factor
affecting the value proposition.
Here's a more in-depth explanation of why A is correct:
Outcomes represent the results that a service consumer desires. These results are dependent on the outputs
generated by the service provider's activities. Outputs are tangible or intangible deliverables. The service
provider must design its services and activities to produce outputs that enable the service consumer to
achieve their desired outcomes. Think of it this way: a cloud service provider offers compute instances
(output), but the outcome is that the customer can run their applications reliably and efficiently, supporting
their business goals. Stakeholders are those who are affected by the outcomes, and they can be either
internal or external to the organization. Understanding what those stakeholders desire is key to delivering
valuable services. This alignment of outputs to desired results for a stakeholder defines outcome-based
thinking, a core ITIL 4 principle. The focus is on achieving tangible improvements and benefits for the
consumers of services.The whole ITIL framework is designed around optimizing the path to the desired
outcome for the stakeholder, making sure it receives value.
For further reading:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Publication: This is the definitive source for understanding ITIL 4 concepts.
ITIL official website: https://www.axelos.com/ - Provides information about ITIL frameworks and
certifications.
Question: 157 CertyIQ
Which skill is required by the 'service level management' practice?
A.Supplier management
B.Technical expertise
C.Event monitoring
D.Problem management
Answer: A
Explanation:
The most fitting skill for the 'service level management' practice is Supplier Management. Service Level
Management (SLM) focuses on defining, agreeing upon, documenting, and managing service levels for IT
services. These services often rely on third-party suppliers to deliver various components or functionalities.
Without effective supplier management, the agreed-upon service levels might become unattainable.
SLM needs to ensure suppliers can meet their contractual obligations regarding service delivery,
performance, and availability. This includes monitoring supplier performance against agreed service level
agreements (SLAs), identifying potential risks related to supplier performance, and managing supplier
relationships. If a supplier fails to deliver as expected, it directly impacts the ability of the IT organization to
meet its commitments to the customer. Therefore, skills in negotiation, contract management, performance
monitoring, and relationship management are crucial for SLM professionals when dealing with suppliers.
While technical expertise, event monitoring, and problem management are essential IT skills, they are not

directly linked to defining and managing service levels related to external suppliers. Technical expertise is
useful across many areas, and Event Monitoring and Problem Management are crucial for service operations,
but Supplier Management directly addresses the dependencies of IT services on external providers, a core
concern of SLM. Effectively managing those dependencies enables the service provider to meet service level
targets.
For further reading on Service Level Management and Supplier Management, refer to the official ITIL 4
Foundation publication and Axelos resources.https://www.axelos.com/(This URL links to Axelos, the
organization behind ITIL. Specific pages on SLM and Supplier Management would require a paid subscription,
but the general site provides information on ITIL best practices.)
Question: 158 CertyIQ
What is a change schedule used for?
A.To help plan emergency changes
B.To help authorize standard changes
C.To help assign a change authority
D.To help manage normal changes
Answer: D
Explanation:
The correct answer is D: To help manage normal changes. Here's why:
The change schedule is a key component of ITIL 4's change management practice, specifically designed to
provide a high-level overview of all planned changes, especially normal changes. Its primary purpose is to help
coordinate these changes, avoid conflicts, and ensure that resources are available when needed.
Normal changes, by definition, follow the standard change management process. This includes assessment,
authorization, and planning, all of which benefit significantly from being visualized within a change schedule.
The schedule allows stakeholders to see the timeline of changes, their dependencies, and potential impacts
on services. It aids in planning capacity, scheduling resources (like personnel and infrastructure), and
communicating upcoming changes to affected parties.
Options A, B, and C are incorrect because they describe functions that are either outside the scope of the
change schedule itself or related to different types of changes. Emergency changes have a rapid, expedited
process; a detailed schedule isn't the priority. Standard changes are pre-approved and don't need the same
level of scheduling as normal changes. The change schedule doesn't assign change authority.
The change schedule helps ensure that normal changes are implemented smoothly, predictably, and with
minimal disruption to IT services. It offers a centralized view for proactively identifying potential collisions or
resource constraints.Authoritative links:
Axelos ITIL 4 Foundation Handbook: This is the official source for ITIL 4 information. (Requires purchase,
generally)
ITIL Foundation Study Guide: Many reputable guides are available online that elaborate on ITIL concepts.
Search for "ITIL 4 Foundation Study Guide Change Schedule". While not official, they distill the information.
Question: 159 CertyIQ
What is the definition of warranty?

A.A means of identifying events that could cause harm or loss
B.A means of determining whether a service is fit for purpose
C.A means of identifying a result for a stakeholder
D.A means of determining whether a service is fit for use
Answer: D
Explanation:
The correct answer is D: "A means of determining whether a service is fit for use." Warranty, in the context of
ITIL 4, refers to the assurance that a service will meet agreed-upon requirements. "Fit for use" emphasizes the
service's ability to be reliably and securely available, have sufficient capacity, and provide the necessary level
of continuity.
While "fit for purpose" (option B) relates to utility, addressing what the service does, warranty addresses how
well it does it. It concerns availability, capacity, security, and continuity. Essentially, warranty ensures the
service operates as intended and meets predefined service level agreements (SLAs). Option A describes risk
management, and option C focuses on stakeholder value, neither of which directly define warranty. ITIL 4
emphasizes that warranty is a crucial aspect of service value, ensuring that the service is reliable and
performs according to expectations. Strong warranty elements build trust with stakeholders and support
consistent service delivery. Warranty parameters are commonly measured using metrics and reported within
SLAs.
For further information, refer to these sources:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Study Guide: Search for "warranty of service" within the guide.
Official ITIL 4 Foundation Publications: These provide the canonical definitions and context.
Question: 160 CertyIQ
Which practice has a purpose that includes managing risks relating to confidentiality, integrity and availability?
A.Change enablement
B.Problem management
C.Information security management
D.Service configuration management
Answer: C
Explanation:
The correct answer is C. Information security management's primary purpose is to protect an organization's
information assets. This inherently includes managing risks related to confidentiality (preventing unauthorized
access to information), integrity (ensuring information is accurate and complete), and availability (ensuring
authorized users can access information when needed).
Change enablement focuses on managing changes to services and infrastructure. Problem management
addresses the root causes of incidents. Service configuration management manages the configuration items
required to deliver services. While these practices can indirectly contribute to security, they don't have the
direct and explicit focus on managing risks to confidentiality, integrity, and availability that information
security management does. Information security management encompasses processes and technologies
designed specifically to safeguard data and systems against unauthorized access, use, disclosure, disruption,
modification, or destruction. It is thus the practice most directly responsible for addressing risks related to the
core tenets of data security.

Authoritative source:
AXELOS. ITIL Foundation: ITIL 4 Edition.
Question: 161 CertyIQ
Which statement about value creating activities is CORRECT?
A.Each value stream should be designed with a specific combination of service value chain activities
B.Service value chain activities have pre-determined dependencies on ITIL practices
C.A value stream is an operating model for creating value through products and services
D.Organizations should ensure that each value stream is applicable to many scenarios
Answer: A
Explanation:
The correct answer is A because the ITIL 4 framework emphasizes that each value stream should be
intentionally designed to achieve a specific outcome. This design process involves carefully selecting and
sequencing the service value chain activities (Plan, Improve, Engage, Design & Transition, Obtain/Build, and
Deliver & Support) that are most relevant to creating that specific value. Different products, services, or
customer segments will likely require different combinations of these activities to optimize value creation.
Option B is incorrect. While ITIL practices support the service value chain activities, there aren't strict,
predetermined dependencies. Practices can be used flexibly across different activities as needed.
Option C is partially correct, but A is more accurate. A value stream is an operating model, but it's more than
just about products and services; it focuses on creating value.
Option D is incorrect. While efficiency is important, trying to make each value stream applicable to many
scenarios would likely lead to generic processes that don't effectively address specific needs and ultimately
reduce the value generated. The focus should be on tailoring value streams. The flexibility to tailor value
streams to specific needs is central to ITIL 4's focus on agility and customer-centricity. Customization allows
organizations to efficiently and effectively create value in a range of scenarios. Value streams are not meant
to be one-size-fits-all.
The key is that value streams should be targeted and adapted to specific value-creation situations.
For further information, refer to official ITIL 4 documentation and resources, such as the AXELOS website and
the ITIL 4 Foundation handbook.
Question: 162 CertyIQ
Which is provided by the 'engage' value chain activity?
A.Ensuring that stakeholder expectations for quality are met
B.Ensuring that stakeholder needs are understood by the organization
C.Ensuring that service components are available when needed
D.Ensuring that services are operated to meet agreed specifications
Answer: B
Explanation:

The 'engage' value chain activity in ITIL 4 focuses on interacting with stakeholders. Its primary objective is to
foster a strong understanding of stakeholder needs and demands. By actively engaging with stakeholders,
organizations can gather crucial feedback and insights. This information helps shape service offerings and
ensures they align with expectations. Options A, C, and D relate to other value chain activities: 'deliver &
support', 'design & transition', and 'obtain/build' respectively.
The 'engage' activity isn't directly responsible for meeting quality expectations, ensuring service component
availability, or operating services to meet agreed specifications. While 'engage' can contribute indirectly to
these aspects through feedback and requirement gathering, its core function is understanding and managing
stakeholder relationships. This understanding is fundamental for delivering value. It enables the organization
to tailor its services and communication to better serve its stakeholders. A deep understanding of stakeholder
needs facilitates effective communication and collaboration throughout the service value system. This
ensures that stakeholders are kept informed and involved in relevant service management activities. This
proactive approach enhances satisfaction and builds trust between the organization and its stakeholders.
Therefore, the correct answer is B because the 'engage' value chain activity directly provides the organization
with the knowledge needed to understand stakeholder needs.
For further research, consult the official ITIL 4 Foundation materials and publications.You can find more
information on the AXELOS website: https://www.axelos.com/Also, consider reading the ITIL 4 Foundation:
Study Guide.
Question: 163 CertyIQ
Which is part of the 'focus on value' guiding principle?
A.Understanding what services help the service consumer
B.Reducing the number of steps in the customer experience
C.Assessing services to identify parts that can be reused
D.Identifying activities that can be achieved in smaller iterations
Answer: A
Explanation:
The correct answer is A, understanding what services help the service consumer, because the 'focus on value'
guiding principle is fundamentally about understanding and prioritizing what the customer perceives as
valuable. This principle emphasizes that all activities within the service value system should directly or
indirectly contribute to delivering value to the stakeholders, primarily the service consumer. Understanding
their needs, expectations, and priorities is critical.
Option A directly aligns with this by highlighting the need to comprehend how specific services address the
consumer's requirements and provide tangible benefits. It necessitates a deep understanding of the
consumer's business objectives and how the IT services contribute to achieving those objectives. Therefore,
any activity that enhances the comprehension of the service consumer's needs and preferences reinforces the
'focus on value' principle.
Option B (Reducing the number of steps in the customer experience) is more closely related to the "optimize
and automate" principle, although it might indirectly contribute to value. Option C (Assessing services to
identify parts that can be reused) aligns more with the "progress iteratively with feedback" or the "keep it
simple and practical" principle, as reuse promotes efficiency and resource optimization. Option D (Identifying
activities that can be achieved in smaller iterations) is a key aspect of "progress iteratively with feedback."
In contrast, 'focus on value' starts and ends with value. Other principles are tools that help achieve that value.

Therefore, simply reducing steps or identifying reusable components, without understanding the consumer's
specific needs and how they translate into delivered value, misses the point of 'focus on value.' Understanding
the customer's definition of value is paramount.For further research, refer to the official AXELOS ITIL 4
Foundation guidance: https://www.axelos.com/
Question: 164 CertyIQ
Which is part of the definition of a customer?
A.The role that defines the requirements for a service
B.A means of enabling value co-creation
C.The role that authorizes budget for service consumption
D.A set of specialized organizational capabilities for enabling value
Answer: A
Explanation:
The correct answer is A, "The role that defines the requirements for a service." This choice aligns with the ITIL
4 definition of a customer as the entity that defines and agrees upon the service requirements and outcomes.
Customers specify what they need from a service, essentially driving the service design and operation to meet
their specific business objectives.
Option B is incorrect because "a means of enabling value co-creation" refers to the service itself, not the
customer. A service is what allows the provider and consumer to work together to create value. Option C is
incorrect because the role that authorizes the budget for service consumption is typically a sponsor or
financial stakeholder, which might be a subset of the customer organization but isn't the defining
characteristic of being the customer. Option D is incorrect because "a set of specialized organizational
capabilities for enabling value" describes a service provider's capabilities, not the customer's role.
In ITIL 4, the customer is central to value creation. Understanding their needs is crucial for delivering effective
services. The customer isn't just a recipient; they are active participants in shaping the service and its
outcomes. They articulate the desired outcomes, which then informs the service provider on how best to
deliver value. This directly influences service level agreements (SLAs) and overall service design. Therefore,
the customer's role in defining service requirements is fundamental to their definition within the ITIL
framework. Their input is critical throughout the service lifecycle, from initial design to ongoing improvement.

Question: 165 CertyIQ
Which guiding principle helps an organization to understand the impact of an altered element on other elements in
a system?
A.Focus on value

B.Start where you are
C.Think and work holistically
D.Keep it simple and practical
Answer: C
Explanation:
The correct answer is C. Think and work holistically. This guiding principle emphasizes understanding how
different parts of an organization, its systems, and its processes are interconnected. It's about seeing the
bigger picture rather than focusing solely on individual components. When an element is altered, a holistic
approach prompts consideration of its ripple effects across the entire system.
Here's why this aligns with the question: Holistic thinking ensures an organization doesn't inadvertently
create unintended consequences by changing one aspect without understanding its dependencies. It
encourages a systems-thinking approach. For example, in a cloud environment, changing a network
configuration might impact the performance of several applications. A holistic view would identify these
dependencies beforehand.
A. Focus on value is important, but it primarily deals with ensuring activities contribute to desired outcomes
and doesn't directly address understanding interconnectedness.
B. Start where you are emphasizes leveraging existing resources and knowledge before creating new ones
but is irrelevant to understanding system dependencies.
D. Keep it simple and practical promotes efficiency and avoiding unnecessary complexity, but doesn't
specifically address understanding interconnected system impacts.
Therefore, "Think and work holistically" is the most fitting principle because it explicitly encourages
examining how changes in one area affect other connected areas, enabling a more informed and responsible
approach to IT service management. It ensures that alterations are assessed within the broader context of the
system, allowing organizations to anticipate and mitigate potential negative impacts while optimizing overall
performance. Without this principle, changes could lead to unexpected outages, performance degradation,
and increased costs, ultimately hindering value creation.
Supporting Links:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Guiding Principles (Official ITIL source explaining the principles)
ITIL Foundation Handbook (Comprehensive guide to ITIL 4 Foundation, requires purchase)
Question: 166 CertyIQ
Which ITIL practice has the purpose to establish and nurture the links between the organization and its
stakeholders at strategic and tactical levels?
A.Supplier management
B.Change enablement
C.Relationship management
D.Service desk
Answer: C
Explanation:
The correct answer is C, Relationship management. This practice focuses specifically on building and
maintaining strong, mutually beneficial relationships between the organization and its stakeholders. These

relationships are essential for understanding stakeholder needs, managing expectations, fostering
collaboration, and ensuring that the organization's services and offerings align with stakeholder
requirements. This happens at both a strategic level, influencing overall business direction, and a tactical
level, supporting day-to-day operations.
Supplier management, while dealing with a subset of stakeholders (suppliers), primarily concentrates on
ensuring suppliers meet their contractual obligations and provide value. It does not encompass the breadth of
relationships covered by relationship management. Change enablement is about managing changes to
services and systems to minimize disruption and risk, and the service desk is the single point of contact for
users needing support. Neither of these practices has the explicit, overarching goal of nurturing strategic and
tactical connections across the full spectrum of organizational stakeholders.
Relationship management seeks to understand each stakeholder's strategic goals and how the organization
can support them. Good relationship management can lead to increased customer satisfaction, better
alignment of IT services with business needs, improved communication, and a greater sense of partnership. It
involves proactively engaging with stakeholders, gathering feedback, and addressing concerns. Effective
relationship management can drive value creation and business outcomes. This encompasses understanding
stakeholder expectations, negotiating service level agreements, and resolving conflicts. It goes beyond
simple transactions to build lasting partnerships.
Relevant link for further research:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation: https://www.axelos.com/certifications/itil-certifications (This is a general link;
specific page for the practice may require searching within the AXELOS site)
Question: 167 CertyIQ
What is the purpose of the 'deployment management' practice?
A.To make new and changed services and features available for use
B.To move new or changed components to live environments
C.To plan and manage the full lifecycle of all IT assets
D.To protect the information needed by the organization to conduct its business
Answer: B
Explanation:
The correct answer is B. To move new or changed components to live environments. Let's break down why.
Deployment Management is specifically concerned with the logistical aspects of transferring new or updated
IT components, like software applications, infrastructure updates, or hardware configurations, from
development or testing environments into the production or "live" environments where users and customers
can access and utilize them. Its focus is on the physical implementation and transition of these changes.
Option A is broader than deployment. Making services available for use is a desired outcome of deployment,
but deployment itself is the means to that end. Option A encapsulates more than just the physical movement.
Option C, asset management, is about tracking and managing IT assets throughout their entire lifecycle –
procurement, usage, maintenance, and disposal. While deployment might involve updating or replacing
assets, the practice itself is not focused on the full lifecycle.
Option D, information security management, centers on protecting organizational data and information
systems. While deployment should be done securely, security is not the primary purpose of the deployment
management practice.

Deployment Management involves activities like planning the deployment strategy (big bang vs. phased),
coordinating with different teams (development, testing, operations), executing the deployment process, and
verifying the deployment's success. A successful deployment aims for minimal disruption and rapid recovery
if issues arise. This can involve using automated deployment tools, infrastructure-as-code principles, and
continuous integration/continuous delivery (CI/CD) pipelines. The practice aims to ensure changes are
implemented effectively, efficiently, and safely. In cloud environments, deployment management is crucial for
scaling resources, implementing updates, and ensuring high availability. Cloud-native technologies like
containers (Docker), orchestration platforms (Kubernetes), and cloud-specific deployment services (e.g., AWS
CodeDeploy, Azure DevOps, Google Cloud Deploy) are often used to streamline deployment processes. The
goal is a stable and reliable live environment for users.
For more information, refer to resources on ITIL 4 practices and specifically search for "Deployment
Management" or "Deployment Automation" examples within ITIL frameworks. You can also explore
documentation from cloud providers on their deployment services.
Question: 168 CertyIQ
Which TWO statements about the guiding principles are CORRECT?
1. The guiding principles support continual improvement
2. Each guiding principle applies to a selection of the available stakeholder groups
3. Organizations should decide which one of the guiding principles is relevant to them
4. Organizations should consider how the guiding principles interact with each other
A.1 and 2
B.2 and 3
C.3 and 4
D.1 and 4
Answer: D
Explanation:
Here's a detailed justification for why the answer is D (1 and 4) for the ITIL 4 Foundation question, along with
supporting information and links:
Justification:
The ITIL 4 guiding principles are a set of recommendations that can help an organization adopt and adapt IT
service management. They are not prescriptive but rather adaptable suggestions that can be applied across a
variety of circumstances.
Statement 1: The guiding principles support continual improvement: This is correct. The guiding principles
are designed to encourage a culture of continual improvement. For example, the "Progress Iteratively with
Feedback" principle directly promotes making iterative changes based on ongoing feedback, which is central
to continuous improvement initiatives. All guiding principles can influence and support improvement
initiatives by providing a consistent approach.
Statement 2: Each guiding principle applies to a selection of the available stakeholder groups: This is
incorrect. The guiding principles are designed to be universally applicable across all stakeholder groups. They
aren't limited to certain audiences but should inform decisions and actions affecting everyone involved.
Statement 3: Organizations should decide which one of the guiding principles is relevant to them: This is
incorrect. All the guiding principles are relevant and should be considered. While organizations can prioritize
certain principles based on their specific context and current needs, they shouldn't outright dismiss any of

them. Ignoring a principle could lead to missed opportunities for improvement or suboptimal outcomes.
Statement 4: Organizations should consider how the guiding principles interact with each other: This is
correct. The guiding principles are interconnected and work best when applied holistically. They aren't meant
to be used in isolation. Considering how they interact ensures a more comprehensive and effective approach
to service management. For instance, "Focus on Value" informs how you apply "Start Where You Are," making
sure you are building upon the existing services and strategies that are working and align with user value.
Similarly, “Collaborate and Promote Visibility” helps to effectively execute “Keep it Simple and Practical”.
Therefore, statements 1 and 4 are correct, making D the correct answer.
Supporting Resources:
Axelos ITIL 4 Foundation Publication: This is the primary source for ITIL 4 information. While access requires
purchase, it provides the most comprehensive details on the guiding principles.
AXELOS Website: https://www.axelos.com/ - Provides information on ITIL certifications and best practices.
Look for details about ITIL 4 and its core concepts.
Various ITIL 4 Blogs and Articles: Search for "ITIL 4 Guiding Principles" to find numerous articles and blog
posts that explain the principles in detail and provide examples of how they can be applied. Example search
phrase: ITIL 4 Guiding Principles Example.
Question: 169 CertyIQ
Which is an activity of 'problem identification'?
A.Analyzing information from software developers
B.Establishing problem workarounds
C.Analyzing the cause of problems
D.Establishing potential permanent solutions
Answer: A
Explanation:
The correct answer is A. Analyzing information from software developers. Here's why:
Problem identification is the initial step in problem management within ITIL 4. It focuses on detecting and
classifying problems. Analyzing information from software developers directly relates to this identification
phase because developers are often the first to notice anomalies, code errors, or system behaviors that
indicate an underlying problem. Their insights provide valuable input for recognizing potential issues.
Options B, C, and D relate to later stages in the problem management process. Establishing workarounds (B) is
about mitigating the impact of a known problem, not identifying it. Analyzing the cause of problems (C) falls
under problem control or problem analysis after a problem has been identified and recorded. Establishing
permanent solutions (D) is a final step in problem management, coming after cause analysis and resolution. It
involves correcting the root cause to prevent recurrence.
Problem identification relies heavily on data gathering and analysis from various sources. Software
developers represent one crucial source, providing technical perspectives essential for pinpointing the
existence of a problem. Early detection and accurate classification during problem identification are crucial to
streamline subsequent steps and minimize the impact of incidents. Therefore, collecting and analyzing
information from software developers is a core activity in 'problem identification.'
Consider these aspects related to cloud environments:

Agile & DevOps culture: Software developers in cloud environments usually deploy updates very rapidly. As
such, the first indications of a problem are usually noticed by the developers.
Microservices architectures: Cloud applications are often deployed in microservices architectures, which
leads to complicated interactions between components. Collecting information from developers regarding
inter-component communication is key to identify problems.
Monitoring tools: Developers use monitoring tools in cloud environments to check for the health of
applications. Problem identification can often start from monitoring tool alerts.
Authoritative links for further research:
ITIL 4 Foundation: ITIL 4 Foundation Study Guide by Claire Agutter: This book is a popular choice for people
looking to get the ITIL 4 Foundation Certification
Axelos ITIL 4 Website: https://www.axelos.com/itil (Official source for ITIL information)
Question: 170 CertyIQ
Which practice uses technologies such as intelligent telephony systems, a knowledge base and monitoring tools?
A.Service configuration management
B.Service desk
C.Problem management
D.Deployment management
Answer: B
Explanation:
The correct answer is B, Service Desk. The Service Desk practice is specifically designed to be the single point
of contact between the service provider and users. It utilizes various technologies to efficiently manage
incidents and service requests.
Intelligent telephony systems (like Interactive Voice Response or IVR) enable automated call routing and
initial issue assessment, streamlining the contact process. A comprehensive knowledge base provides agents
with readily available solutions and information to resolve common issues quickly, promoting faster resolution
times and reducing escalations. Monitoring tools allow the Service Desk to proactively detect and address
potential service disruptions, improving overall service availability and user experience. These tools provide
real-time insights into the health of IT systems, helping the Service Desk anticipate problems before they
impact users.
Service Configuration Management focuses on maintaining information about the configuration items
required to deliver services, not direct user interaction. Problem Management aims to identify the root causes
of incidents and prevent their recurrence, operating further upstream from the user interaction point.
Deployment Management handles the release and deployment of new or changed services, a process distinct
from daily user support. While these other practices are crucial to IT service management, they do not
typically use the specific combination of intelligent telephony, knowledge base, and monitoring tools in the
direct service context of a service desk. The Service Desk practice emphasizes user-centric support and
leverages technology to enhance its efficiency in providing that support.
For further research, refer to the ITIL 4 Foundation guidance and resources:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Handbook: https://www.axelos.com/ (Official source, may require purchase)
Official ITIL 4 publications on reputable online bookstores.

Question: 171 CertyIQ
Which statement about standard changes is CORRECT?
A.A full assessment should be completed each time the change is implemented
B.The change can be implemented with less testing if necessary
C.The appropriate change authority should be assigned to each type of change
D.The change does not require additional authorization
Answer: D
Explanation:
The correct answer is D, "The change does not require additional authorization." Let's examine why the other
options are incorrect and then solidify why D is the correct choice.
Option A is incorrect because standard changes, by their very nature, are pre-authorized. A full assessment
should be completed before they are classified as standard changes, not each time they are implemented.
The point of standardization is to avoid repetitive, time-consuming analysis for each execution.
Option B is incorrect because testing is a crucial part of change management, even for standard changes.
While the scope of testing might be reduced compared to more complex changes, skipping testing entirely is
generally a bad practice and introduces unnecessary risk. Adequate testing verifies the standard change's
continued effectiveness and identifies potential issues early.
Option C is inaccurate. While change authorities exist and are important for overall change management,
standard changes don't typically require assigning a specific change authority each time they're executed.
Their pre-approval means the decision-making is already complete; it's more about following the documented
procedure.
Option D is correct because standard changes are pre-approved. A standard change is a low-risk, well-
understood change with a documented procedure that has been pre-authorized. This pre-authorization
removes the need for individual approval each time the change is requested and implemented. The ITIL 4
Foundation guidance emphasizes streamlining processes where appropriate, and standard changes are a
prime example of this. The risk and impact have been previously assessed and accepted, and the change can
be executed without needing further authorization. This speeds up the change implementation process and
frees up resources to focus on more complex and risky changes. The pre-authorization is based on a thorough
initial risk assessment, defined procedures, and successful prior implementations. It aims to improve
efficiency and reduce potential disruptions. Essentially, a standard change is treated as a routine operation,
not requiring special permission each time.For further research:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Book: The official source for ITIL 4 guidance.
ITIL 4 Foundation Exam Syllabus: Provides a detailed outline of the topics covered in the ITIL 4 Foundation
exam, including change management and standard changes.
Question: 172 CertyIQ
Which TWO are considered part of the 'organizations and people' dimension of service management?
1. Systems of authority
2. Culture
3. Relationships between organizations
4. Workflows
A.1 and 2
B.2 and 3

C.3 and 4
D.1 and 4
Answer: A
Explanation:
The correct answer is A because 'Organizations and People' within the Four Dimensions Model of Service
Management specifically encompasses aspects related to the human element and structural frameworks
within an organization.
'Culture' is a crucial component as it dictates how people interact, collaborate, and behave within the
organization. It shapes the attitudes, values, and beliefs that influence service delivery and improvement. A
healthy service management culture promotes collaboration, innovation, and a customer-centric approach.
'Systems of authority' determine the roles, responsibilities, and reporting lines within the organization. They
establish clear decision-making processes and accountability, ensuring efficient and effective service
delivery. Well-defined authorities enable proper resource allocation and prevent confusion or delays.
'Relationships between organizations' fall under the 'Partners and Suppliers' dimension, as this dimension
deals with external entities involved in service value streams. This includes contracts, service level
agreements, and supplier management.
'Workflows' are more aligned with the 'Information & Technology' dimension, focusing on the flow of data,
knowledge, and processes required to manage and deliver services. This also includes aspects like
automation and tooling.
Therefore, culture and systems of authority are integral parts of defining the organizational structure and
human capital involved in service management. These elements directly affect how services are planned,
delivered, and supported, emphasizing the human and structural aspects within an organization.

detailed explanations)

Question: 173 CertyIQ
Which statement about the 'service request management' practice is CORRECT?
A.Service requests are fulfilled using simple workflows
B.A new workflow is created for each type of request
C.Additional approval is sometimes needed for restoration of service
D.Financial authorization is sometimes required for service requests
Answer: D
Explanation:
Here's a detailed justification for why option D is the most accurate statement about the 'service request
management' practice within the ITIL 4 framework, along with why the other options are less suitable:
The correct answer is D: Financial authorization is sometimes required for service requests. Service requests,

although usually standard and low-risk, can sometimes involve costs that necessitate financial approval.
Examples include requests for additional software licenses, upgraded hardware, or subscriptions to services.
Such requests impact the IT budget and need proper oversight to ensure cost-effectiveness and prevent
uncontrolled spending. This aligns with ITIL's emphasis on value creation and resource optimization.
Option A is incorrect because while service requests typically leverage simple workflows to ensure efficiency
and standardization, it's not always the case. Complex service requests, such as those involving multiple
departments or integrations, might necessitate more intricate workflows. The defining characteristic is pre-
approval and standardization, not inherent simplicity.
Option B is incorrect. Instead of creating a new workflow for each request, service request management aims
to establish standard, repeatable workflows for common request types. The goal is to streamline fulfillment,
not create unique processes for every instance.
Option C is incorrect. Additional approval is more typically associated with incident management, specifically
when restoring service requires changes or interventions that carry risks. Service requests are pre-approved
and low-risk, while incident management often necessitates ad-hoc approvals to quickly resolve service
disruptions.
In summary, service requests, while generally straightforward, can occasionally require financial authorization
due to associated costs, making option D the most accurate statement within the context of ITIL 4.

request management.
