certification.
Question: 174 CertyIQ
What is a cause, or potential cause, of one or more incidents?
A.A problem
B.A configuration item
C.A workaround
D.An incident
Answer: A
Explanation:
The correct answer, A (A problem), is the most accurate description of what the question asks. A problem, in
ITIL 4, is defined as a cause, or potential cause, of one or more incidents. The goal of problem management is
to identify and manage these underlying causes to prevent future incidents from occurring.
A configuration item (B) is a component that needs to be managed to deliver an IT service, and while a faulty
CI can cause an incident or be part of a problem, it isn't the definition of a cause. It's a thing that can be part of
the cause.
A workaround (C) is a temporary solution to reduce or eliminate the impact of an incident or problem, but it is
not the cause itself. It addresses the symptoms, not the root. Workarounds are implemented after an incident
or problem occurs, as a quick fix.

An incident (D) is an unplanned interruption to, or reduction in the quality of, an IT service. While incidents can
reveal problems, they are the effects, not the causes.
Problem management activities include problem identification, problem control, error control, and
workarounds. By managing problems, organizations can proactively reduce the number and impact of
incidents, improve service quality, and lower IT costs. Identifying the root cause of incidents is crucial for
preventing recurrence. Problem management actively searches for the root cause before incidents even
happen, identifying potential problems, making it the perfect fit for the definition.
Therefore, "A problem" is the most accurate and direct answer, representing the underlying cause or potential
cause of incidents. It is the raison d'etre for the problem management practices.
Authoritative link:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Syllabus: (Search for "ITIL 4 Foundation Syllabus PDF" - direct link may change)
This provides the official definitions and concepts.
Question: 175 CertyIQ
Which guiding principle says that it is not usually necessary to build something new?
A.Focus on value
B.Start where you are
C.Progress iteratively with feedback
D.Think and work holistically
Answer: B
Explanation:
The correct answer is B. Start where you are. This guiding principle emphasizes assessing the current state
and leveraging existing resources before embarking on new endeavors.
Here's a detailed justification:
The "Start where you are" principle advocates for a pragmatic approach. Rather than automatically assuming
that something needs to be completely rebuilt, it encourages organizations to thoroughly evaluate what's
already available. This includes examining existing processes, services, capabilities, and skills.
The principle recognizes that there's often valuable knowledge, experience, and infrastructure already in
place. Ignoring these existing assets can lead to wasted effort, duplicated costs, and unnecessary complexity.
For example, an organization considering moving to the cloud might already have on-premises servers or
existing applications. "Start where you are" suggests assessing whether these existing resources can be
migrated or adapted to the cloud environment before developing entirely new cloud-native solutions. Perhaps
a lift-and-shift approach is appropriate, or a phased migration plan.
Often, small improvements to existing systems can yield significant benefits without the disruption and
expense of a complete overhaul. This aligns with lean principles of continuous improvement.
This principle aligns with cloud computing best practices by encouraging efficient resource utilization and
minimizing unnecessary cloud spend. Cloud resources are pay-as-you-go, so avoiding redundant solutions can
translate into significant cost savings.
It is about understanding the current situation, and based on that, create a plan to achieve the desired future
state. It considers the risk and the cost of the current state as well as the constraints that the company might

have.
In contrast:
Focus on value: Emphasizes delivering tangible benefits to stakeholders.
Progress iteratively with feedback: Advocates for incremental improvements based on feedback loops.
Think and work holistically: Encourages a systemic view of the organization and its processes.
While these other principles are important, they do not directly address the concept of leveraging existing
resources before building new ones. "Start where you are" explicitly highlights the importance of assessing
and utilizing what already exists, making it the most appropriate answer.
Therefore, the "Start where you are" guiding principle is the most fitting response because it directly
promotes the idea that building something new is often unnecessary if existing resources can be adapted or
improved.
Authoritative Links:
Axelos ITIL 4 Foundation Handbook.
Official ITIL 4 Foundation certification training materials.
Question: 176 CertyIQ
Which practice includes management of workarounds and known errors?
A.Monitoring and event management
B.Service configuration management
C.Problem management
D.Incident management
Answer: C
Explanation:
The correct answer is C, Problem Management. Here's why:
Problem management focuses on identifying the underlying causes of incidents to prevent future
occurrences. This proactive approach includes the crucial tasks of managing workarounds and known errors.
A workaround provides a temporary solution to reduce or eliminate the impact of an incident or problem, while
a known error is a problem that has been diagnosed but not yet resolved. The problem management practice
actively documents these workarounds and known errors, ensuring this knowledge is available and accessible
to those handling incidents.
Option A, Monitoring and Event Management, focuses on observing services and identifying events, but it
doesn't actively manage workarounds or known errors. Monitoring detects the symptoms, but problem
management addresses the cause.
Option B, Service Configuration Management, is about maintaining information about IT assets and their
relationships. While configuration data can be useful in problem analysis, this practice doesn't directly
manage workarounds or known errors.
Option D, Incident Management, concentrates on restoring service quickly after an incident. While incident
management uses workarounds, it doesn't manage them; the responsibility for managing and documenting
workarounds lies with problem management. Incident management addresses symptoms, while problem
management investigates and fixes causes.

In essence, problem management is the practice explicitly tasked with reducing the likelihood and impact of
incidents by proactively addressing the root causes. It's the central hub for documenting and tracking
workarounds and known errors, making it the most appropriate answer.

ITIL 4 concepts.

best-practices/ (Provides practical insight into Problem Management)
Question: 177 CertyIQ
Which activity is part of the 'continual improvement' practice?
A.Handling compliments and complaints from users to identify improvements
B.Improving relationships with and between stakeholders
C.Prioritizing and creating business cases for improvement initiatives
D.Identifying the cause of unplanned interruptions to service
Answer: C
Explanation:
The correct answer, C, "Prioritizing and creating business cases for improvement initiatives," is directly
aligned with the core purpose of the Continual Improvement (CI) practice within ITIL 4. The CI practice
revolves around regularly assessing services, practices, and overall IT management to identify opportunities
for enhancement and then implementing those improvements. Prioritization is essential because resources
(time, budget, personnel) are always finite. A business case justifies the investment of these resources by
outlining the expected benefits of the improvement. This ensures that improvements are aligned with
organizational goals and provide a return on investment. It's not merely about identifying possible
improvements, but about actively deciding which improvements will create the most value.
Option A, "Handling compliments and complaints from users to identify improvements," represents valuable
input into the CI practice. User feedback is an important source of improvement ideas. However, simply
collecting the feedback is not the complete CI activity. The CI activity acts upon feedback by processing,
prioritizing and implementing it.
Option B, "Improving relationships with and between stakeholders," is relevant to various ITIL 4 practices,
including Relationship Management. Strong stakeholder relationships can certainly facilitate continual
improvement, but it is not the primary activity of the CI practice itself.
Option D, "Identifying the cause of unplanned interruptions to service," is more closely related to the Incident
Management or Problem Management practices. While root cause analysis of incidents can lead to
improvements, the specific activity of identifying the cause is more directly associated with restoring services
and preventing future incidents rather than the broader, strategic approach of CI.
In summary, Continual Improvement is about systematically identifying, prioritizing, and implementing
improvements to services and practices. Creating business cases is a critical part of prioritizing and justifying
these improvements, ensuring that improvement efforts are focused on the most valuable opportunities. The
continual improvement model prioritizes initiatives based on their potential value, feasibility, and alignment
with strategic objectives.
Supporting resources:

AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation: ITIL 4 Edition: This is the official source for ITIL 4 guidance and defines the core
concepts of the Continual Improvement practice.
Official ITIL Website: https://www.axelos.com/ - Provides access to ITIL publications, training, and
certifications. Searching for "Continual Improvement" on this site will offer detailed insights.
Question: 178 CertyIQ
Identify the missing word in the following sentence:
A service is a means of enabling value co-creation by facilitating [?] that customers want to achieve, without the
customer having to manage specific costs and risks.
A.utility
B.warranty
C.outcomes
D.outputs
Answer: C
Explanation:
The correct answer is C. outcomes because the ITIL 4 definition of a service revolves around enabling value
co-creation by helping customers achieve desired results or outcomes. ITIL 4 emphasizes a customer-centric
approach where services are designed to directly contribute to the customer's objectives. The definition
explicitly states that a service facilitates what customers want to achieve, which directly aligns with the
concept of outcomes. Utility and warranty are related but distinct concepts. Utility refers to the functionality
offered by a service (i.e., "fit for purpose"), and warranty refers to the assurance that a service will be
available and reliable (i.e., "fit for use"). While both contribute to value, they don't represent the overarching
reason for a service's existence, which is to deliver a desired outcome. Outputs, on the other hand, are simply
the tangible deliverables of a service. They are inputs to the customer's activities that help achieve outcomes.
Focusing on outputs alone ignores the larger goal of what the customer is trying to accomplish, while
outcomes encompass the ultimate goals and benefits derived from the service. The service should facilitate
the achievement of specific results, thus, the word needed in the blank is outcomes. The value co-creation
aspect of ITIL 4 further reinforces the importance of outcomes, as the service provider and the customer work
together to achieve mutually beneficial results.
For further information, refer to the official Axelos ITIL 4 Foundation syllabus and publications. Unfortunately,
direct URLs to specific pages are not provided due to their paywalled nature. Searching for "ITIL 4 Foundation
definition of service" or "ITIL 4 value co-creation" will yield numerous reliable resources.
Question: 179 CertyIQ
Which is a low risk change that has been pre-approved so that no additional authorization is needed?
A.A standard change
B.A change model
C.An emergency change
D.A normal change
Answer: A

Explanation:
The correct answer is A. A standard change. Here's why:
A standard change in ITIL 4 is defined as a pre-authorized change that is well-understood, low-risk, and
follows a documented procedure or work instruction. Because the risk is low and the steps are clearly defined,
these changes don't require additional approval beyond the initial design and authorization of the change
process itself. The purpose is to improve efficiency and speed of delivery for common requests.
Change Models (B) are templates outlining steps for handling changes, but they don't pre-approve specific
changes. They define the process to be followed for different types of changes, including how authorization
would work.
Emergency changes (C) are changes addressed to restore services that are suffering an outage, or prevent a
disaster that has an imminent chance of occurring. These changes might need expedited approval from the
change authority.
Normal changes (D) require a full change management process, including risk assessment, planning, testing,
and approval, which is not relevant to the given definition of low risk and pre-approved changes.
Standard changes leverage automation and established procedures to minimize disruption. They're often used
for common service requests, like password resets, software installations, or server restarts, that are well-
defined and unlikely to cause problems. By pre-authorizing them, organizations can focus change
management efforts on higher-risk changes that require more scrutiny. In effect, this reduces the change
management overhead.
Here are some authoritative links for further research:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Syllabus: This syllabus outlines the core concepts of ITIL 4, including change
management and the definition of standard changes. While not directly accessible online without course
enrollment, it's the fundamental source for ITIL 4 knowledge.
Official ITIL 4 Publications: AXELOS provides official books for ITIL 4, including the "ITIL Foundation: ITIL 4
Edition" book.
ServiceNow Documentation on Change Management: (ServiceNow is a leading ITSM platform that
implements ITIL principles) https://www.servicenow.com/ (Search their documentation for "Standard
Change").
BMC Blogs on ITIL Change Management: (BMC is another major ITSM vendor)
https://www.bmc.com/blogs/itil-change-management/
These resources provide a comprehensive understanding of standard changes within the ITIL 4 framework.
Question: 180 CertyIQ
Which describes the 'plan' value chain activity?
A.It ensures a shared understanding of the current status and vision for all products and services across the
organization
B.It ensures that services are delivered and supported according to agreed specifications and stakeholders'
expectations
C.It ensures that service components are available when and where they are needed, and meet agreed
specifications
D.It ensures continual improvement of products, services, and practices across all value chain activities
Answer: A
Explanation:

The 'plan' value chain activity in ITIL 4 focuses on strategic alignment and direction. The correct answer,
stating it "ensures a shared understanding of the current status and vision for all products and services
across the organization," directly reflects this core function. 'Plan' isn't about delivering services (that's
'deliver & support'), acquiring components ('obtain/build'), or continual improvement as the primary focus
(that's actually all activities). Its fundamental role is to create a strategic roadmap.
Option A highlights the 'Plan' activity's crucial responsibility for creating a shared understanding and
strategic direction. It aligns the organization towards a common goal regarding its products and services. This
involves assessing the current state, defining a vision, and establishing strategies to bridge the gap. It's about
organizational strategy and portfolio management.
Option B describes elements primarily associated with the 'deliver and support' value chain activity. Option C
aligns more with 'obtain/build'. Option D touches upon continual improvement, which is an embedded aspect
of all the value chain activities rather than being exclusively linked to "Plan". The 'Plan' value chain activity
includes defining the overall strategy, establishing policies and procedures, and allocating resources to
achieve organizational objectives. 'Plan' establishes strategic direction, guiding development, delivery, and
improvement efforts and ensuring alignment.
This involves understanding business needs and translating them into actionable plans. It's essential for
effective governance and ensures all activities contribute towards shared objectives. By creating a clear
vision and strategy, the 'Plan' value chain activity enables organizations to proactively respond to changing
market conditions and evolving customer demands. Essentially, 'Plan' sets the stage for all other value chain
activities to function effectively. It's about creating the strategic blueprint.
For further research, refer to the official ITIL 4 Foundation guidance and resources, available through Axelos.
(https://www.axelos.com/itil) and other ITIL accredited sources.
The correct answer explicitly addresses the core purpose of planning, ensuring everyone is on the same page
and working toward a common goal.
Question: 181 CertyIQ
Which phase of problem management includes analyzing incidents to look for patterns and trends?
A.Problem identification
B.Problem control
C.Error control
D.Post-implementation review
Answer: A
Explanation:
The correct answer is A, Problem Identification. Problem Management aims to prevent incidents and minimize
their impact when they occur. This process encompasses several phases, each with distinct objectives.
Problem Identification is specifically focused on detecting and logging problems. A core activity during this
phase involves proactively analyzing existing incidents and related data, such as incident reports, service
desk logs, and even monitoring alerts, to uncover recurring patterns and trends. These patterns might reveal
underlying issues causing multiple incidents. The goal is to identify potential problems before they cause
significant disruption or impact. Root cause analysis may be initiated, albeit preliminary, to get a sense of
potential underlying issues contributing to recurring incidents.
Problem Control focuses on managing known problems, including finding workarounds and documenting

solutions. Error Control deals with managing known errors, which are problems with known root causes but
unresolved solutions. Post-Implementation Review takes place after a solution has been implemented to
assess its effectiveness and identify areas for improvement, not for initial pattern identification. Therefore,
while Problem Control, Error Control and Post-Implementation Review are all important components of
problem management, they do not primarily focus on the identification of problems through pattern analysis
of incidents. Instead, pattern analysis and trend spotting are primarily associated with the Problem
Identification phase, as this is when the problem is initially discovered and recorded based on observed
incident patterns.
Authoritative links:
Axelos ITIL 4 Foundation Study Guide
https://www.bmc.com/blogs/itil-problem-management/
Question: 182 CertyIQ
Which statement about the 'optimize and automate' guiding principle is CORRECT?
A.Activities should be automated before they are optimized
B.Automation is best applied to non-standard tasks
C.Technology eliminates the need for human intervention
D.Automation frees human resources for more complex activities
Answer: D
Explanation:
The correct answer is D: Automation frees human resources for more complex activities. The 'optimize and
automate' guiding principle in ITIL 4 focuses on improving efficiency and effectiveness. Before automating,
processes should be optimized to ensure automation is applied to a well-understood and efficient process.
Option A is incorrect because optimization should precede automation. Automating a flawed process simply
automates the flaws. Option B is incorrect because automation is most beneficial when applied to
standardized, repeatable tasks. Automating non-standard tasks is often complex and less efficient. Option C
is incorrect because even with automation, human oversight and intervention are often still required for
complex situations, exceptions, and maintenance.
Answer D aligns with the core intention of the principle. Automation aims to reduce manual effort in repetitive
tasks, freeing up human resources to concentrate on more complex problem-solving, strategy, innovation, and
areas where human judgment is crucial. This leads to increased productivity and improved service quality. By
removing human involvement from repetitive tasks, it also reduces the chance for human error. This approach
also allows resources to be allocated to more strategic tasks that can bring higher value. In cloud computing
for example, automation allows for scaling and management of resources without constant human
intervention.
For further research, consider these resources:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Study Guide: This provides a comprehensive overview of the ITIL 4 framework,
including the guiding principles.
Official ITIL 4 Publications: The official AXELOS publications are the definitive source for ITIL 4 guidance.
The ITIL 4 guiding principles: https://www.axelos.com/news/blogs/may-2019/itil-4-guiding-principles

Question: 183 CertyIQ
What is defined as any financially valuable component that can contribute to the delivery of a service?
A.Configuration item
B.Product
C.IT asset
D.Event
Answer: C
Explanation:
The correct answer is C, IT asset. An IT asset, according to ITIL 4, encompasses any component or resource
that holds financial value and contributes to the delivery of IT services. This aligns directly with the question's
definition. IT assets can be tangible (hardware, software) or intangible (intellectual property, virtual machines
in a cloud environment), and their value lies in their ability to facilitate service provision.
A configuration item (CI), while related, is a broader term. It represents any component that needs to be
managed to deliver an IT service. While an IT asset can be a CI, not all CIs are necessarily financially valuable.
For example, documentation or a specific software build script might be CIs but might not have direct
financial value as an asset.
A product is a broader offering – typically a bundle of services and/or goods designed to satisfy a specific
consumer need. While IT assets are used to create products and services, the product itself is not the
component being described as financially valuable. The product uses IT assets.
An event is a change of state that has significance for the management of a configuration item or IT service.
Events can indicate normal operation, warnings, or exceptions. It's a signal, not a component of service
delivery.
Therefore, 'IT asset' is the most precise term to describe a financially valuable component used in service
delivery, as defined by ITIL 4. In cloud computing, this might include virtual servers, storage volumes, or
cloud-based applications, all of which have inherent costs and contribute directly to the services offered by
the cloud provider. Properly managing IT assets in a cloud environment is crucial for cost optimization and
ensuring reliable service delivery. The accurate identification and management of IT assets are key to
implementing effective IT service management practices.
Authoritative links for further research:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Syllabus: (https://www.axelos.com/) (This is the official source for ITIL definitions,
though a paid license or training course is typically needed to access the full syllabus. Look for reputable ITIL
training providers.)
HDI (Help Desk Institute) Articles on IT Asset Management: (https://www.thinkhdi.com/) (HDI provides
resources on IT service management, often touching on IT asset management best practices) (Search their
site for "IT Asset Management")
Question: 184 CertyIQ
Which MOST helps an organization adapt ITIL concepts so that they apply to the organization's specific
circumstances?
A.Continual improvement
B.Service value chain
C.Practices

D.Guiding principles
Answer: D
Explanation:
The correct answer is D. Guiding Principles.
The ITIL 4 guiding principles are designed to help organizations adopt and adapt ITIL concepts in a flexible
way that is relevant and suitable to their specific needs and organizational context. They provide universal and
enduring guidance, irrespective of changes in goals, strategies, type of work, or management structure. The
principles guide decisions and actions, ensuring a consistent and holistic approach to service management.
Let's analyze why the other options are less suitable:
A. Continual Improvement: While crucial for any organization, it is a process and an outcome rather than a set
of adaptable principles that dictate how to approach tailoring ITIL. Continual improvement relies on having the
right principles guiding its direction.
B. Service Value Chain: The service value chain describes activities to create, deliver, and improve services. It
shows how value is created but doesn't offer the overarching guidelines for why and what to adapt within ITIL
based on unique organizational contexts.
The ITIL 4 guiding principles, such as "Focus on value," "Start where you are," "Progress iteratively with
feedback," "Collaborate and promote visibility," "Think and work holistically," "Keep it simple and practical,"
and "Optimize and automate," actively encourage organizations to tailor ITIL practices and processes to their
specific environment. These principles help organizations to avoid rigid adherence to a prescribed framework
and instead focus on the most effective ways to deliver value in their own situation. The guiding principles
provide a compass for making decisions about how to use ITIL in a way that is most beneficial for the
organization.
Therefore, the guiding principles are the MOST helpful in adapting ITIL concepts to the specific
circumstances of an organization.
Authoritative Links:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Guiding Principles: https://www.axelos.com/ (Search within the site)
Official ITIL 4 Foundation Study Guide.
Question: 185 CertyIQ
What is the MAIN benefit of 'problem management'?
A.Restoring normal service as quickly as possible
B.Reducing the number and impact of incidents
C.Maximizing the number of successful changes
D.Managing workarounds and known errors
Answer: B
Explanation:
The most significant benefit of Problem Management within the ITIL 4 framework is reducing the number and
impact of incidents (Option B). While restoring service quickly (Option A) is important, that's primarily the
focus of Incident Management. Problem Management goes deeper, aiming to identify the underlying cause of

incidents and prevent them from recurring. Maximizing successful changes (Option C) is a goal of Change
Management, and managing workarounds (Option D) is a part of Problem Management, not its main objective.
Problem Management proactively analyzes incident trends, looking for patterns that suggest deeper,
unresolved issues. By identifying and resolving these underlying problems, it prevents future incidents and
reduces the overall disruption to services. A key aspect is the creation and maintenance of Known Error
Records (KERs), which document the problem, its workaround (if available), and its ultimate resolution. This
knowledge base helps speed up incident resolution in the short term while the problem is being permanently
fixed. Resolving the root cause leads to improved service stability, increased user satisfaction, and reduced
operational costs associated with repeated incident handling. The ultimate goal is to shift from reactive (fixing
incidents) to proactive (preventing them).
Therefore, reducing the number and impact of incidents is the overarching, most impactful benefit derived
from effective Problem Management. It contributes to a more stable and reliable IT environment, minimizing
disruptions and enhancing business productivity.
For further research, consider exploring these resources:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Handbook: This is the official source for detailed information on ITIL 4 principles
and practices.
ITIL Foundation Study Guides: Numerous reputable study guides are available online and in print, providing
comprehensive coverage of the ITIL 4 Foundation syllabus.
AXELOS Website: https://www.axelos.com/ - Provides information on ITIL certifications and best practices.
Question: 186 CertyIQ
Which guiding principle discourages 'silo activity'?
A.Focus on value
B.Start where you are
C.Collaborate and promote visibility
D.Keep it simple and practical
Answer: C
Explanation:
The correct answer, "Collaborate and promote visibility," directly addresses the issue of 'silo activity' within an
organization. Silos, whether functional teams, departments, or even individuals, operate independently with
limited communication and information sharing. This lack of connection leads to duplicated effort,
inconsistencies, delayed decisions, and ultimately, a reduction in the overall value delivered.
The "Collaborate and promote visibility" guiding principle emphasizes breaking down these silos.
Collaboration encourages teamwork, joint problem-solving, and shared responsibility. Promoting visibility
ensures that information is readily available across the organization, allowing everyone to understand the
dependencies, goals, and challenges faced by different teams. This shared understanding reduces conflicts,
improves decision-making, and streamlines workflows.
In a cloud computing context, for instance, imagine a development team operating in a silo, unaware of the
network configurations or security policies managed by the infrastructure team (also in a silo). Without
collaboration and visibility, the development team might deploy applications that are not properly secured or
configured, leading to potential security vulnerabilities or performance issues. A collaborative approach,
where both teams share information and work together, would result in a more secure and efficiently
deployed application.

Focusing on Value (A) is fundamental but doesn't inherently force cross-functional interaction. Starting where
you are (B) is about incremental improvement, not directly addressing siloed behavior. Keeping it simple and
practical (D) emphasizes efficiency but doesn't necessarily encourage collaboration or transparency between
teams.
Therefore, "Collaborate and promote visibility" is the most relevant guiding principle as it directly combats the
issues caused by siloed working by fostering communication, shared understanding, and teamwork across the
organization, which is especially critical in complex cloud environments. It encourages teams to work together
towards common goals, reducing redundancy and enhancing overall performance. The principle promotes a
culture of transparency where information flows freely, preventing misunderstandings and improving
decision-making processes, all crucial elements for effectively managing resources and delivering value in
any organizational setting.
Further research:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Study Guide: (Official ITIL 4 certification materials will provide comprehensive
descriptions of the guiding principles.) You will need to purchase this or related materials.
CIO.com - What is Silo Mentality?: https://www.cio.com/article/2438680/silo-mentality-definition-and-
remedies.html (Provides a general overview of silo mentality and its negative impacts.)
Question: 187 CertyIQ
What is included in the purpose of the 'relationship management' practice?
A.Identifying, analyzing, monitoring, and the continual improvement of relationships with stakeholders
B.Setting clear business-based targets so that the delivery of a service can be properly assessed
C.Creating collaborative relationships with key suppliers to uncover and realize new value
D.Handling all pre-defined, user-initiated service requests in an effective and user-friendly manner
Answer: A
Explanation:
The purpose of the 'relationship management' practice, as defined in ITIL 4, centers around fostering positive
interactions and value co-creation with stakeholders. Option A accurately reflects this core purpose by
highlighting activities like identifying, analyzing, monitoring, and continually improving relationships. This
proactive and iterative approach ensures stakeholder needs are understood, expectations are managed, and
that the relationships remain mutually beneficial over time.
Relationship management goes beyond simply reacting to issues. It actively seeks to understand stakeholder
perspectives, their value drivers, and how the service provider can best contribute to their success. By
analyzing relationship dynamics, the service provider can identify areas for improvement, address potential
conflicts, and proactively adapt service offerings to better align with stakeholder requirements.
Continuous monitoring of relationships allows the service provider to gauge satisfaction levels, identify
emerging needs, and track the effectiveness of relationship management activities. This feedback loop is
crucial for ongoing improvement and ensuring that the service provider remains a valued partner.
Options B, C, and D represent other ITIL 4 practices. Option B refers to measurement and reporting, option C
hints at supplier management (though is too narrow), and option D touches on service request management.
These practices are important, but they don't represent the primary purpose of relationship management. The
focus of relationship management is on the broader interactions and value exchange with all stakeholders,
not just specific activities or relationships.
In essence, relationship management is about building trust, fostering collaboration, and creating a shared

understanding between the service provider and its stakeholders, ensuring that services are delivered in a
way that meets their needs and drives mutual value. This proactive and strategic approach is essential for
long-term success in today's service-oriented environment.
For further research, consult the official AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation publications or reputable IT service
management resources.
Question: 188 CertyIQ
Which practice facilitates operational communication between the service provider organization and users in the
service consumer organization?
A.Service level management
B.Relationship management
C.Service desk
D.Monitoring and event management
Answer: C
Explanation:
The correct answer is C, Service desk.
The Service desk practice is specifically designed to be the single point of contact between the service
provider and its users. It facilitates communication by handling incidents, service requests, and providing
general information. Its primary goal is to restore normal service operation as quickly as possible and to fulfill
user requests efficiently. This involves operational communication with users about the status of their
requests, resolution of incidents, and announcements of service disruptions.
Service level management (A) focuses on defining, agreeing upon, and monitoring service levels, which is a
more strategic and less frequent communication activity. Relationship management (B) is broader than daily
operational communication and concentrates on managing the overall relationship with the customer
organization. Monitoring and event management (D) pertains to identifying and addressing IT infrastructure
and application issues, which typically involves technical teams rather than direct user communication,
although it might trigger service desk activities. The service desk is the dedicated practice for handling the
day-to-day interactions and operational communications with the service consumer organization's users.
Further research:
AXELOS. ITIL Foundation: ITIL 4 Edition.
Official ITIL 4 Foundation Study Guides.
While direct links to AXELOS content may require purchase, searching for "ITIL 4 Service Desk Practice" or
similar keywords will provide valuable insights on various IT service management resource sites.
Question: 189 CertyIQ
Which dimension considers the application of artificial intelligence to service management?
A.Organizations and people
B.Information and technology
C.Partners and suppliers

D.Value streams and processes
Answer: B
Explanation:
The correct answer, B. Information and technology, is the dimension of service management that most
directly considers the application of artificial intelligence (AI) to service management. Here's why:
The four dimensions of service management (Organizations and People, Information and Technology, Partners
and Suppliers, and Value Streams and Processes) guide a holistic approach to service management. Each
dimension examines different aspects that must be considered when creating, managing, and delivering
services.
Information and Technology: This dimension encompasses the information and knowledge necessary for
managing services, and the technologies supporting them. AI, being a technology, fits squarely within this
dimension. This includes the automation it enables, the data it utilizes, and the intelligent systems it creates to
enhance service delivery. For instance, AI-powered chatbots improve customer service, automated
diagnostics speed up incident resolution, and predictive analytics optimize resource allocation. AI's use in
processing and analyzing service management data (incident reports, change requests, etc.) falls under this
dimension.
Organizations and People: This focuses on the roles, responsibilities, skills, and organizational structure
required to support service management. While AI will undoubtedly impact organizational structures and
skills needed, its application directly falls within the 'Information and Technology' domain.
Partners and Suppliers: This dimension concerns the relationships with vendors and other entities involved in
service provision. While suppliers may provide AI solutions, the dimension addresses the relationship and
contracts, not the technology itself.
Value Streams and Processes: This dimension considers the activities, workflows, controls, and procedures
needed to create and deliver services. While AI can enhance value streams and processes, the technology
itself, and its implementation, remains firmly within the 'Information and Technology' dimension.
Therefore, the application of AI, as a form of technology used to process information and support services,
aligns most directly with the "Information and Technology" dimension of service management.
Authoritative Links for Further Research:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Study Guide: (Purchase typically required) Offers comprehensive information on
all ITIL 4 concepts, including the four dimensions of service management.
Official ITIL Documentation: AXELOS owns ITIL. Their official publications are the most authoritative source.
ITIL 4 Foundation Exam Syllabus: Specifically review the sections on the Four Dimensions of Service
Management to understand the scope of each.
Question: 190 CertyIQ
Which type of change is MOST LIKELY to be initiated as part of the 'service request management' practice?
A.A normal change
B.An emergency change
C.A standard change
D.A change model

Answer: C
Explanation:
The correct answer is C. A standard change is the most likely type of change to be initiated through service
request management. Here's why:
Service request management focuses on fulfilling pre-defined, low-risk, and frequently occurring user needs.
These requests are typically standardized and well-documented, minimizing potential disruption. Standard
changes align perfectly with this characteristic, as they are pre-approved, have established procedures, and
do not require risk assessment for each instance. Examples include password resets, software installations
from a catalog, or access requests that follow a documented workflow.
Normal changes, in contrast, are more complex and require assessment, authorization, and scheduling.
Emergency changes are implemented rapidly to address urgent incidents, bypassing standard change
processes. Change models are frameworks that define the steps for managing specific types of changes, but
they don't initiate changes themselves. The automation and pre-approval inherent in standard changes make
them ideally suited for handling through a streamlined service request process. This efficiency helps IT teams
focus on more complex and strategic initiatives while empowering users to resolve common issues quickly.
Service request management often leverages catalogs and self-service portals to facilitate the request and
fulfillment of these standard changes.
For further reading on ITIL 4 and change management practices, refer to the official ITIL 4 Foundation
publication or resources on the Axelos website:
Axelos Official Website
Question: 191 CertyIQ
Which benefit is MOST aligned with the guiding principle 'progress iteratively with feedback'?
A.Service providers are able to respond more quickly to customer needs
B.Bottlenecks in the service provider's workflow are identified
C.The complexities of the service provider's IT systems are identified
D.The service provider gains a better understanding of the customer experience
Answer: A
Explanation:
The correct answer is A: Service providers are able to respond more quickly to customer needs. Here's why:
The ITIL 4 guiding principle "Progress Iteratively with Feedback" emphasizes breaking down large initiatives
into smaller, manageable pieces. This allows for frequent review and adaptation based on feedback received
at each iteration. This iterative approach fosters agility and responsiveness.
Option A directly aligns with this principle because iterative progress, coupled with constant feedback,
enables service providers to identify and address changing customer needs more rapidly. Each iteration can
be fine-tuned based on the feedback, leading to a faster, more accurate response to customer demands.
Option B, identifying bottlenecks, while important, is not the most direct benefit. Bottlenecks can be identified
through feedback loops in iterations, but the primary focus isn't bottleneck identification.
Option C, identifying IT system complexities, is also indirectly related. Understanding complexities might
emerge from iterative progress, but isn't the core benefit of the "Progress Iteratively with Feedback"

principle.
Option D, gaining a better understanding of the customer experience, is related but less directly than A.
Iterative progress with feedback certainly contributes to improved customer experience understanding, but
the quicker response time afforded by iterative cycles is the most immediate and beneficial outcome
connected directly to this guiding principle.
Therefore, by iterating and incorporating feedback, service providers can rapidly adapt their services, address
emerging needs, and deliver value more efficiently, resulting in a faster response to customer requirements.
This directly embodies the core essence of the guiding principle. It also promotes continuous improvement,
ensuring the service provider's offerings remain relevant and valuable over time.

links to specific pages require a subscription, but you can search for "ITIL 4 guiding principles" on the
AXELOS website.

with Feedback BMC" to find relevant articles. (e.g., https://www.bmc.com/blogs/itil-4-guiding-principles/)
Question: 192 CertyIQ
Which costs are included in the value proposition of a service?
A.Additional expense that the service consumer has because they are using the service
B.Money that the service consumer no longer needs to spend because they are using the service
C.Tangible or intangible results for the service consumer because they are using the service
D.The benefits, usefulness, and importance of the service that are perceived by the service consumer
Answer: B
Explanation:
The correct answer, B, aligns perfectly with the core concept of a value proposition within ITIL 4. A value
proposition articulates the benefits a customer receives from a service, contrasted against the associated
costs and risks. It's about creating a perceived positive trade-off for the customer.
Option B, "Money that the service consumer no longer needs to spend because they are using the service,"
directly addresses the cost aspect of this trade-off, highlighting reduced costs attributable to the service. It
shows the financial gain from using the service.
Option A, "Additional expense that the service consumer has because they are using the service," contradicts
the purpose of a value proposition. While there might be associated costs with utilizing a service, the value
proposition should emphasize the net positive impact, where the benefits outweigh the expenses. Any
additional expenses would likely be considered costs and risks within the broader context of service value
creation, but they are not typically presented as part of the value itself. The value proposition focuses on how
the service minimizes costs or avoids potential expenses.
The other options, C and D, focus on the benefits or usefulness of the service, which are also elements of the
value proposition but not the cost element being specifically questioned. A complete value proposition
encompasses both benefits and costs, however, the specific question asks about the costs included.
Therefore, focusing on reduced expenditure directly reflects the cost component of the value equation,
showing how the service saves the customer money, which is a crucial part of demonstrating the value derived
from utilizing it.

service value and value co-creation.
ITIL 4 Foundation Handbook: A comprehensive guide to the ITIL 4 Foundation material.
"Creating a Value Proposition" - Harvard Business Review: Though not ITIL-specific, this article provides
valuable insights into crafting effective value propositions in a general business context, which is applicable
to IT service management.
https://hbr.org/2015/01/reinventing-your-business-model
Question: 193 CertyIQ
Identify the missing word in the following sentence:
A [?] is the addition, modification, or removal of anything that could have a direct or indirect effect on services.
A.problem
B.risk
C.change
D.configuration item
Answer: C
Explanation:
The correct answer is C, Change. Here's why:
The ITIL 4 Foundation definition of a "Change" directly aligns with the provided sentence. A Change is defined
as the addition, modification, or removal of anything that could have a direct or indirect effect on services.
This encompasses a very broad range of activities, reflecting the dynamic nature of service management,
especially within cloud environments.
Let's examine why the other options are incorrect:
Problem: A Problem is a cause, or potential cause, of one or more incidents. It isn't the action of modifying or
removing something.
Risk: A Risk is a possible event that could cause harm or loss, or make it more difficult to achieve objectives.
While a change can introduce risk, the change itself isn't the risk.
Configuration Item (CI): A CI is any component that needs to be managed to deliver an IT service. Changes
affect CIs, but a CI is not the act of changing itself.
Changes are crucial in ITIL 4 because they must be managed effectively to minimize disruption and ensure
that services continue to meet business needs. In a cloud environment, changes can involve scaling resources,
deploying new applications, patching vulnerabilities, or modifying network configurations. Proper change
management ensures that these changes are planned, tested, and implemented in a controlled manner.
Consider a cloud-based application. Modifying the application code (an addition), scaling up server instances
(another type of addition or modification), or updating the operating system on a virtual machine (another
modification) would all be considered changes. Removing an old, unused application instance would also be a
change.
ITIL 4 emphasizes that all changes should be managed, regardless of their size or perceived risk. Even
seemingly small changes can have unintended consequences if not properly assessed and implemented.

Therefore, "Change" is the only option that fits the core ITIL 4 definition and the context of managing services,
especially within the dynamic and ever-evolving landscape of cloud computing. The ability to rapidly and
safely deploy changes is critical for organizations that want to be agile and responsive to changing business
needs. Change management practices, as defined by ITIL 4, are specifically designed to support this agility
while minimizing risks.
Authoritative Links for further research:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Guidance: (Typically available as part of an official ITIL 4 course or through
AXELOS's subscription services). This is the definitive source for ITIL 4 definitions.
ITIL Foundation Handbook (TSO): A good introductory book outlining ITIL 4 principles.
AXELOS Website: https://www.axelos.com/ (For official ITIL documentation and resources). Although specific
documents behind paywalls, you can get general overviews.
Question: 194 CertyIQ
Which of the four dimensions includes the knowledge bases needed to deliver and manage services?
A.Organizations and people
B.Information and technology
C.Partners and suppliers
D.Value streams and processes
Answer: B
Explanation:
The correct answer is B. Information and technology.
The four dimensions of service management within ITIL 4 represent key perspectives to consider when
designing, managing, and improving services. These dimensions ensure a holistic approach and prevent
overlooking critical aspects.
The "Information and Technology" dimension focuses on the information and knowledge necessary for service
delivery, along with the technologies that support it. This encompasses not only the infrastructure,
applications, and tools used, but also the information managed by these technologies and the knowledge
required to effectively use and manage them. Knowledge bases, essential repositories of information about
processes, incidents, solutions, and best practices, are critical components within this dimension. These
knowledge bases enable efficient incident resolution, facilitate self-service capabilities for users, and support
continuous service improvement. They are fundamental to effective service delivery and management.
Without readily accessible and accurate knowledge, services cannot be efficiently delivered, supported, or
improved.
Organizations and people (A) focuses on roles, responsibilities, culture, and skills needed. Partners and
suppliers (C) addresses relationships with external entities contributing to service delivery. Value streams and
processes (D) concerns the activities, workflows, controls, and procedures that deliver value. While all
dimensions are important, the specific inclusion of knowledge bases directly aligns with the management and
utilization of information within the technology ecosystem.
For further research, consult the official ITIL 4 Foundation guidance:
AXELOS: (Generally requires purchase, but provides the definitive source) https://www.axelos.com/
Official ITIL 4 publications These delve deeper into the four dimensions of service management.

Question: 195 CertyIQ
Staff in an IT organization are very busy, mostly carrying out tasks that add little or no value to the organization or
its customers.
Which guiding principle recommends that the unnecessary work should be eliminated?
A.Keep it simple and practical
B.Think and work holistically
C.Start where you are
D.Progress iteratively with feedback
Answer: A
Explanation:
The correct answer is A. Keep it simple and practical.
"Keep it simple and practical" directly addresses the problem of unnecessary work. This guiding principle
advocates for eliminating processes, activities, and tasks that don't contribute value. It encourages a focus on
what's essential and discourages over-engineering or complex solutions that create extra burdens. The
principle emphasizes streamlining workflows and removing bureaucratic obstacles to improve efficiency and
reduce waste. By consistently questioning the necessity of each activity, organizations can identify and
eliminate non-value-added work, freeing up staff to focus on tasks that directly benefit the organization and
its customers.
The other options are less directly relevant:
Think and work holistically: While important for understanding the interconnectedness of services, it doesn't
specifically target the removal of unnecessary work.
Start where you are: This focuses on improving existing processes, but not necessarily eliminating them if
they are inherently wasteful.
Progress iteratively with feedback: This guiding principle is about managing complex projects and
processes, focusing on phased development and learning from feedback. While it can help identify
inefficiencies, it doesn't primarily aim to eliminate them directly.
Therefore, "Keep it simple and practical" aligns most closely with the scenario described, emphasizing the
removal of activities that add little or no value.
For further information, you can consult these resources:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Handbook
Official ITIL 4 guidance from AXELOS
Question: 196 CertyIQ
Which practice has a purpose that includes the management of financially valuable components that can
contribute to the delivery of an IT service?
A.Deployment management
B.Continual improvement
C.Monitoring and event management
D.IT asset management

Answer: D
Explanation:
The correct answer is D, IT Asset Management, because its core purpose directly aligns with managing
financially valuable components that contribute to IT service delivery. IT Asset Management (ITAM) focuses
on the lifecycle management of all IT assets, including hardware, software, licenses, and even cloud
subscriptions, from procurement to disposal. This encompasses tracking their financial value, utilization, and
risks. These assets form the foundation of IT services and directly impact their cost and effectiveness.
Effectively managing these assets helps organizations optimize spending, reduce waste, improve compliance,
and enhance service performance.
Deployment Management, option A, concentrates on moving new or changed hardware, software,
documentation, or processes into the live environment. While deployment uses IT assets, its primary concern
isn't their overall financial value or lifecycle management, but rather the controlled and efficient release
process. Continual Improvement (option B) aims to align practices and services with changing business needs
but doesn’t specifically focus on the management of financially valuable components themselves. While ITAM
will feed into continual improvement, it is not its sole focus. Similarly, Monitoring and Event Management
(option C) deals with observing services and components to detect issues and potential problems. While it
monitors the performance of IT assets, it doesn’t manage their financial value or lifecycle.
ITAM encompasses the tracking, accounting, and optimization of these financially valuable components,
ensuring they are used effectively and contribute to the delivery of IT services in a cost-efficient manner. For
instance, ITAM helps prevent overspending on cloud resources by identifying underutilized instances or
unused subscriptions.
Therefore, IT Asset Management uniquely emphasizes the financial management and control of the resources
underpinning IT service delivery, making it the most relevant answer.
Further Reading:
AXELOS. ITIL Foundation: ITIL 4 Edition. TSO, 2019.
ServiceNow: What is IT Asset Management (ITAM)? https://www.servicenow.com/workflows/itam/what-is-it-
asset-management.html
Ivanti: IT Asset Management (ITAM) https://www.ivanti.com/solutions/products/asset-management
Question: 197 CertyIQ
Which practice ensures that service actions, that are a normal part of service delivery, are effectively handled?
A.Incident management
B.Service level management
C.Problem management
D.Service request management
Answer: D
Explanation:
The correct answer is D, Service Request Management. Service Request Management is the practice focused
on fulfilling user requests for services and resources that are pre-defined and routine. These requests are a
normal part of service delivery and are typically low-risk. Incident management, on the other hand, focuses on
restoring normal service operation as quickly as possible, minimizing the adverse impact on business
operations. While incident management handles unexpected disruptions, service request management

handles expected, standardized needs. Problem management deals with identifying and resolving the root
causes of incidents to prevent recurrence. Service level management aims to set clear expectations for
service performance and ensure that services are delivered according to agreed-upon service levels. By
defining clear processes and workflows for handling service requests, organizations can ensure that these
actions are efficiently and effectively handled, contributing to improved user satisfaction and productivity.
Service Request Management utilizes pre-approved solutions and automated workflows to accelerate the
fulfillment process. This automation helps minimize manual intervention and ensures consistency across all
requests. The practice also incorporates knowledge management to provide users with self-service options
for common requests. This helps to deflect a portion of the service requests from requiring direct intervention
from service desk personnel. In the context of ITIL 4, Service Request Management contributes significantly
to value co-creation by facilitating seamless access to services and supporting business processes. The ITIL 4
Foundation publication provides in-depth information regarding Service Request Management and its role in
IT service management.
Further reading:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation: https://www.axelos.com/ (Official ITIL website)
Service Request Management in ITIL 4: A Complete Guide: https://www.bmc.com/blogs/itil-service-request-
management/
Question: 198 CertyIQ
A service will be unavailable for the next two hours for unplanned maintenance.
Which practice is MOST LIKELY to be involved in managing this?
A.Incident management
B.Problem management
C.Change enablement
D.Service request management
Answer: A
Explanation:
The correct answer is A. Incident management. Here's why:
An unplanned service outage requiring immediate maintenance directly aligns with the definition of an
incident. ITIL 4 defines an incident as "an unplanned interruption to a service, or reduction in the quality of a
service." The primary goal of incident management is to restore normal service operation as quickly as
possible and minimize the adverse impact on business operations, ensuring that the best possible levels of
service quality and availability are maintained. In this scenario, the service unavailability due to maintenance is
an interruption, necessitating the incident management practice to address it.
Change enablement deals with planned changes, not unplanned disruptions. While the maintenance itself
could have initially been part of a change, the unplanned nature of the event places it firmly within the realm
of incident management. The focus is on restoration, not the change process itself.
Problem management focuses on identifying the underlying cause of incidents to prevent recurrence. While
problem management might be triggered after the incident is resolved to investigate why the unplanned
maintenance was necessary, its immediate involvement in handling the active two-hour outage is secondary to
incident management's role of quickly restoring the service.
Service request management deals with routine requests from users, such as password resets or software
installations, not unplanned service outages. It’s important to distinguish between a request for a service and

an interruption to an existing service.
Therefore, because the scenario explicitly describes an unplanned service interruption, incident management
is the MOST LIKELY practice to be involved in managing the situation by restoring the service.
For further research:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Syllabus: This provides a comprehensive overview of ITIL 4 concepts.
Official ITIL 4 publications such as the ITIL Foundation book, provide detailed explanations of each practice.
Question: 199 CertyIQ
Which practice is MOST associated with the use of empathy to understand users?
A.Service desk
B.Continual improvement
C.Service level management
D.Change enablement
Answer: A
Explanation:
The correct answer is A, Service desk, because it's the practice most directly involved in handling user
interactions and resolving their immediate issues. Empathy is crucial for service desk personnel to effectively
understand user needs, frustrations, and the impact of incidents on their work.
Let's delve deeper:
A Service desk acts as the single point of contact between the service provider and users. They are
responsible for handling incidents, service requests, and providing information. Therefore, demonstrating
empathy is paramount to building rapport, understanding the user's perspective, and effectively
troubleshooting their problems. A service desk analyst who can empathize with a frustrated user can de-
escalate the situation, gather accurate information, and find a suitable solution more efficiently.
B. Continual improvement focuses on improving products, services, and practices over time. While empathy
might play a role in identifying areas for improvement by understanding user feedback, it isn't the primary
focus.
C. Service level management focuses on defining, agreeing on, and monitoring service levels. While
understanding user expectations is important, empathy isn't as directly applied as in a service desk
environment.
D. Change enablement is about assessing, authorizing, and implementing changes to services. Understanding
the impact of change on users is valuable, but direct empathy isn't the core function.
The service desk is where users directly interact with IT support. Therefore, empathy is the most crucial skill
for service desk staff to cultivate and apply daily. A technical answer without considering the user's
perspective might be accurate but ultimately ineffective and frustrating. The human element makes service
desks rely heavily on empathetic communication.
For further reading, explore the ITIL 4 Foundation Handbook, specifically the service desk practice
description. Also, search for articles on "empathy in IT support" to understand its importance in improving
customer satisfaction and service delivery.

Question: 200 CertyIQ
Identify the missing word in the following sentence:
A customer defines the [?] for a service and takes responsibility for the outcomes of service consumption.
A.requirements
B.resources
C.suppliers
D.products
Answer: A
Explanation:
The correct answer is A. requirements. Here's why:
The statement focuses on the customer's role in service definition and outcome responsibility. A customer's
primary action in engaging with a service provider is to articulate their requirements. These requirements
detail what the customer needs from the service, specifying functionality, performance, security, and other
critical attributes.
The customer defining "resources" doesn't fit. Resources are typically managed by the service provider to
deliver the service, not defined by the customer. Suppliers are entities providing resources or components to
the service provider, not something defined by the customer in this context. "Products" are the offerings of a
service provider, and while a customer chooses products, they don't primarily "define" them; instead, they
define the requirements the product should meet. The customer takes responsibility for the outcomes of
service consumption based on whether those initial requirements are successfully met by the service
provided. If the requirements are poorly defined or not adequately understood, the customer still ultimately
bears the responsibility for that lack of clarity. The ITIL framework emphasizes the importance of clearly
defining and understanding customer requirements to ensure service value and satisfaction. This
understanding forms the basis for all subsequent service design, delivery, and improvement activities. The
better the requirements are documented, the more aligned service delivery will be, and the better the
customer will be able to achieve its desired outcomes. Therefore, requirements fit most logically within the
context of customer definition and outcome responsibility.
For further reading on customer requirements and ITIL 4:
AXELOS Official ITIL 4 Foundation Materials: This is the primary authoritative source for ITIL 4.
"ITIL Foundation Handbook" by various authors: This book can provide more in-depth explanations of ITIL 4
concepts.
Question: 201 CertyIQ
Which of the following ensures that a service provider and a service consumer continually co-create value?
A.Service consumption
B.Service offerings
C.Service level management
D.Service relationship management
Answer: D
Explanation:

The correct answer is D, Service Relationship Management (SRM).
SRM is the practice of establishing and nurturing the connection between a service provider and a service
consumer to ensure that value is continually co-created throughout the service lifecycle. It focuses on
understanding the needs of the consumer and ensuring that the service offerings meet those needs
effectively. This includes managing expectations, fostering communication, and establishing clear roles and
responsibilities.
A. Service Consumption refers specifically to the activities a consumer performs to use a service. It is a part of
a larger relationship.
B. Service Offerings describe the value proposition made available to consumers, which is critical, but not a
dynamic, continuous relationship.
C. Service Level Management focuses on defining and managing the agreed-upon level of service provided.
While important for managing expectations and performance, it is primarily focused on the terms of service
delivery, rather than the co-creation and maintenance of overall value.
SRM goes beyond simply delivering services according to agreed-upon levels. It emphasizes building a
partnership between the provider and consumer where feedback is exchanged and the service is continuously
improved to maximize the mutual benefits. This necessitates ongoing communication, understanding of
evolving needs, and a willingness to adapt the service. The continuous feedback loops ensure that the service
is aligned with changing requirements and contributes to shared objectives, thereby promoting the ongoing
co-creation of value. Without active management of this relationship, service offerings can become
misaligned with consumer needs over time, leading to decreased value and potential service disruption.
For further reading on ITIL 4 and Service Relationship Management, refer to official ITIL 4 publications or
trusted resources such as:
AXELOS (official ITIL governing body): https://www.axelos.com/
ITIL Foundation Handbook
Question: 202 CertyIQ
What type of charge is often used for resolving incidents or implementing security patches?
A.Standard change
B.Normal change
C.Emergency change
D.Change model
Answer: C
Explanation:
The correct answer is C. Emergency change.
Here's why: Emergency changes are implemented to resolve incidents or implement security patches as
quickly as possible. These changes typically address critical issues that could severely impact service
availability, business operations, or security posture. Standard changes are pre-approved and low-risk, which
don't usually apply to critical scenarios. Normal changes follow a standard change management process,
requiring assessment, authorization, and scheduling. While more thorough, this process is too slow when
dealing with immediate threats or critical service disruptions. Change models provide templates for handling
changes, but they don't determine the type of change needed.

Incidents require immediate remediation to restore service. Security patches often address vulnerabilities
that, if exploited, could lead to significant damage. The urgency of these situations necessitates bypassing
the typical approval process in favor of swift action. Therefore, emergency change procedures, with their
expedited processes and focus on rapid implementation, are the most suitable approach. In a cloud
environment, quickly patching a vulnerability on a server experiencing high traffic, or applying a critical hotfix
to a database encountering performance problems, might call for an emergency change. Delaying these types
of activities while waiting for formal approvals can have severe consequences. The key differentiator is the
degree of impact and the timeframe of the remediation effort.Emergency changes are often subject to ex-
post review and documentation to ensure compliance and identify areas for improvement in the process.
For more information, refer to:
ITIL 4 Foundation: ITIL 4 Edition: This publication provides a comprehensive overview of ITIL 4 concepts,
including change management and change types.
AXELOS Website: https://www.axelos.com/ This is the official source for ITIL information and resources.
Question: 203 CertyIQ
Which of the following includes configuring components and activities to facilitate outcomes for stakeholders?
A.Service relationship management
B.Service consumption
C.The service value system
D.The 'release management' practice
Answer: C
Explanation:
The correct answer is C. The service value system. Here's why:
The ITIL 4 Service Value System (SVS) describes how all the components and activities of an organization
work together as a system to enable value creation. Central to the SVS is the value chain, which includes
activities like Plan, Improve, Engage, Design and Transition, Obtain/Build, and Deliver and Support. These
activities represent steps an organization takes to create value. Configuring components and activities to
facilitate outcomes directly aligns with the SVS's core purpose of coordinating organizational functions and
resources to realize value for stakeholders.
Let's examine why the other options are incorrect:
A. Service Relationship Management: While vital for understanding and nurturing stakeholder relationships,
this practice primarily focuses on managing the connections between the service provider and consumer,
rather than configuring the entire system for value creation.
B. Service Consumption: Service consumption describes activities undertaken by service consumers and does
not encompass the overall configuration of components to drive outcomes across the wider service
landscape.
D. The 'Release Management' Practice: Release management focuses specifically on the planning,
scheduling, and controlling of software releases, not the broad configuration of organizational components
and activities to facilitate outcomes for all stakeholders.
In essence, the SVS provides the overarching framework. Configuration aimed at facilitating outcomes for
stakeholders requires coordinated effort across the service value chain and supporting guiding principles,
reflecting the holistic nature of the SVS. Only the Service Value System aligns with the concept of a

comprehensive, integrated approach to value creation via strategic configuration.
For further reading:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation materials.
https://www.axelos.com/
