AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Syllabus: (Search for "ITIL 4 Foundation Syllabus" as the specific document
changes periodically. AXELOS is the official source for ITIL.) This document outlines the key concepts and
terminology of ITIL 4, including the purpose and components of service management.
ITIL Foundation Handbook: (Again, search for the latest version. Many accredited training providers offer
study guides that provide detailed information on service desk functions.)
Question: 227 CertyIQ
Which is CORRECT about change authorization?
A.A change authority is assigned each time a standard change is requested
B.Emergency changes are authorized by the technician making the change
C.Assignment of the change authority is based on the change type and model
D.The change authority will ensure changes are authorized after they are deployed
Answer: C
Explanation:
The correct answer is C: "Assignment of the change authority is based on the change type and model." Here's
why:
ITIL 4 emphasizes that change authorization should be risk-based and appropriate to the nature of the
change. Standard changes, normal changes, and emergency changes require different levels and types of
authorization. This aligns with the ITIL 4 guiding principle of "Focus on value" by ensuring resources are
allocated effectively based on the potential impact of the change.
A. Incorrect. Standard changes are pre-authorized. The change authority approves the model for standard
changes initially, not each individual instance of a request.
B. Incorrect. Emergency changes require rapid authorization to restore services quickly, but this doesn't mean
the technician makes the authorization. A designated emergency change authority or a higher-level body,
such as a CAB/EC, usually provides the authorization.
D. Incorrect. The change authority authorizes the change before deployment, not after. Post-deployment
activities involve review and validation.
Therefore, option C reflects the fundamental principle of ITIL 4 that change authorization is context-
dependent and guided by factors such as change type (standard, normal, emergency), complexity, and risk.
The change model defines the steps and authorization requirements for a specific type of change.

Further reading:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Book: The official ITIL 4 Foundation publication provides comprehensive details on
change management and its related concepts.
ITIL 4 Foundation Handbook: This handbook offers supplementary explanations and examples.
https://www.axelos.com/ (Official AXELOS website, the source of ITIL)
Question: 228 CertyIQ
What term is used to describe the functionality of a service?
A.Output
B.Outcome
C.Utility
D.Warranty
Answer: C
Explanation:
The correct answer is C, Utility. Utility, within the context of ITIL 4, refers to the functionality offered by a
service to meet a particular need. In simpler terms, it's "what the service does" for the consumer.
A. Output represents tangible deliverables or artifacts produced by the service. It's a result of the service's
functionality but not the functionality itself.
B. Outcome refers to the result or consequence achieved for the service consumer. It's the impact or benefit
derived from using the service and isn't the definition of the service functionality.
D. Warranty relates to how the service performs and ensures it's "fit for purpose" in terms of availability,
capacity, security, and continuity. Warranty doesn't describe what the service does, but rather the assurance
of its performance.
Therefore, Utility best describes the core functionality provided by a service. For example, a cloud-based
storage service's utility is providing space to store and retrieve data. The availability and security features
would fall under warranty. The output might be the stored files. The desired outcome might be simplified data
management.
In ITIL 4, utility and warranty are key components that define the value a service provides. Utility ensures the
service is fit for purpose (does what is required), while warranty ensures it is fit for use (performs as required).
For further research, consult the official ITIL 4 Foundation guidance from AXELOS:
AXELOS Website (Look for ITIL 4 Foundation information).
ITIL 4 Foundation Syllabus (While not as explanatory, it will use these terms).
Question: 229 CertyIQ
Which practice ensures that a variety of access channels are available for users to report issues?
A.Service desk
B.Service level management

C.Incident management
D.Change enablement
Answer: A
Explanation:
The correct answer is A. Service desk. Here's a detailed justification:
The ITIL 4 practice that primarily focuses on providing a single point of contact and various access channels
for users to report issues is the service desk. Its core function revolves around handling incidents and service
requests, effectively acting as a communication hub between the service provider and its users. To fulfill this
role, the service desk needs to offer a range of accessible channels for users to report problems.
These channels can include telephone support, email, self-service portals, chat applications, and even walk-in
support (depending on the organization). The variety of options ensures that users can report issues using
their preferred method, regardless of their location or technical proficiency. This facilitates quicker issue
reporting and resolution.
Service Level Management (SLM), Change Enablement, and Incident Management, while crucial to IT service
management, don't primarily focus on providing diverse access channels for reporting issues. SLM is about
defining and agreeing upon service levels, Change Enablement deals with managing changes to services, and
Incident Management focuses on restoring normal service operation as quickly as possible. While these
practices interact with the service desk, the service desk is the primary point of contact for users raising
issues. Incident Management benefits from the service desk's efforts by receiving reports to respond to, but
the service desk is where the reporting happens initially.
The goal of a well-designed service desk is to improve user experience and satisfaction by making it easy for
them to get help when they need it. A multi-channel service desk strengthens this by providing more options
to contact the IT organization, creating better communication between users and IT staff.In summary, the
service desk is best suited for providing multiple access channels.
Authoritative Links for further research:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Guidance: Search for ITIL 4 Foundation materials provided by AXELOS, the official
source for ITIL.
ITIL Foundation Handbook: Check out the ITIL Foundation Handbook, often available through authorized
training providers, for detailed explanations.
Question: 230 CertyIQ
Identify the missing word(s) in the following sentence:
The purpose of the problem management practice is to reduce the likelihood and impact of incidents by identifying
actual and potential causes of incidents, and managing workarounds and [?].
A.events
B.changes
C.IT assets
D.known errors
Answer: D
Explanation:
The correct answer is D. known errors. The purpose of Problem Management is to proactively prevent

incidents and minimize their impact. It achieves this by investigating the root causes of incidents, not just
addressing the symptoms.
Known errors play a central role in this proactive approach. A known error is a problem that has been
diagnosed and for which a workaround or permanent resolution exists, but hasn't necessarily been fully
implemented yet. Problem Management actively manages these known errors, ensuring that workarounds are
documented and communicated and that permanent solutions are developed and implemented.
While events (A) are occurrences that can trigger incidents, Problem Management focuses on the underlying
causes of incidents rather than simply reacting to events. Changes (B) are managed by Change Management,
not Problem Management, although Problem Management might identify the need for a change to resolve a
problem. IT assets (C) are relevant to IT Asset Management but are not the primary focus of Problem
Management, which is focused on identifying and preventing the recurrence of incidents.
By managing known errors, Problem Management provides valuable information to Incident Management (to
expedite resolution using workarounds) and Change Management (to implement permanent fixes). Therefore,
'known errors' completes the sentence and best describes the proactive nature of the Problem Management
practice within ITIL 4. The core purpose is not just to address incidents but to learn from them and prevent
future occurrences by addressing the root causes and managing the workarounds and eventual fixes
associated with those root causes (which are then documented as known errors).
Further research:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Guide: (Purchase Required) This guide provides the official definition and purpose
of Problem Management.
ITIL 4 Problem Management Practice Guide: (Purchase Required) Provides more in-depth information.
Online ITIL Resources: Search for "ITIL 4 Problem Management" for articles and blog posts from reputable
sources.
Question: 231 CertyIQ
Which is a key requirement for a successful service level agreements (SLAs)?
A.They should be written using language and terms which all parties will understand
B.They should be based on system-based metrics which are useful to the service provider
C.They should be carried forward, unchanged, from one year to the next to enable consistent service
D.They should avoid ambiguous targets such as those relating to user experience
Answer: A
Explanation:
The correct answer is A: They should be written using language and terms which all parties will understand.
SLAs are agreements between a service provider and a customer that define the level of service expected.
For an SLA to be effective, both parties must have a clear and shared understanding of its contents. This
necessitates using language and terms that are easily comprehensible, avoiding technical jargon or overly
complex phrasing that one party might not grasp. Ambiguity in an SLA can lead to misunderstandings,
disputes, and ultimately, a breakdown in the service relationship. A clearly written SLA prevents
misinterpretations and promotes a shared sense of responsibility.
Option B is incorrect because SLAs should focus on metrics that are relevant to the customer, not just the
service provider. While system-based metrics are important for internal monitoring, the SLA should translate
those metrics into business outcomes the customer cares about.

Option C is incorrect because SLAs need to be reviewed and updated regularly to reflect changes in business
requirements, technology, and the service provider's capabilities. Sticking to an outdated SLA hinders service
improvement and prevents the SLA from accurately representing the current service.
Option D is partially correct, as avoiding ambiguous targets is important, but the best overall answer is A
because clear, understandable language is the foundation for avoiding ambiguity and fostering mutual
agreement. Even well-defined targets are useless if one party misunderstands them. Clarity in language is
paramount in establishing a well-understood framework for expectations.
Further research:
ITIL 4 Foundation Handbook: Provides detailed explanations of service level management principles.
Axelos (ITIL official website): https://www.axelos.com/ Offers resources and information about ITIL best
practices.
BMC Blogs: https://www.bmc.com/blogs/itil-service-level-agreement/ Offers practical insights into SLAs.
Question: 232 CertyIQ
Which is an example of a service request?
A.A request for normal operation to be restored
B.A request to implement a security patch
C.A request for access to a file
D.A request to investigate the cause of an incident
Answer: C
Explanation:
Here's a detailed justification of why "A request for access to a file" is an example of a service request in ITIL
4 Foundation:
In ITIL 4, service requests are defined as requests from a user for something that is a standard part of the
services being offered. They are pre-defined and readily fulfillable. Unlike incidents (disruptions to service),
service requests are not about fixing something broken; they are about getting access to something or
getting something done.
Option C, "A request for access to a file," perfectly aligns with this definition. Gaining access to a file is often a
standard, pre-approved procedure managed through a defined process. The fulfillment typically involves
granting permissions to an existing resource (the file) or provisioning a new resource. This process doesn't
usually involve troubleshooting or resolving a disruption.
Option A, "A request for normal operation to be restored," directly describes an incident. It indicates that
something isn't working as expected and needs fixing to restore the normal service level.
Option B, "A request to implement a security patch," is related to change management, as it involves
modifying the IT infrastructure. While applying a security patch might address a vulnerability caused by an
incident, the act of applying the patch itself falls under change activities aimed at improvement and risk
mitigation.
Option D, "A request to investigate the cause of an incident," relates to problem management. Incident
management deals with restoring service quickly; problem management delves into the underlying root
causes of incidents to prevent recurrence.
Therefore, only option C represents a routine request for a readily available service component, making it a

clear example of a service request according to ITIL 4 principles. Service requests are managed through a
specific workflow, often automated, and are distinct from incident, problem, and change management
processes. They fulfill a user's need for a service or resource without implying a service disruption. This is the
defining characteristic that distinguishes them from other types of IT requests.
Authoritative Links for further research:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Guidance: While behind a paywall, this is the official source.
ITIL 4 Practices Guides (AXELOS): Look for guidance on Service Request Management.
Various ITIL training providers' websites (e.g., ITSM Zone, PeopleCert) often have introductory articles and
blog posts that explain service requests in detail within the ITIL 4 framework.
Question: 233 CertyIQ
Which of the four dimensions focuses on managing data in compliance with industry regulations?
A.Partners and suppliers
B.Organizations and people
C.Value streams and processes
D.Information and technology
Answer: D
Explanation:
The correct answer is D, Information and technology. Here's a detailed justification:
The ITIL 4 framework is structured around four dimensions of service management that collectively consider
all aspects necessary for creating value. These dimensions ensure a holistic approach.
Partners and Suppliers: Focuses on relationships with external entities that contribute to service delivery.
This dimension considers contracts, agreements, and managing supplier performance.
Organizations and People: Deals with the structure of the organization, its culture, roles, responsibilities,
skills, and competencies needed to support service management.
Value Streams and Processes: Defines how an organization's activities are organized, including workflows,
controls, and procedures, to deliver value.
Information and Technology: This dimension encompasses the information and knowledge necessary to
manage services, as well as the technologies, architecture, data, and applications that support service
management. Critically, it also includes considerations for data governance, security, and compliance.
Data management within compliance regulations falls squarely under the Information and Technology
dimension. Industry regulations often dictate how data must be handled, stored, processed, and secured. This
dimension is responsible for ensuring that the technologies used align with these requirements, including
aspects like data encryption, access control, audit trails, and data retention policies. Meeting industry-specific
compliance requirements related to data falls under the domain of information and technology. It
encompasses the technologies and frameworks that govern information flow, security, and governance.
While the other dimensions can indirectly influence data management, the primary responsibility for
managing data in compliance with industry regulations resides within the Information and Technology
dimension.
For further information, you can consult the official ITIL 4 publications or reputable IT service management
resources. Some relevant links include:
Axelos (Official ITIL Website): https://www.axelos.com/

ITIL Foundation Handbook: (Search for "ITIL 4 Foundation Handbook" to find various vendors offering study
guides and resources based on the official handbook)
Question: 234 CertyIQ
When using the ITIL continual improvement model, which information should be produced by an organization in
order to understand where the organization is now?
A.Business objectives
B.Improvement plans
C.Assessment results
D.KPI reports
Answer: C
Explanation:
The correct answer is C. Assessment results.
The ITIL Continual Improvement Model (CIM) begins with understanding the current state. This is crucial
because you can't effectively improve something without knowing its present condition. Assessment results,
like audits, surveys, maturity assessments, and benchmarking reports, directly provide this information. These
results highlight the current strengths, weaknesses, opportunities, and threats (SWOT) related to the IT
services and processes being examined. They offer a baseline for measuring future improvements.
Option A (Business objectives) is important for knowing where you want to be, but it doesn't describe the
current state. Option B (Improvement plans) outlines how you intend to get there, not where you currently are.
Option D (KPI reports) can contribute to understanding the current state, but they are just one piece of the
puzzle. Assessment results encompass a broader and more holistic view of the organization's capabilities and
performance.
Therefore, to "understand where the organization is now," assessment results are the most direct and
comprehensive source of information within the ITIL continual improvement model. They provide the objective
data necessary for identifying areas needing improvement and establishing a starting point for the
improvement journey.
For further research:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Handbook: Provides a comprehensive overview of the ITIL 4 framework, including
the Continual Improvement Model.
Official ITIL Website: (https://www.axelos.com/) Offers resources, publications, and training related to ITIL.
Question: 235 CertyIQ
Which guiding principle leads to a faster response to customer needs by timeboxing activities and learning from
the outputs of previous activities?
A.Focus on value
B.Progress iteratively with feedback
C.Collaborate and promote visibility
D.Optimize and automate
Answer: B

Explanation:
The correct answer is B. Progress iteratively with feedback directly addresses the scenario described. This
principle emphasizes breaking down complex initiatives into smaller, manageable iterations. "Timeboxing
activities" is a core tenet of iterative approaches, where each iteration has a fixed duration.
The phrase "learning from the outputs of previous activities" highlights the feedback loop inherent in iterative
development. Each iteration provides an opportunity to gather feedback and incorporate lessons learned into
subsequent iterations. This allows for continuous improvement and faster adaptation to changing customer
needs. By continuously assessing and refining the product or service, the IT team can ensure they are
delivering value in the most efficient way possible. Iterative approaches contrast sharply with waterfall
methods, which involve large, upfront planning phases.
The "Focus on value" principle (A) is crucial but doesn't inherently dictate the speed of response. While all
improvements should ultimately deliver value, it doesn't specify an approach for accelerating that delivery.
"Collaborate and promote visibility" (C) is important for team cohesion and informed decision-making, but it
doesn't directly address the efficiency gains from iterative development. Likewise, "Optimize and automate"
(D) aims to improve efficiency, but primarily by streamlining existing processes rather than through iterative
improvement cycles. The iterative principle, with its focus on short cycles, feedback loops and adapting
quickly to changing customer needs allows for faster and more effective responses. The other principles
support this but aren't at the core of the scenario.
https://www.axelos.com/guidance-and-best-practice/itil-4/itil-4-guiding-
principleshttps://www.bmc.com/blogs/itil-4-guiding-principles/
Question: 236 CertyIQ
Which practice has a purpose that includes maximizing the number of successful additions, modifications, or
removals of anything that could have an effect on a service?
A.Service request management
B.Incident management
C.Service desk
D.Change enablement
Answer: D
Explanation:
The correct answer is D, Change Enablement. Here's why:
Change enablement (formerly change management) is specifically concerned with controlling changes to
infrastructure, applications, and documentation to minimize risk while maximizing successful service
transitions. The core purpose revolves around supporting the delivery of changes smoothly and efficiently.
The statement aligns directly with this aim by emphasizing "maximizing the number of successful additions,
modifications, or removals."
A. Service Request Management focuses on fulfilling pre-approved service requests, not on managing
broader changes with potential service impact.
B. Incident Management is reactive, addressing disruptions or degradations of service. It doesn't primarily
focus on planning and implementing changes to minimize future incidents.
C. The Service Desk is a function that provides a single point of contact for users, and is not directly
responsible for the success of service changes.

Change enablement aims to balance speed and stability, adopting a risk-based approach to manage the
change process. This ensures successful change implementation while minimizing potential negative impacts
on services. Efficient change enablement helps to keep services aligned with business needs and allows for
the rapid adoption of new technologies. The practice involves assessment, authorization, and planning to
ensure that changes are implemented with minimal disruption and maximum effectiveness.
For further reading and reference, consult the official ITIL 4 Foundation documentation or explore AXELOS's
resources: https://www.axelos.com/ and also consider the ITIL Foundation Handbook.
Question: 237 CertyIQ
In which situation will incident management USUALLY use a separate process?
A.Where no target resolution time exists
B.For low impact incidents
C.Where the cause must be diagnosed
D.For information security incidents
Answer: D
Explanation:
The correct answer is D, "For information security incidents." Here's why:
Incident Management aims to restore normal service operation as quickly as possible, minimizing the impact
on business operations. However, security incidents often necessitate a different, more specialized approach.
Information security incidents, such as data breaches or malware infections, often require a coordinated
response involving security specialists, legal teams, and potentially law enforcement. They frequently trigger
a separate incident response plan, following frameworks like NIST or SANS. These plans have different
priorities than routine service restoration. The focus shifts towards containment, eradication, and recovery of
compromised systems and data, as well as investigation and reporting to comply with regulatory
requirements (e.g., GDPR, HIPAA).
While incident management handles disruptions to IT services, security incidents may stem from
vulnerabilities, exploits, or malicious activities that require in-depth forensic analysis and specialized
handling. Merely restoring the service without addressing the underlying security issue leaves the
organization vulnerable to future attacks.
The other options are less likely to require a separate process:
A. Where no target resolution time exists: The absence of a target resolution time doesn't necessitate a
completely separate process, but rather indicates a need to define or adjust service level agreements (SLAs).
B. For low impact incidents: Low-impact incidents are generally handled through the standard incident
management process, perhaps with a lower priority.
C. Where the cause must be diagnosed: Diagnosing the root cause is a normal part of incident management,
especially when transitioning to problem management.
Therefore, information security incidents often fall outside the scope of standard incident management due to
their unique requirements and potential severity, leading to the activation of a separate incident response
process managed by a specialized team.
Supporting links:

NIST Computer Security Incident Handling Guide:
https://nvlpubs.nist.gov/nistpubs/SpecialPublications/NIST.SP.800-61r2.pdf
SANS Institute Incident Handler's Handbook: https://www.sans.org/reading-
room/whitepapers/incident/incident-handlers-handbook-33901
Question: 238 CertyIQ
Which practice minimizes the impact on normal service operation by managing resources in response to unplanned
reductions in service quality?
A.Incident management
B.Change enablement
C.Service level management
D.Continual improvement
Answer: A
Explanation:
Here's a detailed justification for why Incident Management is the correct answer:
The scenario describes a situation where service quality unexpectedly degrades, and the goal is to minimize
the disruption to normal operations. Incident Management is the practice directly responsible for responding
to and resolving such unplanned interruptions or degradations to service. Its primary objective is to restore
normal service operation as quickly as possible and minimize adverse impacts on business operations,
ensuring user productivity isn't significantly hampered.
Change Enablement (formerly Change Management) focuses on managing changes proactively to minimize
risks. While related to service stability, it doesn't directly address the immediate response to an incident.
Service Level Management defines service levels and manages performance against those agreed levels, but
it isn't the immediate reactive practice. Continual Improvement focuses on identifying and implementing
improvements over time, making it a long-term strategy rather than a direct response to service degradations.
When a service incident occurs (e.g., a server outage, a network failure, or a software bug causing errors),
Incident Management processes are activated. These processes include incident identification, logging,
categorization, prioritization, diagnosis, resolution, and closure. Effective incident management utilizes
resources (personnel, tools, knowledge base) to diagnose the problem, implement workarounds, and
ultimately restore the service to its normal operational state. The goal is to minimize downtime and the
negative impact on users and business processes.
The other options don't directly address the reactive component described. While good change enablement
practices can reduce the likelihood of incidents, and service level management helps define what "normal
service" means and tracks performance against it, and continual improvement helps improve all aspects of
the service, only incident management handles the immediate response and restoration of service when it's
unexpectedly degraded.
Therefore, Incident Management directly addresses the scenario by focusing on restoring service operation
and minimizing the impact of unplanned service disruptions.
Authoritative Links:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Syllabus: This syllabus defines the scope of the ITIL 4 Foundation certification
and provides an overview of Incident Management. (Purchase required: https://www.axelos.com/)
ITIL Foundation Handbook: A comprehensive guide to ITIL 4 Foundation principles. (Purchase required).
Although not freely available online, most IT professionals studying ITIL 4 use it, and it provides in-depth

explanations of all practices.
Question: 239 CertyIQ
Which practice makes use of methods from Lean, Agile and DevOps?
A.Service desk
B.Continual improvement
C.Problem management
D.Incident management
Answer: B
Explanation:
The correct answer is B. Continual Improvement. Here's why:
Continual improvement is fundamentally about identifying, analyzing, and implementing enhancements to
services, practices, or any element of the service value system. It's an ongoing process, not a one-time event.
This inherently aligns with the principles of Lean, Agile, and DevOps.
Lean: Lean focuses on eliminating waste and maximizing value. Continual improvement actively seeks out
inefficiencies and areas for optimization, directly reflecting Lean principles. https://www.lean.org/
Agile: Agile emphasizes iterative development, flexibility, and responding to change. Continual improvement
adopts a similar mindset by encouraging small, frequent improvements rather than large, infrequent
overhauls. https://www.agilealliance.org/
DevOps: DevOps promotes collaboration and automation across the entire service lifecycle. Continual
improvement fosters a culture of feedback and experimentation, which are key to DevOps success. It also
involves automating improvements to increase efficiency. https://www.atlassian.com/devops
The other options are less directly related to the core principles of all three methodologies:
Service Desk: While the service desk can contribute to identifying improvement opportunities, its primary
focus is on providing support and resolving user issues. It utilizes improvement suggestions but isn't the
improvement practice itself.
Problem Management: Problem management aims to prevent incidents from recurring. While it involves
analysis and improvement, it's reactive rather than proactive and continuous like the continual improvement
practice.
Incident Management: Incident management focuses on restoring service as quickly as possible. While
improvements may stem from incident analysis, it doesn't encompass the broader, ongoing, and cross-
functional improvement approach that continual improvement does.
In conclusion, continual improvement is the only practice listed that inherently embodies and leverages the
core methodologies of Lean, Agile, and DevOps to drive ongoing value enhancement within an organization. It
is the active, iterative, and collaborative process that turns ideas into actionable enhancements, reflecting the
spirit of all three frameworks.
Question: 240 CertyIQ
Identify the missing word in the following sentence:
Sponsor is the role that authorizes budget for service [?].
A.value

B.consumption
C.management
D.provision
Answer: B
Explanation:
Here's a detailed justification for why "consumption" is the correct answer:
The sentence focuses on the role of the Sponsor in the context of service budgeting. The Sponsor authorizes
the budget for something directly related to service delivery. The crucial element here is what the budget is
for.
Why "consumption" is correct: Service consumption refers to the use of a service by its consumers. A
sponsor authorizes a budget for this consumption ensuring adequate resources are available for service
delivery. Budgeting specifically for service consumption implies managing the costs associated with the
volume, intensity, or features used by consumers. The sponsor aims to ensure the budget covers the cost of
providing the service as it's being used, thereby aligning financial resources with actual service usage.
Why the other options are incorrect:
Value: While a sponsor wants to create value, the budget isn't specifically for "value" itself but for the
resources to enable the creation of value, specifically as users consume the service.
Management: A service provider internally manage the operations of service. Sponsor is responsible for
providing the budget.
Provision: Service provision refers to the activities to provide the service to the user, meaning setting up a
service. The budget for service provision is for the deployment, configuration, and setup.
In ITIL 4, the focus is on value co-creation through services. Service consumption is a key activity where value
is realized. The sponsor's role in budgeting for consumption reflects the importance of aligning financial
resources with actual service usage, fostering effective value creation. The budget ensures appropriate
support, monitoring, and enhancement occur during consumption.
Therefore, the completed sentence, "Sponsor is the role that authorizes budget for service consumption,"
accurately reflects the financial responsibilities associated with ensuring services are adequately resourced
to meet the needs of service consumers.

related to sponsors, service consumption, and value.

Study Guide.) These often provide explanations of ITIL concepts and the roles involved in service
management.
Question: 241 CertyIQ
Which statement about service offerings is CORRECT?
A.The same product can be used as a basis for more than one service offering
B.Service offerings include the transfer of goods from the consumer to the provider
C.Service offerings describe how providers and consumers cooperate to co-create value

D.Each service should be described to consumers as a single service offering
Answer: A
Explanation:
The correct answer is A. The same product can be used as a basis for more than one service offering.
Here's why:
Service Offerings defined: A service offering is a specific combination of services designed to address the
needs of a particular consumer group. It details what the provider offers, how it's delivered, and how value is
created.
Products as the Foundation: A product is a configuration of an organization's resources designed to offer
value to a consumer. A single product, such as software or hardware, can be utilized in various ways to create
different service offerings tailored to different customer needs.
Multiple offerings from one product: Imagine an organization sells cloud storage. The basic storage itself is
the product. Different service offerings could include: a "Basic Backup" offering with limited storage and
simple recovery, a "Premium Backup" offering with larger storage, faster recovery and advanced security, and
an "Archival Service" offering intended for long term inactive data at a much lower cost. All three originate
from the same storage product.
Why other answers are incorrect:
B: Service offerings generally involve the transfer of goods from the provider to the consumer, not the other
way around. While consumers might provide input or data, the core offering flows from the provider.
C: This is closer to the definition of service relationship management - service offerings are a component of
service relationship management, but the offering itself doesn't describe the cooperation, the service
agreement that comes with it does.
D: Each service may be described to consumers as a single service offering, but not should be. A large
complex service can be broken into service offerings tailored for different consumers.
Authoritative Links:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Syllabus: This is the official source for ITIL 4 definitions and concepts.
Official ITIL 4 Foundation Study Guides: Search for authorized study guides to gain more insight.
Question: 242 CertyIQ
Which can a change schedule be used for?
A.Speeding up the planning and authorization of emergency changes
B.Providing information about deployed changes to help manage incidents and problems
C.Providing a means of initiating and assessing normal changes
D.Tracking and managing improvement ideas from identification through to final action
Answer: B
Explanation:
The correct answer is B: Providing information about deployed changes to help manage incidents and
problems. A change schedule is a document (or tool) that outlines planned changes, their timelines, and
dependencies. Its primary purpose is to enhance awareness and coordination. In the context of incident and
problem management, knowing what changes have been recently implemented provides crucial context. If an
incident arises shortly after a change deployment, the change schedule immediately flags that deployment as

a potential root cause. This allows incident responders to focus their troubleshooting efforts, potentially
speeding up resolution. Similarly, for problem management, the change schedule aids in identifying patterns
and potential systemic issues related to changes.
Option A is incorrect because emergency changes, by their nature, require expedited processes, not relying
on a pre-defined schedule. Option C is not ideal, while a change schedule informs normal changes, it's not the
main tool for initiation and assessment, which primarily relies on change enablement practices. Option D is
unrelated; improvement ideas are managed through a separate process, not a change schedule. ITIL 4
emphasizes the value of transparency and collaboration. The change schedule fosters this by making change-
related information accessible to relevant stakeholders. Ultimately, the change schedule contributes to better
incident and problem resolution by providing crucial historical information about changes, enhancing
situational awareness and guiding diagnostic processes.
For further research, you can consult these resources:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Handbook: Provides detailed explanations of ITIL 4 concepts.
Official ITIL Website: https://www.axelos.com/ - For official definitions and best practices.
Question: 243 CertyIQ
Which is part of the value proposition of a service?
A.Costs removed from the consumer by the service
B.Costs imposed on the consumer by the service
C.Outputs of the service received by the consumer
D.Risks imposed on the consumer by the service
Answer: A
Explanation:
The correct answer, A, aligns with the ITIL 4 definition of value. Value, in the context of ITIL 4, is about utility
(fitness for purpose) and warranty (fitness for use). A key component of providing value is reducing costs for
the consumer. A service that effectively removes costs associated with a business activity contributes directly
to its utility, making it more valuable.
Answer C, while partially correct, only focuses on the outputs. While outputs contribute to the service's utility,
value is not solely determined by the outputs themselves. The value proposition encompasses the holistic
benefit received, including the overall financial impact. A service could have excellent outputs but still not be
considered valuable if its associated costs outweigh the benefits.
Option B is incorrect because imposing costs on the consumer reduces value, not contributes to it. Similarly,
option D, imposing risks, directly reduces the warranty aspect of value. Increased risks negatively impact the
reliability and security of the service. Therefore, they diminish its perceived value.
A value proposition articulates the benefits that a customer can expect from using a service. These benefits
invariably include a positive impact on the consumer’s cost structure. Therefore, cost reduction is a crucial
element of creating and delivering value in a service. Services that lower overhead, reduce labor costs,
improve efficiency, and minimize capital expenditures are considered valuable, therefore making it a part of
the value proposition.The official ITIL 4 Foundation guidance emphasizes the importance of understanding
how services contribute to value co-creation, where both the service provider and consumer play a role in
defining and realizing value. The consumer assesses the service based on its perceived benefits, including the
costs it helps avoid or eliminate.
Further research can be found on AXELOS's website (the official source for ITIL): https://www.axelos.com/

and in ITIL 4 Foundation publications. Also, explore sources like the ITIL Foundation Handbook.
Question: 244 CertyIQ
Why should a service level manager carry out regular service reviews?
A.To ensure that agreements are written simply and are easy to understand
B.To collect information about service consumer goals and objectives
C.To capture information about service issues and performance against agreed goals
D.To ensure continual improvement of services, so that they meet the evolving needs of service consumers
Answer: C
Explanation:
The most appropriate answer is C: To capture information about service issues and performance against
agreed goals.
Service level reviews are a core function of service level management within ITIL 4. Their primary purpose is
to actively monitor and evaluate the service's performance against the service level agreements (SLAs) that
have been established with the service consumer. By carrying out these reviews regularly, the service level
manager can identify trends, pinpoint areas of underperformance, and document any service disruptions or
issues encountered by the consumer. This provides a clear picture of whether the service is meeting the
agreed-upon goals, such as availability, response times, resolution times, and customer satisfaction.
Analyzing this data enables proactive steps to be taken to address potential problems before they
significantly impact the consumer and to refine the service delivery to better align with expectations. Regular
reviews also provide a valuable opportunity to receive direct feedback from the consumer, further informing
service improvement efforts.
While D (To ensure continual improvement of services, so that they meet the evolving needs of service
consumers) is also a correct statement and directly benefited from the feedback of regular service reviews, C
is the most direct purpose of a service level manager conducting regular service reviews.
Here are some authoritative links for further research:
AXELOS Official Website: https://www.axelos.com/ (Provider of ITIL guidance)
ITIL 4 Foundation Handbook: This handbook provides detailed information on ITIL 4 concepts.
Question: 245 CertyIQ
A flaw in an application could cause a service to fail. IT staff are actively analyzing the application to try and
understand what is going on.
What is the correct name for this type of flaw?
A.Problem
B.Incident
C.Event
D.Known error
Answer: A
Explanation:

The correct answer is A, Problem. Here's why:
A problem in ITIL 4 is defined as a cause, or potential cause, of one or more incidents. In this scenario, the flaw
in the application is a potential cause of a service failure (which would manifest as an incident). The IT staff
are actively analyzing the cause (the flaw), making it a problem management activity. Problem management
focuses on identifying, analyzing, and managing the underlying causes of incidents to prevent them from
recurring.
An incident (B) is an unplanned interruption to a service, or reduction in the quality of a service. While a
service failure could lead to an incident, the scenario describes the underlying cause being investigated, not
the service disruption itself. The described situation precedes a potential incident.
An event (C) is any occurrence that has significance for the management of IT infrastructure or the delivery of
IT service. Events can be informational, warning, or exceptional. While the application flaw might generate an
event log, simply identifying it as an event doesn't address the proactive investigation of the cause.
A known error (D) is a problem that has been analyzed and understood, but for which a resolution has not yet
been implemented. The scenario describes active analysis to understand what is going on, implying the flaw is
not yet a known error. It's in the problem investigation phase.
Therefore, because the IT staff are investigating the cause of a potential service failure, the flaw is most
accurately classified as a problem. Problem management processes would then be used to identify, analyze,
and ultimately resolve the flaw to prevent future incidents. The IT staff are trying to move from a potential
problem to identifying the root cause, and then creating a known error record.For further reading on these
definitions, consult the official ITIL 4 Foundation publications or resources such as:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation: https://www.axelos.com/ (Official source, requires purchase)
Simplified ITIL 4 Glossary: https://www.bmc.com/blogs/itil-4-glossary/ (provides definitions).
Question: 246 CertyIQ
Which value chain activity ensures that ongoing service activity meets user expectations?
A.Plan
B.Engage
C.Obtain/build
D.Deliver and support
Answer: D
Explanation:
The correct answer is D, Deliver and Support. The ITIL 4 value chain activity "Deliver and Support" directly
focuses on ensuring that services are delivered and supported according to agreed specifications and service
levels. This activity encompasses tasks such as incident management, service requests, problem
management, and service desk functions. Its core purpose is to ensure that users receive the value promised
by the service, meeting their expectations for functionality, availability, and performance. Specifically, it
addresses ongoing service activity by continually monitoring service performance, resolving issues, and
providing user assistance. This iterative process allows organizations to adapt to changing user needs and
maintain a high level of user satisfaction. While "Engage" is important for understanding user needs and
gathering feedback, it primarily occurs before and after service delivery. "Obtain/build" focuses on service
development, and "Plan" sets the strategic direction, but "Deliver and Support" is where ongoing service
experience is directly managed and improved to meet user expectations. Therefore, "Deliver and Support"
directly contributes to ensuring that the ongoing service activity meets user expectations through continuous

monitoring, support, and problem resolution.

AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Handbook
https://www.axelos.com/
Question: 247 CertyIQ
Which practice's purpose includes creating closer, more collaborative relationships?
A.Supplier management
B.Information security management
C.Release management
D.Service configuration management
Answer: A
Explanation:
The correct answer is A, Supplier Management, because its core purpose is to ensure the organization and its
suppliers work collaboratively to provide seamless, high-quality services. This involves establishing and
nurturing strong relationships, built on trust, communication, and shared goals.
Let's analyze why the other options are less fitting:
B. Information Security Management: Primarily focused on protecting information assets and minimizing
security risks. While collaboration is important for security, the closer, more collaborative relationships aspect
is not its primary objective.
C. Release Management: Concentrates on making new and changed services and features available for use.
Collaboration is vital for successful releases, but the core focus lies on planning, testing, and deploying
changes efficiently.
D. Service Configuration Management: Aims to ensure accurate information about the configuration items
and their relationships. This contributes to service stability and problem resolution, but its main focus is not
relationship building.
Supplier Management inherently demands strong relationships. Organizations rely on suppliers for various
resources, from hardware and software to cloud services and expertise. Effective supplier management
involves:
1. Clear Communication: Open and honest dialogue to ensure alignment and understanding.
2. Contract Management: Agreements that define responsibilities and expectations.
3. Performance Monitoring: Tracking supplier performance and providing feedback.
4. Relationship Building: Cultivating trust and collaboration through regular interaction.
5. Strategic Partnerships: Building long-term relationships with key suppliers.
In the context of cloud computing, supplier management becomes even more crucial. Organizations often rely
heavily on cloud providers for infrastructure, platform, and software services. Therefore, a strong,
collaborative relationship with cloud providers is essential for ensuring service reliability, security, and cost-
effectiveness. This includes proactively discussing service level agreements, security protocols, and future
needs to ensure both parties are aligned in creating a successful partnership.Here is an authoritative link for
further research on the ITIL 4 practice guides. You'll find the supplier management guide
within:https://axelos.com/(Navigate to the ITIL 4 section and look for practice guides.)

Question: 248 CertyIQ
Which TWO are inputs to the service value system?
1. Demand
2. Products
3. Value
4. Opportunity
A.1 and 2
B.2 and 3
C.3 and 4
D.1 and 4
Answer: D
Explanation:
The correct answer is D: 1 and 4 (Demand and Opportunity) because these are explicitly defined as inputs to
the Service Value System (SVS) in ITIL 4.
The Service Value System (SVS) represents how all the components and activities of an organization work
together as a system to enable value creation. Inputs are essential elements that trigger and shape the
activities within the SVS.
Opportunity represents options or possibilities to add value, or otherwise improve the organization. It can
include market trends, technological advancements, regulatory changes, or unmet customer needs. The SVS
needs to be aware of opportunities to develop valuable services.
Demand represents the need or desire for products and services from internal and external customers.
Understanding demand is critical for the SVS to focus its efforts on delivering services that are relevant and
meet customer expectations.
Products (option 2) are outputs from the SVS, specifically from the value chain activities. They are what are
created to satisfy demand and capitalize on opportunities.
Value (option 3) is the ultimate outcome or benefit realized by the consumer. It is the goal of the SVS, not an
input to it. The SVS exists to create value.
Therefore, demand and opportunity directly influence the direction and activities within the SVS, while
products are a result, and value is the objective. This makes option D the accurate selection.For further
information, refer to the ITIL 4 Foundation guidance which explicitly describes opportunity and demand as key
inputs to the SVS.Specifically, review the ITIL 4 Foundation syllabus and the ITIL 4 Foundation: ITIL 4 Edition
textbook published by AXELOS.
AXELOS is the official source of ITIL guidance, and their materials should be considered authoritative. While
not directly linkable online, a search using keywords like "ITIL 4 service value system inputs" can uncover
helpful extracts and explanations from these texts on various IT service management resource sites.
Question: 249 CertyIQ
What role would be MOST suitable for someone with experience of managing relationships with various
stakeholders, including suppliers and business managers?

A.Service level manager
B.Service desk agent
C.Change authority
D.Problem analyst
Answer: A
Explanation:
The Service Level Manager is the most suitable role due to their core responsibility of managing relationships
with various stakeholders, including suppliers and business managers. A key function of a Service Level
Manager is to negotiate, agree upon, and monitor Service Level Agreements (SLAs). These agreements define
the level of service to be provided to the business, involving discussions and agreements with business
managers to understand their needs and expectations. Furthermore, the Service Level Manager is responsible
for managing Underpinning Contracts (UCs) and Operational Level Agreements (OLAs). UCs are agreements
with suppliers necessary to deliver services, requiring the Service Level Manager to manage the supplier
relationship and ensure they meet agreed-upon obligations. OLAs define internal responsibilities within the IT
organization. By proactively managing relationships and agreements, the Service Level Manager ensures that
IT services align with business needs and are delivered effectively.
A Service Desk Agent primarily focuses on resolving incidents and fulfilling service requests, limiting their
stakeholder management scope. Change Authorities mainly assess and authorize changes, with a narrower
focus compared to the Service Level Manager's broader relationship management responsibilities. While
Problem Analysts investigate and resolve problems, their interaction with stakeholders is primarily technical
and problem-focused, not relationship-driven in the same way. The Service Level Manager's role inherently
involves nurturing and maintaining relationships with both internal and external stakeholders to ensure
service delivery meets expectations. Their proficiency in understanding and documenting business
requirements, negotiating terms, and proactively managing performance directly leverages experience in
stakeholder relationship management.
ITIL 4 Foundation: ITIL® Foundation: Study guideITIL 4: Key concepts of service value system
Question: 250 CertyIQ
Which is the addition, modification or removal of anything that could have an effect on services?
A.A change
B.An event
C.A service request
D.A problem
Answer: A
Explanation:
The correct answer is A. Change. A change, within the ITIL 4 framework, is defined as the addition,
modification, or removal of anything that could have a direct or indirect effect on services. This definition
directly aligns with the question's description. Changes are fundamental to service management as they
enable improvement, innovation, and adaptation to evolving business needs and technological advancements.
ITIL emphasizes that managing changes effectively is crucial to minimize disruptions and ensure service
stability. A well-managed change process includes activities like assessing the impact of a proposed change,
planning the implementation, testing, and communicating the change to stakeholders. Proper change

management helps prevent incidents and problems that might arise from poorly executed modifications.
An event (B) is an occurrence that has significance for the management of IT infrastructure or the delivery of
services. While an event can trigger a change, it isn't itself the addition, modification, or removal. A service
request (C) is a formal request from a user for something to be provided – for example, a request for
information or to reset a password. A problem (D) is a cause, or potential cause, of one or more incidents.
Although changes can address problems, the problem itself isn't the action of adding, modifying, or removing.
Therefore, only the definition of a 'change' precisely matches the description provided in the question.
In cloud computing environments, changes are particularly prevalent due to the dynamic nature of resources
and services. Virtual machines might be resized, software versions upgraded, or new services deployed, all of
which constitute changes that must be managed carefully. Without diligent change management, cloud
environments become prone to misconfiguration, downtime, and security vulnerabilities.
Further research on ITIL 4 change management can be found at:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation materials (official source). (Note: these are usually behind a paywall or require
certification access)
Various ITIL 4 training providers and online resources often have simplified explanations of change
management: Search "ITIL 4 change management" on reputable IT service management websites.
Question: 251 CertyIQ
Which guiding principle recommends consideration of the four dimensions in order to make something as effective
and as useful as it needs to be?
A.Focus on value
B.Start where you are
C.Think and work holistically
D.Optimize and automate
Answer: C
Explanation:
The correct answer is C. Think and work holistically.
The ITIL 4 guiding principle "Think and work holistically" emphasizes that service management activities
should consider all relevant aspects and dimensions of a situation to ensure the desired outcome is achieved.
This principle directly aligns with the concept of the four dimensions of service management: organizations
and people, information and technology, partners and suppliers, and value streams and processes. By
considering all four dimensions, organizations can develop a more comprehensive understanding of how
different elements interact and influence the service value system. This holistic view allows for better
decision-making, improved service design, and more effective problem-solving.
Focusing on value (A) is important, but doesn't explicitly link to considering the four dimensions during
implementation. Starting where you are (B) is also a good principle, but it speaks to incremental improvement,
not the specific consideration of dimensions. Optimizing and automating (D) is about efficiency, but efficiency
without considering all the dimensions can lead to unintended consequences. "Think and work holistically"
ensures that optimization and automation are implemented in a way that benefits the entire service value
system. This integrated approach is critical for maximizing effectiveness and utility. It ensures alignment with
business goals, regulatory compliance, and customer needs. Without holistically considering the four
dimensions, isolated improvements can negatively impact other parts of the system, resulting in sub-optimal

results.
Therefore, the "Think and work holistically" guiding principle directly recommends the consideration of the
four dimensions of service management to make something as effective and as useful as it needs to be.
https://www.axelos.com/ (Official ITIL source; requires subscription or purchase for detailed
content)https://www.bmc.com/blogs/itil-4-guiding-principles/ (Provides explanation of ITIL 4 guiding
principles)
Question: 252 CertyIQ
Which practice is MOST LIKELY to make use of artificial intelligence, robotic process automation, and chatbots?
A.Service desk
B.Continual improvement
C.Problem management
D.Incident management
Answer: A
Explanation:
The correct answer is A: Service Desk.
Here's why: Service desks are highly customer-facing and handle a large volume of routine inquiries and
requests. This makes them a prime candidate for automation using AI, RPA, and chatbots.
AI: Can be used for sentiment analysis to understand customer emotions, automate ticket categorization and
prioritization, and provide intelligent self-service options through knowledge base suggestions.
RPA: Automates repetitive tasks like password resets, account unlocks, and basic information retrieval,
freeing up service desk agents for more complex issues.
Chatbots: Provide instant responses to common questions, guide users through troubleshooting steps, and
escalate complex issues to human agents when necessary.
Continual improvement (B), while potentially benefiting from data analysis powered by AI, focuses on overall
process enhancement rather than direct customer interaction and automation of routine tasks. Problem
management (C) benefits from AI for root cause analysis, but doesn't have the high-volume, repetitive tasks
ideal for RPA and chatbots. Incident management (D), similar to problem management, focuses on restoring
service quickly, and while AI can aid in diagnosis, the breadth of service desk automation applications is
greater. The high volume of tickets and standard requests that the service desk manages makes AI and
automation essential for efficiency and customer satisfaction. The service desk can utilize these technologies
to personalize interactions, predict customer needs, and improve overall service delivery.
Relevant links:
ITIL 4 Foundation: No specific link directly addresses this use case, but understanding the Service Value
System and Practices is key. Search for ITIL 4 online courses and resources.
Robotic Process Automation (RPA): https://www.uipath.com/rpa/robotic-process-automation
Artificial Intelligence (AI) in Customer Service: https://www.zendesk.com/blog/ai-customer-service/
Chatbots for Service Desk: Search "chatbots for IT service desk" for various vendor solutions and use cases.
Question: 253 CertyIQ

What is a problem that has been analyzed but has not been resolved?
A.Workaround
B.Incident
C.Known error
D.Risk
Answer: C
Explanation:
Here's a detailed justification for why "Known error" is the correct answer in the context of ITIL 4 Foundation,
explaining why the other options are incorrect, and providing resources for further study:
The core concept here revolves around how ITIL handles deviations from expected service operation. A known
error is the status assigned to a problem that has been diagnosed to its root cause, but for which a permanent
resolution is not yet available. It's an acknowledgment that the issue is understood, but fixing it is pending.
The ITIL framework utilizes the "Known Error" status to proactively mitigate the impact of recurring problems
while a permanent resolution is being developed. This proactive approach is vital for maintaining service
stability and minimizing disruptions to end-users.
Now, let's examine why the other options are incorrect:
A. Workaround: A workaround is a temporary solution to reduce or eliminate the impact of an incident or
problem. It doesn't address the root cause, but rather provides a way to continue working despite the issue.
It's a band-aid, not a fix.
B. Incident: An incident is an unplanned interruption to an IT service or reduction in the quality of an IT service.
While incidents may stem from problems, an incident itself doesn't represent a problem that has been
analyzed. An incident triggers the problem management process, and that process might eventually lead to
the identification of a known error.
D. Risk: A risk is a potential event that could cause harm or loss, or make it more difficult to achieve
objectives. While a problem can certainly pose a risk to service delivery, the term "risk" itself doesn't describe
a problem that has been investigated but not resolved. Risk management is related but distinct from problem
management.
In summary, a problem identified as having been analyzed but not resolved perfectly describes a "Known
Error," a key element in ITIL's problem management practice. By identifying and documenting these known
errors, organizations can improve incident resolution times, prevent similar incidents from occurring, and
ultimately improve service quality.
Here are authoritative links for further research on this topic:
1. Axelos (Official ITIL Website): While direct links to specific ITIL 4 content require
registration/purchase, the Axelos website provides the most comprehensive and authoritative
information on ITIL concepts. https://www.axelos.com/
2. AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Book: This book serves as the official guide and provides a complete
overview of the ITIL 4 framework.
3. ITIL Foundation Handbook: (Van Haren Publishing) Many publishers provide ITIL related guides. You
can research reputable publishers for more information.
By consulting these sources, you can gain a deeper understanding of ITIL 4 Foundation principles and
practices.

Question: 254 CertyIQ
Which is described by the 'organizations and people' dimension of service management?
A.Workflows and controls
B.Communication and collaboration
C.Inputs and outputs
D.Contracts and agreements
Answer: B
Explanation:
The correct answer, B (Communication and collaboration), aligns perfectly with the 'organizations and people'
dimension of service management within ITIL 4. This dimension focuses on the human element of service
delivery. It emphasizes how an organization is structured, its roles and responsibilities, and the required skills
and competencies of the workforce. Crucially, it also highlights the importance of effective communication
and collaboration between individuals, teams, and even external stakeholders.
Option A (Workflows and controls) is more closely associated with processes and value streams. Option C
(Inputs and outputs) relates to information and technology, and Option D (Contracts and agreements) falls
under partners and suppliers.
The 'organizations and people' dimension underscores that technology alone isn't sufficient for successful
service management. A well-defined organizational structure coupled with a culture of open communication
and effective teamwork are critical enablers. This includes fostering a collaborative environment where
knowledge is shared freely and individuals are empowered to contribute their expertise. Without strong
communication channels and collaborative practices, even the best technological solutions and processes can
fail to deliver expected business outcomes. Essentially, this ITIL dimension focuses on the essential elements
of creating a service-oriented culture within an organization and emphasizes the importance of
communication and collaboration to reach mutual goals. ITIL 4 recognizes that people and their interactions
are just as essential as the tools and processes utilized.
Further reading on this topic can be found at:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation materials: The official ITIL 4 Foundation documentation provides a comprehensive
explanation of all four dimensions of service management. (You typically need to purchase the manual)
Various articles and blogs on ITIL 4: Searching for "ITIL 4 organizations and people dimension" will provide
numerous resources.
Question: 255 CertyIQ
Which facilitates outcomes that customers want to achieve?
A.Service
B.Warranty
C.Organization
D.IT asset
Answer: A

Explanation:
The correct answer is A. Service.
A service, in the context of ITIL 4, is defined as a means of enabling value co-creation by facilitating outcomes
that customers want to achieve, without the customer having to manage specific costs and risks. The core of a
service lies in its ability to deliver value to the customer by helping them reach their desired results. This is
achieved by providing functionality and utility that meet the customer's needs.
Warranty, on the other hand, is a guarantee that a product or service will meet certain specifications and
perform as promised. It focuses on assurance and reliability, rather than the direct facilitation of outcomes.
Organizations are entities that consume and/or provide services but do not directly facilitate outcomes. IT
assets are valuable resources owned or controlled by an organization, but also do not directly facilitate
outcomes for customers. It's important to differentiate assets from services, as assets are simply components
that can be used by a service. The service leverages those assets to deliver value. The service, through its
functionality and utility, is therefore the element directly helping the customer to achieve desired outcomes.
A customer engages with a service to achieve a specific objective.
https://www.axelos.com/
Question: 256 CertyIQ
Which practice recommends that organizations develop competencies in techniques such as strength, weakness,
opportunity, and threat (SWOT) analysis, and balanced scorecards?
A.Incident management
B.Continual improvement
C.Service request management
D.Change enablement
Answer: B
Explanation:
The correct answer is B, Continual Improvement. Here's why:
Continual improvement is a practice in ITIL 4 that emphasizes the recurring organizational activity performed
at all levels to ensure that service management continually meets stakeholders’ expectations. It's about
regularly assessing and improving services, processes, and the organization itself. SWOT analysis and
balanced scorecards are tools directly used to understand the current state and identify areas for
enhancement.
SWOT analysis helps organizations understand their internal strengths and weaknesses as well as external
opportunities and threats, providing a strategic overview to guide improvement efforts. Balanced scorecards
provide a framework for translating an organization's strategic objectives into a set of performance measures
viewed from multiple perspectives (financial, customer, internal processes, learning and growth). The analysis
derived from SWOT allows the identification of improvement initiatives that address identified weaknesses,
leverage strengths, capitalize on opportunities, and mitigate threats. These findings feed directly into a
continual improvement register.
Incident management focuses on restoring service operations as quickly as possible. Service request
management handles routine user requests. Change enablement controls changes to services. While these
practices benefit from improvement, they don't directly involve the comprehensive analysis techniques
mentioned in the question. Continual improvement practice is specifically designed to use such

methodologies to drive consistent and sustained progress.
Further research on ITIL 4's continual improvement practice can be found on Axelos' official website and in
related ITIL 4 publications:
Axelos Official Website (Search for ITIL 4 continual improvement practice)
ITIL 4 Foundation Handbook (This is a sample link - search for authorized ITIL 4 Foundation publications)
Question: 257 CertyIQ
What is a cause, or potential cause, of one or more incidents?
A.A configuration item
B.A workaround
C.An incident
D.A problem
Answer: D
Explanation:
The correct answer is D. A problem. Here's why:
A problem, in ITIL 4, is defined as a cause, or potential cause, of one or more incidents. It represents an
underlying issue that, if not addressed, will continue to manifest as incidents. Incident management focuses
on restoring service quickly, while problem management focuses on identifying and resolving the root cause
to prevent future incidents.
Option A, a configuration item (CI), is a component that needs to be managed to deliver an IT service. A faulty
CI can cause an incident or a problem. However, it is not the definition of what a problem is.
Option B, a workaround, is a temporary solution to reduce or eliminate the impact of an incident or problem. It
doesn't address the root cause. It circumvents the issue.
Option C, an incident, is an unplanned interruption to an IT service or a reduction in the quality of an IT service.
While incidents are related to problems, they are the result of problems, not the cause of them. A single
problem can cause multiple incidents.
Therefore, only a problem fits the definition of a "cause, or potential cause, of one or more incidents." Problem
management activities are specifically designed to investigate and resolve these underlying causes, thereby
reducing the frequency and severity of future service disruptions.
Here are authoritative links for further research:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Guidance: This is the official source for ITIL 4 information. While you typically
need to purchase the manual, summaries and explanations are widely available online through reputable
training providers.
ITIL Foundation Exam Study Guide by Liz Gallacher: Many guides available on Amazon, etc. Search for most
recent published editions that align with ITIL 4.
Question: 258 CertyIQ
Which is a recommendation applying the guiding principle 'keep it simple and practical'?

A.Communicate in a way the audience can hear
B.Sometimes nothing from the current state can be re-used
C.If a practice is easier to follow it is more likely to be adopted
D.Fast does not mean incomplete
Answer: C
Explanation:
The correct answer is C: "If a practice is easier to follow it is more likely to be adopted." This aligns directly
with the guiding principle of "Keep it simple and practical." The core idea is to avoid unnecessary complexity
and focus on what delivers value in the most straightforward way. Simplicity fosters understanding, reduces
errors, and encourages wider adoption.
Option C highlights that when a practice is easy to understand and implement, it is more likely to be used
effectively and consistently. This directly translates to practical application because it reduces friction and
maximizes the chances of the practice successfully contributing to desired outcomes. Simplifying processes
helps to minimize training requirements, reduce the risk of misinterpretation, and increase overall efficiency.
A simple and practical practice is easier to integrate into existing workflows, reducing resistance to change
and improving user satisfaction.
Option A focuses on effective communication, which is related to clarity, but doesn't inherently address
simplification or practicality in the same way. Effective communication supports many guiding principles, but
is not solely related to 'Keep it simple and practical'.
Option B, asserting that nothing from the current state can be reused, goes against the principle. Reusing
existing assets, where appropriate, aligns with efficiency and avoiding unnecessary reinvention, making
things more practical. Throwing everything away and starting from scratch increases complexity and effort.
Option D, emphasizing that "fast does not mean incomplete," is a useful reminder regarding quality, but does
not directly connect with simplification or practicality as strongly as option C. It is more related to Value and
collaborate.Therefore, only option C directly reflects the philosophy of streamlining processes for ease of use
and implementation, essential for adhering to the "Keep it simple and practical" guiding principle in ITIL 4.
Supporting references (ITIL 4 Foundation Study Guides and related resources): There are no specific URL to
explain this, but searching 'ITIL 4 guiding principles' or ITIL official documentation for ITIL 4 foundation and
reviewing 'Keep it simple and practical' principle provides further understanding.
Question: 259 CertyIQ
Which practice has a purpose that includes responding to conditions that could lead to potential faults or
incidents?
A.Incident management
B.Service request management
C.Monitoring and event management
D.Change enablement
Answer: C
Explanation:
The correct answer is C, Monitoring and event management. Its core purpose is to systematically observe
services and service components, and to record and report changes of state as events. Crucially, it identifies

deviations from normal operation that could lead to incidents. This proactive stance distinguishes it from
Incident Management.
Incident Management focuses on reacting to disruptions that have already occurred, aiming to restore service
as quickly as possible. While incident management prevents further damage, it doesn't address the root cause
of potential future disruptions.
Service Request Management handles routine requests for services, information, or access. It does not
address underlying system conditions or potential fault detection.
Change Enablement focuses on managing the risk associated with changes. While it contributes to stability, it
doesn't actively monitor for conditions that precede incidents. Change enablement reduces the likelihood of
change related incidents, it is not the core area focused on observing changes of state as events, which is the
domain of Monitoring and Event Management.
Monitoring and event management leverages automation and analysis to detect patterns indicative of
potential problems before they impact users. This proactive detection is a fundamental aspect of preventing
incidents and maintaining service availability. Therefore, "responding to conditions that could lead to potential
faults or incidents" directly aligns with the purpose of Monitoring and Event Management.
For further information, refer to the official ITIL 4 Foundation guidance:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Study Guide.
https://www.axelos.com/ (AXELOS official website - look for ITIL 4 information).
Question: 260 CertyIQ
What role would be MOST suitable for a new graduate with great levels of empathy and understanding of business
issues?
A.Service level manager
B.Service desk agent
C.Change authority
D.Problem analyst
Answer: B
Explanation:
The most suitable role for a new graduate with high empathy and understanding of business issues is a
Service Desk Agent. Here's why:
Direct Customer Interaction: Service Desk Agents are the first point of contact for users experiencing issues
or requesting services. This role directly leverages empathy to understand user frustrations and address their
needs effectively.
Business Context: Understanding business issues allows the agent to prioritize incidents and service
requests based on their impact on the organization's operations. They can tailor their communication and
solutions to align with business goals.
Opportunity for Growth: Starting as a Service Desk Agent provides a solid foundation for understanding IT
services and processes. The graduate can then move to roles like Problem Analyst or Service Level Manager
later, armed with hands-on experience.
Entry-Level Position: Service Desk Agent roles often require less technical expertise upfront compared to
Change Authorities or Problem Analysts. The graduate can learn the technical aspects on the job while
utilizing their existing strengths.
Empathy is Crucial: A Service Desk Agent with empathy can effectively de-escalate situations, build trust

with users, and ensure customer satisfaction. This is especially important in a service-oriented environment.
Other Roles are Less Suitable: Service Level Managers typically require experience in service management
and negotiation. Change Authorities need a strong understanding of change management processes and
technical implications. Problem Analysts need analytical skills and knowledge of root cause analysis
techniques.
Authoritative Links for further research:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Guidance: https://www.axelos.com/ (The official source for ITIL guidance)
HDI Support Analyst Role Description: https://www.thinkhdi.com/ (HDI provides resources and standards for
IT service and support professionals.)
Question: 261 CertyIQ
Which practice nurtures links with stakeholders at strategic and tactical levels?
A.Supplier management
B.Relationship management
C.Continual improvement
D.Service level management
Answer: B
Explanation:
The correct answer is B. Relationship management. Here's why:
Relationship management focuses on establishing and nurturing strong connections with all stakeholders
involved in IT services, including customers, suppliers, and internal departments. It operates at both strategic
(long-term goals and direction) and tactical (day-to-day operations) levels. This practice aims to understand
stakeholder needs, manage expectations, and ensure everyone works collaboratively towards shared
objectives. Effective relationship management involves regular communication, feedback loops, and a
commitment to mutual understanding.
Supplier management, while important for managing vendors, primarily focuses on ensuring suppliers meet
contractual obligations and deliver value. Continual improvement aims at optimizing processes and services
but doesn't directly address stakeholder relationships. Service level management focuses on defining and
managing service levels with customers.
Relationship management explicitly addresses building and maintaining relationships, encompassing the
broad spectrum of stakeholders at both strategic and tactical levels. This holistic approach ensures
