alignment, trust, and effective collaboration, which are crucial for successful IT service delivery and value
creation. By cultivating strong relationships, organizations can better understand evolving needs, proactively
address concerns, and foster a collaborative environment that drives innovation and continuous improvement.
This involves understanding stakeholder perspectives and communicating the IT organization's value
proposition clearly. It allows for better alignment of IT strategy with business needs and supports more
effective resource allocation. Relationship management enables IT to proactively identify and address
potential issues, fostering a more stable and reliable service environment.
Authoritative Links for Further Research:
Axelos ITIL 4 Foundation Syllabus: https://www.axelos.com/ (Search for ITIL 4 Foundation syllabus on the
Axelos website)
ITIL Practitioner Guidance: https://www.axelos.com/ (Look for ITIL Practitioner guidance documents on the

Axelos website)
Question: 262 CertyIQ
Which is a way of applying the guiding principle 'focus on value'?
A.Understanding how service consumers use services
B.Comprehending the whole, but doing something
C.Recognizing the complexity of systems
D.Doing fewer things, but doing them better
Answer: A
Explanation:
The correct answer is A because 'focus on value' is about understanding how your work directly contributes to
the customer's outcomes and benefits. Identifying how service consumers actually use services is the most
direct way to understand the value being realized. It helps identify if the services are meeting needs and
where improvements can be made.
Option B, "Comprehending the whole, but doing something," while alluding to a holistic approach (perhaps
related to thinking holistically), doesn't directly address value delivery or user needs. It is vague and doesn't
specify how the "something" being done contributes to customer outcomes.
Option C, "Recognizing the complexity of systems," relates more to understanding interdependencies and
potential risks, which aligns more with "think and work holistically" or "keep it simple and practical." While
important, it's not the core of focusing on value.
Option D, "Doing fewer things, but doing them better," touches on optimization and efficiency (possibly
aligning with "optimize and automate"), but doesn't inherently guarantee the things being done are valuable
to the customer. Improving efficiency on a non-valuable task doesn't create value. Focusing on value requires
knowing what is truly important to the customer.
The ITIL 4 guiding principles emphasize customer-centricity and value creation as paramount. Understanding
user needs and service usage patterns allows organizations to align their efforts, resources, and service
design to deliver maximum value, thereby fulfilling the "focus on value" principle. By observing service
consumption, organizations can gain valuable insights into customer preferences, pain points, and desired
outcomes. This enables them to prioritize enhancements, tailor services, and measure the impact of their
efforts on customer satisfaction and business value. Prioritizing features based on actual usage patterns
ensures resources are used in the most effective
way.https://www.axelos.com/https://www.bmc.com/blogs/itil-4-guiding-principles/
Question: 263 CertyIQ
Which of the following is NOT recommended by the guiding principle 'start where you are'?
A.Asking questions that appear to be stupid
B.Identifying what is available to be leveraged
C.Building something completely new
D.Collecting data directly from the source

Answer: C
Explanation:
The guiding principle 'Start where you are' emphasizes avoiding reinventing the wheel and leveraging existing
resources and knowledge when embarking on new initiatives or improvements. It advocates for a pragmatic
approach, building upon what already exists rather than prematurely discarding it.
Option C, "Building something completely new," directly contradicts this principle. Starting where you are
implies examining existing services, processes, documentation, and expertise before considering a
completely fresh start. It suggests identifying what works well and what doesn't, understanding the current
state, and using this understanding as a foundation for improvement or change. Building something
completely new without first assessing the current situation is inefficient and potentially wasteful, ignoring
valuable lessons and resources.
Options A, B, and D all align with the 'Start where you are' principle. Asking questions, even if they seem basic
(A), is essential for understanding the current state. Identifying available resources for leverage (B) is a core
component of utilizing what already exists. Collecting data directly from the source (D) provides accurate
insights into the current situation, informing decisions for improvement. By starting with a clear
understanding of the existing environment, organizations can make informed decisions, avoid unnecessary
work, and ensure that new initiatives are aligned with business needs.
Therefore, building something completely new goes against the spirit of the 'Start where you are' guiding
principle, which prioritizes leveraging existing assets and knowledge before embarking on entirely new
endeavors. This approach fosters efficiency, reduces risk, and promotes continuous improvement by building
upon established foundations.
Authoritative Links:
Axelos ITIL 4 Foundation Syllabus: (Search for official ITIL 4 Foundation resources on the Axelos website or
accredited training providers' sites. These resources will provide the official definitions and explanations of
the ITIL guiding principles.)
Question: 264 CertyIQ
Which is a use of a continual improvement register?
A.Planning changes, assisting in communication, avoiding conflicts, and assigning resources
B.Selecting the right method, model or technique for identifying improvements
C.Tracking and managing improvement ideas from identification through to final action
D.Describing the services designed to meet the needs of a consumer group
Answer: C
Explanation:
The most accurate answer is C. Tracking and managing improvement ideas from identification through to
final action.
A continual improvement register (CIR) serves as a central repository for improvement opportunities. Its
primary purpose is to systematically manage ideas, requests, and suggestions for enhancements across the IT
service management ecosystem. The CIR allows organizations to document each improvement idea, track its
progress through various stages (e.g., identification, assessment, planning, implementation, review), and
ultimately ensure its resolution. This centralized tracking promotes transparency, accountability, and
effective prioritization. By documenting each stage of the improvement journey, the CIR allows for better

resource allocation and management of improvement initiatives. It facilitates monitoring of Key Performance
Indicators (KPIs) related to improvement efforts. In essence, the CIR helps organizations to move from simply
identifying areas for improvement to actively implementing and tracking them, maximizing the positive impact
on service delivery. A well-managed CIR ensures that no improvement opportunity is forgotten and that all
ideas receive proper consideration and follow-up.
Here's why the other options are less suitable:
A.Planning changes, assisting in communication, avoiding conflicts, and assigning resources: While these
activities are related to service management, they're not the primary focus of a CIR. Change management,
communication plans, and resource allocation are distinct processes, although the CIR can inform them.
B.Selecting the right method, model or technique for identifying improvements: This is more about the
improvement identification phase. The CIR handles the tracking after identification.
D.Describing the services designed to meet the needs of a consumer group: This describes a service
definition or service catalog entry, not the purpose of a continual improvement register.
For further research on the continual improvement register:
AXELOS Official ITIL 4 Foundation Materials: The official study guide is the most authoritative source. While
not directly linkable, searching for "ITIL 4 Continual Improvement Register" on Google Books will often reveal
relevant excerpts from official publications.
ITIL 4 Foundation Handbook: A more detailed exploration of the ITIL framework and its key concepts,
including continual improvement and the CIR, can be found within this handbook.
Question: 265 CertyIQ
Which practice uses pre-defined, standardized procedures to enable fulfilment times to be clearly communicated?
A.Incident management
B.Service level management
C.Problem management
D.Service request management
Answer: B
Explanation:
The provided answer key is incorrect. The correct answer is D. Service request management. Here's why:
Service request management focuses on fulfilling pre-defined, standardized user requests for services or
information. These requests are usually low-risk, common, and well-documented. Because they are
standardized, fulfillment times can be accurately predicted and clearly communicated to users. This
predictability is a key characteristic of service request management. Standardized procedures are developed
and implemented in service request management that are not implemented in problem, incident, or service
level management.
Incident management focuses on restoring normal service operation as quickly as possible after an
interruption. While speed is important, the priority is resolution, and communicating precise fulfillment times
may be less crucial than simply getting the service back up. In some scenarios, standardized procedure can be
used in incident management, but this is usually for the highest priority incidents.
Problem management aims to identify and resolve the underlying causes of incidents to prevent them from
recurring. This is a proactive practice, and fulfillment times aren't a primary concern, although communication

about progress on investigations is important.
Service level management defines and manages service level agreements (SLAs) between the service
provider and the customer. While SLAs set expectations for service performance, they don't directly involve
fulfilling individual requests or communicating specific fulfillment times for those requests.
Service request management's focus on pre-defined processes and readily available solutions makes it the
most suitable practice for communicating clear fulfillment times. Pre-defined procedures is unique to Service
Request Management when talking about ITIL 4.
Authoritative links:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Study Guide
Official ITIL 4 publications
Question: 266 CertyIQ
Which TWO of the following are considerations of change enablement?
1. Managing the people aspects of change
2. Ensuring that organizational transformations are successful
3. Maximizing the number of successful service changes
4. Ensuring that changes are properly assessed
A.1 and 2
B.2 and 3
C.3 and 4
D.1 and 4
Answer: C
Explanation:
Here's a detailed justification for why option C (3 and 4) is the correct answer, focusing on ITIL 4 Foundation
principles:
Change enablement in ITIL 4 focuses primarily on managing service changes, not organizational
transformations in general. While organizational transformation can involve changes, change enablement's
scope is specifically the assessment, authorization, and deployment of changes to IT services.
Consideration 1, "Managing the people aspects of change," is more aligned with organizational change
management, which is a separate discipline. While change enablement considers the impact on users, its
primary focus isn't on managing the broader human aspects of change.
Consideration 2, "Ensuring that organizational transformations are successful," is too broad. It's the role of
senior leadership and organizational change management teams, not specifically change enablement.
Consideration 3, "Maximizing the number of successful service changes," is a core goal of change
enablement. This encompasses a smooth transition, reduced incidents, and minimal disruption. ITIL 4's
emphasis on value creation relies on the successful implementation of changes. Change Enablement seeks to
balance the need for agility in delivering changes with the need to minimize risk and ensure stability of the IT
services.
Consideration 4, "Ensuring that changes are properly assessed," is critical. Change enablement ensures
appropriate impact assessment, risk analysis, and resource allocation for proposed changes. This assessment
ensures that changes are deployed in a safe and controlled manner. This allows the change authority to
approve or reject a change based on its assessed risks and benefits.

Therefore, the most relevant considerations within the scope of change enablement are maximizing
successful service changes and ensuring proper assessment of changes. This focus is clearly outlined in ITIL
4 guidance.
To understand the purpose of ITIL Change Enablement practices, see these resources:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Manual: This is the official source.
Official ITIL Website: https://www.axelos.com/
These resources will reinforce that change enablement is centrally concerned with the smooth and effective
implementation of service-related changes through proper assessment and execution.
Question: 267 CertyIQ
How can a service consumer contribute to the reduction of risk?
A.By providing the service in accordance with requirements
B.By ensuring that the service provider's resources are correctly configured
C.By fully understanding their own requirements for the service
D.By managing the detailed level of risk on behalf of the service provider
Answer: C
Explanation:
The correct answer is C. By fully understanding their own requirements for the service. Here's why:
A service consumer's clear understanding of their needs directly impacts risk mitigation. When consumers
articulate precise and comprehensive requirements, the service provider can tailor the service to meet those
specific demands. This reduces the risk of misalignment, leading to dissatisfaction, inefficient resource
allocation, and potential service failures. A well-defined scope minimizes ambiguity and sets clear
expectations for both parties.
Option A (providing the service in accordance with requirements) is incorrect because the service consumer
doesn't provide the service; the service provider does. Option B (ensuring the service provider's resources are
correctly configured) is also incorrect. Resource configuration is the responsibility of the service provider.
Option D (managing the detailed level of risk on behalf of the service provider) is inaccurate because risk
management remains primarily with the service provider, even though consumers contribute to risk mitigation.
By contrast, if a consumer has vague or poorly defined requirements, the service provider may make incorrect
assumptions, leading to a service that doesn't meet the actual business need. This disconnect creates risks
around business outcomes, financial investment, and user experience.
In the ITIL 4 framework, collaborative value co-creation between service providers and consumers is
emphasized. A key part of this collaboration is that the consumer clearly communicates their needs.
Understanding the customer's expectations reduces scope creep, which helps control costs and timelines for
service delivery. When requirements are understood, providers can accurately assess and plan capacity,
preventing under- or over-provisioning.
For further reading:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation: ITIL 4 Edition: This is the official certification body's core text, providing a
thorough explanation of service value systems and practices.
ITIL Foundation Handbook: Many such handbooks exist from various publishers, but they typically summarize

the ITIL 4 Foundation concepts.
Question: 268 CertyIQ
In which case would a problem be logged as part of the problem identification?
A.When the cause is identified but not resolved
B.After receiving of error information from a supplier
C.When a user reports an unplanned service interruption
D.After a workaround is identified and documented
Answer: B
Explanation:
The correct answer is B. A problem should be logged as part of problem identification after receiving error
information from a supplier. Problem management focuses on preventing incidents from recurring. Error
information from a supplier can indicate a recurring underlying issue that needs investigation.
Option A, where the cause is identified but not resolved, describes a later stage in problem management –
problem control – not the initial identification. Option C, an unplanned service interruption reported by a user,
is typically addressed through incident management first. While it might lead to problem management if
recurrence is suspected, the initial action is incident resolution. Option D, a documented workaround, is also
part of problem control, aimed at mitigating the impact of a known problem while a permanent solution is
sought, and doesn't initiate the problem identification process.
Error information directly suggests a potential underlying problem that needs investigation to prevent future
incidents. Suppliers often provide error logs or reports related to their services, which can be crucial for
proactive problem management. Receiving this information triggers the need to log and analyze the potential
problem.
Further reading:
AXELOS - ITIL 4 Foundation: ITIL Problem Management: https://www.axelos.com/ (Official ITIL source
requires paid access, but provides comprehensive details on Problem Management)
BMC - ITIL Problem Management: https://www.bmc.com/blogs/itil-problem-management/ (Describes the
Problem Management process in detail.)
Question: 269 CertyIQ
Identify the missing word in the following sentence.
The purpose of the service configuration management practice is to ensure that accurate and reliable information
about the configuration of [?], and the CIs that support them, is available when and where it is needed.
A.organizations
B.outcomes
C.IT assets
D.services
Answer: D
Explanation:

The correct answer is D. services. Here's why:
The service configuration management practice focuses on understanding and managing the components
(Configuration Items or CIs) that contribute to delivering services. The goal is to have a clear and accurate
record of these components and their relationships to ensure services can be delivered effectively and
efficiently.
Let's break down why the other options are less appropriate:
A. organizations: While organizations use services, configuration management is not primarily about
managing organizations themselves. It's about the resources (CIs) that underpin the services the organization
uses or provides.
B. outcomes: Outcomes are the results achieved by using services. While service configuration management
contributes to achieving desired outcomes, its direct focus is on managing the configuration of the
components that enable those services.
C. IT assets: While IT assets are part of the configuration, the scope of service configuration management is
broader. It focuses on the entire configuration required to deliver a service, not just individual IT assets. The
context is about the entire ecosystem that supports a particular service.
Service configuration management is critical for incident management, problem management, change
management, and release management. By having a clear understanding of the configuration, organizations
can resolve incidents faster, identify the root cause of problems more effectively, plan changes with greater
confidence, and deploy releases more smoothly. All of these are aimed at ensuring the consistent and reliable
delivery of services.
In essence, the service configuration management practice ensures a service provider understands all the
components and dependencies required to deliver services, leading to greater stability, reliability, and
efficiency. It's a foundational element of service management according to ITIL 4 principles.
Supporting Links:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation: (This would be the primary source, but it is proprietary. Searching for ITIL 4
Foundation on Axelos' website will provide more information.)
Generic definition of configuration management: https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Configuration_management
(While not specific to ITIL, it provides a general understanding of the concept.)
Question: 270 CertyIQ
Which practice helps to ensure that the services delivered to customers are aligned with their needs?
A.Service level management
B.Change enablement
C.Problem management
D.Service request management
Answer: A
Explanation:
The correct answer is A, Service Level Management (SLM). SLM is the practice of setting clear, measurable
objectives for IT services and ensuring that these services are delivered to meet agreed-upon service levels. It
focuses on defining, negotiating, agreeing on, and monitoring these levels to ensure customer satisfaction.
Service level management plays a vital role in aligning services with customer needs. It accomplishes this by
establishing Service Level Agreements (SLAs) that outline performance targets for different aspects of the

service, such as availability, response time, and throughput. This alignment begins with understanding the
customer's business requirements and translating them into tangible service level objectives.
By actively monitoring performance against these agreed-upon SLAs, SLM ensures that the service delivered
consistently meets customer expectations. This involves proactive measurement, analysis, and reporting of
service performance, enabling timely identification and resolution of issues that could impact service levels.
This practice involves continuous feedback and improvement to adapt SLAs and service offerings in response
to changing customer needs and business priorities.
Change enablement (B) focuses on managing changes in a controlled manner. Problem management (C) deals
with identifying and resolving the root causes of incidents. Service request management (D) handles user
requests for standard services. While all contribute to IT service delivery, none directly focus on defining and
managing service performance against customer needs as SLM does.
Therefore, service level management stands out as the practice that specifically ensures services are aligned
with customer needs through clearly defined service levels and continuous monitoring.
Further research:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Handbook: Provides a comprehensive overview of ITIL 4 practices.
Service Level Management Best Practices: https://www.bmc.com/blogs/service-level-management-best-
practices/
ITIL Foundation: Service Level Management: https://www.exin.com/certifications/itil-certifications/itil-4-
foundation
Question: 271 CertyIQ
Which service request management decisions require that policies are established?
A.Deciding how degradations of service are resolved
B.Deciding how to handle service requests where the steps are unknown
C.Deciding which service requests require approval
D.Deciding when workarounds should be used
Answer: C
Explanation:
The correct answer is C, deciding which service requests require approval. Here's why:
Service Request Management focuses on fulfilling pre-defined requests from users, often routine and low-
risk. Policies are vital for governing which of these requests need approval. Approvals add a layer of oversight
and control, ensuring resources are used appropriately and that changes align with organizational standards.
This control is especially crucial for requests that involve costs (like new software licenses), access to
sensitive data, or changes to critical systems. Without established policies, approval processes become
inconsistent, potentially leading to unauthorized resource allocation, security breaches, or disruptions.
Policies define clear criteria (e.g., cost thresholds, user roles, data access levels) that determine when
approvals are required.
Option A (degradations) relates to incident management, not service request management. Option B
(unknown steps) falls under problem management or a more complex service request that might need to be
escalated. Option D (workarounds) belongs within incident or problem management contexts.
Therefore, pre-defining which requests need the formal checkpoint of approval is essential to service request
management policy, ensuring governance and controlled resource allocation. This allows for efficient

processing of routine requests while flagging higher-impact or riskier requests for review and authorization.
Further Research:
AXELOS - ITIL 4 Foundation Study Guide: https://www.axelos.com/ (Official ITIL Source, requires purchase or
subscription for full access, but provides the definitive guide.)
Service Request Management: Search for "Service Request Management ITIL 4" on your preferred search
engine to find various articles and blog posts explaining the concept within the ITIL 4 framework.
Question: 272 CertyIQ
Which dimension of service management considers how activities are coordinated?
A.Organizations and people
B.Information and technology
C.Partners and suppliers
D.Value streams and processes
Answer: D
Explanation:
The correct answer is D. Value streams and processes.
Here's a detailed justification:
The ITIL 4 Foundation guidance uses four dimensions of service management to ensure a holistic approach to
service delivery. These dimensions represent perspectives that should be considered for any aspect of the
service management system. One of these dimensions is Value streams and Processes.
Value streams and processes are specifically concerned with how the various parts of the organization work
together to create value. This includes the activities, workflows, controls, and procedures needed to achieve
defined objectives. The coordination of activities is central to how value streams are designed and managed. A
well-defined value stream maps out how different activities link together, ensuring a smooth and efficient
flow of work towards value creation. Processes, which are sets of interrelated activities, also require careful
coordination to ensure their effectiveness. Process documentation often specifies dependencies and
integrations needed for optimal performance.
Options A, B, and C are also dimensions of service management but are less directly related to the
coordination of activities:
A. Organizations and people: This dimension focuses on the roles, responsibilities, organizational structure,
culture, and skills required for service management. It is essential for effective coordination but it isn't about
the mechanisms of that coordination.
B. Information and technology: This dimension considers the information management aspects and the
technologies used to support service management. While technology is important, the question specifically
asks about coordination of activities, which falls more squarely within the realm of process and value stream
design.
C. Partners and suppliers: This dimension addresses relationships with external entities and how they
contribute to service value. While partner management necessitates coordination, this coordination is not
about the internal execution and linking of activities within the service provider's organization that value
streams and processes manage.
Therefore, understanding how activities are linked, sequenced, and controlled (i.e., coordinated) is directly
relevant to the design and management of value streams and processes. This makes option D the most

accurate answer.
Further reading:
Axelos ITIL 4 Foundation Guidance: This is the primary source of information on ITIL 4 concepts.
Official ITIL Website: (https://www.axelos.com/)
Question: 273 CertyIQ
A user contacts the service desk to ask how they can create a report.
Which practice is MOST LIKELY to contribute to resolving this issue?
A.Incident management
B.Service level management
C.Service request management
D.Change enablement
Answer: C
Explanation:
The correct answer is C, Service Request Management. Here's why:
A user asking "how to" perform a task (create a report) aligns perfectly with the definition of a service
request. Service requests are standardized, low-risk requests for pre-defined services, information, advice, or
access. Providing instructions falls directly within the scope of this practice.
Incident management focuses on restoring normal service operation as quickly as possible to minimize the
impact on business operations. This is typically related to unplanned interruptions or reductions in service
quality, like a broken application or a system outage. The user's inquiry doesn't suggest any disruption.
Service Level Management (SLM) concerns itself with establishing agreements with customers regarding the
level of service they can expect. While SLM may ensure that adequate documentation or training is available
for users, it is not directly responsible for fulfilling the specific request for information on how to create a
report.
Change enablement focuses on controlling changes to minimize risk. Creating a report, in itself, isn't a change
to the IT infrastructure or services.
Service Request Management is designed to efficiently handle these types of common requests. By having a
documented process and potentially pre-written instructions (knowledge base articles, FAQs, etc.), the
service desk can quickly and effectively resolve the user's question.
Therefore, of the options, Service Request Management is the most likely to contribute to resolving this issue.
Further Research:
Axelos ITIL 4 Foundation: ITIL 4 Edition: Standard reference material.
Official ITIL website: Provides a lot of information on ITIL best practices https://www.axelos.com/
Question: 274 CertyIQ
Which practice has a purpose that includes the management of financially valuable components that can
contribute to the delivery of an IT service?

A.Service configuration management
B.IT asset management
C.Change enablement
D.Deployment management
Answer: B
Explanation:
IT Asset Management (ITAM) is the practice directly concerned with managing the lifecycle of all IT assets
within an organization. Its purpose includes tracking the financial value of these assets. IT assets encompass
hardware, software, licenses, and even cloud instances. A key aspect of ITAM is optimizing asset utilization,
ensuring cost-effectiveness, and minimizing risks associated with asset ownership.
The focus of ITAM is to understand the financial implications of IT assets from purchase to disposal. This
includes depreciation, maintenance costs, and potential resale value. By closely monitoring these financial
components, organizations can make informed decisions about IT investments. Unlike other options, ITAM
directly addresses the management of financially valuable components.
Service Configuration Management, on the other hand, focuses on identifying, controlling, recording, and
verifying service assets and configuration items (CIs). Change Enablement focuses on assessing, authorizing,
and managing changes. Deployment Management is about moving new or changed hardware, software,
documentation, processes, or any other component of a service to a live environment.
While the other practices might indirectly impact the financial aspects of service delivery, ITAM is the only
practice that explicitly deals with the financial value and lifecycle management of IT assets that contribute to
IT service delivery. Therefore, ITAM aligns most closely with the question's emphasis on managing financially
valuable components.
For further research, consider exploring the following links:
Axelos ITIL 4 Foundation Guidance
ITAM Review
ServiceNow IT Asset Management
Question: 275 CertyIQ
Which practice MOST requires staff who demonstrate skills such as empathy and emotional intelligence?
A.Service request management
B.Continual improvement
C.Problem management
D.Service desk
Answer: D
Explanation:
The correct answer is D, Service Desk. Here's why:
The Service Desk practice is the primary point of contact between the service provider and the users. This
means Service Desk staff are constantly interacting with users, often when those users are experiencing
issues, frustrations, or need assistance understanding services. Therefore, skills like empathy and emotional
intelligence are critical. Service Desk agents need to understand the user's perspective, acknowledge their

feelings, and communicate solutions in a clear and supportive manner.
Service Request Management, while also involving user interaction, is typically focused on fulfilling pre-
defined, standard requests. While good communication is important, empathy and emotional intelligence are
less critical than in resolving complex, potentially stressful situations. Continual Improvement focuses on
analyzing data and implementing changes to improve services; emotional intelligence plays a smaller role
compared to the Service Desk. Problem Management concentrates on identifying the underlying causes of
incidents. While collaboration is necessary, empathy isn't the primary skill required. It focuses on analytical
and problem-solving skills to prevent future incidents.
The service desk staff often need to handle emotional customers. The service desk staff also need to be good
listeners to understand the customer issues. Service desk staff will need to build rapport with the customer to
instill confidence.
ITIL 4 Foundation Handbook: (Although specific scenarios aren't detailed, the role of the Service Desk as the
primary user interface underscores the importance of communication skills).
Axelos - ITIL 4: (Provider of ITIL framework - Check their official documentation for details regarding
practices and required skills.)
Therefore, due to its direct and frequent interaction with users during sometimes stressful situations, the
Service Desk practice most requires staff with empathy and emotional intelligence.
Question: 276 CertyIQ
What is the customer of a service responsible for?
A.Defining the requirements for the service
B.Provisioning the service
C.Using the service
D.Authorizing the budget for the service
Answer: A
Explanation:
The justification for selecting "Defining the requirements for the service" as the customer's responsibility
within the ITIL 4 Foundation framework centers on the fundamental principle of value co-creation. ITIL 4
emphasizes that service value is jointly created by the service provider and the consumer (customer). The
customer is the ultimate beneficiary of the service. Therefore, to ensure the service is fit for purpose and fit
for use, the customer must clearly articulate their needs and expectations.
Defining requirements involves specifying the features, functionality, performance, and other attributes that
the service must possess to meet the customer's business objectives. Without a clear understanding of these
requirements, the service provider cannot effectively design, develop, and deliver a service that delivers the
desired outcomes. While the service provider may assist in refining these requirements through consultation
and analysis, the responsibility for outlining the core needs ultimately rests with the customer.
Option B, "Provisioning the service," falls under the purview of the service provider. Provisioning involves the
activities of deploying, configuring, and making the service available to the customer. Option C, "Using the
service," is an action performed by the customer, but it's a consequence of the service being provisioned and
meeting the requirements. Option D, "Authorizing the budget for the service," while related to the customer's
role in consuming the service, is primarily a financial or procurement activity, not directly related to the
service definition.

Therefore, the most accurate and fundamental responsibility of the customer in the context of ITIL 4 is to
define their service requirements, ensuring the service provider has a clear understanding of the desired
outcomes and can tailor the service accordingly. This lays the foundation for a successful service relationship
and co-creation of value.
For further reading and authoritative information, consult the official ITIL 4 publications from Axelos and the
ITIL Foundation Handbook. You can also find useful information on the AXELOS website.
Question: 277 CertyIQ
When using the 'continual improvement model', which information should be produced by an organization in order
to understand where the organization is now?
A.Business objectives
B.Improvement plans
C.Assessment results
D.Measurable targets
Answer: C
Explanation:
The question addresses the initial step of the continual improvement model in ITIL 4, specifically focusing on
understanding the current state of the organization. Option C, "Assessment results," is the most accurate
answer because the 'Where are we now?' stage in the continual improvement model is fundamentally about
evaluating the current situation. Assessment results, such as audits, surveys, performance reviews, and
benchmarking data, provide concrete information regarding current performance, strengths, weaknesses, and
areas requiring attention.
These results are essential for establishing a baseline and identifying gaps between the current state and the
desired state. Without this understanding, subsequent steps in the model, such as defining objectives and
planning improvements, will be misdirected and ineffective. Business objectives (Option A) define the 'Where
do we want to be?' stage. Improvement plans (Option B) are developed after assessing the current state,
representing the 'How do we get there?' stage. Measurable targets (Option D) also belong to the 'Where do
we want to be?' stage, defining what 'success' looks like.
The assessment phase directly aligns with the principle of starting where you are. You can't define relevant
improvements or targets if you haven't truthfully evaluated your existing conditions. For example, assessment
results could reveal inefficient processes, low customer satisfaction scores, or inadequate resource
utilization. These insights then become the foundation for prioritizing and implementing improvement
initiatives. In cloud computing, this could involve assessing the efficiency of current cloud resource allocation,
cost optimization strategies, or security posture.
The ITIL 4 framework emphasizes data-driven decision-making throughout the continual improvement model,
making the collection and analysis of assessment results critical. Therefore, understanding the current state
through thorough assessment is a fundamental requirement for effective continual improvement.
Relevant resource:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation: Details the ITIL 4 framework, including the continual improvement model. (You can
find ITIL documentation and resources on the AXELOS website or through accredited training providers.)

Question: 278 CertyIQ
Which statement about value streams is CORRECT?
A.Each value stream must include all six value chain activities
B.Each value stream must include suppliers or partners
C.Each value stream must be designed for a specific scenario
D.Each value stream must include all 34 ITIL practices
Answer: C
Explanation:
The correct answer is C, "Each value stream must be designed for a specific scenario."
Value streams represent a series of steps an organization undertakes to create and deliver value to a
consumer. They are context-specific, meaning a single organization can have multiple value streams tailored
to different customer segments, product lines, or specific needs. Each value stream aims to address a
particular scenario or customer journey, focusing on the required activities, resources, and controls to achieve
a specific outcome. This targeted approach ensures that the value creation process is optimized and aligned
with the customer's expectations.
Option A is incorrect because not every value stream needs to encompass all six value chain activities (Plan,
Improve, Engage, Design and Transition, Obtain/Build, and Deliver and Support). Value streams are designed
based on the specific scenario and can involve only the necessary activities to deliver value.
Option B is incorrect as external suppliers or partners are not mandatory in all value streams. Some value
streams can be entirely internal, relying on the organization's resources and capabilities. The involvement of
external parties depends on the nature of the service and the requirements of the scenario.
Option D is incorrect because ITIL practices are resources to be used within value streams, not a mandatory
component of every value stream. The practices applied depend on the requirements of the value stream.
Therefore, designing a value stream for a specific scenario ensures that it is optimized for that particular
situation and efficiently delivers the intended value.
Further research:
AXELOS. ITIL Foundation: ITIL 4 Edition. TSO, 2019.
Official ITIL 4 Foundation Study Guides. (Available through accredited training providers).
Question: 279 CertyIQ
Which guiding principle recommends using ideas from ITIL, Lean, DevOps, Kanban, and other sources to help drive
improvements?
A.Optimize and automate
B.Think and work holistically
C.Start where you are
D.Focus on value
Answer: A
Explanation:

The question asks which guiding principle recommends incorporating ideas from various frameworks like ITIL,
Lean, DevOps, and Kanban for driving improvements. While "Start where you are" (D) advises leveraging
existing resources and knowledge before introducing new solutions, and "Think and work holistically" (B)
encourages considering the big picture and interconnectedness, "Optimize and automate" (A) directly aligns
with the spirit of integrating diverse methodologies for enhancement.
"Optimize and automate" seeks to maximize efficiency and streamline processes. Integrating ideas from ITIL
(for service management), Lean (for waste reduction), DevOps (for collaboration and automation), and Kanban
(for workflow management) directly contributes to optimization. For example, using ITIL best practices for
incident management and then automating aspects of it using DevOps principles enhances service delivery.
Similarly, applying Lean principles to eliminate unnecessary steps in a process managed according to ITIL
guidelines streamlines the workflow. Kanban can provide a framework for visually tracking and managing the
improvement initiatives themselves.
Therefore, "Optimize and automate" is the most suitable guiding principle because it explicitly promotes the
adoption of diverse approaches to enhance processes and systems, mirroring the scenario described in the
question. While "Start where you are" is about leveraging existing resources, it doesn't inherently suggest
actively incorporating ideas from diverse frameworks like the other principles do. The key is the active
integration of different methodologies to drive improvements and maximize efficiency, which falls directly
under the scope of "Optimize and automate."
ITIL 4 Guiding Principles: https://www.axelos.com/resource-hub/itil-4-guiding-principles
Lean Principles: https://www.lean.org/
DevOps Principles: https://www.atlassian.com/devops
Kanban Principles: https://www.atlassian.com/agile/kanban
Question: 280 CertyIQ
Which is an activity in the 'problem control' phase of problem management?
A.Re-assessing a known error to manage the ongoing impact
B.Implementing a technical fix to resolve an issue
C.Documenting the steps in a workaround
D.Reviewing incident records to identify trends
Answer: C
Explanation:
The correct answer is C. Documenting the steps in a workaround.
Here's why:
Problem control focuses on preventing incidents from happening by proactively addressing underlying
problems. A key activity within this phase is developing and documenting workarounds. A workaround
provides a temporary way to mitigate the impact of an incident or problem without fully resolving the root
cause. By documenting the steps of a workaround, IT teams can ensure consistent application across
incidents and reduce the overall impact on users. This facilitates faster incident resolution, even if the
problem itself remains unresolved in the short term. The documentation helps to quickly restore service and
reduce downtime until a permanent solution is in place.
Let's examine why the other options are less suitable:
A. Re-assessing a known error to manage the ongoing impact: Re-assessing known errors is more aligned

with error control, the second phase of problem management, after problem analysis has identified a root
cause and the error exists.
B. Implementing a technical fix to resolve an issue: Implementing a technical fix addresses the resolution of
the problem, not the initial control phase. This is more related to change management or even incident
resolution after the root cause has been identified and fixed through error control.
D. Reviewing incident records to identify trends: Reviewing incident records is more associated with problem
identification, which precedes the problem control phase. It is crucial for identifying potential problems, but it
is not the control activity itself.
Therefore, documenting workaround steps aligns most closely with the proactive nature of problem control,
which aims to reduce the negative impact of incidents stemming from known problems.
Here are some resources for further reading:
Axelos ITIL 4 Foundation Syllabus: Although paywalled, this is the definitive source.
BMC Blogs - ITIL Problem Management: https://www.bmc.com/blogs/itil-problem-management/
Atlassian - What is Problem Management?: https://www.atlassian.com/itsm/problem-management
Question: 281 CertyIQ
Which practice nurtures links with stakeholders at strategic and tactical levels?
A.Supplier management
B.Relationship management
C.Service desk
D.Service level management
Answer: B
Explanation:
The correct answer is B. Relationship management focuses on building and maintaining strong connections
with stakeholders, encompassing both strategic and tactical interactions. This involves understanding
stakeholder needs, managing expectations, and fostering collaboration to ensure alignment between the IT
organization and the broader business goals.
Supplier management (A) primarily deals with third-party vendors providing goods and services. While
relationships are part of supplier management, its focus is narrower than nurturing broad stakeholder
relationships at all levels. Service desk (C) primarily handles incident resolution and service requests,
engaging with users on a transactional, operational level. Service level management (D) focuses on defining
and managing service level agreements (SLAs) and targets. While important for managing expectations, it
doesn't inherently encompass the broader nurturing of relationships at all levels.
Relationship management, on the other hand, proactively engages stakeholders to understand their needs,
communicate strategic directions, and gather feedback for service improvement. This holistic approach builds
trust and ensures that IT services are aligned with business objectives. Tactical relationships are nurtured
through regular communication, performance reporting, and ongoing collaboration on operational matters.
Strategic relationships involve participation in planning sessions, providing input on business strategy, and
ensuring IT capabilities are aligned with long-term goals.
Therefore, relationship management is the practice most directly involved in nurturing links with stakeholders
at both strategic and tactical levels, making it the most accurate choice.

Question: 282 CertyIQ
Which practice has a purpose that includes managing authentication and non-repudiation?
A.Information security management
B.Change enablement
C.Service configuration management
D.IT asset management
Answer: A
Explanation:
The correct answer is A, Information Security Management. Here's why:
Information Security Management's purpose is to protect the organization's information. This protection
extends to confidentiality, integrity, and availability. Authentication and non-repudiation are crucial
components of maintaining information security.
Authentication verifies the identity of users or systems, ensuring that only authorized individuals or processes
can access sensitive information or resources. This directly contributes to confidentiality by preventing
unauthorized access.
Non-repudiation ensures that a sender of a message or originator of data cannot deny sending or creating it.
This is vital for maintaining the integrity of information, as it provides proof of origin and prevents repudiation
of actions. Digital signatures, a key security mechanism, enable non-repudiation.
Change Enablement (B) focuses on managing changes to minimize risks and disruptions. While security is
considered, authentication and non-repudiation are not its core purpose.
Service Configuration Management (C) manages the configuration of IT assets, ensuring that services are
delivered as agreed upon. While it supports security through configuration controls, it doesn't directly handle
authentication and non-repudiation.
IT Asset Management (D) tracks and manages IT assets throughout their lifecycle. While asset inventory aids
security, its primary focus isn't authentication or non-repudiation.
Therefore, Information Security Management is the practice most directly concerned with managing
authentication and non-repudiation to protect information.
Further Research:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Syllabus: (Look for sections related to Information Security Management and its
objectives). AXELOS is the official source for ITIL. Since direct links to specific pages change frequently,
searching "AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Syllabus" will provide the most up-to-date location.
NIST Cybersecurity Framework: (https://www.nist.gov/cyberframework). The NIST framework details
security functions including identification, authentication, and access control, aligning with the concepts
discussed in ITIL's Information Security Management practice. Although not specific to ITIL, NIST is an
authoritative body in Cybersecurity.

Question: 283 CertyIQ
Which statement about service offerings is CORRECT?
A.The same product can be used as a basis for more than one service offering
B.Service offerings include the transfer of goods from the consumer to the provider
C.Service offerings describe service actions performed by users
D.Each service should be described to consumers as a single service offering
Answer: A
Explanation:
The correct answer, A, "The same product can be used as a basis for more than one service offering,"
accurately reflects the ITIL 4 definition of service offerings. A service offering is a description of one or more
services, designed to address the needs of a target consumer group. It includes goods, access to resources,
and service actions. Crucially, a single product, like a software application or a cloud infrastructure platform,
can be leveraged in multiple distinct service offerings, each tailored to specific customer needs and packaged
with different support levels, features, or pricing models. For example, a cloud storage product could be
offered as a basic backup service, a high-availability data archiving service, or a collaboration platform – all
leveraging the same underlying storage technology.
Option B is incorrect because service offerings involve the transfer of value to the consumer from the
provider, not the other way around.
Option C is incorrect because service offerings primarily describe the provider's actions, not the users'. The
description should detail what the service provider does to deliver the service.
Option D is often not practical or beneficial. Organizations can offer a single service through multiple
carefully tailored offerings, each catering to distinct user segments or specific scenarios. This allows for
better alignment of service delivery with customer needs and budget. Bundling components or varying service
levels around a base offering improves the overall value proposition.
Essentially, a product is a component that enables a service, while the service offering defines how that
product is delivered and supported to meet specific consumer requirements. The core ITIL 4 guidance
emphasizes this distinction to encourage a service-centric, rather than technology-centric, approach to IT
management. A cloud provider might offer several service offerings using the same virtual machine
technology, each with different performance guarantees, support levels, and pricing plans.
For further research, refer to the official ITIL 4 publications by Axelos:
Axelos website
ITIL Foundation Handbook
Question: 284 CertyIQ
What is a problem that has been analyzed but has not been resolved?
A.Workaround
B.Incident
C.Known error
D.Event
Answer: C

Explanation:
The correct answer is C. Known error. Here's why:
A known error in ITIL 4 is a problem that has been successfully diagnosed and analyzed, meaning its root
cause has been identified, but a permanent resolution or fix is not yet implemented. This is a crucial state in
problem management because it provides valuable information, especially the documented cause, which can
be leveraged to minimize the impact of recurring incidents stemming from the same underlying problem.
Workaround (A) is a temporary solution that reduces or eliminates the impact of an incident or problem, but
does not resolve the underlying issue. It's a method to keep services running, not a stage in problem
resolution where analysis has been completed.Incident (B) is an unplanned interruption to, or reduction in the
quality of, an IT service. It's the symptom of a potential underlying problem, not the problem itself after
analysis.Event (D) is any occurrence that has significance for the management of IT infrastructure or services.
Events are used to signal normal operation, abnormal operation, or other changes in state; they aren't related
to the problem-solving process directly.
The key differentiator is that a known error reflects a deep understanding of why something is happening,
even if a permanent fix isn't ready. This understanding allows for proactive measures, like documented
workarounds, to be shared with support teams. These teams can then quickly address related incidents,
reducing downtime and improving user experience. The benefit of tracking known errors reduces the time to
resolution for future incidents stemming from the same root cause. Furthermore, identifying known errors
helps prioritize problem resolution efforts based on impact and frequency of associated incidents. The
Problem Management practice's goal is not just to fix problems but also to reduce their negative impact in the
meantime, and known errors facilitate this.
Further research:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Syllabus: (Search for "ITIL 4 Foundation Syllabus" on Google. AXELOS is the
official source for ITIL) - This provides the official definitions and concepts.
ITIL Foundation Handbook (Official AXELOS Publication): This handbook contains comprehensive
information related to the ITIL framework.
Question: 285 CertyIQ
What ensures that a service provider and a service consumer continually co-create value?
A.Service consumption
B.Service offerings
C.Service relationship management
D.Service level management
Answer: C
Explanation:
The correct answer is C. Service relationship management (SRM). Here's why:
Service relationship management is the practice of establishing and nurturing mutually beneficial
relationships between service providers and service consumers. It's not just about a single transaction; it's
about ongoing collaboration and co-creation of value over the service lifecycle. SRM encompasses
identifying, analyzing, and managing the needs and expectations of both the provider and the consumer to
ensure that the service continuously meets those evolving needs. Through consistent communication,
feedback loops, and collaborative planning, SRM facilitates a deep understanding of the business value the
service delivers and how it can be improved.

Service offerings (B) are specific packages of services, resources, and access offered to customers. While
vital, they don't ensure ongoing value co-creation in themselves. Service consumption (A) is the activity of
using services, but this is a passive activity. It is the input required by SRM. Service level management (D) is
focused on defining, agreeing upon, and monitoring service levels. This ensures the service meets defined
performance targets, but it doesn't necessarily guarantee that the provider and consumer are working
together to create value. A good service level helps guarantee the quality, availability, and function of the
service.
SRM, in contrast, actively drives the alignment of business goals and service delivery, enabling continuous
improvement and the realization of mutual value. Effective SRM fosters trust, transparency, and shared
responsibility, crucial for the successful and sustainable delivery of IT services. It involves understanding the
customer's business context and adapting the service to better meet their needs, ultimately leading to
improved business outcomes.
Further Reading:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Syllabus: https://www.axelos.com/ (Official source, requires registration)
ITIL Foundation Handbook: https://www.tsoshop.co.uk/itil-4-foundation (Official handbook can be purchased)
Question: 286 CertyIQ
When working on an improvement iteration, which concept helps to ensure that the iteration activities remain
appropriate in changing circumstances?
A.Minimum viable product
B.Feedback loop
C.Analysis paralysis
D.Direct observation
Answer: B
Explanation:
The correct answer is B. Feedback loop. Here's why:
A feedback loop is a crucial element in iterative improvement processes, ensuring adaptability and relevance
in dynamic environments. It involves collecting information about the outcomes of activities, analyzing this
information, and using it to adjust subsequent steps. In the context of an improvement iteration, a feedback
loop allows the team to monitor progress, identify any deviations from the desired outcome, and make
necessary corrections.
Minimum Viable Product (MVP) focuses on delivering a basic, functional version of a product or service to
gather early user feedback, but doesn't inherently ensure continuous adaptation within a single iteration.
Analysis paralysis refers to overthinking and delaying action due to excessive analysis, which is the opposite
of what's needed for iterative improvement. Direct observation, while valuable, is only one method of
gathering input and does not encompass the closed-loop system of a feedback loop.
A robust feedback loop incorporates various mechanisms, such as regular meetings, surveys, stakeholder
reviews, and performance metrics, to gather diverse perspectives and insights. This data-driven approach
enables the team to make informed decisions and refine their approach as needed. By continuously
monitoring and adapting, the team can ensure that the improvement iteration remains aligned with changing
circumstances and delivers the desired outcomes. Without a structured feedback loop, improvement efforts
may become misaligned with evolving needs and priorities, leading to inefficiencies and reduced
effectiveness.

Therefore, a feedback loop is essential for ensuring that improvement iteration activities remain appropriate
and effective in dynamic environments, enabling continuous learning and adaptation.
Further Reading:
ITIL 4 Foundation Handbook
https://www.axelos.com/ (Official ITIL Website)
Question: 287 CertyIQ
What is the definition of 'service management'?
A.A result for a stakeholder enabled by one or more outputs
B.A formal description of one or more services, designed to address the needs of a target consumer group
C.Joint activities performed by a service provider and a service consumer to ensure continual value co-creation
D.A set of specialized organizational capabilities for enabling value for customers in the form of services
Answer: D
Explanation:
Service management centers around providing value to customers through carefully designed and managed
services. Option A refers to value, a consequence, not the definition of service management itself. Option B
describes a service offering or portfolio, again, a component of service management rather than the definition
of the entire practice. Option C describes value co-creation, a goal and activity within service management,
but not the core definition.
Option D, "A set of specialized organizational capabilities for enabling value for customers in the form of
services," accurately encapsulates the essence of service management. It highlights that service
management is about the capabilities an organization possesses and cultivates, rather than a single activity or
output. These capabilities encompass processes, functions, roles, and resources that are orchestrated to
design, deliver, manage, and improve services. The core purpose is to leverage these capabilities to enable
value for customers. This aligns directly with the fundamental principles of ITIL 4, which emphasizes a value-
driven approach to IT service management. Essentially, service management is how organizations structure
themselves and operate to deliver value through services. It encompasses all the activities and resources
necessary to plan, design, deliver, operate, and control IT services offered to customers. ITIL 4 focuses on a
holistic approach, encompassing all aspects of service management from strategy to operations, with a
continual focus on improvement.
Further research can be conducted on the Axelos website and through ITIL 4 Foundation
publications.https://www.axelos.com/
Question: 288 CertyIQ
Which is a description of service provision?
A.A way to help create value by facilitating outcomes that service consumers need
B.Activities that an organization performs to deliver services
C.A formal description of one or more services, designed to address the needs of a service consumer
D.Cooperation between two organizations to ensure that a service delivers value

Answer: B
Explanation:
The correct answer is B: "Activities that an organization performs to deliver services." This aligns directly with
the ITIL 4 definition of service provision. Service provision encompasses all the actions, resources, and
management an organization undertakes to make a service available to its customers or users. It includes
service management activities like configuration, monitoring, support, and continuous improvement, all
contributing to the delivery of the service.
Option A describes value co-creation through service consumption, focusing on the outcomes and customer
needs being met through service usage, which relates more to value creation in general within a service
relationship. Option C describes a service offering, which is a specific package designed to address a service
consumer's needs, rather than the broader activities involved in delivering that offering. Option D addresses
service relationships and collaboration between organizations, which forms a part of service management but
is not the comprehensive definition of service provision itself. Service provision necessitates the planning,
building, and execution of processes and resources to enable service operation. ITIL 4 emphasizes a holistic
approach, and service provision is at the heart of service management.For a deeper understanding, refer to
