Question: 289 CertyIQ
How is a 'continual improvement register' used?
A.To provide a structured approach to implementing improvements
B.To authorize changes to implement improvement initiatives
C.To organize past, present, and future improvement ideas
D.To record requests for provision of a resource or service
Answer: C
Explanation:
The correct answer is C. To organize past, present, and future improvement ideas.
A Continual Improvement Register (CIR) serves as a central repository for tracking and managing
improvement opportunities throughout their lifecycle. It is not a structured methodology for implementation
(A), nor does it authorize changes (B), or record service requests (D). Its primary purpose is to document a
range of improvement ideas – those already implemented (past), those currently being worked on (present),
and those identified for potential future action.
The register typically includes details such as the description of the improvement, its priority, potential
benefits, responsible party, status, and related costs. This centralized view aids in prioritizing improvements,
allocating resources effectively, and ensuring that no good idea is lost or forgotten. It supports a culture of
continuous improvement by providing a structured way to capture, evaluate, and track improvement efforts. It
allows the organization to learn from past initiatives and to make informed decisions about future
improvements, thus enabling ongoing enhancement of IT services and processes.
Think of it as a backlog or repository specifically for improvement actions. Instead of service request
ticketing, it holds improvement suggestions and their associated details. This repository encourages
collaboration and knowledge sharing, as anyone can contribute ideas and track their progress. This supports
the "continual improvement" practice in ITIL 4, emphasizing the iterative nature of service

management.Authoritative link to related material is the official ITIL 4 guidance and Axelos resources.
Question: 290 CertyIQ
Which is an input to the service value system?
A.A need from consumers for new or changed services.
B.The system of directing and controlling an organization
C.A model to help meet stakeholders' expectations
D.Recommendations to help an organization in all aspects of its work
Answer: A
Explanation:
The correct answer is A: A need from consumers for new or changed services.
The ITIL 4 Service Value System (SVS) describes how all the components and activities of an organization
work together as a system to enable value creation. Inputs are essential triggers that initiate activities within
the SVS. A primary input to the SVS is a need or opportunity, which most often originates from the consumer
or stakeholder. This need can be a requirement for new services, modifications to existing services, or the
resolution of issues impacting service delivery. Recognizing and understanding these needs is the starting
point for planning, designing, building, and delivering value.
Options B, C, and D, while relevant to ITIL and service management, are not direct inputs to the SVS.
Governance (option B) guides the SVS but is not an input in the same sense as a customer need. Models to
meet stakeholder expectations (option C), such as the Four Dimensions or guiding principles, provide
frameworks for how the SVS operates but are not inputs. Recommendations (option D), while potentially
useful, are typically the outputs of analysis or problem-solving processes within the SVS, rather than initiating
the whole system. Therefore, consumer needs are a direct trigger driving the SVS activities and are
considered inputs.ITIL 4 Foundation materials clearly state that needs and opportunities are key inputs into
the SVS.https://www.axelos.com/
Question: 291 CertyIQ
Which organization delivers outputs or outcomes of a service?
A.A service consumer delivers outcomes of the service
B.A service consumer delivers outputs of the service
C.A service provider delivers outcomes of the service
D.A service provider delivers outputs of the service
Answer: D
Explanation:
The correct answer is D. A service provider delivers outputs of the service.
ITIL 4 defines a service provider as an organization that provides services. The core purpose of a service
provider is to enable value co-creation by managing resources, capabilities, and activities to deliver outputs
and subsequently contribute to outcomes for the service consumer. The outputs are the tangible deliverables

of the service, which the service consumer then uses to achieve their desired outcomes.
A service consumer doesn't directly deliver outputs; instead, they consume the outputs provided by the
service provider. Options A and B incorrectly assign the delivery of outputs or outcomes to the service
consumer when it is the service provider's responsibility. Option C is partially correct in that a service provider
contributes to outcomes, but the question specifically asks about who delivers outputs. The service provider
directly delivers the outputs and those outputs enable outcomes.
Therefore, the service provider is the entity directly responsible for delivering the tangible results or
"outputs" of the service to the consumer. The consumer then uses those outputs to achieve their own desired
outcomes.
Further research on these concepts can be found in the official ITIL 4 Foundation guidance:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Publication: https://www.axelos.com/ (This is the official source, but access may
require purchase of the publication). While a direct link to a free, authoritative explanation of this specific
definition is often behind a paywall, searching for "ITIL 4 service provider definition" on reputable IT service
management websites can yield helpful summaries based on the official documentation. For example,
searching "ITIL 4 Service Provider vs Consumer" on websites of major IT training companies could provide
helpful blog posts and articles.
Question: 292 CertyIQ
Which practice requires focus and effort to engage and listen to the requirements, issues, concerns, and daily
needs of customers?
A.Service request management
B.Service desk
C.Supplier management
D.Service level management
Answer: D
Explanation:
The correct answer is D. Service Level Management (SLM).
Service Level Management is fundamentally about defining, agreeing upon, documenting, and managing
service levels with customers. This requires a deep understanding of the customer's business needs,
expectations, and priorities. To achieve effective service level agreements (SLAs), SLM necessitates
continuous engagement with customers to elicit their requirements, proactively address any issues or
concerns, and stay attuned to their evolving daily operational demands. Listening is paramount because SLAs
must reflect what is truly important to the customer's success. SLM involves regular communication,
feedback loops, and performance reporting that keeps the customer informed and engaged. It's not merely
about meeting targets; it's about building a strong relationship based on trust and shared understanding.
While the other options involve customer interaction, they aren't primarily focused on proactively engaging
and listening to understand the customer's holistic needs and concerns to the same extent as SLM. Service
Request Management is reactive, focusing on fulfilling predefined requests. The Service Desk provides
support but doesn't necessarily delve deep into understanding the customer's broad requirements. Supplier
Management is about managing relationships with external providers, not end-users or customers.
https://www.axelos.com/ (ITIL official website - requires subscription for detailed
content)https://www.bmc.com/blogs/itil-service-level-management/ (provides a basic overview)

Question: 293 CertyIQ
What is the cause, or potential cause, of one or more incidents?
A.A problem
B.A known error
C.An event
D.A change
Answer: A
Explanation:
The correct answer is A (A problem). Here's why:
A problem, in ITIL 4 terms, is defined as the cause or potential cause of one or more incidents. Incidents are
disruptions or degradations of services. Problems are investigated to find the root cause of these incidents
and prevent future occurrences.
A known error (B) is a problem that has been diagnosed and a workaround or resolution is available. It's the
result of problem management, not the cause of incidents.
An event (C) is simply a notification of a change of state, and while events can trigger incidents, they aren't
the cause of the underlying issue. An event is not the same as a problem. An event might be a server crashing,
which leads to an incident, but the problem is the underlying reason the server crashed (e.g., a memory leak or
hardware failure).
A change (D) might introduce a problem (e.g., a faulty software update), but it's the problem itself, triggered
by the change, that is the cause of the incident. The change is merely the trigger. For example, a change to a
firewall rule might create a security vulnerability. This change caused a problem.
Therefore, the most accurate response is A. ITIL 4 focuses on preventing incidents by identifying and
resolving underlying problems. Problem Management is the practice dedicated to reducing the likelihood and
impact of incidents by identifying actual and potential causes of incidents, and managing workarounds and
known errors. This helps in minimizing business disruptions and improves overall IT service stability.
ITIL 4 Foundation: ITIL 4 EditionAxelos ITIL 4 Glossary
Question: 294 CertyIQ
Which value chain activity is concerned with the availability of service components?
A.Obtain/build
B.Design and transition
C.Deliver and support
D.Plan
Answer: A
Explanation:
The correct answer is A (Obtain/build). The question asks which value chain activity is concerned with the
availability of service components. The "Obtain/build" value chain activity focuses on ensuring that resources,

service components, and services are available when and where they are needed. This includes sourcing,
procuring, or creating these components. Availability management, a key practice within ITIL, is closely tied to
ensuring components are ready for deployment and use. Building in resilience and redundancy during the
obtain/build phase is crucial for maintaining high availability. While "Deliver and support" (C) does focus on
the operational delivery of services and resolving issues, the foundational work of ensuring components are
available in the first place happens during "Obtain/build." Without the right components available, delivery
and support cannot function effectively. Design and transition (B) focuses on planning and implementing new
or changed services, but it's the obtain/build activity that physically makes those components available. Plan
(D) is a strategic activity and does not directly deal with the physical availability of components. Therefore, the
activity most directly concerned with the availability of service components is obtain/build.
Authoritative link for further research on ITIL 4 Value Chain: https://www.axelos.com/ - This is the official
website for AXELOS, the organization behind ITIL. While specific documents might require purchase, it's the
definitive source of information. Look for descriptions of the ITIL 4 service value chain and each activity.
Question: 295 CertyIQ
Which is the FIRST action when optimizing a service?
A.Assess the current state
B.Understand the organizational context
C.Agree the future state
D.Implement the improvements
Answer: B
Explanation:
The correct answer is B. Understand the organizational context. Here's a detailed justification:
Optimizing a service within the ITIL 4 framework is an iterative process of improvement. Before embarking on
any changes, it's crucial to have a firm grasp of the environment the service operates within. Understanding
the organizational context sets the stage for effective optimization.
Here's a breakdown:
1. Organizational Context is Foundational: ITIL 4 emphasizes that services are delivered within a
specific business environment. Factors like organizational culture, business goals, customer needs,
and the overall IT strategy heavily influence how a service should be optimized. Ignoring these
factors leads to misaligned improvements.
2. Assessment Follows Understanding: While assessing the current state (option A) is necessary, it's
most valuable after you understand why the organization is the way it is. Without context, the
assessment can be myopic and miss crucial dependencies or limitations dictated by the broader
business environment.
3. Future State Relies on Context: Agreeing on the future state (option C) also hinges on
understanding the organization. The desired future state should be realistic, aligned with business
objectives, and achievable given the organization's resources and capabilities. This is only possible
with contextual awareness.
4. Implementation is the Last Step: Implementing improvements (option D) is the culmination of the
optimization process. It only comes after understanding the context, assessing the current state, and
agreeing on the future state. Implementing without these steps is likely to result in wasted effort and

potentially disruptive changes.
5. ITIL 4 Guiding Principles: The "Focus on Value" and "Start Where You Are" guiding principles
reinforce this approach. Understanding the context allows you to identify what truly delivers value to
the organization and to make incremental improvements based on the existing environment.
Therefore, by first understanding the organizational context, service improvements are more likely to align
with business goals, meet stakeholder needs, and ultimately deliver sustainable value. This approach
minimizes risk and increases the likelihood of successful optimization.
Further reading:
ITIL 4 Foundation: ITIL 4 Edition: Numerous books and online courses cover the ITIL 4 foundation principles,
including the importance of understanding context.
Axelos Website: https://www.axelos.com/ This is the official website for ITIL. It provides information on ITIL 4
and related topics. Specifically, look for details on the guiding principles.
Question: 296 CertyIQ
Which practice would be MOST involved in assessing the risk to services when a supplier modifies the contract
they offer to the organization?
A.Service request management
B.Change enablement
C.Incident management
D.Service level management
Answer: D
Explanation:
The correct answer is D, Service Level Management. Here's why:
Service Level Management (SLM) focuses on establishing and managing agreements about the level of
service provided to customers. These agreements, often documented in Service Level Agreements (SLAs), are
directly affected when a supplier modifies their contract. A modified contract from a supplier providing a key
service component directly alters the terms under which that service is delivered. SLM is responsible for
ensuring that the agreed-upon service levels are still achievable given the change in supplier contract.
SLM plays a vital role in identifying the impact of the contract change on existing SLAs and operational level
agreements (OLAs). It assesses whether the new contractual terms will negatively impact service delivery,
potentially leading to SLA breaches or affecting customer satisfaction. It involves proactively identifying and
mitigating risks associated with these changes to ensure that services remain within acceptable performance
levels.
Furthermore, SLM is responsible for communicating these changes and their potential impact to relevant
stakeholders. Adjustments to SLAs or OLAs may be necessary to reflect the altered supplier agreement. SLM
will be actively engaged in renegotiating internal agreements to align with the revised supplier terms.
While Change Enablement (B) would be involved in managing the implementation of changes resulting from
the contract modification, SLM is primarily concerned with assessing the risk to service levels caused by the
changes to the contractual agreement. Incident management (C) deals with restoring services after a
disruption, not proactively assessing risk. Service request management (A) focuses on fulfilling routine user
requests.

SLM ensures that any alterations to supplier agreements align with the organization's service level targets
and maintains service quality despite external changes. It bridges the gap between supplier contracts and
customer expectations, actively working to reduce the risks associated with supplier modifications. Therefore,
Service Level Management is the MOST involved in assessing the risk.
For further information on ITIL 4 practices, you can refer to:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Handbook: This is the official guide to ITIL 4.
ITIL official website: https://www.axelos.com/
Question: 297 CertyIQ
Which is a financially valuable component that can contribute to the delivery of a service?
A.Sponsor
B.Configuration item
C.IT asset
D.Service offering
Answer: C
Explanation:
The correct answer is C. IT asset. Here's why:
An IT asset is a financially valuable component that contributes to the delivery of a service. IT assets
encompass all the resources an organization owns or controls that contribute to the delivery of IT services.
They have a financial value that needs to be managed. This includes hardware, software, networks, and even
intellectual property. Effective management of IT assets ensures optimal utilization and contributes to the
overall financial performance of the service.
Let's examine why the other options are less accurate:
A. Sponsor: A sponsor provides funding and support for a service, but is not a physical or virtual component of
the service itself. While essential, their contribution is financial and strategic rather than a component directly
delivering the service.
B. Configuration item: A configuration item (CI) is any component that needs to be managed in order to deliver
an IT service, but not all CIs are financially valuable. While all IT assets are CIs, not all CIs are IT assets. For
instance, documentation can be a CI but doesn't inherently have a financial value like a server or a software
license does.
D. Service offering: A service offering describes the value provided to a specific customer or user group. While
it has financial implications, it is not a financially valuable component in the way a tangible or intangible asset
is.
Therefore, only an IT asset directly represents a resource with intrinsic financial worth that directly aids
service delivery. The ITIL framework emphasizes managing these assets to ensure value realization and return
on investment.
Further research:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Handbook
https://www.axelos.com/

Question: 298 CertyIQ
Which term is used to describe removing something that could have an effort on a service?
A.A change
B.An incident
C.A problem
D.An IT asset
Answer: A
Explanation:
The correct answer is A, Change. A change, within the ITIL 4 framework, is defined as the addition,
modification, or removal of anything that could have a direct or indirect effect on services. This explicitly
includes removing components or elements from the service environment.
An incident is an unplanned interruption to a service or reduction in the quality of a service. While removing
something could potentially cause an incident, the action itself is not an incident.
A problem is the cause, or potential cause, of one or more incidents. Again, removing something might reveal
a problem, but the removal itself isn't the problem.
An IT asset is any valuable component that contributes to the delivery of an IT product or service. While
removing an IT asset is a change, the term "IT asset" itself describes what is being removed, not the process
of removal.
Therefore, "change" is the most accurate term to describe the action of removing something that has an
effect on a service, as it directly addresses the process of modification within the ITIL framework. The other
options relate to outcomes or states of the system after or potentially before the action. Removing a faulty
server (an IT asset) to improve service stability is a change; the unplanned downtime while removing it could
be an incident, and the faulty server could be due to an underlying problem. But the act of removing the server
itself is the change.Furthermore, a well-managed change process considers the impact of the change,
minimizing the potential for incidents.
Here are a couple of useful resources for further research:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Syllabus: This document details the core concepts of ITIL 4.
Official ITIL 4 publications: The AXELOS website (the governing body for ITIL) provides access to official
publications and training materials.
Question: 299 CertyIQ
Which TWO BEST describe the guiding principles?
1. Short-term
2. Standards
3. Recommendations
4. Long-term
A.1 and 4
B.2 and 3
C.3 and 4
D.1 and 2
Answer: C

Explanation:
The correct answer is C, because ITIL guiding principles are best described as recommendations and long-
term strategies.
ITIL guiding principles are not short-term (option 1) because they provide enduring guidance applicable across
numerous circumstances, regardless of changes in goals, strategies, type of work, or management structure.
They are designed to be consistently applied over time.
ITIL guiding principles aren't rigid standards (option 2). While they influence practices, they don't prescribe
specific actions. Instead, they offer adaptable recommendations that organizations can tailor to their unique
context.
The ITIL guiding principles are definitely recommendations (option 3). They provide advice and guidance on
how to approach service management activities and decisions. They encourage flexible and thoughtful
application rather than strict adherence.
Finally, the ITIL guiding principles are long-term (option 4). They represent enduring values and approaches
that should inform an organization's service management decisions and actions over the long haul, ensuring
consistency and alignment with overall objectives. The principles create a foundation for continuous
improvement.
Therefore, "Recommendations" and "Long-term" (option C) best characterize the nature and purpose of ITIL
guiding principles, differentiating them from prescriptive standards and short-sighted approaches. They are
meant to provide persistent direction and influence behavior across all activities.
Further research:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Handbook
https://www.axelos.com/
Question: 300 CertyIQ
Which BEST describes the focus of the 'think and work holistically' principle?
A.Breaking down large initiatives into smaller pieces of work
B.Integrating an organization's activities to deliver value
C.Eliminating unnecessary steps to deliver valuable outcomes
D.Considering the existing organizational assets before building something new
Answer: B
Explanation:
The "think and work holistically" principle within ITIL 4 emphasizes the importance of considering the
interconnectedness of all activities within an organization and its ecosystem when delivering value. Option B,
"Integrating an organization's activities to deliver value," perfectly captures this essence. This principle
promotes a system-thinking approach, recognizing that changes in one area can impact others.
Breaking down large initiatives (Option A) aligns more with iterative development or DevOps practices.
Eliminating unnecessary steps (Option C) relates to efficiency and lean principles, not necessarily holistic
thinking. Considering existing assets (Option D) is important but doesn't encompass the full scope of holistic
consideration.
"Think and work holistically" requires understanding how different organizational units, IT systems, and
stakeholders interact. It encourages collaboration across silos and a unified approach to service management.

This ensures that value is delivered not just by individual components but through a well-integrated system. It
involves considering not just the internal organizational elements but also external factors like partners,
suppliers, customers, and the broader business ecosystem. By taking a broader view and integrating all
necessary activities, organizations can maximize value creation and avoid unintended consequences. An
organization should look at the big picture to deliver value and not just focus on individual parts or
steps.Links:https://www.axelos.com/https://www.bmc.com/blogs/itil-4-principles/
Question: 301 CertyIQ
Which is the FIRST thing to consider when focusing on value?
A.Defining customer experience and user experience
B.Understanding what is valuable to the service consumer
C.Ensuring value is co-created by improvement initiatives
D.Identifying the service consumer who will receive value
Answer: D
Explanation:
The correct answer is D. Identifying the service consumer who will receive value.
Here's a detailed justification:
When focusing on value within the ITIL 4 framework, the crucial first step is to understand who will be
receiving that value. Before you can define customer experience, understand what they consider valuable, or
even co-create value, you must know who the service consumer is. This identification process is fundamental
because it allows you to tailor your understanding of "value" to their specific needs, priorities, and context.
Understanding who benefits from a service is a pre-requisite to what constitutes value.
Only by identifying the service consumer (the individual or group receiving value) can one then effectively
explore what is valuable to them (option B). You can't understand their perception of value without first
knowing who "they" are. It is important to know if you are targeting end-users, developers, or the business as
a whole. Each would interpret the service in a completely different way. Similarly, you can't effectively define
the customer/user experience (option A) without knowing the characteristics, expectations, and existing
relationships of the service consumer. Co-creation of value (option C) is also a later step that builds upon
understanding the consumer. You must understand who you're co-creating with.
Therefore, "Identifying the service consumer who will receive value" is the most logical and foundational first
step in focusing on value. It sets the stage for all subsequent activities related to understanding and
delivering value.

AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Syllabus: This is the primary source for ITIL 4 concepts.
