Question: 302 CertyIQ
Identify the missing word in the following sentence.
An organization which is undertaking an improvement initiative should [?] the existing methods and services when
building for the future.

A.Discard
B.Improve
C.Consider
D.Re-use
Answer: C
Explanation:
The correct answer is C. Consider.
An organization embarking on an improvement initiative needs to carefully consider its existing methods and
services. Simply discarding them (A) would be wasteful and potentially lose valuable knowledge. Immediately
improving (B) them without proper assessment might lead to optimizing flawed processes. Blindly re-using (D)
everything may prevent the necessary changes for true improvement.
Consideration allows for a thorough evaluation. This involves analyzing the strengths and weaknesses of the
current state, understanding what works well, and identifying areas needing enhancement. This balanced
approach enables informed decisions about which elements to retain, modify, or replace. It's not about
discarding everything and starting from scratch, nor is it about blindly sticking to the status quo.
By considering the existing methods and services, the organization can leverage its past experiences and
avoid repeating mistakes. They can identify best practices to retain and build upon, while simultaneously
addressing inefficiencies and areas for improvement. This strategy ensures that the future state builds upon a
solid foundation and minimizes disruptions. Choosing between discarding, reusing, or improving requires a
deep understanding of the current situation. Failing to consider all elements can lead to inefficiencies and a
less effective outcome. ITIL 4 places emphasis on holistic thinking and continuous improvement, meaning a
balanced evaluation process is key.
Consideration enables identifying valuable assets that can be effectively integrated into future solutions. It
helps to ensure that the investment in past services is not completely lost, maximizing the return on
investment. The consideration phase involves risk assessments and feasibility studies, which is important in
the realm of ITIL and service management. Without this assessment, any improvement initiative could fail to
deliver the desired outcomes.
Therefore, consider is the most appropriate word, as it emphasizes the necessary evaluation and analysis
required before making decisions about the existing methods and services in the context of an improvement
initiative.
Refer to the following sources for more information:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Syllabus: https://www.axelos.com/ (Official source, requires
registration/purchase)
ITIL Foundation Handbook: Various publishers offer handbooks; search online retailers. Look for editions
covering ITIL 4.
Question: 303 CertyIQ
What is the difference between the 'incident management' and 'service desk' practices?
A.Incident management resolves issues, service desk investigates the underlying causes of issues
B.Incident management restores service operation, service desk provides communication with users
C.Incident management manages interruptions to services, service desk monitors achieved service quality
D.Incident management resolves complex issues, service desk resolves simpler issues

Answer: B
Explanation:
The best answer is B: Incident management restores service operation, service desk provides communication
with users. Here's why:
Incident Management Focus: Incident management is primarily concerned with restoring normal service
operation as quickly as possible to minimize the adverse impact on business operations. Its core objective is
rapid recovery.
Service Desk's Role: The service desk is a single point of contact between the service provider and the users.
A key function is communication, keeping users informed about service disruptions, progress on incident
resolution, and any workarounds available. It provides support, answers queries, and logs incidents.
Why Other Options are Less Accurate:
A is incorrect because while incident management restores service, problem management (not service desk)
investigates underlying causes.
C is incorrect because both practices deal with service interruptions, and monitoring service quality is a
broader responsibility.
D is incorrect because the complexity of the issue isn't the defining difference; both practices may handle
issues of varying difficulty, and escalation procedures exist for complex incidents.
ITIL 4 Guiding Principles: The core principle of 'Focus on Value' is supported by swiftly restoring services,
minimizing business impact, and communicating to users clearly about the value of IT.
Practical Application: Think of a web application outage. Incident management would be the processes to
bring the website back online. The service desk would be the team answering user calls, emails, and providing
updates on the situation.
In summary: Incident management focuses on restoring service, while the service desk focuses on
communication and user support. They work closely together but have distinct primary objectives.
Authoritative Links:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Syllabus (This is the official source but requires purchase)
BMC Blogs - What is a Service Desk?
Atlassian - Incident Management
Question: 304 CertyIQ
Which step of the 'continual management model' defines measurable targets?
A.Where do we want to be?
B.What is the vision?
C.How do we get there?
D.Where are we now?
Answer: A
Explanation:
The correct answer is A, "Where do we want to be?" within the ITIL 4 Continual Improvement Model. This
stage focuses on defining specific, measurable, achievable, relevant, and time-bound (SMART) goals. It

translates the overarching vision into practical and quantifiable targets that the organization aims to achieve
through its improvement efforts. This stage sets the direction and provides a clear destination for the
improvement journey.
The "Where do we want to be?" stage essentially defines the desired future state. It requires a thorough
understanding of the current state (analyzed in the "Where are we now?" stage) and a clear vision of where
the organization aims to be after implementing improvements. By defining measurable targets, organizations
can track progress, assess the effectiveness of improvement initiatives, and make necessary adjustments
along the way. Without clearly defined targets, improvement efforts can become aimless and lack focus.
Option B, "What is the vision?" represents the high-level aspirational statement that guides the entire
improvement effort. It provides the overall direction but doesn't necessarily contain measurable targets.
Option C, "How do we get there?" focuses on planning the actions and activities needed to achieve the
defined targets. This stage involves developing strategies, tactics, and timelines. Option D, "Where are we
now?" is about assessing the current situation and understanding the baseline against which improvement
will be measured.
Therefore, defining measurable targets is the core function of the "Where do we want to be?" stage, making A
the most accurate answer. It is about setting performance objectives which are crucial for any successful
business process improvement, including those leveraging cloud computing. These objectives must align with
business strategy, customer demand and IT service availability and
performance.https://www.axelos.com/https://www.bmc.com/blogs/itil-4-continuous-improvement-model/
Question: 305 CertyIQ
What is included in the purpose of the 'release management' practice?
A.Authorizing changes to proceed
B.Making new features available for use
C.Moving new software to live environments
D.Ensuring information about services is available
Answer: B
Explanation:
The correct answer is B: Making new features available for use.
Release management's core purpose is to make new and changed services and features available for use. This
includes planning, building, testing, and deploying these new capabilities into a live environment, ultimately
enabling users to benefit from them. While moving new software to live environments (option C) is a
component of release management, it's not the encompassing purpose. Release management encompasses
activities beyond just the deployment itself. Authorizing changes (option A) is the domain of change
control/change enablement, and ensuring information about services is available (option D) is more related to
service level management and service desk. Release management ensures that new features and
functionalities are delivered effectively to users. This involves aspects of planning, design, build,
configuration, testing, and release itself. The final goal is that the end users can access and make effective
use of these new and changed components of IT services.
For further information, refer to official ITIL 4 documentation and resources, such as the Axelos website:
https://www.axelos.com/.

Question: 306 CertyIQ
Why should a service level agreement include bundles of metrics?
A.To reduce the number of metrics that need to be measured and reported
B.To help focus on business outcomes, rather than operational results
C.To ensure that the service levels have been agreed with customers
D.To ensure that all services are included in the service reports
Answer: B
Explanation:
The correct answer is B: To help focus on business outcomes, rather than operational results.
Service Level Agreements (SLAs) shouldn't just be about technical metrics in isolation. They should translate
how those metrics impact the customer's business. Bundling metrics helps achieve this. A bundle, carefully
constructed, can represent a specific business outcome. For example, instead of just tracking server uptime,
network latency, and database response time separately, an SLA could bundle these into a metric
representing "Order Processing Performance," directly tied to the speed and reliability with which customers
can place orders.
Focusing on bundled metrics forces service providers to think about how their services contribute to the
customer's overall business goals. It shifts the conversation from technical details to business value. While
individual metrics are important for diagnosing problems, the SLA should emphasize what the customer cares
about – the impact on their revenue, efficiency, or customer satisfaction. It allows for better communication
and alignment between the provider and consumer by concentrating on results that resonate with business
leaders. Therefore, by bundling metrics, SLAs can demonstrate a service's worth in clear, business-relevant
terms, enhancing the overall service experience.
Incorrect answers:
A. To reduce the number of metrics that need to be measured and reported: While simplification can be a
benefit, the primary purpose isn't simply to reduce the number of metrics. It's about making them more
meaningful.
C. To ensure that the service levels have been agreed with customers: Customer agreement is a general
requirement for all SLA content, not specifically for bundled metrics.
D. To ensure that all services are included in the service reports: Inclusion of all services in reports is a
general reporting requirement and not related to bundling metrics.
Relevant Resources:
ITIL 4 Foundation: ITIL 4 Edition (Refer to service level management and its purpose.)
What is an SLA? Best practices for service-level agreements (Atlassian Article on SLAs)
Question: 307 CertyIQ
Which of the four dimensions contributes MOST to defining activities needed to deliver services?
A.Partners and suppliers
B.Organizations and people
C.Value streams and processes
D.Information and technology

Answer: C
Explanation:
The correct answer is C, Value streams and processes. Here's why:
The ITIL 4 framework emphasizes a holistic approach to service management, represented by the Four
Dimensions Model. This model considers four perspectives that collectively ensure a balanced and effective
approach to value creation. These dimensions are: Organizations and People, Information and Technology,
Partners and Suppliers, and Value Streams and Processes.
While all four dimensions contribute to service delivery, the Value Streams and Processes dimension is the
most directly related to defining the activities needed to deliver services. This dimension focuses on how an
organization organizes its activities, workflows, controls, and procedures to achieve agreed-upon objectives. It
defines the steps and interactions required to create and deliver value to customers.
Value streams represent the series of steps an organization undertakes to create and deliver products and
services to a consumer. They encompass the end-to-end activities that contribute to the realization of value.
Processes, on the other hand, are structured sets of activities designed to accomplish a specific objective.
They are components within a value stream. Therefore, understanding and designing value streams and
processes is crucial for outlining the activities needed to bring a service to life.
The other dimensions are important enablers, but they don't directly define the activities. Organizations and
People provide the structure and human resources, Information and Technology provides the tools, and
Partners and Suppliers provide external resources. However, it is the Value Streams and Processes that
explicitly map out what needs to be done, by whom, and how, to provide services. Without well-defined value
streams and processes, even the best organization, technology, and partnerships will fail to deliver consistent
and valuable services. They dictate the actual tasks performed.
For further reading, you can refer to:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Publication: (Available for purchase) - This publication provides a comprehensive
overview of the ITIL 4 framework, including the Four Dimensions Model.
Official ITIL Website: https://www.axelos.com/ - This website provides information about ITIL certifications,
training, and resources.
Question: 308 CertyIQ
Which practice balances management of risk with maximizing throughput?
A.Problem management
B.Incident management
C.Continual improvement
D.Change enablement
Answer: D
Explanation:
The correct answer is D, Change Enablement.
Change Enablement (formerly known as Change Management) is the ITIL 4 practice that balances the need
for beneficial changes with the need to protect the organization from risks associated with those changes. It's
not about preventing all changes; it's about ensuring changes are properly assessed, authorized, and
implemented in a way that minimizes negative impacts. This directly aligns with the goal of maximizing

throughput while carefully managing risk.
Problem Management focuses on identifying and resolving underlying causes of incidents, not specifically on
managing the risks associated with implementing changes. While problem management can contribute to risk
reduction, it's not the primary practice for balancing risk and throughput.
Incident Management prioritizes restoring normal service operation as quickly as possible, minimizing
disruption to the business. It reacts to issues, whereas Change Enablement is proactive in assessing and
mitigating risks before changes cause incidents.
Continual Improvement is a broader practice encompassing all areas of service management, including
change enablement, incident management, and problem management. It doesn't directly focus on the specific
balancing act of risk and throughput like Change Enablement does. Change Enablement is a specific practice
that contributes to Continual Improvement.
Change enablement processes include risk assessments, authorization workflows (often involving a Change
Authority or CAB), and implementation planning, all designed to allow valuable changes to be deployed
safely. By carefully evaluating and approving changes, Change Enablement maximizes the opportunity to
deliver value quickly (throughput) while minimizing the probability or impact of adverse outcomes (risk). The
practice's objective is to support changes with appropriate planning and governance, hence balancing agility
and stability.
Further research:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Handbook: (This is the official source but often requires purchase/subscription)
This is the primary source for understanding ITIL 4 concepts.
Official ITIL Website (AXELOS): https://www.axelos.com/ (Look for white papers and articles on Change
Enablement)
Various ITIL 4 blogs and articles: Search the web for "ITIL 4 Change Enablement" to find various articles and
blog posts explaining the practice. Be aware that some sources may not be authoritative.
Question: 309 CertyIQ
Which is recommended as part of the 'progress iteratively with feedback' guiding principle?
A.Analyze the whole situation in detail before taking any action
B.Reduce the number of steps that produce tangible results
C.Prohibit changes to plans after they have been finalized
D.Organize work into small manageable units
Answer: D
Explanation:
The correct answer is D. Organize work into small manageable units.
Here's why: The 'progress iteratively with feedback' guiding principle emphasizes breaking down complex
tasks into smaller, more manageable pieces. This approach allows for frequent review, adaptation based on
feedback, and faster realization of value. Organizing work into small units facilitates iterative progress by
allowing teams to complete and demonstrate value incrementally, gather feedback on each increment, and
adjust future increments based on that feedback. This supports agility and responsiveness to changing
requirements.

Option A is incorrect because 'progress iteratively with feedback' promotes acting and learning rather than
extensive analysis upfront. Option B contradicts the principle; it seeks to increase the frequency of tangible
results through short iterations. Option C opposes the entire idea of incorporating feedback and adapting
plans. It's rigid, while iterative progress requires flexibility.
Organizing work into small manageable units provides several benefits:
Faster feedback cycles: Smaller units allow for quicker completion and demonstration, leading to more
frequent feedback opportunities.
Improved risk management: Identifying and addressing issues early reduces the impact of potential
problems.
Increased flexibility: Adjusting plans becomes easier because changes are contained within smaller units.
Enhanced collaboration: Smaller units facilitate closer collaboration and communication among team
members.
Better quality: Frequent feedback loops lead to improvements and higher-quality output.
In short, breaking down tasks into smaller, manageable units aligns perfectly with the iterative nature of the
'progress iteratively with feedback' guiding principle, allowing for continuous improvement and
adaptation.https://www.axelos.com/https://www.bmc.com/blogs/itil-4-guiding-principles/
Question: 310 CertyIQ
What is included in the purpose of the 'continual improvement' practice?
A.Creating collaborative relationships with key suppliers to realize new value
B.Aligning the organization's practices and services with changing business needs
C.Identifying and continually improving relationships with and between stakeholders
D.Ensuring that delivery of services is properly assessed, monitored, and improved against targets
Answer: B
Explanation:
The most accurate answer is B. Aligning the organization's practices and services with changing business
needs is the core essence of continual improvement within ITIL 4. Continual improvement isn't just about
fixing what's broken; it's a proactive approach to ensuring IT services remain relevant and valuable as
business priorities evolve. This alignment involves assessing current performance, identifying areas for
enhancement, and implementing changes that directly support the organization's strategic goals. It is a
cyclical process of identifying opportunities for improvement, planning improvements, implementing those
improvements, and measuring the results.
Option A focuses primarily on supplier relationships, which is relevant but not the primary goal of the
Continual Improvement practice. While suppliers are important, the practice's broader scope covers all
aspects of service management. Option C emphasizes stakeholder relationships, which are also crucial, but
are a part of service relationship management, not continual improvement's core purpose. Option D, while
touching upon improvement, is more focused on performance monitoring and assessment, which falls under
different practices such as incident management, problem management, etc.
Continual improvement facilitates adaptation to shifting market demands, technological advancements, and
regulatory changes. By continuously evaluating and refining processes, IT can proactively address potential
issues and capitalize on emerging opportunities. The ITIL 4 framework highlights the importance of a holistic
approach to improvement, involving all stakeholders and considering the entire value stream. The seven
guiding principles of ITIL 4 further reinforce this focus, including "Focus on value," "Start where you are," and

"Progress iteratively with feedback." These principles underscore the need for a practical and adaptable
approach to improvement.
For further research, refer to the official ITIL 4 Foundation guidance published by AXELOS:
https://www.axelos.com/ and explore articles and blogs discussing continual service improvement in the
context of ITIL 4.
Question: 311 CertyIQ
How does the 'incident management' practice set user expectations?
A.By using collaboration tools to communicate effectively
B.By agreeing, and communicating target resolution times
C.By assigning resources to ensure that all incidents are resolved as quickly as possible
D.By automated matching of incidents to known errors
Answer: B
Explanation:
The correct answer is B. Here's why:
Incident Management's role in setting user expectations revolves around transparency and predictability
regarding service restoration. Option B, "By agreeing, and communicating target resolution times," directly
addresses this. When incidents occur, users are most concerned about when their services will be restored.
Establishing Service Level Agreements (SLAs) or Operational Level Agreements (OLAs) dictates target
resolution times for different incident severities. Communicating these targets provides users with a realistic
expectation of when they can anticipate a resolution. Without such communication, users are left in the dark,
leading to dissatisfaction and a perception of poor service. While using collaboration tools (A) and assigning
resources quickly (C) are good practices, they don't inherently set expectations. Automated matching to
known errors (D) is proactive but doesn't directly manage user expectations in the context of incident
management communication.
Target resolution times, often defined within SLAs/OLAs, are actively managed through incident prioritization,
resource allocation, and escalation procedures. When incidents occur, incident management teams use these
predefined goals to focus on the most critical items, communicating progress and estimated resolution times
to impacted users. This proactive communication helps users understand the resolution process and keeps
them updated.
https://www.axelos.com/ - The official source for ITIL information.https://www.bmc.com/blogs/itil-incident-
management/ - Provides a general overview of ITIL Incident Management.
Question: 312 CertyIQ
What is a user?
A.The role that defines the requirements for a service
B.The role that directs and controls an organization
C.The role that uses services
D.The role that authorizes budget for service consumption

Answer: A
Explanation:
The provided answer, A ("The role that defines the requirements for a service"), is incorrect in the context of
ITIL 4 Foundation. The correct answer is C ("The role that uses services").
Here's a justification:
ITIL 4 defines key concepts and roles related to service management. A user is the individual or group that
consumes or utilizes the services provided by a service provider. Their primary interaction with the service
provider is through the utilization of these services to achieve their own goals. The defining characteristic of a
user is their consumption of services.
Option A, "The role that defines the requirements for a service," describes the role of stakeholders involved in
service design, development, and improvement, not the everyday consumer of the service. While users might
provide feedback or input on requirements, their defining role is service consumption.
Option B, "The role that directs and controls an organization," refers to leadership or governance roles within
an organization.
Option D, "The role that authorizes budget for service consumption," describes a stakeholder with financial
responsibilities, not necessarily the person using the service.
In essence, a user's primary characteristic is service usage. ITIL 4 focuses on value co-creation, and users are
a critical part of that equation, receiving value by using the services. Understanding the user's needs and
usage patterns is vital for effective service management and continual improvement.
Authoritative Links:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Syllabus: https://www.axelos.com/ (While you may need to purchase the syllabus
or course materials for explicit definitions, it's the official source)
Official ITIL 4 publications (available for purchase) provide in-depth explanations of key concepts like service
users.
Question: 313 CertyIQ
How do 'continual improvement registers' help to create value?
A.By making improvements visible
B.By monitoring achievement against service level targets
C.By assigning change authorities for change requests
D.By documenting all improvement ideas in a single place
Answer: D
Explanation:
The correct answer is D. By documenting all improvement ideas in a single place.
Continual Improvement Registers (CIRs) are crucial for value creation because they serve as a centralized
repository for all improvement opportunities, ideas, and proposals identified across the organization. This
central location fosters transparency and ensures no valuable suggestion is overlooked. By documenting
these ideas, the CIR provides a comprehensive overview of potential enhancements to processes, services, or
products. This centralized approach facilitates prioritization based on factors like potential value, feasibility,
and resource availability. Without a CIR, improvement ideas might be scattered, forgotten, or duplicated,

leading to inefficiencies and lost opportunities to enhance value for both the organization and its customers.
The structured documentation within the CIR enables effective tracking of improvement initiatives, allowing
for progress monitoring and performance measurement. Furthermore, the CIR promotes collaboration among
teams by providing a shared platform for discussing and refining improvement ideas. The visibility afforded by
the CIR helps to cultivate a culture of continuous improvement, encouraging everyone to contribute to
enhancing service quality and creating value. The register provides a historical record of improvements, which
can be valuable for future decision-making and training. Making improvements visible (A) is a positive
consequence of using a CIR, but documenting all ideas is the fundamental purpose. Monitoring service level
targets (B) and assigning change authorities (C) are activities related to service level management and change
management, respectively, and are separate from the primary function of a CIR.
Supporting links:
AXELOS - ITIL 4 Foundation: Continual Improvement: https://www.axelos.com/ (Official ITIL provider -
requires subscription or course access for detailed information)
BMC Blogs - What is ITIL 4? A quick guide for beginners: https://www.bmc.com/blogs/itil-4-guide/ (General
overview; search for "continual improvement")
Question: 314 CertyIQ
Which statement about the inputs and outputs of the value chain activities is CORRECT?
A.Each value chain activity receives inputs and provides outputs
B.The organization's governance will determine the inputs and outputs of each value chain activity
C.Some value chain activities only have inputs, whereas others only have outputs
D.Inputs and outputs are fixed for each value chain activity
Answer: A
Explanation:
The correct answer is A: "Each value chain activity receives inputs and provides outputs."
Here's the justification:
The ITIL 4 value chain is a fundamental concept that outlines how an organization creates value. Each activity
within the value chain is interconnected and transforms inputs into outputs, ultimately contributing to the
overall value proposition for the customer. Each activity's output becomes input for a subsequent activity. If
an activity only had inputs or outputs, it would disrupt the flow of value creation and prevent the realization of
benefits. This inherent input/output relationship ensures a continuous and connected series of actions that
progress towards delivering a valuable service or product.
Option B is incorrect because while governance influences value chain activities, it doesn't determine the
specific inputs and outputs. The nature of the activity itself does. Governance provides the framework and
policies, but the operational aspects dictate the inputs and outputs.
Option C is incorrect. The core of the ITIL 4 value chain hinges on transformation. Every activity must
transform inputs to outputs.
Option D is incorrect because inputs and outputs can change based on the specific circumstances, context,
and demand. While activities have general input/output categories, their exact nature is not fixed.
Therefore, A is the only statement that accurately reflects the fundamental nature of value chain activities in
ITIL 4.

Further reading:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Syllabus: (Refer to the official ITIL 4 Foundation syllabus for a comprehensive
understanding of the value chain. It is usually accessed through accredited training providers.)
ITIL Foundation Handbook: (This handbook, or similar publications from accredited training organizations,
provides detailed explanations of the ITIL 4 concepts, including the value chain.)
The value chain's inherent input/output model emphasizes the importance of understanding the entire
process and how each activity contributes to value creation. Without this continuous flow, value delivery
would be impossible.
Question: 315 CertyIQ
What is the value of a service?
A.A tangible or intangible deliverable of the service
B.The amount of money that is created or saved for the service consumers by using the service
C.The benefits, usefulness, or importance of the service, as perceived by the stakeholders
D.A result for a stakeholder enabled by the outputs of the service
Answer: C
Explanation:
The correct answer, C, defines the value of a service as the benefits, usefulness, or importance of the service,
as perceived by the stakeholders. This aligns perfectly with the core concept of value creation in ITIL 4, which
emphasizes understanding and meeting the specific needs and expectations of all involved parties. Value is
not simply a financial metric (eliminating option B), nor is it solely about the service's output (eliminating
option A). Instead, value is subjective and contingent on the stakeholder's perception of the service's
contribution to their goals.
Option D, while related to value, focuses on the result enabled by the service's outputs. This is closer to
describing an outcome than the overall perceived value. Value encompasses not just the outcome, but also
the manner in which it's delivered, the experience of using the service, and the impact on the stakeholder's
objectives. In cloud computing, for example, a cloud-based server (the output) enabling faster application
deployment (the result) creates value because it increases business agility and reduces time-to-market,
aligning with business stakeholder needs. Stakeholders such as customers, users, sponsors, and even service
providers all have varying perspectives on the worth a service offers. By identifying these varied values,
service providers can better target improvements to maximize the perceived benefit. ITIL 4 places strong
emphasis on co-creation of value; the service provider and consumer should work together to ensure that the
service provided meets the needs of the consumer. This collaborative approach helps in understanding how
the service affects the consumer's business and operations, which subsequently affects the consumer's
perception of the service's overall value. This collaborative process is what enhances trust and mutual benefit
between the parties involved. Thus, capturing the entirety of the benefit falls best under option C.
For further research, refer to:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Handbook: This provides comprehensive coverage of ITIL 4 concepts.
ITIL 4 Managing Professional (MP) books: These books go into detail concerning practical application of ITIL
principles.
Official AXELOS website: (axelos.com) Provides information about ITIL certifications and resources.

Question: 316 CertyIQ
Which is the MOST LIKELY way of resolving major incidents?
A.A support team following detailed procedures for investigating the incident
B.Users establishing a resolution using self-help
C.A temporary team working together to identify a resolution
D.The service desk identifying the cause and a resolution
Answer: C
Explanation:
The justification for answer C being the most likely way to resolve major incidents lies in the nature of such
incidents themselves. Major incidents are defined as high-impact, high-urgency events causing significant
disruption to business operations. A support team with detailed procedures (A) is typically suited for known,
recurring issues, not novel, large-scale disruptions. Self-help (B) is unlikely to be effective for complex
incidents affecting a broad user base. While the service desk plays a critical role (D) in identifying and
escalating incidents, they usually don't possess the specialized expertise needed for rapid resolution of major
incidents.
Major incidents often require a coordinated, cross-functional response. This is why a temporary team, also
known as an incident resolution team or war room team, is formed. This team brings together specialists from
different areas (network, security, applications, etc.) to collaboratively investigate, diagnose, and implement a
resolution under high pressure. This approach allows for diverse perspectives and faster decision-making,
critical for minimizing downtime and business impact. The "swarm intelligence" generated by this team is
crucial for troubleshooting complex, unprecedented issues. Option C explicitly acknowledges the temporary,
collaborative, and solution-focused approach characteristic of major incident management.
Here are authoritative links for further research on Major Incident Management:
Axelos ITIL 4 Foundation Handbook: https://www.axelos.com/ (Official ITIL source - requires purchase or
subscription but provides definitive guidance)
Atlassian - Major Incident Management: https://www.atlassian.com/it-solutions/incident-
management/major-incident (Offers practical guidance on establishing an incident management process)
PagerDuty - Major Incident Management: https://www.pagerduty.com/incident-response/major-incident-
management/ (Provides insights on best practices and tools for major incident response)
Question: 317 CertyIQ
What is the CORRECT order for the three phases of problem management?
A.Problem control, error control, problem identification
B.Problem identification, problem control, error control
C.Error control, problem control, problem identification
D.Problem identification, error control, problem control
Answer: B
Explanation:
The correct order for the three phases of problem management in ITIL 4 is Problem Identification, Problem
Control, and Error Control. This sequence ensures a systematic and efficient approach to resolving underlying
issues in IT services.

Problem Identification is the first and crucial step. It involves detecting and logging problems. This can arise
from analyzing incidents, monitoring systems, or proactively searching for potential issues. Identifying
patterns and trends in incidents often reveals underlying problems. A well-defined problem statement is
essential to focus subsequent efforts.
Next comes Problem Control. This phase focuses on analyzing the problem, determining its root cause, and
developing workarounds to mitigate its impact on users. Techniques like the "5 Whys" or Ishikawa diagrams
(fishbone diagrams) are commonly used to uncover the root cause. Workarounds are temporary solutions to
reduce the negative impact of the problem while a permanent fix is being developed.
Finally, Error Control is about identifying a permanent solution to the problem, testing the solution
thoroughly, and implementing it to resolve the underlying issue. This involves implementing change
management procedures and ensuring that the fix is properly documented. Error control also addresses
Known Errors, which are problems where the root cause has been diagnosed but a solution hasn't been
implemented yet. Error records are maintained to facilitate future problem resolution.
The order is important because you can't control a problem until you've identified it, and you can't resolve the
error until you've controlled the problem and discovered its root cause. By following this structured approach,
organizations can proactively manage their IT services, reduce the number of incidents, and improve overall
service quality.
For further reading, refer to the ITIL 4 Foundation syllabus and publications:
Axelos: https://www.axelos.com/ (Official source for ITIL information). Note that direct links to specific
syllabus content may require a subscription or purchase. Look for "ITIL 4 Foundation" materials.
ITIL Foundation Exam Study Guide: Numerous guides are available through online retailers. Search for "ITIL 4
Foundation Exam Study Guide." Ensure that the guide is based on the latest ITIL 4 principles.
Question: 318 CertyIQ
What is included in the purpose of the 'IT asset management' practice?
A.Supporting decision-making about purchase, re-use, retirement, and disposal of assets
B.Providing information on how assets are configured and the relationships between them
C.Making new and changed assets available for use
D.Moving assets to live or other environments for testing or staging
Answer: A
Explanation:
The correct answer is A, supporting decision-making about purchase, re-use, retirement, and disposal of
assets, because IT Asset Management (ITAM) is fundamentally concerned with the full lifecycle of IT assets.
This includes the strategic planning and financial considerations surrounding those assets. Its purpose is to
ensure that an organization knows what IT assets it has, where they are, who owns them, how they are being
used, and what their financial impact is.
Answer B, providing information on how assets are configured and the relationships between them, aligns
more closely with the Configuration Management practice, not ITAM. While ITAM benefits from Configuration
Management data, its primary focus isn't the technical details of configuration.
Answer C, making new and changed assets available for use, falls under the scope of Service Validation and
Testing or Release Management, rather than ITAM. ITAM tracks the asset; other practices are involved in
deployment.

Answer D, moving assets to live or other environments for testing or staging, relates to Deployment
Management or Release Management. Again, ITAM provides the foundational data about the asset, but does
not perform these specific actions.
ITAM supports informed decision-making by providing the data needed to optimize asset utilization, minimize
costs, and manage risks associated with IT assets. Without effective ITAM, organizations can overspend on
unnecessary assets, underutilize existing assets, and be exposed to security and compliance risks. The
practice optimizes the financial management of IT, extending asset value through smart decisions about
acquisition, allocation, usage, and disposition. These lifecycle decisions necessitate data regarding both
technical and business considerations.
For further research, refer to the official ITIL 4 Foundation publication and AXELOS resources. Although
freely available specific citations related to this are limited without the publication itself, searching "ITIL 4 IT
Asset Management" on AXELOS' website and other reputable IT service management resources will yield
substantial supporting information.
Question: 319 CertyIQ
Which component is focused on the activities needed by an organization to help it co-create value?
A.Guiding principles
B.Service value chain
C.Continual improvement
D.Practices
Answer: B
Explanation:
The correct answer is B, the Service Value Chain. The Service Value Chain outlines the key activities an
organization undertakes to create value from demand to realization. Its primary function is to enable the
organization to co-create value with its customers and other stakeholders by transforming inputs into
valuable products and services. Each activity within the value chain (Plan, Improve, Engage, Design &
Transition, Obtain/Build, and Deliver & Support) contributes to this co-creation process.
The 'Engage' activity is particularly focused on fostering good relationships with stakeholders and
understanding their needs. 'Design and Transition' ensures that new and changed services meet these needs.
'Obtain/Build' secures the resources necessary to provide services. 'Deliver and Support' directly provides the
service and resolves issues. 'Plan' and 'Improve' underpin the whole process by ensuring strategic direction
and continuous enhancement. Therefore, the entire service value chain as a whole is critical for the activities
needed by an organization to help it co-create value.
Guiding principles (A) are high-level recommendations guiding organizations in all circumstances, regardless
of changes in their goals, strategies, type of work, or management structure. Continual improvement (C) is
about consistently enhancing services and practices, but it's not solely focused on co-creation activities.
Practices (D) are sets of organizational resources designed for performing work or accomplishing an
objective, like incident management or service desk, but, again, the Service Value Chain represents a more
comprehensive and integrated view of co-creation activities.
https://www.axelos.com/ - Look for ITIL 4 Foundation information and
resources.https://www.bmc.com/blogs/itil-service-value-chain/ - For details about the Service Value Chain.

Question: 320 CertyIQ
Why and how is a user MOST LIKELY to contact the service desk?
A.To discuss the cause of an incident via a phone call
B.To report a problem using a mobile app
C.To request access to a resource via a self-service portal
D.To authorize an emergency change via live chat
Answer: B
Explanation:
The justification for option B, "To report a problem using a mobile app," being a likely scenario for a user
contacting the service desk stems from several factors related to modern IT service management and user
convenience. While options C and D represent valid service desk interactions, reporting a problem (an
incident) is statistically the most frequent reason for contact. Mobile apps are increasingly popular channels
for this due to their accessibility and ease of use.
Consider the user's perspective: encountering an issue preventing them from working. A mobile app offers
immediate reporting from anywhere. Self-service portals (option C) are better suited for planned requests like
access to resources. Authorizing an emergency change (option D) would typically involve authorized
personnel, not the average user. Discussing the cause of an incident (option A) is typically the service desk's
task, not the initial contact reason for the user.
Furthermore, modern service desk platforms are optimized for mobile reporting. They allow users to quickly
describe the issue, attach screenshots or videos for clarity, and receive updates on the resolution progress.
This structured approach facilitates faster incident resolution and improves user satisfaction. The immediacy
and accessibility of mobile apps align perfectly with the need for prompt incident reporting in today's fast-
paced work environments. The increased use of self-service portals and automation does shift some
interactions away from direct contact, but incident reporting remains a key driver of user-service desk
interaction, often initiated via mobile channels.
Therefore, the combination of the frequency of incidents and the convenience of mobile apps makes option B
the most probable scenario for a user's initial contact with the service desk.
Relevant links for further research:
ITIL 4 Foundation Guidance: AXELOS (official ITIL body) - https://www.axelos.com/
Service Desk Institute: https://www.servicedeskinstitute.com/
Question: 321 CertyIQ
What is used as a tool to help define and measure performance?
A.A change schedule
B.An incident record
C.A continual improvement register
D.A service level agreement
Answer: D
Explanation:
The correct answer is D, a Service Level Agreement (SLA). SLAs are formally negotiated agreements between

a service provider and a customer that define specific services, service targets, and responsibilities. Their
primary function is to establish clear expectations regarding the level of service to be delivered and how its
performance will be measured.
SLAs explicitly outline metrics such as availability, response times, resolution times, and other key
performance indicators (KPIs). These metrics are essential for measuring the success of a service and
ensuring it meets the customer's needs. The agreement also specifies the consequences of failing to meet
these targets, which often include penalties or credits. By clearly defining these performance standards,
SLAs provide a tangible framework for monitoring, evaluating, and managing service performance. They
ensure both the service provider and the customer have a shared understanding and a measurable way to
track success.
A change schedule (A) is used for planning and managing changes to IT services, not directly measuring
performance. An incident record (B) documents individual incidents and their resolution, providing data for
analysis but not a comprehensive performance measurement tool. A continual improvement register (C)
tracks improvement opportunities, but it doesn't define the baseline performance to be measured. Only the
SLA sets the predefined and agreed-upon metrics and targets necessary for performance measurement.
For further research, refer to the ITIL 4 Foundation handbook or explore resources on AXELOS's official
website: https://www.axelos.com/ and search for information about Service Level Agreements in IT service
management. Also, search for "ITIL 4 service level agreement" in reputable search engines.
Question: 322 CertyIQ
Which of the four dimensions contributes is concerned with service integration and management?
A.Partners and suppliers
B.Organizations and people
C.Value streams and processes
D.Information and technology
Answer: A
Explanation:
The correct answer, focusing on service integration and management within the four dimensions of ITIL 4, is
A. Partners and suppliers. This dimension encompasses the relationships an organization has with external
entities that contribute to the delivery of services. Effective service integration often relies on seamlessly
incorporating services and components provided by various partners and suppliers.
Partners and suppliers are critical for sourcing resources, capabilities, and specialized expertise needed for
service provision. This dimension addresses how to manage these relationships effectively to ensure value co-
creation. Integration and management activities include contract management, performance monitoring, and
ensuring alignment with organizational goals. For example, if a cloud provider relies on a CDN for content
delivery, the relationship with that CDN becomes part of its service provision model and needs integration.
Without proper management of partners and suppliers, service quality, availability, and overall value can be
negatively impacted. ITIL 4 emphasizes the importance of considering the entire ecosystem involved in
service delivery, not just internal resources.
While the other dimensions also contribute, they are not as directly concerned with service integration and
management from an external perspective. Organizations and people (B) focuses on internal structures and
skills. Value streams and processes (C) describe how activities are organized to create value. Information and
technology (D) addresses the tools and data used in service delivery. Although all are important to the overall

picture, the active integration and management of services obtained from external entities are the primary
focus of the 'Partners and Suppliers' dimension.For further research, consider the following links:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Guidance: (Check the latest official guidance for the most up-to-date information
on ITIL 4)
ITIL 4 Foundation Study Guides: Many reputable sources (e.g., on Pluralsight or Udemy) provide detailed
explanations of the four dimensions.
Question: 323 CertyIQ
What may form part of a service request procedure?
A.The timescale for restoration of service
B.The method of diagnosing the cause
C.Authorization in accordance with a security policy
D.Escalation to the appropriate change authority
Answer: C
Explanation:
The correct answer is C, Authorization in accordance with a security policy. Service request procedures
outline the steps to fulfill a service request. Security authorization is a crucial part of ensuring that only
authorized individuals can request and receive specific services, thus protecting sensitive data and systems.
This authorization step verifies the requester's right to access the service based on pre-defined security
policies.
Option A, The timescale for restoration of service, is typically more relevant to incident management. Incident
management focuses on restoring normal service operation as quickly as possible after a disruption. Option B,
The method of diagnosing the cause, is applicable to problem management where the root cause of incidents
is investigated and resolved. Option D, Escalation to the appropriate change authority, belongs to change
management. Change management focuses on managing changes effectively to minimize risk. While a service
request could trigger a change request, the escalation itself is not inherently part of the standard service
request procedure.
Service request procedures are streamlined, pre-approved processes for fulfilling common, low-risk requests.
They are designed to be efficient and minimize disruption to operations. Authorization steps ensure adherence
to security standards and prevent unauthorized access or misuse of resources. For further reading on service
request management, consult official ITIL 4 guidance and documentation.
Question: 324 CertyIQ
When applying the 'collaborate and promote visibility' principle to an organization's initiative, which is NOT a
necessary action?
A.Basing decisions about the initiative on visible data
B.Communicating information about the initiative to other parts of the organization
C.Ensuring everyone involved in the initiative is in agreement about it before starting
D.Considering different methods of communication for the different audiences
Answer: C

Explanation:
The question asks which action is NOT necessary when applying the 'collaborate and promote visibility'
guiding principle to an organizational initiative. The correct answer is C: Ensuring everyone involved in the
initiative is in agreement about it before starting.
Let's break down why. The 'collaborate and promote visibility' principle emphasizes the importance of working
together and ensuring information is accessible and transparent. Option A, basing decisions on visible data,
directly aligns with visibility, fostering informed decision-making based on shared understanding. Option B,
communicating information about the initiative to other parts of the organization, ensures transparency and
allows for feedback and collaboration across different teams. Option D, considering different methods of
communication for different audiences, acknowledges the importance of tailoring information for effective
understanding and engagement, thereby supporting both collaboration and visibility.
However, requiring complete agreement from everyone before starting an initiative is impractical and often
counterproductive. While collaboration aims to gather diverse perspectives and build consensus, striving for
unanimous agreement can lead to analysis paralysis and prevent progress. Initiatives often require
compromise and the acceptance of different viewpoints, not necessarily full agreement. The 'collaborate and
promote visibility' principle emphasizes inclusive participation and transparent communication, not
necessarily unanimous consent before action. In fact, striving for total agreement can stifle innovation and
prevent necessary changes. Consider a large IT transformation project; expecting everyone to be in lockstep
agreement before even starting is unrealistic given the complexity and breadth of impact.
Therefore, while fostering collaboration and visibility are critical, expecting universal agreement before
starting an initiative is not a core requirement and can be detrimental to progress.
Further reading:
ITIL 4 Foundation: ITIL Guiding Principles: Search online for resources explaining ITIL 4's guiding principles
in detail.
AXELOS: AXELOS is the owner of ITIL. Their website often contains resources on ITIL 4, though some require
paid subscriptions.
Question: 325 CertyIQ
Which practice identifies changes of state related to infrastructure, services, and business processes?
A.Monitoring and event management
B.Service configuration management
C.Change enablement
D.Information security management
Answer: A
Explanation:
The correct answer is A: Monitoring and event management. This practice is specifically designed to observe
and track the status of IT infrastructure, services, and business processes, registering changes of state as
events. These events can indicate normal operation, potential problems, or actual incidents. Monitoring and
event management tools are configured to detect these state changes, triggering alerts when predefined
thresholds are breached or specific events occur. This allows IT teams to proactively identify and respond to
issues, preventing disruptions or minimizing their impact.

Service Configuration Management (B) focuses on maintaining information about configuration items (CIs)
required to deliver IT services, their relationships, and their history, but it doesn't actively monitor state
changes in real-time. Change Enablement (C) is about managing changes to minimize risks and disruptions,
but it doesn't itself monitor the state of systems. Information security management (D) protects information
assets and is not directly responsible for actively monitoring all state changes related to infrastructure and
services. Monitoring provides real-time awareness, making it the primary practice responsible for identifying
state transitions. It's the "eyes and ears" of the IT
environment.https://www.axelos.com/https://www.bmc.com/blogs/itil-monitoring-event-management/
Question: 326 CertyIQ
Identity the missing word(s) in the following sentence.
When an organization is assessing its current state, it should use [?] to obtain accurate measurements.
A.Reports
B.Assumptions
C.Source data
D.Risk management techniques
Answer: C
Explanation:
The correct answer is C. Source data is the most appropriate choice because it directly refers to the original,
untampered information needed for an accurate assessment of the current state. Source data offers objective
evidence rather than subjective opinions or analyses.
Here's why the other options are less suitable:
A. Reports: While reports provide summaries and interpretations, they are derived from source data. Relying
solely on reports introduces the risk of bias, errors, or outdated information. The assessment should use the
original data before it is processed into reports.
B. Assumptions: Basing an assessment on assumptions undermines its validity. Assumptions are untested
beliefs and can lead to inaccurate conclusions.
D. Risk management techniques: Risk management techniques are useful in planning for potential issues but
do not provide the fundamental data needed to understand the current state.
For an organization to accurately assess its present condition, it needs to gather raw, unaltered data. This
"source data" might include metrics on incident volumes, server utilization rates, customer satisfaction
scores, or the number of successful deployments. This data forms the bedrock of a reliable evaluation,
allowing for identification of trends, strengths, and weaknesses. Accurate measurement using source data
allows organizations to make fact-based decisions and implement improvements effectively. This approach
helps them avoid decisions rooted in conjecture or incomplete information, which could lead to misallocation
of resources and ineffectual strategies.
Think of source data as the foundation of the assessment process. It ensures integrity and objectivity, leading
to a more realistic and useful understanding of the organization's current position. This data is vital for
informed strategic planning, performance management, and continuous improvement initiatives.
Further reading:
ITIL 4 Foundation guidance - various resources available online and in books.
ISO/IEC 20000 (Service Management) - outlines best practices that often involve precise assessments using
accurate data.

Question: 327 CertyIQ
How should a process design allow for exceptional situations?
A.Create rules to handle exceptions generally
B.Remove the option for process exceptions
C.Create an additional process for each exception
D.Include all exception steps in the main process
Answer: A
Explanation:
The correct answer is A: "Create rules to handle exceptions generally."
Here's a detailed justification:
ITIL 4 emphasizes flexibility and adaptability in service management. Processes are not rigid blueprints, but
rather frameworks that should accommodate real-world variations. Exceptional situations are inevitable in
any service, and ignoring them would lead to process breakdowns and customer dissatisfaction.
Option A aligns with this philosophy by advocating for the creation of rules. These rules represent pre-defined
logic to handle common deviations from the standard process flow. This is far more efficient and practical
than other options.
Option B, removing exceptions, is unrealistic. Services operate in dynamic environments and eliminating all
variations is impossible, and frankly, counterproductive.
Option C, creating separate processes for each exception, results in process proliferation and becomes
exceedingly difficult to manage. It negates the purpose of having standardized processes in the first place.
Imagine a cloud provider having a unique instance provisioning process for every different customer
requirement – it would become chaotic.
Option D, including all exception steps in the main process, bloats the process and makes it overly complex
and difficult to follow for normal situations. It significantly impacts operational efficiency and clarity.
ITIL's approach supports a more adaptable and manageable system. By anticipating common exceptions and
building rules to handle them, organizations can maintain process efficiency while still addressing unforeseen
situations effectively. The general rules allow for flexibility in applying to similar, but not identical,
exceptions. This prevents service disruptions and fosters a proactive approach to service management. This is
a key aspect of maintaining service quality and customer satisfaction, especially in cloud computing
environments where agility and rapid response are crucial. A generalized, exception-handling mechanism is
essential for maintaining service stability and responsiveness in a complex cloud service.
Further research on ITIL 4 processes and exception management:
AXELOS Official ITIL 4 Guidance: https://www.axelos.com/ (Look for official documentation related to
process design and exceptions)
ITIL Foundation Handbook: Many reputable ITIL training providers offer handbooks that elaborate on these
concepts. Searching for "ITIL 4 Foundation Handbook" will yield several options.
Question: 328 CertyIQ

Which practice needs the right culture to be embedded across the entire organization?
A.Service request management
B.Service level management
C.Change enablement
D.Continual improvement
Answer: D
Explanation:
The correct answer is D, Continual Improvement. Continual improvement necessitates a pervasive culture of
learning, reflection, and proactive action across all levels and departments of an organization. It's not simply a
process implemented by a specific team; instead, it's a mindset that encourages everyone to identify and
implement improvements in their daily work. Without this embedded culture, improvement efforts will be
isolated and ineffective, failing to achieve sustainable benefits.
Service request management (A) focuses on fulfilling user requests efficiently, while service level
management (B) concentrates on defining and meeting service performance targets. Change enablement (C)
manages changes to IT infrastructure and services. While all these practices benefit from a positive
organizational culture, they don't require a fundamental cultural shift across the entire organization to
function effectively in the same way as continual improvement. Continual Improvement is the practice that is
wholly dependent on the organisation's adoption of a learning and iterative ethos.
A robust continual improvement program necessitates open communication, collaboration, and a willingness
to experiment and learn from failures. It requires empowering employees to identify improvement
opportunities and providing them with the resources and support to implement changes. This cultural shift
takes time and effort, but it ultimately leads to a more agile, innovative, and customer-centric organization. In
short, a culture is a prerequisite, not merely an asset to this process. Without it, the other ITIL practices will be
unable to feed into a holistic method of developing the organisation's efficacy.See here for a better
description of continual improvement: https://www.axelos.com/news/blogs/november-2019/itil-4-continual-
improvementSee here for a more general description of ITIL4: https://www.bmc.com/blogs/itil-4-practices/
Question: 329 CertyIQ
Which term could be used to refer to a single person who has independently subscribed to a service?
A.Supplier
B.Service desk
C.Service provider
D.Organization
Answer: D
Explanation:
Here's a detailed justification for why "Organization" is the best answer:
The question asks which term describes a single person independently subscribing to a service.
Understanding the key ITIL 4 definitions is crucial here.
Organization: In ITIL 4, an organization is defined as a person or a group of people that has its own functions
with responsibilities, authority, and relationships to achieve its objectives. A single person subscribing to a
service fits this description; they are acting as an entity with the intent of fulfilling their needs. In this context,

the person becomes an organization of one. The definition aligns with a customer perspective.
Supplier: A supplier is a third party that provides goods or services that are incorporated into an
organization's own services. An individual subscribing to a service is not a supplier; they are a consumer.
Service Desk: The service desk is a function dedicated to providing support to service users. This term is
irrelevant to a single individual subscribing to a service.
Service Provider: A service provider delivers services. The individual subscribing is receiving the service, not
providing it.
Therefore, although seemingly counter-intuitive to think of a single person as an "organization", within the
framework of ITIL 4 and its conceptualization of entities engaging with services, this is the closest and most
accurate fit among the choices provided. The person represents a self-contained unit with needs and the
intent to satisfy them through a service.
For further clarification on ITIL 4 definitions, refer to the official AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation guidance:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation: https://www.axelos.com/
Question: 330 CertyIQ
What is the MOST LIKELY reason that incident management would need a temporary team to work together?
A.To escalate an incident to a supplier or partner
B.So customers and users are provided with timely updates
C.To resolve a complex or major incident
D.So users can resolve their own incidents with self-help
Answer: C
Explanation:
The most likely reason Incident Management requires a temporary team is to address complex or major
incidents. Here's why:
Incident Management focuses on restoring normal service operation as quickly as possible with minimal
disruption to the business. Complex or major incidents, by their very nature, represent significant disruptions
that often require specialized knowledge and coordinated effort beyond the capacity of the standard Incident
Management team.
Option A is less likely because escalating to a supplier usually follows defined procedures and doesn't
necessarily require a full temporary team within the organization. While involving the supplier is crucial,
internal coordination and communication are paramount.
Option B, providing timely updates, is a crucial aspect of Incident Management but not a primary driver for
forming a dedicated, temporary team. Communication roles would likely be integrated into the incident
response structure but would not necessitate a whole team formation independently.
Option D, enabling self-help, focuses on proactive knowledge provision and empowers users to resolve
common issues, but isn't directly linked to resolving escalated incidents.
A major incident, due to its scale and impact, demands the attention of specialists from various departments
(e.g., networking, servers, databases, applications) who need to collaborate effectively. A temporary team
allows for focused problem-solving, dedicated resources, and efficient communication channels to rapidly
diagnose, troubleshoot, and resolve the incident. This ensures a coordinated and streamlined approach,

minimizing the impact on business operations. The team may consist of incident managers, technical experts,
communication specialists, and even business stakeholders depending on the severity and scope. This
specialized team structure enables a faster and more effective return to normal service compared to a single
incident manager attempting to manage a complex, widespread outage. The formation of the temporary team
reflects the urgent need to resolve the incident effectively and return operations to normal quickly.
Further information can be found on these sites:
Axelos ITIL 4 Foundation Guidance: https://www.axelos.com/ (Purchase Required)
ITIL Foundation Handbook: (Various publishers, search online for "ITIL Foundation Handbook PDF")
Question: 331 CertyIQ
Which is MOST LIKELY to be achieved by following a detailed procedure?
A.Assessing a change
B.Resolving an incident
C.Managing a service request
D.Investigating a problem
Answer: C
Explanation:
The correct answer is C. Managing a service request. Here's why:
Service requests are standardized, low-risk, and often involve fulfilling pre-approved actions. They are best
managed through well-defined, repeatable procedures. A detailed procedure ensures consistency, efficiency,
and predictable outcomes when handling common requests like password resets, software installations, or
access permissions.
Option A, Assessing a change, while benefiting from structure, involves more evaluation and judgment than a
service request. Change assessments consider impact, risk, and resource availability, requiring more flexibility
than a fixed procedure allows.
Option B, Resolving an incident, often involves troubleshooting and investigation to identify the root cause.
While some common incidents may have documented steps, the variety and complexity of incidents
necessitate adaptability and problem-solving skills beyond a rigid procedure.
Option D, Investigating a problem, is a complex process that aims to determine the underlying cause of one or
more incidents. It involves data analysis, hypothesis testing, and potentially experimentation. A detailed
procedure wouldn't be effective for such an exploratory and unpredictable activity.
A detailed procedure excels in managing repetitive, well-understood tasks with predictable outcomes,
aligning perfectly with the nature of service requests. The other options require more adaptability and critical
thinking than a rigidly defined procedure can accommodate.
Supporting Resources:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Study Guide: (Purchase Required) Provides comprehensive information on ITIL 4
concepts, including service request management.
ITIL Official Website: (Search for Service Request Management) Offers resources and information on ITIL
best practices.

Question: 332 CertyIQ
Which of the four dimensions focuses on roles, responsibilities, and systems of authority?
A.Value streams and processes
B.Partners and suppliers
C.Organizations and people
D.Information and technology
Answer: C
Explanation:
The correct answer is C, Organizations and people. This dimension focuses on how the service provider is
structured and managed, including roles, responsibilities, and systems of authority, communication,
collaboration, and the skills and competencies of personnel. It addresses organizational structure, culture,
leadership styles, and workforce management. It includes defining roles and responsibilities, creating clear
lines of reporting, and establishing decision-making processes.
Value streams and processes (A) focuses on how the organization delivers value to the customer, not
necessarily on the internal structure. It outlines the activities, workflows, controls, and procedures needed to
achieve agreed-upon objectives.
Partners and suppliers (B) concentrates on the relationships the organization has with external entities
involved in the design, development, deployment, delivery, support, and continual improvement of services.
Information and technology (D) covers the information and knowledge needed to manage services, as well as
the technologies that support those services. While roles interact with technology, the core focus of this
dimension is on the technology itself, data, information management, and architectures.
Therefore, only the "Organizations and people" dimension explicitly encompasses the aspects of roles,
responsibilities, systems of authority, organizational structure, and workforce management mentioned in the
question.
Further resources:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Handbook
Official ITIL 4 Foundation Examination Study Guide
Question: 333 CertyIQ
What is CORRECT about service request management?
A.Service requests can be used to restore service
B.Complex service request procedures should be avoided
C.Compliments can be handled as service requests
D.A new procedure is required for each new service request
Answer: C
Explanation:
The correct answer is C: Compliments can be handled as service requests. Here's why:
Service request management focuses on fulfilling predefined and standardized requests from users. These
requests are typically low-risk, frequently asked, and well-understood. While not always the primary focus,

capturing user compliments and feedback can absolutely be integrated into a service request management
system. This allows for the systematic collection and analysis of positive feedback, which can then be used to
improve service quality, identify areas of strength, and motivate service staff. A service request form could
include an option for "Providing Compliment/Positive Feedback."
Option A is incorrect because service requests are generally not used to restore service. Restoring service is
the domain of incident management. Incidents are unplanned interruptions or reductions in the quality of an IT
service, and they require a different process for resolution, often involving more urgency and technical
expertise.
Option B is misleading. While overly complex procedures should always be avoided in any process, including
service request management, some service requests might require more detailed procedures due to the
nature of the request (e.g., requesting access to sensitive data might necessitate multiple approvals). The aim
is to streamline, not eliminate necessary controls.
Option D is also incorrect. A core principle of service request management is the standardization of processes.
Creating a new procedure for each new service request would defeat the purpose of standardization and lead
to inefficiency. Instead, service requests are categorized, and pre-defined procedures are applied based on
the category.
Therefore, capturing and handling compliments within the structured framework of service request
management allows organizations to systematically gather valuable positive feedback, complementing the
typical focus on resolving issues and fulfilling standard needs.
Further reading on ITIL 4 service request management can be found here:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Guidance: This provides the official definition and explanation of service request
management within the ITIL 4 framework. Note: Access typically requires purchase or subscription.
Various IT service management blogs and articles: Search for "ITIL 4 service request management" on
reputable IT service management websites and blogs for practical examples and implementations.
Question: 334 CertyIQ
What ensures that service providers and service consumers continue to create value together?
A.Service consumption
B.Service offerings
C.Service level management
D.Service relationship management
Answer: D
Explanation:
The correct answer is D, Service Relationship Management (SRM). SRM is the practice of establishing and
nurturing mutually beneficial relationships between service providers and service consumers. It focuses on
ensuring that both parties understand each other's needs, expectations, and contributions throughout the
service lifecycle. This ongoing dialogue and collaboration are crucial for sustained value creation.
SRM encompasses activities like understanding customer requirements, managing expectations, providing
proactive communication, and addressing concerns. It also involves monitoring customer satisfaction and
identifying opportunities for service improvement and innovation. By actively managing the relationship,
service providers can better align their services with the evolving needs of their customers.
Service consumption (A) is merely the act of utilizing a service, not the ongoing management of the

relationship. Service offerings (B) are packages of services designed to address specific customer needs, but
they don't guarantee a continuous, value-driven relationship. Service Level Management (C) focuses on
defining, agreeing on, and monitoring service levels, which are an important aspect of a service offering, but it
doesn't encompass the broader aspects of understanding customer business needs and fostering a
collaborative relationship. While SLM contributes to customer satisfaction, it is SRM that ensures the ongoing
creation of value by fostering a strong, collaborative, and evolving partnership. Therefore, SRM provides a
holistic approach that ensures both service providers and consumers benefit continuously, leading to a
sustained, mutually beneficial relationship.Authoritative Links:
AXELOS - ITIL 4 Foundation Guidance: https://www.axelos.com/ (Official source - search for relevant topics)
BMC - ITIL 4: https://www.bmc.com/blogs/itil-4-guide/ (Provides a comprehensive overview of ITIL 4)
Question: 335 CertyIQ
What are the KEY stakeholder groups that service providers should cooperate with?
A.Suppliers
B.Customers
C.Relationship managers
D.Developers
Answer: B
Explanation:
The most important stakeholder group for service providers to cooperate with is customers. While suppliers,
relationship managers, and developers are important, direct engagement with customers is paramount for
service delivery success. ITIL 4 emphasizes value co-creation, which means the service provider and customer
actively work together to achieve desired outcomes. Understanding customer needs, expectations, and
feedback is crucial for designing, delivering, and improving services that meet those needs. Without close
cooperation with customers, the service provider risks delivering services that are irrelevant, ineffective, or
poorly aligned with business objectives.
Customer cooperation enables service providers to:
Gain insights into evolving business requirements and priorities.
Proactively identify and address service gaps.
Solicit feedback for continuous service improvement.
Manage customer expectations effectively.
Build strong, long-term relationships based on trust and mutual benefit.
Suppliers are important for providing resources, relationship managers facilitate interactions, and developers
build the solutions. However, the customer ultimately determines the value and success of the service.
Therefore, prioritizing customer cooperation is fundamental to ITIL 4 principles. Relationship managers act as
crucial intermediaries in facilitating this customer-service provider interaction, but the customer is still the
focus. Successful collaboration between service provider and customer ensures that the delivered IT services
are valuable and aligned to business needs. ITIL 4 shifts the focus to value-driven services rather than simply
following prescribed processes, with the customer central to this value.
