Question: 336 CertyIQ
Which statement about the purpose of the Monitoring and event management practice is TRUE?
A.Minimize the negative impact of incidents by restoring normal service operation as quickly as possible
B.Support the agreed quality of a service by handling all pre-defined, user-initiated service requests in an
effective and user-friendly manner
C.Systematically observe services and service components, and record and report selected changes of state
identified as events
D.Maximize the number of successful service and product changes by ensuring that risks have been properly
assessed, authorized and managed within a schedule
Answer: C
Explanation:
The correct answer is C. Systematically observe services and service components, and record and report
selected changes of state identified as events.
Here's why:
The ITIL 4 Monitoring and Event Management practice focuses specifically on proactively watching services
and infrastructure to detect issues or deviations from normal operation. Its primary purpose is to identify,
analyze, and report on events that occur within the IT environment. By constantly observing the environment
and detecting anomalies, it enables timely intervention and prevents potential disruptions. These events can
signify issues, potential failures, or even opportunities for optimization. The systematic observation helps
ensure the stability and performance of IT services.
Option A describes the purpose of Incident Management.Option B describes the purpose of Service Request
Management.Option D describes the purpose of Change Enablement.
Further resources to explore this topic include:
Axelos ITIL 4 Foundation Study Material: This is the official source for ITIL 4 information.

Question: 337 CertyIQ
Identify the missing word(s) in the following sentence.
The purpose of the problem management practice is to reduce the likelihood and impact of incidents by identifying
actual and potential causes of incidents and managing [?] and known errors.
A.events
B.changes
C.configuration items
D.workarounds
Answer: D
Explanation:
The correct answer is D. workarounds.

The purpose of the problem management practice within ITIL 4 is to proactively prevent incidents and
minimize their negative effects. It achieves this by systematically identifying the underlying causes of
incidents (problems) and by managing both problems themselves and the known errors associated with them.
A known error is a problem that has been diagnosed and for which a temporary solution, or workaround, has
been identified.
Problem management focuses on long-term solutions. When the root cause of an incident is found, a fix can
be applied. However, until that fix is implemented, a workaround is used to reduce or eliminate the impact of
the incident. Managing these workarounds is crucial because they represent temporary solutions that can be
implemented quickly, allowing users to continue working while a more permanent fix is developed and
deployed through change management processes.
Events, changes, and configuration items are important considerations in ITIL, but they do not directly address
the immediate need to mitigate the impact of a known error the way a workaround does. Event management
deals with detecting and responding to significant occurrences. Change management focuses on controlling
changes to the IT environment. Configuration management tracks and manages IT assets. While these
practices often interact with problem management, workarounds are specifically tied to addressing known
errors while a permanent solution is sought.
Therefore, workarounds fill the gap between identifying a known error and implementing a permanent fix.
Problem management actively manages these temporary solutions to minimize the disruption caused by
incidents.
Further research on ITIL 4 problem management and known errors can be found at these authoritative
sources:
AXELOS Official Website: This is the governing body for ITIL, and its website provides comprehensive
information, resources, and training on the ITIL framework. While specific URLs may change, searching for
"ITIL 4 Problem Management" on their site is a good starting point.
ITIL 4 Foundation Handbook: This book provides a detailed overview of the ITIL 4 framework, including the
purpose and activities of the problem management practice.
Question: 338 CertyIQ
Which describes an unresolved problem which has been already analysed?
A.A workaround
B.An incident
C.A known error
D.A risk
Answer: C
Explanation:
The correct answer is C, a Known Error. Here's why:
A known error is the status assigned to a problem that has been analyzed but not yet resolved. This means the
root cause of the problem has been identified and documented, even though a permanent solution is not yet
implemented. The focus shifts to managing the known error and its impact until a resolution becomes
available.
Let's examine why the other options are incorrect:
A. A workaround: A workaround is a temporary solution to reduce or eliminate the impact of an incident or

problem. It does not represent a fully analyzed issue. It's a method to bypass the problem, not to resolve it.
B. An incident: An incident is an unplanned interruption to a service or a reduction in the quality of a service.
It's a discrete event, not a problem that has undergone root cause analysis. Incidents can lead to problem
management and the identification of known errors.
D. A risk: A risk is a potential event that could cause harm or loss, or make it more difficult to achieve
objectives. While problems can introduce risks, a problem that's already been analyzed is no longer just a
potential issue; it's a realized issue captured as a known error.
The key aspect that differentiates a known error is the analysis that has already been performed. The problem
management process investigates incidents to identify underlying problems. When the root cause is
understood but a solution is not yet available, the problem becomes a known error. This allows service
providers to proactively manage the situation, inform users, and potentially implement workarounds until a
permanent fix can be deployed. By documenting the known error, valuable information is preserved for future
incidents and problem resolution efforts.
Further research can be found on the following websites:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation materials (official source).
https://www.bmc.com/blogs/known-error-database/
https://www.atlassian.com/itsm/incident-management/known-error
Question: 339 CertyIQ
Which practice conducts reviews to validate that services are covering the needs of the customer?
A.Monitoring and event management
B.Service level management
C.Change enablement
D.Service desk
Answer: B
Explanation:
The correct answer is indeed B, Service Level Management.
Service Level Management (SLM) is the practice responsible for setting clear expectations for service
performance and ensuring that services are delivered to meet agreed-upon levels. A core component of SLM
is conducting regular reviews of Service Level Agreements (SLAs) and Operational Level Agreements (OLAs).
These reviews are specifically designed to validate that services are not only performing technically as
expected but also actively covering the actual needs of the customer.
This includes evaluating customer satisfaction with the service, analyzing service performance against
defined metrics, and identifying areas for improvement. These reviews assess whether the agreed-upon
service levels still align with the customer's business requirements. If the reviews reveal a mismatch, the
SLAs need to be adjusted to better reflect the customer's evolving needs.
Monitoring and event management (A) focuses on detecting deviations from normal operation but doesn’t
inherently ensure customer needs are met. Change enablement (C) manages changes to services but doesn't
have the core function of verifying customer satisfaction. The service desk (D) handles incidents and service
requests but does not specifically conduct reviews to validate service coverage of customer needs from a
strategic, agreement-driven perspective. The validation of the SLAs based on customer needs is a key
element of SLM.

Therefore, only Service Level Management directly incorporates reviews to validate that services continue to
address customer needs.
Authoritative links:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Study Guide
https://www.axelos.com/ (Official AXELOS website)
Question: 340 CertyIQ
What is MOST LIKELY to be handled as a service request?
A.Managing an interruption to a service
B.An emergency change to apply a security patch
C.The implementation of a workaround
D.Providing a virtual server for a development team
Answer: D
Explanation:
Here's a detailed justification for why option D is the most likely to be handled as a service request in an ITIL 4
context, along with supporting concepts and authoritative links:
Service requests are standard, low-risk changes or requests for information. They are pre-approved and don't
necessarily represent a break or deviation from normal service operation. Options A, B, and C all involve some
form of disruption or deviation from the norm.
Option A (Managing an interruption to a service): An interruption represents an incident. Incidents are
managed through incident management practices, which aim to restore normal service operation as quickly as
possible.
Option B (An emergency change to apply a security patch): Emergency changes fall under change
management (or change enablement in ITIL 4) practices, specifically expedited procedures. These are not
typical service requests due to the urgency and potential impact.
Option C (The implementation of a workaround): A workaround is a temporary solution to reduce or eliminate
the impact of an incident or problem. This is associated with incident or problem management.
Option D (Providing a virtual server for a development team): Requesting a virtual server is often a standard,
predefined service offering. The process is typically automated or semi-automated, with pre-approved
configurations and service level agreements. The request is fulfilled through established workflows, without
causing any disruption to existing services. It's something development teams routinely need and has likely
been established in the service catalog.
Therefore, providing a virtual server aligns perfectly with the characteristics of a service request in ITIL 4
because the action does not involve a disruption to service. It is a standard, low-risk, pre-approved request
that ITIL 4 suggests should be requested via a service request.
Authoritative Links:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Guidance: This is the primary source for ITIL 4 principles and practices. (You
would typically access this through official training or publications)
Service Request Management: https://www.bmc.com/blogs/itil-service-request-management/ (A
vendor'provided overview of service request management. While vendor-specific, it explains the concept.)
ITIL Incident Management: https://www.atlassian.com/itsm/incident-management (Details on incident
management).

Question: 341 CertyIQ
Which practice guarantees that users have a range of access channels to choose from to report problems?
A.Service desk
B.Service level management
C.Incident management
D.Change enablement
Answer: A
Explanation:
The correct answer is A, Service Desk.
A Service Desk is designed to be the single point of contact between the service provider and the users. Its
core function is to provide support and address user inquiries, incidents, and service requests. To effectively
fulfill this purpose, a well-designed Service Desk offers various communication channels, guaranteeing users
have multiple ways to report issues. These channels can include phone, email, self-service portals, chat, and
even social media, ensuring accessibility and convenience based on user preference and urgency. The
existence of multiple channels is critical for efficient incident reporting and resolution.
Incident Management, while crucial for restoring service after an incident, focuses on the process of handling
incidents once they are reported, not on providing the reporting channels themselves. Service Level
Management defines the service targets and agreements but doesn't directly dictate how users report
problems. Change Enablement is related to managing changes to the IT environment in a controlled manner,
and therefore not directly related to providing access channels for users to report problems. Only Service
Desk is specifically designed and implemented to provide varied channels for users to reach support teams
and log incidents, making option A the most fitting.
For further reading on Service Desk and its functions, consult:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation guidance: https://www.axelos.com/ (Specifically, review the Service Management
practices, in particular, the Service Desk practice.)
HDI (Help Desk Institute): https://www.thinkhdi.com/
Question: 342 CertyIQ
A user wants to know how to create a report, so they come into contact with the service desk.
Which practice is MOST LIKELY to help with the solution of this issue?
A.Incident management
B.Service level management
C.Service request management
D.Change enablement
Answer: C
Explanation:
The correct answer is C, Service Request Management. Here's why:
Service Request Management is designed to handle routine requests from users, such as requests for

information, access, or standard changes. Asking "how to create a report" falls squarely within this category.
It's a common, well-defined need that the service desk should have a standard procedure for addressing. The
service desk agents can readily offer instructions, documentation, or point the user to the relevant training
materials or knowledge base articles concerning report creation. This is a proactive activity that enhances
user productivity.
Incident Management, on the other hand, focuses on restoring service after a disruption or failure. While a
user's inability to create a report might eventually lead to a problem, the initial request is for guidance, not a
resolution to a service outage.
Service Level Management (SLM) is concerned with defining, agreeing upon, and managing service levels, not
handling individual user requests. It ensures IT services meet defined business needs. SLM would be involved
in ensuring the reporting service itself is available and meeting performance targets, but not in guiding a user
on how to use it.
Change Enablement (formerly Change Management) focuses on controlling changes to the IT infrastructure.
While a significant change to the reporting system could prompt a need to update user guides, the user's
request here is simply about learning existing functionality.
In summary, helping a user create a report is a typical service request. The service desk utilizes established
procedures within service request management to address such queries promptly and efficiently, promoting
user satisfaction and productivity.
Authoritative links:
AXELOS - ITIL 4 Foundation: ITIL 4 Edition: No direct link as it's a copyrighted book, but widely available.
Service Request Management Definition: While ITIL's own direct documentation is behind a paywall, various
IT service management resources and training providers offer explanations of service request management
aligned with ITIL principles (search for "ITIL Service Request Management").
Question: 343 CertyIQ
How can service consumers contribute to risk mitigation?
A.Through the provision of services according to predefined needs
B.By ensuring that the service provider has configured correctly its resources
C.By being fully aware of their own requirements for the service
D.By controlling the specific level of risk on the service provider’s behalf
Answer: C
Explanation:
The correct answer is C: By being fully aware of their own requirements for the service. Here's a detailed
justification:
Risk mitigation in ITIL 4 involves identifying, assessing, and controlling risks. Service consumers play a vital
role in this process. Understanding and clearly articulating their requirements for a service is fundamental to
identifying potential risks associated with that service. When consumers clearly define their needs (e.g.,
security, performance, availability, compliance), the service provider can better assess the potential risks of
failing to meet those needs. This allows for proactive measures to be implemented to mitigate those risks
before they materialize into actual incidents or service disruptions.
Option A is incorrect because simply consuming services according to predefined needs doesn't inherently
contribute to risk mitigation. It describes a general aspect of service consumption, not risk management.

Option B is incorrect because it's the service provider's responsibility to configure resources correctly, not the
service consumer's. While consumers might provide feedback if they notice issues, it's not their primary role in
risk mitigation.
Option D is incorrect because the service consumer doesn't typically directly control the risk level on the
service provider's behalf. They contribute to risk assessment through articulating their needs, but the service
provider is ultimately responsible for managing and controlling the risk to their infrastructure and services.
Therefore, by providing a complete and accurate understanding of their needs, service consumers enable the
service provider to identify risks more effectively and implement appropriate mitigation strategies. This
contributes to a more robust and reliable service delivery. Clear requirements act as a baseline against which
the service provider can assess and manage risk.
Further research can be conducted on the ITIL 4 framework and its guidance on risk management within the
service value system.https://www.axelos.com/https://www.bmc.com/blogs/itil-risk-management/
Question: 344 CertyIQ
A good way to apply the ITIL guiding principle ‘focus on value’ is to:
A.Understand why services are used by service consumers
B.Understand the whole, but do something
C.Be aware of system complexity
D.Do less tasks but in a better way with higher quality
Answer: A
Explanation:
Here's a detailed justification for why option A is the most accurate answer to the question "A good way to
apply the ITIL guiding principle ‘focus on value’ is to:".
The ITIL 4 guiding principle of "Focus on Value" emphasizes that everything the organization does should
directly or indirectly contribute to value for its stakeholders. This means understanding who the stakeholders
are, what value means to them, and how each activity supports that value creation.
Option A, "Understand why services are used by service consumers," directly addresses this core concept. By
understanding the reasons service consumers use a service, you gain insight into the specific value they
derive from it. This understanding enables you to prioritize improvements, modifications, or even
decommissioning of services based on their contribution to the end-user's needs and desired outcomes. It
ensures that IT efforts are aligned with delivering demonstrable business value.
Options B, C, and D, while potentially beneficial in general service management practices, do not directly
focus on understanding and maximizing value for service consumers in the same way as Option A. Option B is
about a more holistic view (systems thinking), C is about addressing complexity and option D is about
optimizing tasks to perform better with higher quality. While these are all valid, they are not as central to the
"focus on value" principle as knowing why a service is actually being used in the first place.
Therefore, understanding the reasons behind service consumption allows for a more targeted and effective
approach to value creation, making option A the best representation of the "focus on value" principle.
Authoritative Links for Further Research:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Guidance: (Requires purchase/subscription but provides the most authoritative
definition of the guiding principles.)

ITIL Guiding Principles: https://www.bmc.com/blogs/itil-guiding-principles/ (BMC blog, but explains guiding
principles)
Question: 345 CertyIQ
Which of the following guiding principles proposes the elimination of unnecessary work?
A.Keep it simple and practical
B.Think and work holistically
C.Start where you are
D.Progress iteratively with feedback
Answer: A
Explanation:
The correct answer is A. Keep it simple and practical.
The "Keep it simple and practical" guiding principle emphasizes the importance of simplicity and avoiding
unnecessary complexity in processes, services, and workflows. A core tenet of this principle is to streamline
activities and eliminate any tasks or steps that do not directly contribute to value creation. This aims to reduce
waste, improve efficiency, and enhance the overall effectiveness of service management practices.
While the other principles are valuable, they don't directly address the elimination of unnecessary work:
Think and work holistically: Focuses on understanding the interconnectedness of different elements within a
system or organization.
Start where you are: Advises leveraging existing resources and knowledge instead of starting from scratch.
Progress iteratively with feedback: Promotes incremental improvements based on continuous feedback
loops.
The "Keep it simple and practical" principle is about stripping down processes to their essential components,
discarding redundancy, and focusing on delivering value with the least amount of effort. This aligns directly
with the concept of eliminating unnecessary work, as it encourages practitioners to challenge the status quo
and identify areas where processes can be simplified and streamlined. By focusing on what is truly necessary
and valuable, organizations can improve efficiency, reduce costs, and enhance the customer experience.
Further research can be conducted on the ITIL 4 guiding principles at these links:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Guiding Principles
BMC ITIL 4 Guiding Principles Explained
Question: 346 CertyIQ
Which of the following statements is included in the ‘improve’ value chain activity’s purpose?
A.Ensure the continual improvement of practices across all value chain activities
B.Ensure services continually meet expectations for quality, costs, and time to market
C.Ensure a shared understanding of the improvement direction for services across the organization
D.Ensure continual engagement and good relationships with all stakeholders
Answer: A

Explanation:
The correct answer is A. The 'Improve' value chain activity in ITIL 4 focuses on enhancing practices and
services. Its core purpose is to ensure the continual improvement of all practices across all value chain
activities. This aligns perfectly with the answer choice A. The 'Improve' activity seeks to identify opportunities
for betterment and implement changes to make processes, services, and ultimately, the value stream more
effective and efficient. This includes analyzing data, feedback, and trends to discover areas needing
enhancement. It emphasizes a proactive and iterative approach to improvement throughout the entire
organization and all its activities within the service value system.
While option B touches on service quality and meeting expectations, it is more closely tied to the 'Engage' and
'Deliver & Support' value chain activities, which are directly responsible for delivering services that meet
customer requirements. Option C, while relevant to improvement, is more aligned with governance and
strategic direction setting, rather than the immediate operational focus of the 'Improve' activity. Option D
emphasizes stakeholder relationship management, which is the primary concern of 'Engage'. 'Improve' is
about making things better, not just maintaining relationships or meeting immediate expectations. Continuous
improvement is the hallmark of the 'Improve' activity, making option A the most accurate choice.

Question: 347 CertyIQ
Which of the following statements about change authorization is CORRECT?
A.Every time a standard change is requested a change authority is assigned
B.The technician making an emergency change can authorize such changes
C.The change type and model is the basis for assigning the change authority
D.Ensuring that changes are authorized after their deployment is done by the change authority
Answer: C
Explanation:
Here's a detailed justification for why option C is the correct answer and why the other options are incorrect,
focusing on ITIL 4 Foundation principles:
Option C is the CORRECT answer: The change type and model is the basis for assigning the change
authority.
Explanation: ITIL 4 emphasizes a risk-based approach to change management. The change authority should
be appropriate for the type of change being implemented. Standard changes, normal changes, and
emergency changes all require different levels of authorization. The change model defines the steps for a
specific type of change, including who can authorize it. A change authority is determined by the change type
and the change model, ensuring appropriate governance based on potential risk and impact. A standard
change requires lower-level authorization than a Normal or Emergency change.
Why other options are incorrect:
A. Every time a standard change is requested a change authority is assigned: While standard changes have
an authorization process defined in the change model, the change model pre-authorizes the change. Thus, a

change authority may not be assigned every single time a standard change is requested, as they are pre-
approved.
B. The technician making an emergency change can authorize such changes: In most cases, the technician
may enact the change, but authorization requires a Change Authority with appropriate levels of responsibility
to assess risk and impacts. Although, sometimes, that technician may be the change authority, especially in
small organizations. This option is too generalized.
D. Ensuring that changes are authorized after their deployment is done by the change authority: Changes
must be authorized before deployment; otherwise, that poses a business risk. The Change Authority ensures
authorization before a change is deployed, not after. After deployment, the Change Authority may assess
post-implementation reviews and learnings.
In summary: Selecting the Change Authority based on the change type and the Change Model ensures
appropriate authorization for each change based on its risk and impact.
Authoritative Links for Further Research:
Axelos ITIL 4 Foundation Syllabus: https://www.axelos.com/ (Specifically, review Change Enablement in the
syllabus). While a direct link to a specific page isn't available, you can search for "Change Enablement" within
the ITIL 4 documentation.
Official ITIL 4 Publications: Access through Axelos or accredited training providers. (Search for "Change
Enablement" within the publications).
Question: 348 CertyIQ
Which statement about a ‘continual improvement register (CIR)’ is TRUE?
A.Used to help plan changes, assist in communication, avoid conflicts, and assign resources
B.Used to select the right method, model or technique for identifying improvements
C.Used to track and manage improvement ideas from identification through to final action
D.Used to provide a formal description of one or more services, designed to address the needs of a target
consumer group
Answer: C
Explanation:
The correct answer, C, directly aligns with the purpose and function of a Continual Improvement Register
(CIR) within the ITIL 4 framework. A CIR serves as a centralized repository for capturing and managing
improvement opportunities identified throughout the service lifecycle. Its primary function is to systematically
track improvement ideas from their initial suggestion, through analysis and prioritization, to their eventual
implementation and review. This ensures that no potential improvement is overlooked and that all efforts are
focused on delivering maximum value to the organization and its customers.
Option A is incorrect because it describes the purpose of a change schedule or change management system,
which focuses on planning, communication, conflict avoidance, and resource allocation for changes, not
specifically improvement ideas. Option B describes elements of improvement identification and prioritization,
but a CIR is not the tool used for selecting methods, models, or techniques. It’s the register where the results
of that selection, in the form of improvement ideas, are stored. Option D is incorrect as it describes a service
portfolio or catalog, which details the services offered to target consumer groups, not the mechanism for
managing continuous improvement.
The ITIL 4 framework emphasizes continual improvement as a key principle. The CIR supports this principle by
providing a structured approach to managing improvement opportunities. This allows organizations to
systematically identify, prioritize, and implement improvements to their services, processes, and overall

operations. By maintaining a centralized record of improvement ideas, the CIR facilitates collaboration,
transparency, and accountability in the improvement process. In essence, the CIR is the engine that drives
continual improvement within an ITIL 4-aligned organization. By meticulously tracking each improvement idea,
from its inception to its completion, the CIR ensures that the organization is constantly evolving and adapting
to meet the changing needs of its stakeholders.
Further research can be conducted on the AXELOS website, the official source of ITIL, or through reputable IT
service management resources that discuss ITIL 4's Continual Improvement Practice.
Question: 349 CertyIQ
Which of the following practices suggests that organizations should develop competencies in methodologies and
techniques, like SWOT (strength, weakness, opportunity and threat) analysis and balanced scorecard review, in
order to meet their needs?
A.incident management
B.Continual improvement
C.Service request management
D.Change enablement
Answer: B
Explanation:
The correct answer is B, Continual Improvement, because it directly emphasizes the ongoing effort to improve
products, services, and practices. It necessitates the adoption of various methodologies and techniques to
assess the current state, identify improvement opportunities, and measure progress. Methodologies like
SWOT analysis (Strengths, Weaknesses, Opportunities, Threats) and balanced scorecard review are key
components within a continual improvement approach. These tools help organizations understand their
internal and external environments and measure performance across different dimensions, guiding
improvement initiatives. Incident management focuses on restoring normal service operation as quickly as
possible, while service request management handles routine requests. Change enablement controls changes
to minimize risks. While these practices might benefit from improvement initiatives, they don't inherently drive
the need to develop competencies in methodologies like SWOT or balanced scorecard. Continual
improvement, on the other hand, explicitly requires understanding the current state and opportunities for
progress which is facilitated by these analytical techniques. Organizations that embrace a continual
improvement culture actively seek and leverage such methodologies to enhance their processes and
outcomes. Therefore, the suggestion to develop competencies in SWOT and balanced scorecard aligns most
closely with the goals and principles of Continual Improvement.
Further Reading:
ITIL 4 Foundation: ITIL® 4 Edition - AXELOS
ITIL 4 Continual Improvement - AXELOS Blog
The Practical Guide to ITIL 4 Continual Improvement - BMC Blogs
Question: 350 CertyIQ
Which of the following statements about 'outcomes' is TRUE?
A.The delivery of products to a stakeholder is enabled by outcomes
B.The level of expenses regarding a technology for a service is defined by an outcome

C.An outcome depends on at least one output to deliver a result
D.Outcomes provide assurance to stakeholders regarding the performance of a service
Answer: C
Explanation:
The correct answer is C: "An outcome depends on at least one output to deliver a result." Let's break down
why.
Outcomes in ITIL 4 represent the results a service consumer desires. They are about value. They're the
tangible or intangible benefits the consumer receives from the service.
Outputs are the tangible deliverables of a service. They are what the service provider provides to the
consumer.
Think of it this way: you want the outcome of a working, secure network (business value). The outputs might
be network devices configured correctly, security policies implemented, and performance monitoring tools
running (tangible results).
An outcome requires outputs. You can't achieve a desired result (the outcome) without something being
delivered (the output). The output is a necessary condition for achieving the outcome.
Option A is incorrect because outputs (not outcomes) enable the delivery of products to a stakeholder. Option
B is wrong because the level of expenses relates to resources, cost, and not the desired result of using a
service. Option D is not completely accurate. While outcomes contribute to assurance, assurance itself is a
broader concept encompassing reliability, security, and compliance.
Therefore, option C is the only statement that accurately reflects the relationship between outputs and
outcomes in the ITIL 4 framework. The outputs are instrumental in achieving the desired outcomes and
delivering value to the service consumer.
For further research on ITIL 4 concepts and their application, consider the following resources:
AXELOS Official Website: https://www.axelos.com/
ITIL Foundation Handbook
Question: 351 CertyIQ
A good way to apply the ITIL guiding principle 'keep it simple and practical' is to:
A.Communicate so that the audience will hear
B.Re-use nothing from the current state
C.Adopt a practice which is easy to follow
D.Understand that fast does not mean incomplete
Answer: C
Explanation:
The best way to apply the 'keep it simple and practical' ITIL 4 guiding principle is to adopt a practice which is
easy to follow (Option C). This principle emphasizes efficiency and effectiveness by focusing on doing what is
necessary and avoiding unnecessary complexity.
Option A, "Communicate so that the audience will hear," is valuable for effective communication, but it doesn't
directly address simplicity and practicality. Good communication can be complex if not streamlined. Option B,

"Re-use nothing from the current state," directly contradicts the principle. Re-using what works in the current
state promotes efficiency and avoids reinventing the wheel. A practical approach often involves building on
existing systems and processes. Option D, "Understand that fast does not mean incomplete," is a general
awareness of quality and completeness, but doesn't directly guide you towards simplicity. Completeness can
be achieved even with complex processes.
Adopting an easy-to-follow practice directly embodies simplicity. By ensuring a practice is straightforward
and readily understood, it reduces the risk of errors, minimizes training requirements, and enables faster
implementation. Simpler processes are often more practical because they require fewer resources and are
easier to maintain. It helps maintain focus and avoid unnecessary steps. For example, implementing a self-
service portal with a straightforward interface simplifies IT requests and aligns with this principle.
Further reading on ITIL 4 guiding principles can be found on Axelos' official website (axelos.com) and various
IT service management resources. A good starting point is the ITIL Foundation syllabus, which you can find by
searching for "ITIL 4 Foundation Syllabus" on Google. Look for PDF documents provided by Axelos partners or
training providers. The official Axelos website requires purchasing access to their materials.
Question: 352 CertyIQ
When considering the type of relationship required with other organizations involved in the design and delivery of
services, which dimension of service management are you utilizing?
A.Organizations and people
B.Information and technology
C.Partners and suppliers
D.Value streams and processes
Answer: C
Explanation:
The correct answer is C: Partners and suppliers.
The "Partners and Suppliers" dimension of service management directly addresses the relationships an
organization has with other entities that contribute to service design, development, delivery, support, and
continual improvement. This dimension focuses on how an organization integrates external resources and
capabilities into its service value system.
When considering the type of relationship required with other organizations, you are explicitly analyzing the
nature of your collaborations. This involves understanding which partners and suppliers are crucial to service
delivery. Elements like contracts, agreements, and shared responsibilities, all fall under this dimension. It also
includes supplier management, contract management and how external providers are integrated into the
value stream.
Options A, B, and D, while important dimensions, don't directly address the relationship aspect. Organizations
and People (A) concentrates on the internal organizational structure, skills, and culture. Information and
Technology (B) looks at the technology components and data management aspects. Value Streams and
Processes (D) considers the flow of activities and processes. Only "Partners and Suppliers" considers
relationships with external organizations.
Considering that the question specifically pertains to the relationships with other organizations involved, the
"Partners and Suppliers" dimension is the most relevant and accurate choice.

Question: 353 CertyIQ
Which service value chain activity relates with buying new products?
A.Engage
B.Obtain/build
C.Plan
D.Improve
Answer: B
Explanation:
The correct answer is Obtain/Build because this activity within the ITIL 4 service value chain specifically
focuses on the acquisition or creation of resources needed to deliver services. Buying new products directly
aligns with obtaining resources from external suppliers.
The Engage activity is concerned with managing relationships with stakeholders, including users, customers,
suppliers, and partners. While buying products might involve supplier interactions, the core function of
Engage isn't the procurement itself.
The Plan activity focuses on establishing direction, defining objectives, and determining strategies. While
planning might lead to a decision to purchase new products, the actual purchasing happens within
Obtain/Build.
The Improve activity focuses on continual improvement of services and practices. Purchasing new products
could be a result of an improvement initiative, but the actual transaction falls under Obtain/Build.
Obtain/Build encompasses activities such as sourcing components, manufacturing, and service creation.
Buying a new product is a direct example of obtaining a resource to support service delivery or improvement.
It involves procurement, vendor selection, and contract management, all of which fall squarely within the
scope of Obtain/Build. This activity ensures that the necessary components and services are acquired or
developed in a timely and cost-effective manner to meet the organization's needs. Thus, it directly aligns with
the action of buying new products.

Question: 354 CertyIQ
Which of the following is a necessity to a successful service level agreement (SLAs)?
A.The language and terms used in the SLA should be commonly understood by all parties
B.Base the SLA on system-based metrics that are useful to the service provider
C.In order to promote consistent service, they should be earned forward, unchanged, from one year to the next
D.Vague targets, such as those related to user experience, should be avoided
Answer: A

Explanation:
The correct answer is A: "The language and terms used in the SLA should be commonly understood by all
parties."
Here's a detailed justification:
A Service Level Agreement (SLA) is a crucial contract defining the level of service a provider will offer to a
customer. Its success hinges on clear communication and mutual understanding. If the language and terms
within the SLA are ambiguous or overly technical, misunderstandings will arise, leading to disputes and
dissatisfaction. An SLA's purpose is to set expectations and hold the provider accountable. This accountability
is impossible if the agreement is interpreted differently by the involved parties. All stakeholders must have a
shared understanding of the terms and conditions.Option B is incorrect because basing an SLA solely on
system-based metrics beneficial to the provider neglects the customer's perspective and actual service
experience. Customer-centric metrics are critical for overall satisfaction.Option C is incorrect because SLAs
need regular review and adjustments. Business needs, technology, and customer requirements evolve,
demanding flexibility in the SLA. Rigid adherence to unchanged SLAs can lead to obsolescence and
misalignment with current needs.Option D is incorrect because while vague targets are problematic,
completely avoiding user experience (UX) considerations is not the answer. SLAs should incorporate well-
defined, measurable metrics related to UX where possible, rather than ignoring the customer's experience.
User experience impacts business outcomes and should be considered.
Therefore, clear, understandable language for all parties is fundamental to an effective and successful
SLA.Further Research:
ITIL 4 Foundation Handbook
Axelos Official Website
Question: 355 CertyIQ
Identify the missing word(s) in the following sentence.
A(n) [?] is the cause, or potential cause, of one or more incidents.
A.Known error
B.Change
C.Event
D.Problem
Answer: D
Explanation:
The correct answer is D. Problem. Here's why:
A problem in ITIL 4 is defined as a cause, or potential cause, of one or more incidents. Incidents are unplanned
interruptions to an IT service, or reductions in the quality of an IT service. A problem aims to investigate the
root cause behind those incidents and prevent them from recurring. Problem management is about
identifying, analyzing, and managing the causes of incidents.
A known error (A) is a problem that has been analyzed and understood but hasn't yet been resolved. It's a
state of a problem, not the definition of what a problem is.
A change (B) is the addition, modification, or removal of anything that could affect IT services. While changes
can cause problems, they are not the definition of a problem itself. Changes are managed to minimize

disruptions and risks, but a problem exists independently of any specific change.
An event (C) is any occurrence that has significance for the management of IT services. Events can be normal
(e.g., successful login) or exceptional (e.g., server failure). While incidents are a type of event, problems are
the underlying causes that are investigated based on a pattern of events/incidents. Therefore, an event is not
the potential or actual cause of one or more incidents in the same way a problem is.
In summary, while changes can cause problems, and incidents are a symptom of them, the ITIL framework
specifically defines a problem as the root cause or potential root cause of one or more incidents. Problem
management processes focus on finding and addressing these underlying problems. This aligns directly with
the core purpose of the ITIL framework: to improve IT service management and prevent disruptions.
Supporting Links:
ITIL 4 Foundation: ITIL 4 Edition by AXELOS: (Refer to sections defining "Problem," "Incident," "Change," and
"Event")
AXELOS ITIL Website: https://www.axelos.com/ (Official source for ITIL information)
Question: 356 CertyIQ
Which term is used to describe removing something that could have an effect on a service?
A.A change
B.An incident
C.A problem
D.An IT asset
Answer: A
Explanation:
The correct answer is A. A change.
Justification:
In ITIL 4, a change is defined as the addition, modification, or removal of anything that could have a direct or
indirect effect on IT services. This broad definition encompasses far more than simply altering code or
configuration files. Removing a server, decommissioning a database, or even updating a software library can
all be considered changes.
The key principle here is potential impact. If removing something (hardware, software, configuration item, etc.)
could affect a service, then the action of removing it falls under the umbrella of change management. ITIL 4
emphasizes careful planning, risk assessment, and authorization for all changes to minimize disruptions and
maintain service stability. This is because unauthorized or poorly managed changes are a significant source of
incidents and service outages.
Option B, An incident, is an unplanned interruption to a service, or reduction in the quality of a service.
Removing something might cause an incident, but the act of removal itself is not the incident.
Option C, A problem, is the cause of one or more incidents. Again, removing something might reveal a problem
or resolve a problem, but the removal is not the problem itself.
Option D, An IT asset, refers to any financially valuable component that can contribute to the delivery of an IT
product or service. While removing an IT asset would likely be managed as a change, the term 'IT asset' itself
doesn't describe the action of removal and its potential impact. The question specifically asks for a term
describing the action of removing something with potential impact, which is change.

Therefore, the most accurate ITIL 4 terminology for removing something that could impact a service is a
change, making it the correct answer. Effective change management processes, as defined by ITIL 4, help
organizations to carefully manage this process and mitigate potential negative impacts to the business.
Supporting documentation:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation: ITIL 4 Edition: This is the core text and provides detailed definitions of ITIL 4
concepts.
ITIL Foundation Handbook: ITIL 4 Edition: A supplementary guide that reinforces the principles of ITIL 4.
(Available through various online retailers).
Official ITIL website (AXELOS): https://www.axelos.com/ Provides official resources, training, and
certifications related to ITIL. While specific pages may change, searching for "ITIL 4 Change Management" on
the site will yield relevant information.
Question: 357 CertyIQ
Which approach is CORRECT when applying the guiding principle "˜keep it simple and practical'?
A.Only add controls and metrics when they are needed
B.Design controls and metrics first, then remove those not adding value
C.Design controls and metrics and add them individually until all are implemented
D.Only add controls and metrics that are required for compliance
Answer: A
Explanation:
The guiding principle "Keep it simple and practical" emphasizes efficiency and avoiding unnecessary
complexity. Option A, "Only add controls and metrics when they are needed," directly aligns with this
principle. It promotes a lean approach where controls and metrics are implemented based on demonstrable
need, preventing over-engineering and wasted resources. Option B is the opposite of the principle, leading to
potential wasted effort in creating unnecessary components. Option C introduces the risk of inefficient and
overly complex implementation of controls and metrics. Option D focuses narrowly on compliance, potentially
overlooking improvements that could be achieved by addressing real business needs, and can therefore
become a rigid application without consideration for simplification. Applying controls or metrics prematurely
or comprehensively introduces operational overhead and unnecessary complexity. Keeping things simple and
practical means only adding what is required to deliver value and manage risk.
Key aspects of the guiding principle are:
Focus on value: Every control and metric must demonstrably contribute to a desired outcome.
Streamline processes: Remove redundancies and unnecessary steps.
Prioritize action: Don't over-analyze or over-document; focus on getting things done efficiently.
Start small: Implement changes incrementally and assess their impact.
Option A supports these aspects by emphasizing need-based implementation, minimizing wasted effort, and
facilitating incremental adjustments.
Further Information:
AXELOS. ITIL Foundation: ITIL 4 Edition. TSO, 2019.
Official ITIL documentation, available via AXELOS.

Question: 358 CertyIQ
Which is considered by the "˜partners and suppliers' dimension?
A.Using artificial intelligence
B.Defining controls and procedures
C.Using formal roles and responsibilities
D.Working with an integrator to manage relationships
Answer: D
Explanation:
The "partners and suppliers" dimension of ITIL 4 focuses on the relationships an organization has with
external entities providing services or components needed for value creation. These entities could include
cloud providers, software vendors, consultants, or outsourcing firms.
Option D, "Working with an integrator to manage relationships," directly addresses this dimension. Integrators
are often used to manage complex multi-vendor environments, ensuring smooth coordination and integration
between different suppliers, especially crucial in cloud environments that commonly involve services from
multiple providers (IaaS, PaaS, SaaS). This management includes contract negotiation, performance
monitoring, and issue resolution.
Options A, B, and C are not directly related to the "partners and suppliers" dimension:
A. Using artificial intelligence: AI could potentially be utilized by partners or suppliers, but it's not the core
focus of the dimension itself. The dimension centers on the relationship aspect.
B. Defining controls and procedures: Controls and procedures fall under the "information and technology"
dimension and the "value streams and processes" dimension.
C. Using formal roles and responsibilities: While important for any organizational structure, formal roles are
more relevant to the "organizations and people" dimension.
Therefore, selecting an integrator specifically addresses the challenges of managing external relationships
and ensuring the coordinated delivery of services, a key aspect of the "partners and suppliers" dimension. A
well-managed relationship with an integrator is crucial for leveraging external capabilities effectively and
realizing the benefits of cloud services.
Further resources:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation: ITIL 4 Edition: This book provides a detailed explanation of the four dimensions of
service management.
ITIL 4 Foundation Study Guide: Offers a comprehensive overview of ITIL 4 concepts and principles.
In conclusion, the most appropriate answer is D because it directly involves managing the relationships with
external entities critical for delivering services, particularly in complex cloud-based environments.
Question: 359 CertyIQ
Which is one of the MAIN concerns of the "˜design and transition' value chain activity?
A.Understanding the organization's vision
B.Understanding stakeholder needs
C.Meeting stakeholder expectations
D.Ensuring service components are available

Answer: C
Explanation:
The correct answer is C. Meeting stakeholder expectations.
The "Design and Transition" value chain activity focuses on ensuring that new or changed services are built
and deployed effectively, meeting the agreed-upon requirements and, crucially, stakeholder expectations.
While understanding the organization's vision (A) and stakeholder needs (B) are important inputs into the
design and transition activity, the main concern during design and transition is actually delivering a service
that satisfies the expectations derived from those needs and vision. Ensuring service components are
available (D) is also vital, but it's primarily a concern of the "Obtain/Build" value chain activity.
Design and transition encompasses planning, designing, building, testing, and deploying services. This
includes ensuring that the service is fit for purpose (meets the required functionality) and fit for use (meets
performance, usability, and other non-functional expectations). If stakeholder expectations are not met, even
a perfectly functional service may be deemed a failure. The transition phase, in particular, emphasizes change
enablement, ensuring changes are smoothly implemented with minimal disruption and achieve the intended
outcome. Therefore, proactively managing and meeting stakeholder expectations throughout the design and
transition is paramount to successful service delivery within the ITIL 4 framework. The focus isn't just about
technical implementation, but also about the perceived value and utility of the service from the stakeholder
perspective. Meeting expectations means ensuring communication, addressing concerns, and delivering a
solution that aligns with their understanding of the service's purpose and benefits.
Further reading on ITIL 4 Value Chain Activities and stakeholder management in service design and transition
can be found at:
Axelos ITIL 4 Foundation Handbook: Provides a comprehensive overview of ITIL 4 concepts, including the
Service Value System and value chain activities. (This is generally a paid resource).
Official ITIL 4 Documentation (e.g., on AXELOS website): Look for resources detailing the Design and
Transition activity, focusing on meeting customer/stakeholder expectations in service delivery.
Question: 360 CertyIQ
Which is a result of applying the guiding principle "˜progress iteratively with feedback'?
A.The ability to discover and respond to failure earlier
B.Standardization of practices and services
C.Understanding the customer's perception of value
D.Understanding the current state and identifying what can be reused
Answer: A
Explanation:
Here's a detailed justification for why option A is the correct answer, explaining why iterative progress with
feedback leads to earlier failure detection and response:
The "progress iteratively with feedback" guiding principle emphasizes breaking down large initiatives into
smaller, manageable chunks. Each iteration represents a mini-project with specific goals and deliverables.
Crucially, at the end of each iteration, feedback is actively sought and incorporated.
This iterative approach allows for early and frequent testing of assumptions and design choices. If an error is
introduced or an assumption proves incorrect, it is likely to be identified within the short iteration cycle,
before it cascades and impacts a larger portion of the project. The small scope of each iteration makes

debugging and correction more manageable and less costly. This stands in contrast to a waterfall approach
where errors might not surface until much later, requiring extensive rework.
Furthermore, the feedback loop encourages continuous improvement. By regularly seeking input from
stakeholders and users, the team gains valuable insights into potential issues or unmet needs. This proactive
feedback mechanism allows for adjustments to be made promptly, preventing potential failures from
escalating. Early failure detection also means resources are not wasted on pursuing dead ends, and the
project can pivot more efficiently. This ultimately leads to better alignment with user requirements and
improved quality.
Standardization (B) can be helpful, but isn't the core result of iterative progress with feedback. Understanding
the customer's perception of value (C) is important, but relates more strongly to the "focus on value" principle,
even though feedback can contribute to it. Understanding the current state (D) is linked to the "start where
you are" principle. Option A directly demonstrates the benefit of short cycles and fast feedback within those
cycles.
In essence, applying the "progress iteratively with feedback" guiding principle creates a safe-to-fail
environment, allowing for continuous learning and adaptation throughout the project lifecycle.Links for
further research:
AXELOS - ITIL 4 Guiding Principles: Look up the official descriptions from AXELOS (the creators of ITIL):
https://www.axelos.com/ (This is the general website; you'll need to search for ITIL 4 and the Guiding
Principles).
PeopleCert - ITIL 4 Foundation: PeopleCert is an examination institute for ITIL. Their resources provide an in-
depth exploration of ITIL 4 concepts: https://www.peoplecert.org/ (Similar to AXELOS, you'll need to search
for ITIL 4 Foundation).
Question: 361 CertyIQ
Which should be handled by "˜service request management'?
A.A request to implement a security patch
B.A request to provide a laptop
C.A request to resolve an error in a service
D.A request to change a target in a service level agreement
Answer: B
Explanation:
The correct answer, B. "A request to provide a laptop," falls under service request management because it's a
standardized, pre-defined procedure for fulfilling a user's need for a common IT resource. Service Request
Management focuses on fulfilling these routine requests efficiently.
A request to implement a security patch (A) is typically handled by Incident Management or Change
Management, as it addresses a potential service disruption or a necessary alteration to the service itself.
Resolving an error in a service (C) also falls under Incident Management, dealing with unplanned interruptions
or degradations. Finally, changing a target in a service level agreement (D) involves Change Management and
potentially Service Level Management processes because it's a modification to the service itself.
Service requests are usually low-risk, well-understood, and require minimal evaluation before being fulfilled.
Providing a laptop is a standard offering with an established fulfillment process (e.g., approval, procurement,
configuration, delivery). Therefore, its best categorized as a service request. The other options involve more
complex problem-solving, risk assessment, or strategic decision-making, making them unsuitable for simple

service request handling.
For further research:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation: https://www.axelos.com/certifications/itil-certifications (This is the official source
for ITIL information. While a specific page defining Service Request Management isn't directly linked,
exploring the general certification provides access to related documentation and definitions).
BMC Blogs - ITIL Service Request Management: https://www.bmc.com/blogs/itil-service-request-
management/ (This blog post offers a clear explanation of service request management and its relation to
other ITIL processes.)
Question: 362 CertyIQ
What can help to reduce resistance to a planned improvement when applying the guiding principle "˜collaborate
and promote visibility'?
A.Restricting information about the improvement to essential stakeholders only.
B.Increasing collaboration and visibility for the improvement.
C.Involving customers after all planning has been completed.
D.Engaging every stakeholder group in the same way, with the same communication.
Answer: B
Explanation:
The correct answer, "Increasing collaboration and visibility for the improvement," directly aligns with the ITIL
4 guiding principle of "collaborate and promote visibility." This principle emphasizes the importance of open
communication, transparency, and inclusive engagement throughout any change initiative. By actively sharing
information, involving relevant stakeholders, and fostering a collaborative environment, organizations can
significantly reduce resistance to planned improvements.
Option A, restricting information, directly contradicts this principle. Keeping information limited breeds
mistrust and uncertainty, leading to increased resistance as people feel excluded and uninformed about
potential impacts.
Option C, involving customers only after planning, misses a critical opportunity to gather valuable input early
in the process. Early customer engagement allows for adjustments based on their needs and concerns,
making the final improvement more relevant and acceptable. Delaying involvement often results in rework
and increased resistance as solutions may not meet customer expectations.
Option D, engaging every stakeholder group in the same way, neglects the diverse needs and perspectives of
different stakeholder groups. Effective communication requires tailoring the message and approach to
resonate with each specific group, ensuring that their individual concerns are addressed appropriately. A one-
size-fits-all approach is often ineffective and can increase resistance.
Therefore, increasing collaboration and visibility ensures that all stakeholders are informed, involved, and
have a chance to contribute to the improvement process. This fosters a sense of ownership and
understanding, ultimately reducing resistance and increasing the likelihood of successful implementation. It
acknowledges that change is easier to accept when the reasons for it are clear, the process is transparent,
and stakeholders feel heard and valued.For further research on ITIL 4 guiding principles, refer to the official
AXELOS ITIL documentation and resources.
https://www.axelos.com/

Question: 363 CertyIQ
Which describes a "˜change authority'?
A.A model used to determine who will assess a change
B.A person who approves a change
C.A tool used to help changes
D.A way to manage the people aspects of change
Answer: B
Explanation:
The correct answer, B, that a "change authority" is a person who approves a change, directly aligns with the
core principles of ITIL 4 change management practices. ITIL 4 emphasizes controlled and authorized changes
to IT services and infrastructure. A change authority is a crucial role responsible for evaluating the risk,
impact, and feasibility of a proposed change. Their approval signifies that the change has been thoroughly
reviewed and aligns with the organization's change management policies and objectives.
Option A, referring to a model for assessing changes, is partially correct. A change authority does assess
changes but isn't the model itself; assessment is part of their role. Option C, a tool used to help changes,
points toward change management systems or tools, which support the process but aren't the authority
figure. Option D, managing the people aspects of change, touches on organizational change management, a
related but distinct area from the specific role of a change authority in ITIL 4. While a change authority needs
to consider the impact on people, their primary responsibility is the formal approval of the change based on
technical and business criteria. The change authority ensures that changes are introduced in a planned and
controlled way, minimizing disruption and maximizing benefits. Without this designated approval,
unauthorized or poorly planned changes could lead to service outages, data loss, or security vulnerabilities.
Therefore, the person responsible for granting formal approval of a change embodies the role of the change
authority as defined by ITIL 4 best practices.
For further research, refer to the official ITIL 4 documentation and resources provided by AXELOS, the
governing body of ITIL. Specifically, review the sections on change enablement and organizational structure
within the ITIL 4 Foundation materials. Also, exploring articles related to change management best practices
and responsibilities of change advisory boards (CABs) can offer additional insights into the role of the change
authority.
Question: 364 CertyIQ
When is the earliest that a workaround can be documented in "˜problem management'?
A.After the problem has been logged
B.After the problem has been prioritized
C.After the problem has been analyzed
D.After the problem has been resolved
Answer: A
Explanation:
The correct answer is A: After the problem has been logged. Here's a detailed justification:
Workarounds are temporary solutions implemented to reduce or eliminate the impact of an incident or

problem for which a full resolution isn't immediately available. In problem management, the primary goal is to
identify the root cause of incidents and prevent recurrence. However, during the investigation process,
services might still be disrupted. Therefore, documenting a workaround as early as possible is crucial.
Option A is correct because the moment a problem is logged, even without prioritization, analysis, or
resolution, the need for a workaround might be apparent. The very act of logging a problem indicates an issue
that disrupts service. If a workaround exists (even a known, previously documented one for similar issues), it
should be associated with the problem record immediately.
Option B is incorrect. While prioritization helps focus efforts, the workaround doesn't depend on prioritization.
A workaround can be identified and documented before the problem's priority is determined.
Option C is incorrect. Analyzing a problem takes time. Waiting until analysis is complete before documenting a
workaround delays providing relief to users and potentially increases the impact of the incident. The
workaround may even inform the analysis.
Option D is incorrect. If the problem is resolved, a workaround is no longer needed. The goal of a workaround
is to provide temporary relief until a permanent solution is implemented. Documenting a workaround only
after resolution defeats the purpose of having one.
Essentially, the sooner a workaround is documented and implemented, the faster the impact on business
operations is minimized. This aligns with ITIL 4's focus on value creation through faster resolution and reduced
disruption. The documented workaround also helps knowledge sharing within the team.
In the context of cloud computing, where services are often highly automated and scalable, prompt
workaround documentation can allow for faster temporary deployments or reconfigurations to mitigate
issues, minimizing the impact on users.
Consider a scenario where a specific cloud region experiences latency. A workaround might be routing traffic
to a different region. This workaround should be documented immediately upon logging the problem, not after
analyzing the root cause of the latency or waiting for a full resolution.
Here are some authoritative links for further research:
AXELOS ITIL 4 Foundation Guidance: (Refer to an ITIL 4 Foundation study guide or official publication.
Specific page numbers may vary.)
Problem Management Institute (PMI) Resources: https://www.pmi.org/ (While not directly ITIL, PMI offers
insights into project and problem management.)
ITIL Official Website (AXELOS): While often behind a paywall, searching for ITIL 4 Problem Management best
practices online can yield relevant articles.
Question: 365 CertyIQ
Which is an activity of "˜problem identification'?
A.Analyzing information from software developers
B.Establishing problem workarounds
C.Analyzing the cause of problems
D.Establishing potential permanent solutions
Answer: A
Explanation:

The correct answer is A, analyzing information from software developers, because problem identification
focuses on initially recognizing and defining a problem, rather than already working towards solutions,
workarounds, or root cause analysis. Problem identification is the preliminary stage where potential issues are
spotted, often through various channels, including communication with those directly involved in development
and maintenance like software developers. They possess valuable insights into system behavior, errors, and
anomalies that can indicate underlying problems.
Analyzing information from software developers can reveal patterns, recurring incidents, or specific bug
reports that point towards a common root cause or a wider system issue. This initial analysis helps to frame
the problem accurately. Establishing workarounds (B) comes later, once a problem is understood but a
permanent fix isn't immediately available. Analyzing the cause of problems (C) falls under problem analysis, a
subsequent activity to problem identification. Establishing potential permanent solutions (D) is part of
problem control or incident resolution, which are also later stages in the overall problem management
process. Identifying a problem is more about recognizing its existence and defining its scope based on initial
data, including reports or insights from sources like software developers. Their input often acts as the first
trigger that a deeper problem exists, requiring further investigation. In the ITIL 4 framework, early detection
and proper classification of problems are crucial for efficient resolution and prevention of future incidents.
Consider a cloud application experiencing intermittent performance slowdowns. Reports from end-users
might be vague. However, information from software developers regarding recent code deployments or newly
discovered resource bottlenecks during peak hours provides vital clues that point towards specific areas to
investigate. This information helps define the problem accurately, differentiating it from, say, a network issue.
For further research, refer to the official ITIL 4 Foundation publications and accredited training materials.
While specific web links to official materials can vary, searching for "ITIL 4 Foundation Problem Management"
or "ITIL 4 Problem Identification" will lead to valuable resources. The Axelos website (the owner of ITIL) is a
good starting point. Also consider referencing ITIL guides on platforms like ITSM.tools or similar resources
focused on IT Service Management.
